Et l’apelerent li ancien «cure contuse», et est que tu faices a rere au malaide qui a ceste maladie les poilz qu’il ait ou front, puis li fai III fendures ou front igalment selonc la longesce dou front; et soit l’une des fendures ausi com II doi tout emmi lou front en avalant aval jusc’a neif, et les autres II as II costelz par desus les papieres, et te garde de l’incision des arteres que sont as II costez par desus les papieres; et aloigne ta main de la continuation des II mandibules, et soit chescune plaie la quantiteit de III dois au traver joins; et aies apparillie une piece d’esponge et mout de drapelz ses por essuer lou sanc, puis boute le spatumile agut de II pars de coi ci est li forme:	And the ancients called it "cure contuse," and you make the patient who has this illness have hair on his forehead, then you make III incisions on the forehead equally according to the length of the forehead; and let one of the incisions be as II digits in the middle of the forehead going down until the nose, and the other two at each side above the temples, and beware of cutting into the arteries that are at both sides above the temples; and keep your hand away from the continuation of the two mandibles, and let each wound be the size of III digits across; and prepare a piece of sponge and much cloth for wiping the blood, then put the spatula sharp on both sides as here is the form:
des l’incision qui est dever la temple jusc’a la seconde incision; et escorche tout le keur qui est entre les II fendures a tot lou syfac qui est sus l’os, puis fai autreteil des la moiene incision jusc’a l’autre seconde, et puis estrai fuer cest spatumile.	from the incision which is above the temple until the second incision; and scrape all the flesh that is between the II incisions to the surface of the skin which is over the bone, then do the same from the middle incision until the other second incision, and then remove with this spatula.
si boute en la premiere fendure l’estrument qui est apelez «cultellaire», et est tresbien trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part est souef, ne mie trenchans, et c’est li forme:	Insert into the first groove the instrument called "cultellaire," and it is very well sharpened on one side, and on the other side it is smooth, not sharp, and this is its form:
Et met le costeit taillant vers la char aerse au keur, et lou costeit souef vers l’os, et lou boute tant qu’il veigne a la moiene fendure.	And place the cutting edge towards the flesh of the heart, and the smooth side towards the bone, and insert it until it reaches the middle groove.
Et cope toz les vasselz que dessendent dou chief as eulz tant que l’incision soit continue jusc’a ceu qui apert dou keur, et puis autreteil fai en la moiene fendure jusc’a l’autre defuer; et puis estrai dou sanc igalment, et espresse lou leu por le sanc pris; puis met en chescune fendure une tente de viel coton, et met sus drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile et en aisil, et garde que apostemes chaus n’i veigne; et au tier jor deslie lou liien, et i amenistre grant planteit d’aigue tede, puis lou cure d’oignement basilicon avec oile roset, et d’autres cures dont on cure plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And cut all the vessels that descend from the head to the eyes so that the incision is continuous until it reaches those near the heart, and then make another incision in the middle groove until the other side; and then draw out blood evenly, and apply pressure to stop bleeding; then place a wad of old cotton in each groove, cover with cloths moistened with wine, oil, and honey, and guard against abscesses from forming; and on the third day loosen the bandage, and bring plenty of cold water, then treat with basilicon ointment mixed with rose oil, and other treatments used for wounds until it is healed.
dou reume des eulz	of the rheum of the eyes
Quant a aucun vienent catarre agut acostumeement, et tu vois les eulz tenves et petis, et afoiblir la veue, et les papieres brulees; et li poil chieent, et ou chief en parfont a dolor ague, et li malaides esternue; adonques saiches par ces accidens que celles matieres et cil catharre ne vient fuer que de maintes voines, et li muedre cure que i est, si est ceste.	When catarrh frequently afflicts someone, and you see the eyes swollen and small, and the sight weakening, and the membranes burned; and the hair falls out, and in the head there is pain from ague, and the patient sneezes; then by these symptoms you know that these matters and this catarrh do not come except from many veins, and if there is any mucus that needs to be cleared, it is this.
Et est que tu comande au malaide a rere son front, puis fai une grant fendure emmi lou front, et une autre dou large I poc.	And it is that you instruct the patient behind their forehead, then make a large incision across the forehead, and another at the back of the head.
Et comence des la fendure de la temple senestre a la temple destre, et soit li incision jusc’a l’os; et esloigne ta main des ners des temples que muevent au mengier; et quant li os est descovers, si essue tout le sanc a une esponge, et puis desevre entre les II levres de la fendure et i met coton viel, et tentes de lin; puis lie desus drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile, et te garde d’aposteme chaut; quant il est ostez, si covient que tu frottes l’os tant que chars i comence a naistre, puis le cure de choses exiccatives, que font enjanrer char.	And start from the incision at the left temple to the right temple, and make the incision until it reaches the bone; and keep your hand away from the nerves of the temples that move when chewing; and when the bone is exposed, wipe all the blood with a sponge, then separate between the two edges of the cut and place old cotton there, and cover with bandages made of linen; then bind on wet cloths in wine and oil, and guard against hot abscesses; when it is removed, you must rub the bone until flesh begins to grow, then treat it with substances that stimulate growth.
En teil maniere: pren II parties de flor de froment, et de colofoine IIII parties, et en fai emplaustre; et l’aministre en ces plaies por enjanrer char per tout.	In such a manner: take two parts of wheat flour, and four parts of colophony, and make a poultice; and apply it to these wounds to regenerate flesh throughout.
de l’estoupement des oreilles	of the blockage of the ears
Tout ceu que chiet ens oreilles est une des IIII choses: ou grains, ou beste, ou piere de mine ou semblans chose si com fer; ou semence, si com jaisses, feves, pois; ou chose defluans si com aigue et aisilz et semblans choses.	All that falls into the ears is one of the four things: grains, animals, stones from mines or similar things such as iron; seeds, such as peas, beans, and lentils; or flowing substances such as water and pus and similar things.
Quant il chiet en l’oreille piere ou autre maniere de chose que ne s’ajoste mie a l’oreille, ne ne croist en l’oreille, si met l’oreille au solel.	When a stone or any other substance that does not fit into the ear and does not grow in the ear falls into it, place the ear towards the sun.
Se tu vois la piere, si distille aucun poc d’oile violet ou oile de sisament, puis i amenistre extraction; et lou fai esternuer de condisi, et li estoupe les narines quant li esternuemens vient, et met entor l’oreille pieces de drapelz ou laine; et estent l’oreille au desus.	If you see the stone, then distill a little violet oil or sesamum oil, and proceed with extraction; and make them sneeze with something dry, and plug their nostrils when they are about to sneeze, and place pieces of cloth or wool around the ear; and stretch the ear upward.
Mout de fois vient fuer par ceste cure; et s’elle ne vient fuer, se li amenistre extraction as pinceures subtilz, de coi ci est li forme:	Often the stone comes out through this treatment; and if it does not come out, proceed with extraction using delicate forceps, which are described here:
S’elle saut fuer as pinceures, c’est boin; se ceu non, si amenistre extraction a l’oncine subtil de petite doubleure; et s’elle ne saut par ceu, si fai une caine d’arain et boute lou chief de la cainne ou pertuis de l’oreille fort, et estoupe ceu qui est entor la cainne de cire mole si que li vens n’i puisse entrer avec la cainne; puis le trai fuer forment, car mout de fois vient fuer si com nos avons dit; et s’elle ne vient fuer en teil maniere, si prent glut de coi en prent les oisiaus, et met en som aucun estrument qui soit a point por ceu faire, et met un poc de coton entor; puis presse le glut sus la piere ou quel chose que ce soit, et trai fuer.	If it comes out with the forceps, that is good; if not, proceed with extraction using a fine double probe; and if it does not come out by this method, make a thread of silk and insert one end of the thread into the ear canal firmly, then plug around the thread with soft wax so that no air can enter through the thread; then pull it out forcefully, as often it comes out in this manner as we have said; and if it does not come out by such means, take glutinous material which birds use to stick their feathers together, place a small instrument at one end of it properly, wrap some cotton around it; then press the glutinous material onto the stone or whatever it is, and pull it out.
Et s’elle ne saut fuer de toutes ces choses que nos avons dit, si te haste de fendre l’oreille ainsois que aposteme chalz i veigne, et spasme; et li maniere de la fendure si est que tu faices premier sainier lou malaide de la cephalique, et estrai dou sanc selonc la mesure de sa vertu, puis fai seoir lou malaide entre tes mains et li torne l’oreille au desus, et fent une petite fendure en la racine de l’oreille a la graisse ou leu dependant; et soit li fendure ausi com une lune, tant que tu viegnes a la piere, puis l’oste selonc ton pooir, et la suce hastanment a ta bouche; et la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if she cannot escape from all these things that we have said, hurry to cut the ear as one would for an abscess or cramp; and the manner of cutting is that you first bleed the patient with cephalic bleeding, and extract blood according to the measure of her strength, then seat the patient between your hands and turn the ear upwards, and make a small incision at the root of the ear where it hangs down; let the cut be as crescent-shaped as possible until you reach the stone, then remove it as much as you can, and suck it quickly into your mouth; continue treating until she is well.
Et se c’est grains qui est ens et il enfle, si aministre extraction; et si’il ne puet issir, si amenistre I spatumile tenve subtil selonc ceste forme:	And if this grain is inside and it swells, then administer extraction; and if it cannot come out, then administer a fine poultice according to this form:
et amenistre incision de celui grain.	and administer an incision of that tumor.
Mais ne faire mie ceu quant tu penses que li grains est moistes por la moistor de l’oreille, tant que tu en aies fait maintes pieces; puis l’estrai as pinceures subtilz et au succier, si com nos avons dit, si que li estractions soit aligie.	But do not do this when you think the tumor is moist due to moisture from the ear, until you have done many cases; then extract it with fine forceps and suction, as we have said, so that the extraction is gentle.
En l’aigue donques que chiet en l’oreille covient que li malaides use d’esternuement de condisi premiers, et ample l’oreille de viel coton.	In acute cases where water enters the ear, the patient should use sneezing with pepper first, and plug the ear with old cotton.
Et soit gisans sus celle oreille meisme ou li aigue est.	And lie down on the side where the water is.
s’elle saut fuer per ceu, c’est boin.	if it comes out because of that, it is good.
se ceu non, si prent maintes pieres selonc li longesce de ton doit tenves et legieres, et les eschaufe un poc au feu; et em mette li malaides une ou pertus de son oreille, et saille sus i. de ses piez d’autre part, et fiere d’une autre piere sus la piere qui est en l’oreille; et ne cesse de faire ceu de piere em piere tant que li aigue isse toute fuer, et ensi saut elle toute fuer; et se tu vues, si prent I jonc, et boute l’un des chiés en l’oreille, et l’autre chief emprent de feu tant que li plus dou jonc soit ars; puis refai autreteil d’autres jons tant que li aigue isse toute, si com nos avons dit en la piere.	If not that, take many stones according to the length of your thumb, light and easy, and warm them slightly over the fire; then place one stone in the patient's ear, and press with another stone on the stone which is in the ear; and do not stop pressing stone upon stone until all the water comes out, and thus it will come entirely out; and if you wish, take a reed, and insert one end of it into the ear, and set fire to the other end so that the softer part of the reed burns; then repeat this with other reeds until all the water comes out, as we have said about the stones.
En l’estraction de la beste, s’elle est de petit cors, si com puce et semblans chose, cure la si com nos avons dit en la division; mais s’elle est de grant cors c’on la puisse sentir, si amenistre extraction de pinceures; et c’est li chose plus legiere a oster qui soit en l’oreille.	In the removal of the creature, if it is small in size, such as a flea and similar things, treat it as we have said in the division; but if it is large enough to be felt, remove it with forceps; and this is the easiest thing to extract from the ear.
En l’estraction des vers enjanrez as oreilles, quant tu lou cures si com nos avons dit en la division et ou traitier des distillations, et li cure ne profite mie, si covient que tu regardes l’oreille au soleil: s’il i apert nulz vers, si les trai as pinceures subtilz, et s’il n’aperent, si prent la cainne de coi ci est li forme:	In the extraction of worms from the ears, when you treat them as we have said in the division and in the treatment of distillations, and the cure does not help, then it is necessary that you look at the ear in the sun: if any worms are visible, remove them with fine tweezers, and if none appear, take the chain which is of this form:
Et soit estroite desoz et large desus.	And let it be narrow below and wide above.
Et boute lou plus subtil chief en l’oreille selonc la quantiteit de la soffrance dou malaide, puis succe forment a tot la caine; fai ceu sovent tant que tuit li ver issent.	And insert the finer end into the ear according to the severity of the patient's pain, then gradually form it all along the chain; do this often until all the worms come out.
Et s’il n’obeissent a issir, si estoupe entor la cainne de coton si com j’ai dit en la piere; et s’il ne saillent fuer si com nos avons dit, si aministre distillations que li ancien ont esprovees en l’ocision des vers, et tu les troveras ou traitier des distillations; et si distille tes oiles et tes medicines en l’oreille a tout cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme si com tu vois:	And if they do not come out, wrap the chain with cotton as I have said about stones; and if they do not emerge as we have said, administer distillations that the ancients have tested for worm removal, which you will find in the treatment of distillations; and distill your oils and medicines into the ear using this instrument, which has the form as you see:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain estrois desoz a I petis pertuis, et desus overs por distiller; et por presser dedens la distillation a I estrument d’arain bien fait por ceu, et se tu vues pren I raseur et envoloupe entor la pointe avenanment coton; puis i giete ton oile ou ton jus, et ceu que tu vues de tes medicines en la cainne, et li caine soit en l’oreille; puis boute dedens lou raseur a tout lou coton, et presse ta main tempreement tant que li oile soit distilleit ou chevement de l’oreille; et lou sente li malaides dedens, et soit li distillations I poc eschaufee au feu ainsois c’on la distille en l’oreille; et garde qu’elle ne soit trop froide, car li medicine ne seroit mie si bone.	And whether of silver or brass, make it narrow with small holes, and place something above to drop through; and for pressing within the distillation use a well-made brass instrument, and if you wish take a razor and wrap around the tip some linen cloth; then pour your oil or juice, and whatever medicine you want into the channel, and let the channel be in the ear; then put inside the razor all the cloth, and press with your hand gently until the oil is distilled within the ear; and let the patient feel it inside, and keep the distillation a little warmed by fire as one distills in the ear; and beware that it does not become too cold, for the medicine would not be so good.
de l’estoupement des oreilles	of the obstruction of the ears
Aucun enfant naissent qui n’ont nul pertus ens oreilles; et ceste meisme chose avient as homes par estoupement de plaie, ou de char nee dedens l’oreille, et cist estoupemens vient aucune fois em parfont en l’oreille, si c’on ne lou puet veoir; et aucune fois avient I poc defuer lou pertus, et lou voit om bien.	Some children are born without any hole in their ears; and the same thing happens to adults due to an obstruction of a wound, or flesh grown inside the ear, and these obstructions sometimes come from deep within the ear, so that one cannot see them; and sometimes it is possible for pus to exit the hole, and then one can see it clearly.
Celle donques que vient em parfont, si c’on ne la puet veoir, est de grief sanation em plusors dispositions, et en cele c’on voit covient que tu mettes l’oreille dou malaide au soleil; et regarde dedens: se tu vois l’opilation apparent, si la oevre a tot cest spatumile de coi ci est li forme:	That which comes from deep within and cannot be seen is difficult to treat in many cases, and for the one that can be seen, you should place the patient's ear towards the sun; and look inside: if you see inflammation apparent, then proceed with this spatula of such a form:
Et soit agus et trenchans devant et derrier tout plain, si qu’il ne blece l’oreille; se li opilation est de char nee ou cors de l’oreille, si la tien as pinceures subtilz, et la cope legierement, tant que celle chars soit toute ostee.	And let it be sharp and cutting in front, and smooth behind so that it does not hurt the ear; if the inflammation is flesh grown or part of the ear's body, then hold it with fine forceps, and gently scrape it away until all the flesh is removed.
Et se li opilations est em parfont en l’oreille, si pren I raseur subtil legier et l’eschaufe un petit au feu, puis li met ou cors de l’oreille.	And if the wax is placed in the ear, take a fine razor and warm it slightly over the fire, then place it on the flesh of the ear.
Se tu sens l’opilation dont li malaides sent grieteit a l’oïr, perce legierement, et garde que tu ne grever les ners de l’oreille; puis met en l’oreille une tente selonc la largesce dou pertus, et la moille en l’oignement egyptien.	If you feel the wax and the patient feels pain in the ear, pierce it gently, and be careful not to damage the nerves of the ear; then place a tent in the ear according to the width of the opening, and moisten it with Egyptian ointment.
Fai ceu aucun jor tant que li plaie soit soudee, ou tu pren une tente et la moille en aigue rose, et poudre sus vitriole broiet; et se tu vois enflee l’oreille, si couvient que tu traies la tente et remue une autre tente moillie en cerote qui soit fait d’oile roset et de cire, tant que li enfleure soit ostee; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Do this for several days until the wound is sealed, when you take a tent and moisten it with rose water, and sprinkle powdered vitriol on it; and if you see that the ear is swollen, then you should remove the tent and replace it with another tent moistened in cerate made of rose oil and wax, until the swelling is gone; then treat it until it is healed.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si plonge une esponge et drapelz en aigue froide, et le met sus l’oreille, et use d’autres cures qui oste lou decorrement de sanc qui sont ou traitier des destillations.	And if bleeding occurs, plunge a sponge and cloths in cold water, and place it on the ear, and use other treatments that stop the bleeding which are in the treatment of hemorrhages.
de la char des papieres	of the flesh of papers
Cist althelul que vienent em papieres des eulz quant ils sont moiste et sont sec, si covient que tu les estendes de tenailles et de pinceures, et le cope d’un spatumile de ses racines; puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet.	This eyelid that comes on papers when they are moist and dry, you must stretch it with pliers and forceps, and cut a piece from its root with a scalpel; then place powdered vitriol over the area.
Et se sans en decort, si le cauterize dou cautere lenticulaire subtil, et li cauterizeir aprés l’incision vaut mues; et maintes fois repairent, cant aucune chose demoure de lor racines; et quant elles sont cauterizees par feu, si sont arses celles racines et ne revienent mie.	And if they do not peel off, cauterize them with a lentil-shaped cautery and let them heal after incision; and often they repair themselves, as some part remains of their roots; and when they are cauterized by fire, those roots are burned and do not return.
de la gresle	from the hailstone
Maintes fois vienent em papieres des eulz unes choses que semblent gresle en sa forme et en sa duresce, et por ceu est ceste maladie apelee «grandine», et est une assemblee de moistor grosse en la papiere desus et desoz; li ovraiges est telz: pren warde se li grandine se muet d’une part et d’autre, et c’est legiere chose a savoir; fent la donques dou large, puis l’escorche de chescune partie legierement, puis la prent as pinceures, et la cope.	Many times, things that resemble hailstones in form and hardness appear on the eyelids, and for this reason, this disease is called "hail," and it is a collection of thick moisture in the upper and lower lid; the treatment is as follows: observe if the hail moves from side to side, which is easy to know; then cut it widely, then gently scrape each part, then take it with forceps, and cut it.
se tu ne la pues coper sens percier un poc la papiere, si ne grieve rien au malaide; et se li fendure est grans, si l’assemble a une costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee; et s’elle est petite, si n’i faire point de force, car li oignemens la restoure tantost et enjanre char.	If you cannot cut it without piercing a bit of the membrane, do not cause any harm to the patient; and if the incision is large, then stitch it up with a suture, and treat it until it heals; and if it is small, make no forceful action, for the ointment will heal it quickly and regenerate flesh.
Et se li grandine est dessendans au dedens de l’oreille vers la partie desus, si enverse la papiere, et estent la grandine a unes pinceures, et la cope et presse d’une part et d’autre; et se li papiere est esloignie par l’incision, ce ne grieve rien; et quant li grandine est copee, si leive l’oil d’aigue salee, et cure le leu de ceu qui enjanre char tant que li malaides soit sanez.	And if the grain is descending inside the ear towards the upper part, then invert the membrane, and extract the grain with forceps, and cut and press from both sides; and if the membrane is separated by incision, it does no harm; and when the grain is removed, pour in salt water, and treat the area that regenerates flesh until the patient is healed.
de la graisse des eulz	of the grease of the eyes
Exinach est une graisse qui est enjanree en toiles des papieres desus, et ce avient plus as enfans c’a nules gens, et grieve mout a lor eulz, et li vienent li catharre as matinees, et ne pueent regardeir la lumiere dou soleil por ceu que les larmes se hastent a lor eulz; et por ceu se couchent il sor lor faices adés, et dorment sus, et sont lor papieres desoz lor sorcilz moistes que li enfleure et li apparance ont covert de l’exinach qui apert en l’oil.	Exinach is a grease that is generated in the membranes of the eyes, and this happens more often with children than adults, and it greatly troubles their eyes, and they get catarrh in the mornings, and cannot look at the light of the sun because tears rush to their eyes; and for this reason they lie down on their faces immediately, and sleep like that, and their membranes under their eyebrows become moist, which is covered with exinach that appears in the eye.
Et quant tu presses lou leu a tes dois et sent l’exirnach entr’ous.	And when you press the area with your thumbs and feel the exinach between them.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain; et puis pren I drapeil de lin, et appareille une tente em maniere d’un cercle selonc la quantiteit que conteigne exirnach de chescune partie, puis le met sus li; et presse a tes dois d’une part et d’autre, si que li exirnach soit assemblez emmi le cercle; puis fent em mileu de la moistor au spatumile trenchant une fendure dou large, et ne soit mie plus grans que li plaie c’on fait a la sainie de voinne; et fent le cuir em parfont tant que tu veignes a l’exirnach; et em plusors dispositions vient exirnach de la fendure, selonc la forme d’une piece de graisse blainche.	And the method of work is that the patient places their head on your lap; then take a linen cloth and prepare a tent in the shape of a circle according to the amount of exinach in each part, then place it over them; and press with your thumbs from both sides so that the exinach gathers within the circle; then cut an incision through the moisture with a sharp spatula, no wider than the vein-cutting wound; and cut the skin perfectly until you reach the exinach; and in many cases, the exinach comes out of the incision, resembling a piece of white grease.
Estrai la donques a tout une piece de drap charpit entre tes dois au defuer, et torne ta main a destre et a senestre tant qu’il soit espars; et garde que tu n’ajoster en la fendure, que tu ne viegnes a tout le spatumile jusc’a l’oil, que tu ne le bleces.	Draw it out then in one piece of torn cloth when you remove it, and turn your hand right and left until it is spread; and be careful that you do not press into the opening, so as not to bring all the spatumile up to the eye, so as not to injure it.
Et se li exirnach n’apert en l’encomencement de la fendure, si acroi un poc la fendure legierement tant qu’il apere; puis l’estrai si com nos avons dit, puis moille drapelz en aisil et en aigue, et met sus le leu, et estrain de bendelz.	And if the excrement does not appear at the beginning of the opening, then widen the opening slightly until it appears; then draw it out as we have said, then moisten cloths in oil and water, and place them on the area, and pull out bandages.
Et si a de tels homes qui broient seil et mettent sus por corrompre cele moistor qui est demoree.	And there are such people who grind salt and put it on to corrupt the moisture that remains.
Puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then treat him until he is well.
Et s’il vient au leu aposteme chaut, si lou cure d’emplaustres assouajant tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if he comes to the place of an abscess that is hot, treat him with soothing plasters until he is well.
des poilz des papieres	of the hair of the eyebrows
Quant em papieres naissent poilz ajostez autre que li naturez, et sont enveillit, si nuisent as eulz, et font venir manieres de maladies si com larmes acostumees et mollifications des papieres et albugine, tant que c’est cause de la destruction des eulz; et est li cure selonc IIII manieres: ou par cautere ensamble feu, ou par medicine ague selonc ceu qu’il est devant ou chapistre de cautere, et est fais ou par incision et costure ou par caines, selonc ceu que je dirai.	When hairs grow in the eyebrows that are not natural and become inflamed, they harm the eyes and cause various diseases such as habitual tears and inflammation of the eyelids and conjunctiva, to the point where it leads to the destruction of the eyes; and the treatment is according to four methods: either by cautery with fire together, or by medicine as previously described in the chapter on cautery, and can also be done by incision and suturing, or by cauterization, as I will explain.
Il covient que tu mettes lou chief dou malaide en ton sain, puis torne la papiere de l’oil a ta main senestre; s’elle est convertie, c’est boin; se ceu non, si i boute une aguille a tout I fil desus; et soit ce delez la marge de la papiere ou li poil naissent delez ces poilz, et trai I fil au desus a tout la papiere, et la torne au raseur; puis fent en la partie desoz la papiere, desoz les poilz ajostez, a tout le spatumile copant, des le grant larmier jusc’au petit; puis estrai I fil, et met desoz la papiere une petite tente de couton et de drapeil, puis seigne sus la papiere une figure d’enche, si com la fuelle de mirte, et toutevoie il covient que li figure soit selonc la quantiteit que tu vues eslever la papiere qui est devisez a toz.	It is necessary that you place the head of the patient in your lap, then turn the paper of the eye to your left hand; if it turns well, it is good; if not, put a needle along all the thread; and let this be next to the margin of the paper where the hair grows among these hairs, and draw the thread above all the paper, and turn it at the edge; then cut in the part below the paper, below the adjacent hairs, up to the spatumile cutting from the large tear duct to the small; then extract the thread, and place under the paper a small pad of cotton and linen, then sew on the paper a figure of an incision, like the leaf of myrtle, and always it is necessary that the figure be according to the quantity that you wish to raise the paper which is designated for all.
Et si a teil qui a mestier c’on cope grant quantiteit de la papiere selonc ceu que li papiere est mollifie; puis fent a tout le spatumile sus les II lignes que tu as signiet, et comence des lou grant larmier jusc’a petit; et soit li une des fendures pres des poilz naturez en la groissece d’un raiz, puis boute l’oncine en l’un des II angles dou keur, puis l’escorche toute; puis assemble les II levres a une costure d’une aguille a tout I fil de laine subtil, et essue le sanc, et fai aerdre la superfluiteit des filz sus les II sorcilz a tout aucunes choses gluans, se tu vues faire ce; et se ce non, si n’en aies cure, puis laisse la costure et les filz jusc’a III jors ou IIII; puis cure la plaie sens costure de choses sechans et constrignans, car li papiere se relive au soudement de la plaie et l’assemblement de li, mais li costure est muedre (si com dirent li ancien), et c’est ovraiges sens paor; et si a une autre maniere: et est que tu seignes la papiere d’une figure qui soit ausi com li fuelle de mirte, si com nos avons conteit, a III oncines desevrez selonc la forme qui est ci:	And if there is need for one to cut a large quantity of the paper according to how the paper is softened; then cut all over the spatulum on both lines that you have marked, and start from the larger tear up to smaller ones; and let one of the cuts be near the natural hairs in the thickness of a root, then insert the needle into one of the two corners of the wound, then skin it entirely; then stitch together the two lips with a seam using a fine needle and thread of linen, and wipe away the blood, and remove any excess threads above both eyebrows if you wish to do so; and if not, do not worry about it, then leave the seam and the threads for three or four days; then treat the wound without stitching from dry and binding substances, because the paper lifts up immediately at the edge of the wound and its assembly, but the stitch is uncomfortable (as the ancients say), and these are works without fear; and there is another way: which is to mark the paper with a shape that resembles the leaf of myrtle, as we have recounted, for three inches apart according to the form which is here described:
puis cope ceu qui sormonte as petites forces igalment selonc la forme qui est ci:	Then cut those which rise above the smaller parts equally according to the shape which is here:
Et se tu n’as pooir de tenir les tenailles, et li chose n’est mie igalz, si prent une aguille ou il ait I fil, et la boute emmi la figure; et boute I autre fil delez lou grant larmier, et lou secont fil delez lou petit, et assemble entre tes dois les filz igalment; puis lieve ta main igalment, et lieve tout le cuir sus coi tu as signiet, si com nos avons conteit, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie par costure, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et se aposteme vient a ton incision, si l’apaise de cerote et de semblans oignement assouajans; et aucune fois avient que li poil de la papiere sont convertit: si covient que tu uses ceu que nos avons dit de l’incision; mais li costure en l’une et en l’autre est plus artificialz.	And if you cannot hold the forceps, and the parts are not even, then take a needle with a thread, and insert it in the shape; and place another thread next to the large wound margin, and the second thread next to the small one, and join between your two threads evenly; then lift your hand evenly, and lift all the skin on which you have marked, as we have recounted, then stitch together both edges of the wound; and if an abscess comes from your incision, soothe it with cerate and similar soothing ointments; and sometimes the hair on the paper turns: then it is necessary to use what we have said about the incision; but the stitching in one and the other way is more artificial.
Li cure des caines si est selonc ceste forme: et est que tu convertisses la papiere et la fent dedens selonc ceu que j’ai dit, et puis fai II caines par art, et II liiens subtilz ausi lonc com li papiere et li largesce dou spatumile est; et cope as II chiés de II pars ou tu tiens les filz; puis assemble l’un et l’autre subtilment sus ceu que sormonte de la papiere de l’oil, et estrain les II cainnes des II parties forment; et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, et li cuir qui iert estrainte morra et nercira et porrira, tant qu’il cherra par lui.	The treatment of the canthi is as follows: and it is that you turn the paper and cut inside according to what I have said, and then make two canthi by art, and two fine threads as long as the paper and the width of the spatula are; and tie at the two corners where you hold the threads; then join one with the other delicately over what protrudes from the paper of the eye, and pull the two canthi from both sides firmly; and leave it thus for some days, and the skin which is pulled will die off and heal and grow back, until it falls off by itself.
S’il tarde, si le cope a unes forces, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et quant li plaie iert soudee, et si ert levee li papiere, et ne poindront plus li poil; et c’est li forme des II cainnes que tu feras selonc ceste figure, et selonc ceste quantiteit de lonc et de large:	If it delays, cut it with force, then treat until it is healed; and when the wound has sealed, and if the paper is raised, and no hair will grow again; and this is the form of the two canthi that you will make according to this figure, and according to this measure of length and width:
li ovraiges est telz que tu preignes une aguille subtil, et i boute I fil de soie souef et subtil; puis assemble les chiés et noe l’un et l’autre subtilment, et soit li longesce des filz une palme de lonc; puis ordene en la chasse I autre fil subtil de soie briément, et noe les chief dou fil; puis mette li malaides son chief en ton sain; et soit delez lou soleil si que li ovraiges soit declairiez, car c’est uns ovraiges subtilz et menus, puis boute l’aguille a tout la chasse en la racine dou poil ajosteit, et la fai percier en la papiere hastanment tant que tu la traies desus lou poil natureil; puis estrai le poil jusque sus la chasse, et boute en la chasse celui poil, s’il en i a I ou II ou III ou plusors; puis estrai ta main tant que li poilz veigne fuers a tout la chasse en la papiere avec lou poil natureil.	The work is such that you take a fine needle, and pass a thin silk thread under it; then join the heads and tie one to the other subtly, and let the length of the threads be one palm long; then arrange in the socket another thin silk thread briefly, and knot the ends of the thread; then place the patient's head on your hand; and let it be near the sun so that the work is illuminated, for this is a subtle and delicate work, then insert the needle throughout the socket at the root of the hair adjacent to it, and make it pierce through the membrane quickly until you draw it above the natural hair; then extract the hair up to the socket, and place in the socket that hair if there are one or two or three or more; then withdraw your hand so that the hairs become exposed throughout the socket with the natural hair.
Et se li chasse est traite et li poilz ne vient fuer avec li, si trairas la chasse au desoz a tout le fil que tu i as ordeneit, tant que li chasse veigne fuer dou pertus desus et que tu la voies par la vision de l’oil; adonques si trairas la chasse et le fil, et clo l’oil et lou laisse clo II jors ou III, tant que li poil s’aerde en son leu et naisse li char sus; et se li poilz est petis, si acompaigne I poil lonc des chevoulz naturez, et soit alevez avec celui ou tu le laisse, tant qu’il soit eslongiez et puis le lieve.	And if the chaser is treated and the hair does not come out with it, then pull the chaser to the back along the entire thread that you have attached, until the chaser comes out from above the hole and you see it through your eye; then pull out the chaser and the thread, close the eye and leave it closed for two days or three, until the hair hardens in its place and flesh grows over; and if the hair is short, attach one long hair of natural ones next to where you left it, and lift it along with that one until it is pulled out.
de la porriture de l’oil	from the pus of the eye
Quant ceste maladie qui est apelee «aleacrati» ou li porriture vient en l’oil, si en i a de II manieres: l’une natureil, et l’autre innatureil.	When this disease called "aleacrati" or pus comes in the eye, there are two ways it can occur: one naturally, and the other unnaturally.
Et avient par soudement de plaie, ou de tailleure ou de cautere, et par semblans choses.	And it happens by sudden incision, or cutting, or cautery, and by similar things.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige en li est que tu fendes celle soudure, et dessevre les levres de li, et met dedens tentes de lin, et la lie tant qu’elle soit sanee; et ne covient mie que tu uses en la cure de li de choses que sechent et restraignent.	And the method of the work is that you should split the incision, and separate its edges, and place lint inside, and keep it until it heals; and it is not appropriate to use in treating it things that dry out and constrict.
Car se tu fais ceu, si revient li maladie pire que li premiere; mais i oevre de choses amollissans, si com fenugreic; et l’arose d’aigue ou altee et semence de lin soient cuites, et oignemens dyaquilon fondut en aucun des oiles, et i envoloupe une tente, et le cure de ceu.	For if you do this, the illness will return worse than before; but use softening things, such as fenugreek; and boil water or ale with flax seeds, and melt dairy fat in some oil, and wrap a lint cloth around it, and treat with that.
Et li tresors de ta cure si est que tu te dones en garde qu’ele ne soude mie selonc la forme qu’elle fut devant; et cist ovraiges que nos avons dit nen est fuers que adresemens de ceste maladie, qu’elle ne reviegne selonc la forme qu’elle fut devant.	And the treasure of your cure is that you must take care that it does not close in the same form as before; and all these works we have mentioned are nothing but arrangements to prevent this disease from returning in the same form as before.
de la char qui vient en l’oil	of the flesh that comes to the eye
Ceste maladie que est desoz qui vraiement est apelee «axacrati», et est naturelz et accidens.	This disease which is called "axacrati" in truth, and its nature and accidents.
Li accidens vient de plaie et de fendure et de cautere et de choses semblans; et li voie de l’ovraige en li si est que tu preignes un aguille, en coi il ait I fil double, et la fiche en la char, et li fai percier des le senestre larmier tant c’a destre, si que li filz veigne en II chiés de la char; puis estent la char au desus a tout l’aguille, et la cope a I spatumile large.	The accidents come from wounds and cuts and cautery and similar things; and the method of treatment is that you take a needle with double thread, insert it into the flesh, and pierce from the left tear duct to the right, so that the thread comes out in two places on the skin; then stretch the flesh over the entire needle, and cover it with one spatula width.
Et se li figure de la papiere revient selonc ceu qu’il covient, c’est boin; se ceu non, si pren I raseur et le met en la fendure, et torne la papiere, et fent II fendures ou costeit dedens la papiere; et soient li chiés des II fendures des II angles de l’incision que tu as copeit, et soit fais uns angles si que quant elles sont assemblees, que li figure soit ausi com li figure d’une lettre qui a non «I griesche»; puis oste celle char, selonc la quantiteit que ses costez est agus desoz, de ceu qui enseut la papiere, puis ajoste les II parties desevrees, et les cout d’un fil de lainne; puis lou cure de ceu que nos avons dit des medicines mollifians, et de tentes, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the figure of the paper returns as it should be, that is good; if not, take the scraper and place it in the fissure, and turn the paper, and make two incisions on the side inside the paper; and let the ends of the two incisions be at the two corners of the cut you have made, and form them into angles so that when they are joined, the figure is as the shape of a letter called «I Greek»; then remove that flesh according to the sharpness of its sides underneath, from what was under the paper, then join the two separated parts together with thread; then treat it with what we have said about softening medicines and tents until it is healed.
Et se li maladie vient de fendure ou de costure ou de cautere, si covient que tu fendes une fendure plainne desoz les poilz des papieres, et selonc ceu qui est ci devant; puis desevre entre les II leivres d’une tente, si com j’ai dit; et doit on faire l’ovraige selonc la forme de la maladie, car elle est mout diverse en forme, et li saiges maistres appareille engien de tout som pooir coment il faice revenir la figure a sa forme natureil; et li malaides meisme, selonc ceu qu’il i covient d’ovraige et d’estrumens em plusors dispositions.	And if the illness comes from a fissure or seam or cautery, it is necessary that you make a full incision under the hairs of the paper, as was said before; then separate between the two leaves of a tent, as I have said; and one must perform the work according to the form of the disease, for it is very diverse in shape, and wise masters equip themselves with all their power to restore the figure to its natural form; and the patient himself, according to what there is need of work and instruments in various circumstances.
dou soudement de la papiere	of the sudden swelling of the skin
Quant ceste soudure avient a mains homes en teil maniere que li papiere desus est sodee avec le blanc de l’oil, et ne puet movoir ne faire ses ovraiges naturez, si covient donques que tu i boutes la pointe d’un raseur desoz la papiere, et la lieve en haut; et l’estent as pinceures, tant que tu copes ceu qui est aert au spatumile subtil, qui ne soit mie trop agus ne trop trenchans, si que li malaides ne puisse soffrir que li spatumile trop agus ne blecent l’oil; et soit ton incision, dont tu escorche celle assemblee, legierement, si que li papiere reviegne selonc sa forme natureil; et est sanee toute celle assemblee, et font aucune fois en l’oil aigue salee, et le leve d’aigue douce, et de coliere; puis met entre la papiere et l’oil une tente de lin, et met sus l’oil laine moillie en abun d’uef; et aprés le tier jor use dou coliere et des choses soudans tant qu’il soit sanez.	When this swelling occurs in such a manner that the skin above is swollen with the white of the eye, and he cannot move or perform his natural tasks, then you should insert the tip of a razor under the skin, and lift it up; and hold it with pincers, until you cut away what is attached to the delicate membrane, which must not be too sharp or cutting, so that the patient cannot bear for the sharp membrane to scratch the eye; and make your incision where you peel off this assembly lightly, so that the skin returns according to its natural form; and heal completely this assembly, and sometimes put salt water in the eye, and lift it with clear water; then place between the skin and the eye a pad of linen, and apply wool moistened abundantly with egg white; and after three days use poultices and soothing things until he is healed.
de l’ungle de l’oil	of the nail of the eye
Saiches que li ungle est selonc II manieres: elle est nervouse et semblans a I dur syfac, et une autre qui n’est mie nervouse, mais est semblans a blainche moistor congelee, que quant on la touche de fer et on la cuide panre as pinceures, si ne puet om; et l’une et l’autre semblance encomence devers le grant larmier, et croist poc et poc tant qu’ele cuevre toute la veue et toute la lumiere et le movement de l’oil.	Know that the nail is according to two manners: one is nervous and similar to a hard surface, and another which is not nervous, but resembles frozen white moisture, such that when it is touched by iron and one thinks to remove it with pincers, it cannot be done; and both similarities begin near the large tear duct, and grows little by little until it covers all of the sight and all the light and movement of the eye.
Et li maniere de l’incision si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, puis li oevre les eulz; et lieve la papiere a ta main, puis coil l’ungle as pinceures de petite doubleure, et l’estent au desus; puis pren une aguille, et i met I poil de cheval, ou de vaiche, ou de buef, et I fil fort; et double la pointe de l’aguille un poc et la fiche emmi l’ungle, et la perce a tout l’aguille, et lie l’ungle d’un fil et l’estent au desus, et escorche a tout lou poil le costeit de l’ungle qui enseut la prunele et la soie au poil jusc’au chief, puis cope lou remanant en la racine dou larmier a tout lou spatumile subtil et as petites forces, et laisse la char natureil ou larmier, si que par l’incision ne veigne li cors des larmes acostumeement; et aucune fois s’estent li ungle a l’oncine soulement, et au fil, si com nos avons dit; puis l’escorche on a tout le spatumile souef de coi ci est li forme:	And the manner of the incision is that the patient places their head in your lap, then you work with their eyes; and lift the paper with your hand, then coil the nail with pincers gently, and stretch it above; then take a needle, and put horsehair, or goat hair, or beef bristle on it, and strong thread; and bend the point of the needle a little and insert it into the nail, and pierce through completely with the needle, and tie the nail with a thread and stretch it above, and scrape along the side of the nail from where the grain is until the top, then cut the remaining part at the root of the tear duct with the delicate spatula and small forces, and leave the natural flesh of the tear duct so that by the incision there does not come blood tears habitually; and sometimes the nail stretches only to the hook, and with the thread, as we have said; then scrape all along the lower part where this form is:
Et garde que li spatumile ne touche la toile charnue et la rompe, et que li prunele ne soit percie; et aprés l’incision giete en l’oil un poc de seil broiet, et dou coliere fait de litargire, et le laisse jusc’a l’autre jor; puis le cure de ceu qu’il i covient tant qu’il soit sanez.	And make sure that the spatumile does not touch the delicate flesh and tear it, and that the probe is not pierced; and after the incision sprinkle a little bit of ground sulfur and litargiric paste into the eye, and leave it until the next day; then treat it with what is necessary until it is healed.
Et se li ungle n’est mie nervouse, et tu ne pues bouter l’aguille, et li uncines n’i puet entrer, maintes fois est curee ceste semblance d’ungle de medicines; et naissent sicom j’ai conteit en la division, et se tu la vues coper, si oevre l’oil dou malaide, et pren le spatumile legier poc agut selonc ceste forme:	And if the nail is not loose and you cannot insert the needle, and the forceps cannot enter, this kind of nail is often treated with various medicines; it grows as I have described in the division, and if you wish to cut it, proceed carefully with the patient's eye; take a light, sharp spatumile according to this form:
Et reis l’ungle desus subtilment, et se tu vois qu’elle amenuise point et li rasion i apresse, si distille de ta bouche en l’oil coliere fait de litargire et dou coliere rouge et seil broiet, et estoupe l’oil jusc’a l’autre jor; puis rencomence l’autre ovraige selonc ceste meisme oevre, tant qu’elle soit toute ostee.	And lift the nail gently above, and if you see that it is becoming thinner and the tissue around it is pressing in, then distill from your mouth into the eye a paste made of litargiric red precipitate and ground sulfur, and plug the eye until the next day; then resume the work according to this same method until it is completely removed.
Se aucune chose ne t’est contraire en l’oil, si com aposteme chaus, adonques la lait, et cure premier l’aposteme chaut tant qu’il soit sanez, puis rencomence l’ovraige si com devant, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If anything is contrary in the eye, such as a hot abscess, then treat it, and first heal the hot abscess until it is healed, then resume work as before, until it is healthy.
Et se li apparance de la chair dou larmier nuit en l’oil par grant nuisement, si la sospent a l’oncine, et en cope une partie et non mie tot, que cors de larmes n’i viegne; puis distille en l’oil coliere rouge qui est fais de litargire.	And if the appearance of the flesh of the eyelid harms the eye greatly, then suspend it at the corner, and cut a part but not all, so that no tears come from the wound; then drip into the eye red myrrh made of litharge.
de la char qui naist sus la prunelle	of the flesh that grows over the pupil
Es eulz d’aucuns homes naist aucune fois char rouge, et cuevre la prunele et restraint sus les papieres et les torne au defuer, et semble une rose de balauste; et li ovraiges si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, puis li oevre les eulz, et coil toute celle char as uncines convenaubles a ceu, et la sostien a la force; puis cope la premiere char, et vai tout copant au raseur jusc’a la fin, et te garde que tu ne bleces l’oil a l’ovraige; et soit li incision dou spatumile que nos avons dit en l’incision de l’ungle et as petites forces de coi on oste lou sebel, si com li forme aprés cest chapistre lou demostre; et quant li incision est acomplie et ostee toute li char, si emple l’oil de seil broiet ou tu i distille coliere rouge et semblans medicines corrosives, et met sus l’oil defuer coton avec abin d’uef, si qu’il soit asseurez d’aposteme chaut; et s’il i demore rien, et li sans chaus te sormonte, et tu doutes aposteme chaut, si laisse l’oil et cure l’aposteme de choses apaisant aposteme chaut; puis revien a ton ovraige tant qu’il soit sanez, et ensi fai cant chars est ajostee en l’oil par ceste semblance.	In some people's eyes, red flesh sometimes grows and covers the pupil, restraining it against the membranes and turning it outward, resembling a white rose; the treatment is for the patient to place their head on something clean, then work on the eye with uncies appropriate for this condition, supporting the eyelid with force; then cut away the first layer of flesh, cutting continuously until all has been removed, being careful not to damage the eye during the procedure; make an incision as described in the nail cutting and small bone removal section we mentioned earlier; when the incision is complete and all the flesh has been removed, apply egg white mixed with a corrosive medicine such as myrrh, and place cotton soaked in it over the eye to prevent a hot abscess; if there remains any doubt about a hot abscess, treat it with soothing remedies for hot abscesses; then return to your work until the eye is healed, and so on when similar conditions affect the eye.
Mais toutevoie il covient que tu aliges la cure de chescun oil foible de la voie natureil; et de la voie accident, en ovraige de fer; et ne bouter mie ta main en aucun de ces ovraiges tant que tu voies que cist membres soit soffrans celui ovraige.	However, you must ensure that the treatment for each weak eye follows the natural way; and by an accidental cause, use ironwork; and do not touch any of these works with your hand until you see that this member can endure the work.
des voines des eulz	of the veins of the eyes
Sebel sont voinnes rouges que sont covertes sus l’oil, et tolent a la veue son ovraige et afoiblissent l’oil toz jors.	Red veins that cover the eye cause discomfort in its function and weaken the eye all day.
Mestier est donques au premier que tu regardes se li oil, en coi sebel est, est fors, et n’i a autre maladie fuers que lou sebel; adonques le coil en teil maniere: comande au malaide qu’il mette son chief en ton sain, puis sospent celles voines a tout l’oncine selonc sa sapience, et soit li oncines subtilz double selonc ceste forme:	Therefore, first you must check if the eye, in which the ailment is present, is only affected by this issue and there is no other disease except for the ailment; then treat it as follows: instruct the patient to place his head on your lap, then suspend those veins along the entire needle according to your expertise, and let the needles be fine double according to this form:
Et soient dui oncine par degrez en I cors selonc ceste forme:	And let two needles be graduated in the body according to this form:
puis c’on coil as forces celles voinnes subtilment, et essue lou sanc houre aprés autre, tant que tu voies removoir celles voines fuers de l’oil; et garde que tu ne blecier l’oil as pointes des spatumiles, et fai cest ovraige a houre de midi devant lou soleil, et soies mout fervans en ton ovraige si que tu ne copes fuer que celles voinnes; et quant tu avras ce fait, si distille en l’oil coliere vert et rouge por corrumpre ceu qui est demorez dou sebel.	Then, as you coil and force those veins gently, and wipe the blood hour after another, until you see those veins removed from the eye; and be careful that you do not injure the eye with the points of the spatumiles, and perform this work at noon in front of the sun, and be very diligent in your work so as not to leave any part behind other than those veins; and when you have done this, then drip into the eye green and red collyrium to destroy what remains of the pain.
Et se tu n’as pooir de coillir tout ceu en celle houre, si fai emplastre sus l’oil de choses apaisans la dolor des eulz, et le laisse aucuns jors tant que li dolors soit apaisie et soit asseurez d’aposteme chaut, puis rencomence selonc ceste maniere qui est devant tant qu’il soit sanez; et c’est li forme des forces:	And if you do not have the power to collect all of that at that hour, then apply a poultice to the eye with things that ease the pain of the eyes, and leave it for several days until the pain is eased and the risk of a hot abscess is assured, then restart according to this method until he is healed; and this is the form of forcing:
de la fistule de l’oil	Of the fistula of the eye
Li mire si nomment «arissati» fistule: quant tu la cures per cautere et par medicine ague ardant selonc ceu que j’ai devant dit, et elle n’est mie sanee, si est engien en li que tu fendes sus l’aposteme, lai ou il doit meurer, et trai toute la moistor que i est, tant que li os soit descovers.	The physician calls this type of fistula "arissati": when you treat it with cautery and hot medicine as I have said before, and it is not healed, then there is pus that you must cut open at the abscess, where it should be drained, and draw out all the moisture that is inside until the bone is exposed.
Et quant li os iert descovers, et tu verras la corruption et la noiror, si la reis a tout l’estrument de coi ci est li forme; et est apelez «aspre chief», et soit fait de feir inde a I chief reont, et soit pointoiez si com une lime si com il est en la presente forme:	And when the bone is exposed, and you see the corruption and the blackness, then remove it with all the instruments as described here; and it is called "aspre chief," and should be made of iron bent into a shape like a comb, pointed like a file as shown in this form:
Et met sus lou leu de l’os corrumput, puis le torne entre tes dois, et presse ta main un poc tant que tu saiches que celle corruption est rese; et fai ceu aucune fois, puis restoure lou leu de medicines exiccatives.	And place it on the site of the corrupted bone, then turn it between your two hands, and press gently until you know that the corruption has been removed; do this several times, then restore the area with drying medications.
se li leus est soudez, et char i naist, et li cors de la bowe est soudez, et remaint ensi XL jors, et il ne renovele et n’est mie apostemez, et accidens mavais n’i vient, saiches qu’il est sanez; se ceu non, si n’i a autre engien que de ramener la fistule au pertus dou neif selonc ceste forme: et est que tu descuevre de l’os la seconde fois par fer, et par medicines agues, et quant il iert descovers si prent I foret selonc ceste forme, et soit li chiés de fer a III angles, et li fust soit atenuis jusc’a chief si com tu vois ci:	If the tissue is sealed and flesh grows there, and the body of the bowel is sealed, and it remains thus for forty days, and it does not renew itself and is not infected, then know that it is healthy; if this is not the case, then there is another intention to bring the fistula back to the anus according to this form: which is that you uncover the bone a second time with iron, and by means of hot medicines, and when it is uncovered take one tube according to this form, and let the head of iron be at three angles, and the shaft should taper until the top as you see here:
puis le met sus l’os delez lou larmier, et esloigne ta main de l’oil I poc, puis torne a tot le foret tant qu’il perce l’os et le sent li malaides par ceu que li vens en ist s’il tient sa main sus son neif; et pues restoure lou leu de medicines seches, si com je t’ai ensigniet, et quant li char naist et endurcist li leus, si vait li matiere au neif; si est plus legiere chose au malaide.	Then place it on the bone near the lamina, and withdraw your hand from the eye one inch, then turn back the tube until it pierces the bone and the patient feels it when he holds his hand over his anus; and afterwards restore the place with dry medicines as I have taught you, and when the flesh grows and hardens the tissue, remove the matter to the anus; this is a lighter thing for the patient.
de l’issue de l’oil	From the exit of the eye
Quant li eulz apert fuer dou tout en tout, et il ne vient point de destorbier au nef, ne amenuisement, si covient que tu lies lou malaide; puis le saine, puis li met ventouses ou haterel sens ferir por succier, puis met sus l’oil I liien fait d’acaice et de aloe et d’encens et de sarcocolle, et puis estrain l’oil, et l’emplaustre sus de bendes et de drapelz; et li maniere des drapelz si est que tu preignes drapelz assez molz, et double chescun en IIII, et puis met l’un sus l’autre selonc la quantiteit que li eulz en ait mestier; puis l’estrain par desus d’un bendeil dur forment, et rencomence les ventouses por succier sens ferir; puis oste les ventouses et laisse l’oil estraint jor et nuit, et se li liiens amolist, si covient que tu l’estraignes mout; puis oste lou liien aprés le jor et la nut, et se tu vois l’oil repairier, c’est boin; se ce non; si rencomence l’emplaustre et les drapelz et lou liien et les ventouses tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the eye is fully opened and there is no disturbance in the vessel or reduction in size, you must bind the patient; then heal it, then apply cups to suck without hitting, then place on the eye a poultice made of cedar, aloes, incense, and saffron, and then press the eye; and the method of bandages is that you take soft cloths, and double each in four, and then place one over another according to the size needed for the eye; then press it with a hard bandage, and repeat the cups to suck without hitting; then remove the cups and leave the eye pressed day and night, and if the poultice becomes loose, you must press it strongly again; then remove the poultice after one day and night, and if you see the eye healing, that is good; if not, restart the poultice and bandages and pressing with cups until it is healthy.
dou derrompement de toile uvee	from the rupture of a woven membrane
Quant disruptions vient en la toile uvee, puis apert, et vient fuer des papieres si com I grain de resins, et est espoantauble a veoir; adonques se tu la vues coper, li ovraiges est telz que tu boutes une aguille en la racine des la partie desoz jusc’a celi desus, puis boute une autre aguille ou il ait I fil double des la partie dou larmier; et la fai percier, et laisse la premiere aguille selonc la disposition; puis cope lou leu dou fil double et lie une partie de l’uve entor, et l’estraint bien, puis estrai l’aguille et met sus l’oil lainne moillie en abun d’uef; et le laisse tant que li filz chiece avec l’uve, puis cure l’oil de choses confortans tant que li plaie soit sanee; et aucune fois li plaie est restrainte par l’uve chescune part d’un cercle de drap, tant qu’elle soit sanee.	When a disruption comes in the woven membrane, it is opened up, and there appears pus like resin seeds, which are alarming to see; then if you wish to repair it, proceed as follows: pierce with a needle at the root of the part below until reaching the upper part, then insert another needle where there is double thread from the part of the eyelid; make holes accordingly, and leave the first needle in place according to the disposition; then cut out the area of double thread and tie one part of the uvea around it tightly, then extract the needle and apply wool moistened abundantly with egg white over the eye; let it remain until the thread comes off with the uvea, then treat the eye with comfort-giving substances until the wound is healed; sometimes the wound is restrained by a circular bandage of cloth on all sides until it heals.
Et se li eulz done grant apparance, si le perce au spatumile subtil qui viegne em parfont de l’oil, et corre la moistor albuginé et dessende li eulz, et entre ens tantost; puis l’estrai tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the eye shows great appearance, then pierce it with a fine spatula that comes in line with the eye, and drain the white moisture and lower the eye; then extract it until it is healed.
de la bowe de l’oil	from the socket of the eye
Ceste maladie qui est apelee «alcunnati» nen est fuers que bowe qui est assemblee en l’oil, semblant a aigue dessendant, et ce n’est mie aigue; et li maniere de l’apparance de l’ovraige si est que tu faices seoir lou malaide sus I siege appareilliet et droit, puis prent le chief entre tes mains de II pars, et lou muef tant que tu voies la bowe venir au desus a tes eulz; puis soit ens fichie, et ne dessende et soit descombree li lumiere, et voie li malaides les choses si com il soloit; et s’elle ne dessent desoz, saiches que c’est aigue, et se li dessendemens de la bowe n’est appareilliez si com nos avons dit.	This disease which is called "alcunnati" is nothing but an accumulation in the eye, resembling fluid descending, yet it is not actually fluid; and the manner of its appearance is such that you seat the patient on a prepared and straight chair, then take his head between your hands from both sides, and move it until you see the accumulation come above to your eyes; then fix it there so that it does not descend and obscure the light, and let the patient see things as he usually would; and if it descends below despite this, know that it is fluid, and if the descent of the accumulation is not prepared as we have said.
si fai seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, puis prent le spatumile subtil et fent sus la toile cornee I poc par la continuation de la conjunctive avec la toile cornee et la corone, tant que li bowe isse; et quant elle ert issue, si distille en l’oil aigue chaude mellee a miel, ou aigue ou fenugreic est boillis et miel, puis soit curee d’autre cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	Situate the patient between your hands, then take the spatula and make an incision through the corneal tissue along the conjunctiva and the cornea, until the pus comes out; and when it is out, drip into the eye hot honey mixed with honey, or water boiled with fenugreek and honey, then cure it further as needed until it heals.
des aigues de l’oil	for the waters of the eye
Nos avons jai les semblances des aigues en la division, et ceu qu’il covient por percier; si en oevre selonc la santeit.	We have described the appearances of the waters and what is necessary to pierce them; act according to the health.
Il covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains croisiet, fuers de la lumiere por le soleil, et li lie l’oil sain et estreint mout fort; puis met la papiere de l’oil a ta main senestre se li eulz est senestres, ou a ta main destre se li eulz est destres; puis prent en ta main destre, se li eulz est senestres, l’estrument qui est apelez «almagda», ou a ta main senestre, se li eulz est destre; puis met la pointe de l’estrument delez la corone par la groissece d’un rait en celle blenchor de l’oil a la partie dou menor larmier, puis boute l’estrument qui est apelez «almagda» vertuousement, et trestorne ta main tant qu’il perce en la blenchor de l’oil, et sente que almagda viegne a la chose vuide; et covient que li mesure de la voie almagda soit au parfont de la mesure des l’espaice qui est des la prunele jusc’a la fin de la noirour; et c’est li corone de l’oil; si verras l’os en celle papiere por la clarteit de la toile cornee, et pues met l’estrument jusc’a leu ou li aigue est, puis l’espresse desoz une voie aprés autre.	You should seat the patient between your crossed hands, away from sunlight, and hold the healthy eye tightly with one hand; then place the paper of the affected eye in your left hand if it is the left eye, or in your right hand if it is the right eye; then take with your right hand, if the eye is the left, the instrument called "almagda," or with your left hand if the eye is the right; then place the tip of the instrument next to the cornea at a thickness of one thread on that white part of the eye near the inner corner, and gently insert the instrument called "almagda" vertically, turning your hand until it penetrates into the white part of the eye and you feel the almagda enter an empty space; and the length of the path of the almagda should be perfectly measured from the center of a plum to its end, which is the darkness; this is the cornea; through the clarity of the corneal tissue, you will see bone in that paper, and then place the instrument until it reaches where the fluid is, and express it out one channel at a time.
se li aigue dessent maintenant, si voit li malaides devant lui et l’estrument en son oil.	If the water flows now, the patient sees before him and the instrument in his eye.
Aprés repose I petit, et se li aigue remonte la seconde voie, met la fuer avec l’estrument, et quant elle est ens fichie et ele ne monte, si estrai almagda legierement en tornoiant ta main poc et poc; et puis remette en aigue un poc de seil gemme, et leive de ceu l’oil dedens.	After resting for a short time, if the water rises again through the second route, apply force with the instrument, and when it is firmly placed and does not rise, gently extract almagda by turning your hand little by little; then add a bit of powdered gemstone to the water, and lift the eye from there.
Puis met par defuer l’oil estoupes ou lainne moillie en oile roset et en abun d’uef, et lie avec l’oil sain.	Then place over the eye plugs made of linen soaked in rose oil and an abundance of egg whites, and bind it with a healthy eye.
Nos, et cil qui sont de nostre tens, mettons sus comin broiet avec abun d’uef.	We, and those of our time, apply it mixed with egg whites in abundance.
Et se almagda n’i puet entrer en l’oil par sa duresce, car il i a de teilz homes qui ont trop durs les eulz, si covient que tu preignes l’estrument qui est apelez «alberit», de coi ci est li forme:	And if alum cannot enter the eye due to its hardness, because there are people who have eyes that are too hard, then you must use the instrument called "alberit," of which this is the form:
Et perce donques la conjunctive soulement, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, mais fai I leu subtil, puis i boute almagda, si com nos avons dit; et au complissement de l’uevre appareille au malaide I dorteur avenant, en coi il dorme sus son dos en I leu tenebrous; et soit deveez de toz movemens, et preigne legieres viandes, et ne mueve son chief ne a destre ne a senestre, et soit liiez selonc sa disposition jusc’a tier jor; puis le deslie en cele maison meisme tenebrouse, et esprueve sa veue, et lou fai veoir aucunes choses, et puis li remet lou lien jusc’a septime jor; et ne covient mie que tu faices ceu en l’oure de la cure ou aprés l’incision maintenant, mais il covient que tu aliges ceu, por ceu que li aigue monte hastanment.	And pierce then the conjunctiva only, and do not go too deep, but proceed carefully, then insert alum as we have said; and at the completion of the work prepare for the patient a dark room where he can sleep on his back in a dim place; and ensure that he remains motionless, and gives him light foods, and does not move his head neither to the right nor left, and bind him according to his condition until the third day; then unbind him in the same dark room and test his sight, showing him some objects, and then rebind him until the seventh day; and it should not be done during the hour of treatment or immediately after incision, but you must wait because the fluid rises quickly.
se apostemes chaus vient, que tu desliies l’oil devant le septime jor, et l’adrece de ceu qui assouaige aposteme; et quant il est apaisiez, si deslie la veue et met sus sa faice I orilliet por covrir aucun jor, et soit adés en celle maison tenebrouse.	If abscesses occur, that you should loosen the eye before the seventh day, and direct it to him who reduces abscesses; and when it is calmed, then release the sight and place on its face a small bandage for some days, and let it be immediately in that dark house.
Et puis isse de la maison poc et poc, et se convertisse en ses cas; et saiches que nulz deciples ne se doit entremettre en cest cas.	And then leave the house little by little, and return to his usual duties; and know that no disciple should intervene in this case.
Et uns vint a nos qui estoit de la Yrach, qui nos dist que en som pais faisoit om almagda perciet, a coi on succe l’aigue, mais toutevoie je n’en vis onques nul en nostre terre, ne je ne lou lis onques en livres des anciens; et par aventure c’est une novele chose.	And one came to us who was from the Iraque, who told us that in his country they make small incisions for urine retention, to which water is drained, but nevertheless I have never seen any such thing in our land, nor have I read about it in ancient books; and perhaps it is a new thing.
Et ce sont les semblances des formes de almagda, por ceu que cil qui ne les conoit les voie; et soient d’arain proprement:	And these are the likenesses of the forms of almonds, for those who do not know them see; and they are of brass properly:
Et soient li chief d’aus de ceste meisme subtiliteit, et li derriene en III angles ague.	And let the heads of these be of the same subtlety, and the rear in three acute angles.
de la char sor le neis	of the flesh on the nose
Aucune fois naissent ou neis chars ajostees diverses, de coi il i a aucunes qui semblent scorpions a mout de piez; et si i a de telz ou il ait char enchancree de fuxe color, et si a char souef de bone color.	Sometimes flesh on the nose grows in various forms, some of which seem like many-legged scorpions; and there are such cases where it has grown with a purple hue, and there is flesh underneath of good color.
En celle donques de ces chars qui est souef, et ne mie enchancree, covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains encontre lou soleil; et oevre ses narines, et giete l’oncine a celles chars, et les trai fuers; pues cope ceu que tu em pues sostenir au spatumile subtil agut d’une part, tant que tu saiches que celle char est toute ostee.	Then for the flesh that is underneath and not raised, you must seat the patient between your hands facing the sun; work his nostrils, and apply the lancet to those growths, and extract them forcibly; then hold as long as you can with a fine sharp spatula on one side, until you know that all of the flesh has been removed.
Et s’il en remaint aucune chose c’on ne puisse coper, si l’ovrez a tout I des estrumens subtil legierement, si qu’il n’i demoure rien; et se sans te sormonte, ou aposteme chaus, si lou secort si com il covient; et se c’est apostemes malignes, si te haste et lou cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez et soient ostees toutes les chars, puis giete ou neis aisil et aigue ou vin.	And if there remains anything that you cannot cut, then treat it with the finest instrument gently, so nothing remains; and if pus overflows from an abscess, then drain it as is proper; and if these are malignant abscesses, then hasten and cauterize them until the pus is stopped and all the flesh removed, then apply fresh and clean water or vinegar or wine.
Se li neis oevre, et moistors en vient jusc’a palais, saiches qu’il est sanez; et se moistors ne perce si com il covient, saiches qu’il i a char nee en l’os desus, a coi li estrumens ne vient mie por taillier: adonques covient il que tu i boutes I fil de lin un poc gros, et soit noez de mains nous, et ait entre chescun nout d’espaice I doit ou moins; et mette li malaides lou chiés dou fil en son neif a som pooir, et traie en odorant tant qu’il viegne par lou neif dedens la bouche; et maintes fois font ensi li enfant as escoles, et c’est legiere chose a celui qui le vuet faire; puis tien le chief qui vient par lou neif a une main, et l’autre chief qui vient par la bouche a l’autre main, et saiche l’un aprés l’autre en soiant as nous qui sont ou fil.	If the nostril works and mucus reaches up to the palate, know that it is clear; and if mucus does not flow properly, know there is flesh grown on the bone above, which the instrument cannot cut: then you must insert a thick linen thread, tied with knots every inch or so; and have the patient place one end of the thread in their nose as far as possible, and pull it out through the nostril until it comes out into the mouth; and often children at school do this, and it is an easy thing for whoever wants to do it; then hold one end that comes from the nose with one hand, and the other end that comes from the mouth with the other hand, and remove them one by one while carefully examining the knots on the thread.
Fai ceu tant que tu saiches que li nout ont corrompue celle char, puis trai lou filz, essue le sanc, et moille lou fil en oignement egiptien, et le remet derechief au neis si com devant; fai ceu III jors ou plus, tant que li oignemens corrode tout ceu qui est demorez de char; et puis met ou neis une caine de plonc aucuns jors tant qu’il soit sanez, et s’il a mestier de medicines sechans, si en use; et c’est li forme de l’estrument por purgier lou chief, a coi on distille les oiles et les medicines ou neis:	Do this until you know that the pus has corrupted the flesh, then pull out the thread, clean the blood, and soak the thread in Egyptian ointment, and put it back into the nose as before; do this for three days or more, until the ointment corrodes all that remains of the flesh; and then place a plug of some kind in the nose for several days until it is healed, and if there is need for drying medicines, use them; and this is the form of the instrument to purge the head, through which oils and medicines are dripped into the nose:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, semblant a une lampe overte, si com une cainne, et li conduis ausi; et se tu vues, si fai une cainne close, et soit li estrumens plains por espurgier lou chief; et ait I mainche au chief por lou tenir quant on chaufe l’oile ou aucune liquor.	And it may be made of silver or brass, resembling an open lamp, like a plug, and the conduit is also like this; and if you wish, make a closed plug, and let the instruments be full for purging the head; and have a handle at the top to hold when heating oil or any liquid.
de la char sor le neis	of the flesh upon the nose
Maintes fois naist au chief dou neis une maladie qui est apelee «telul», et croist et devient grans adés, tant qu’il est vis chose au regarder; et por ceu covient que tu lou copes au comencement, et l’oste tout fuer, puis met sor leu lou cautere ou la medicine ardant; et s’on le tarde a coper tant qu’il soit grans, si pren warde s’il est durs, de fuxe color, de povre sens: si ne lou touchier mie de fer car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, car quant on le cope aucune fois, si en vient grant malice au malaide; et se li apostemes est de soef touchement, non mie de fuxe color, et tu vois c’on le puisse tout coper, si vuide le malaide et lou cope sens paor, et cure le leu de choses sechans et restraignans.	Many times a disease called "telul" is born on the head of the nose, and it grows and becomes large in time, to the point that it is visible upon looking at it; therefore, you must cut it at the beginning, remove it completely, then apply the cautery or hot medicine over it. If one delays cutting it until it becomes large, take care if it is hard, reddish in color, and has poor sensation: do not touch it with iron because it is a chronic abscess, for when you cut it even once, much harm will come to the patient; but if the abscess can be completely cut with gentle pressure, without being hard or reddish in color, then empty the patient's body of harmful fluids and cut it fearlessly, and treat the area with drying and constricting substances.
quant li neis est copez et cosus	When the skin is cut and sewn
Saiches que quant solutions de continuation vient en une de ces cartillagines ovraiges, i profite poc, fuer que en aucuns homes.	Know that when a solution of continuation comes in one of these cartilage works, it benefits little, except in some men.
Il covient donques cant ceu avient a aucun, si regarde se li plaie est fresche a tout son sanc; et adonques ajoste les II levres a une costure, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et se les levres sont ja desevrees d’une part et d’autre, si covient que tu escorches toutes les parties de lor keur tant qu’elles sainent, puis assemble les II levres a une costure, et l’estraint, et poudre sus poudre de sanc de dragon, et encens broiet; et met sus les poudres une piece d’emplaustre de fort ou d’autre emplaustre soudant, et le laisse tant qu’il chiece par lui, puis le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.
