Then when this happens to anyone, look to see if the wound is fresh with all its blood; and then join the two edges in one seam, then care for it until it heals; and if the edges are separated on both sides, you must scrape all parts of their rawness until they bleed, then bring together the two edges in one seam, and bind it tightly, and sprinkle powdered dragon's blood and ground incense; and apply a piece of strong or other adhesive plaster over the powders, and leave it until it is dry, then treat with ointment until it heals.
Li maniere de la costure si est que tu assembles la solution: ou par aguilles, si com nos avons dit en la costure dou ventre; ou par fil, si com je le t’ai fait savoir.	The method of stitching is that you assemble the solution: either by needles, as we have said in the stitching of the abdomen; or by thread, as I have told you.
des apostemes des levres	of abscesses of the lips
A mains homes avient dedens les levres aposteme dur, semblans a grains de veces, et menor et plus grant; adonques couvient que tu tornes les levres, et fendes sus chescun nout, et le prent as pinceures et le cope en chescune partie; puis emple lou leu aprés l’incision de vitriole broiet, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; et puis lou leive d’aisil, et cure lou leu de choses seches tant qu’il soit sanez.	In some people, there is a hard abscess on the lips, resembling grains of wheat, small and large; then you must turn the lips inside out, cut into each node, grasp it with forceps, and cut in every part; then fill the place after an incision with broiled vitriol until the blood stops flowing; and then clean the area with water, and treat the wound with dry substances until it is healed.
de la char des gencives	of the flesh of the gums
Maintes fois naist sus les gencives char ajostee, que li ancien apelent «albulus»; si covient que tu la sostienes as tenailles, et la cope a sa racine, et laisse corre la bowe ou le sanc; puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet, ou autres poudres restraignans et desiccatives; et se celle char revient aprés l’incision, et maintes fois avient, si la cope la seconde fois, et la cauterize: si ne revient mie aprés le cautere; et ce sont les formes des estrumens por coper.	Often a piece of flesh grows on the gums which the ancients call "albulus"; you must hold it with forceps and cut it at its root, letting the blood or pus flow freely; then apply vitriol powder or other powders that are astringent and drying; if this flesh returns after cutting, as often happens, cut it again and cauterize: it will not return after cautery; these are the forms of instruments for cutting.
des sordens	of foulness
Aucunes fois sont assemblees au chief des dens, dedens la bouche entre les gencives, escorces qui sont laides et aspres; et aucune fois sont li dent noir et citrin et vers, tant que li corruption vient a la gencive, et sont li dent puant; si covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, et ses chiés soit en ton saint, et reis les dens ou les escorces aperent, tant qu’il n’i demore rien; et ensi fai de la noiror et de la verdor, et de la jaunice et des autres taiches, tant qu’elles soient mondees; et s’on oste ceu que i est a la premiere rasion, c’est boin; se ceu non, si rencomence a rere le secont jor et lou tier, tant que tu aies tout reis; et saiches que li dent ont mestier de diverses formes d’estrumens por reire, selonc ceu que li oevre lou demoustre, por ceu que li raseur dont on reit defuer les dens ont autres formes que cil dont on reit entre les dens; et cestes formes et autres soient avec toi appareillies.	Sometimes there are assembled at the roots of the teeth in the mouth between the gums, crusts that are unpleasant and rough; and sometimes the teeth turn black or yellowish-green and have decay to such an extent that corruption reaches the gum, making the tooth foul-smelling; you must seat the patient between your hands, and place his chin on your knee, and remove the teeth or crusts thoroughly until nothing remains; and thus do for the blackness, greenness, and yellowness, and other stains, until they are clean; if what needs to be removed is taken out at first attempt, it is good; if not, start again from the second day and third, until you have removed everything; and know that teeth require various forms of instruments for removal, according to what the work shows, because the remover from which teeth need to be extracted has different shapes than those used between the teeth; and these forms and others should be prepared with you.
Il covient quant tu cures lou dent de sa dolor que tu tardes dou traire tant com tu pues, car ce ne doit om mie faire; car c’est une substance mout haute jusc’a donc c’on n’ait point d’excusation dou raier.	It is necessary when you treat the tooth of its pain that you delay pulling as much as you can, for one must not do this; for it is a very high substance until there is no excuse for extracting.
Adonques quant li malaides est constrains dou traire, si covient que tu soies certains dou dent doillant.	Then when the patient is constrained to pull, it is necessary that you be certain of the tooth causing pain.
Maintes fois desoit li dolor lou malaide, et cuide qu’elle soit ou dent saint, et fait traire le boin dent; et toutevoie ne se depart mie li dolor per ceu, tant que li malvais estrais, car nos l’avons ja veut faire a ces sainors; et quant tu es bien certains dou dent doillant, si covient que tu escorches entor lou dent a tout i. spatumile fort por warder la gencive de toutes pars; puis le mues a tes dois ou as tenailles subtilz au premier poc et poc, tant qu’il soit bien eslochiés, puis i afferme bien les tenailles; et soit li chiés dou malaide en ton saint entre tes genous, et lou tien bien si qu’il ne se mueve.	Many times the pain deceives the patient, and they believe it to be in a good tooth, and pull out the healthy tooth; yet the pain does not depart through this, until the bad one is extracted, for we have already done this with these patients; and when you are well certain of the painful tooth, you should cauterize around the tooth thoroughly within an inch to protect the gum from all sides; then gently pull it with your hands or fine pliers little by little, until it comes out well, then firmly secure the pliers; hold the patient's head between your knees and keep a firm grip so that it does not move.
Aprés estrai lou dent droitement sens brisier, et s’il ne saut fuer, si prent aucun de ces estrumens et le boute dedens de chescune part legierement, et lou remuef si com tu as fait premier.	After extract the tooth straight without breaking it, and if it does not come out forcefully, take any of these instruments and push into each side gently, and move it as you did first.
Et se li dens est perciez et mengiez, si covient que tu l’emplisses de drapelz, lai ou li pertus sont; et si l’estraint subtilment as tenailles, que il ne brise a l’estraindre; et covient mout saigement ovrer entor la gencive por deschaucier lou dent.	And if the tooth is perforated and eaten away, it is necessary that you fill it with strips of cloth where the hole is; and if you extract it gently with pliers, so as not to break it when extracting; and it is very necessary to work around the gum to loosen the tooth.
Et te done bien en warde que tu ne le brises, et en remaigne une partie, et reveigne au malaide par la malice de la racine plus grans dolors de la premiere.	And be very careful that you do not break it, and leave a part behind, and return to the patient due to the mischief of the root greater pain than before.
Et te warde que tu ne faices mie ensi com font li ignorant sainor, qui par lor haste et par lor hardiesce brisent aucune fois le charreit, et n’i amenistrent mie ceu que nos avons conteit; mais font venir aucune fois par l’oquison de ceu grant maladie por les racines que i demorent, ou por lou charreit qu’il brisent, si com nos avons sovent veut; et quant li dens est trais, si lavez lou leu de vin ou d’aisil et de seil; et se decorremens de sanc i vient, que sovent avient, si emple lou leu de vitriole broiet; et se ceu ne vaut, si le cauterize.	And beware that you do not act as the ignorant surgeons do, who by their haste and boldness sometimes break the bone, and do not bring about what we have described; but rather cause sometimes through this action serious illness due to the roots that remain there, or for breaking the bone, as often happens; and when the tooth is extracted, wash the place with wine or vinegar and salt; and if bleeding persists, which often occurs, fill the place with powdered vitriol; and if that does not help, cauterize it.
Les formes des estrumens, a coi om muet les dens premier, soient a longes pointes et a gros mainches, qu’il ne doublent mie quant tu trairas le dent; et ce sont les formes:	The shapes of the instruments used to extract teeth first should have long points and thick handles, so they do not double back when you pull the tooth; and these are their forms:
Et soient de gros membres si qu’il ne ploient mie au traire, et soient de fer inde bien fait, et soient dentez por mues tenir.	And let them be thick members so that they do not bend at all, and let them be of well-made iron, and let them be toothed to hold the hairs.
de la racine des dens	from the root of the teeth
Quant li racine demoure au traire, si covient que tu mettes sor le leu coton moilliet em burre I jor ou ij.,	When the root remains in the wound, you should apply cotton moistened with butter to the area for one or two days.
tant que li leus soit amolis, pues i boute les tenailles qui sont apelees «algefri», de coi li chiés semblet bec de soigne; et soient dedens faites ausi com une lime et c’est li forme:	until the flesh is softened, then you can apply the pincers called "algefri," which make the root look like a bird's beak; and they should be inside as sharp as a file, and this is their shape:
Et se les racines ne vuellent issir a tout ces tenailles, si covient que tu descuevre la char tot entor la racine, et i met l’estrument qui est apelez «althali», c’est a savoir palainche, de coi ci est li forme:	And if the roots do not come out with these pincers, you should expose the flesh all around the root and apply the instrument called "althali," which is a plane, and this is its shape:
Et soit fors et gros si qu’il ne brise mie, et se li racine saut par ceu, c’est boin; se ceu non, si t’aide de toz les estrumens, de coi les formes vienent ci aprés:	And let it be sharp and thick so that it does not break, and if the root jumps out from there, that is good; if not, then assist with all the instruments, of which the forms come next:
Et si s’aide on de cest estrument qui ait II rains, de coi ci est li forme:	And if one assists with this instrument that has two prongs, of which here is the form:
et d’autres ferremens qui sont devant en la rasion des dens, et de cest estrument qui semble unes grans tenailles, dont ci est li forme:	and other instruments which are mentioned before in the ratio of teeth, and of this instrument that resembles large tongs, of which here is the form:
Et soit cist estrumens fors qu’il ne puisse brisier, et saiches que mout d’estrumens de dens sont; et ausi d’autres estrumens, qui ne sont mie contez; et li saiges maistres subtilz trueve par soi meisme son estrument, selonc ceu que ses ovraiges et li maladie li demoustre, car il i a de teilz maladies ou li ancien n’enseignerent point d’estrument por la diversiteit d’au;s et s’om brise point dou charreit ou des autres os, ou il porrit, si i cerche as estrumens qu’il i covient, que je t’ai dit, et t’aide des gestes, de coi ci est li forme:	And let this instrument be sharp so that it cannot break, and know that there are many instruments for teeth; and also other instruments which are not described; and the wise masters find their own tools by themselves according to what their work and the disease show them, because there are such diseases where the ancients did not teach any tool due to variety of cases; and if one does not break the flesh or other bones, then search for the instruments that should be used, which I have told you, and help with gestures, of which here is the form:
Et soient gros et bien tenant por tenir l’os, qu’il n’eschaipe, mais le puisse tenir et oster; et puis restoure lou leu de medicines convenant a ceu, et s’il ait en l’os porriture, et elle est petite, si la reis a tout cest estrument:	And let them be thick and well holding to keep the bone from escaping, but able to hold and remove it; then restore the place with medicines suitable for this, and if there is putrefaction in the bone and it is small, remove it entirely with this instrument:
Quant li dent apperent ne mie selonc lou cors natureil, et li forme est laide, et meismement en femmes puceles, si covient que tu saiches se li dens est neis aprés lou dent, et n’est mie en droit leu, et on ne lou puet soier ne limer: adonques lou raie; et s’il est aers avec lou dent, si prent cest estrument dont ci est li forme, et est semblans a I petit bec, et soit de fer inde agut en som:	When the tooth appears not according to its natural form and the shape is ugly, especially in virgin women, then you must know if the tooth has grown after another tooth, and it is not in the right place, and cannot be smoothed or filed: then remove it; and if it grows crooked with another tooth, take this instrument whose form is here described, and looks like a small beak, and should be made of sharp iron:
Et lou cope poc et poc em mains jors por la duresce dou dent, et por ceu que tu ne mueves les autres, et s’il est apparans c’on le puisse limer, si lou lime d’une teil lime com ci est li forme:	And cut it bit by bit over several days due to the hardness of the tooth, and so as not to move the others, and if it appears that you can file it, then file it with a tool like this one whose form is shown:
et est ausi com li lime de coi on fait les aguilles; et en lime lou dent poc et poc em mains jors legierement, si qu’il ne se mueve tant qu’il chiece; puis la plaine en la fin a tout aucun raseur, et se li dens est trop trenchans et il blece la lengue, si covient limer l’aspreteit tant qu’il soit igalz, si qu’il ne blece la lengue ne ne corrompe la parole.	And it is like the file used to make needles; and with this file one gently files down the tooth bit by bit each day, so that it does not move until it fits; then finally it becomes smooth for any razor, and if the tooth is too sharp and cuts the tongue, one must file down its roughness until it is even, so that it neither cuts the tongue nor impedes speech.
quant li dent lochent	when the tooth loosens
Quant li dent devant lochent, ou par percussion ou par cheoir, et li malaides ne puet presser sus ceu qu’il menjue qu’il ne chient, et tu les as curez de medicines restrignans, et ceu ne vaut; si les covient restraindre d’un fil d’or, car li filz d’argent devient vert et porrit, mais li ors ne se mue onques; et soit li filz moiens ne trop gros ne trop menus, selonc la quantiteit de l’espaice entre les dens; et se tu vues adrecier les dens, si pren lou fil et lou boute double entre les II dens sains, puis met les chiés entre les dens meus, s’il en i a I ou plusors, tant que tu veignes saigement jusc’au dent sain d’autre part; puis rencomence la coverture jusc’a la partie ou tu encomensas, et estrains ta main subtilment et saigement, tant qu’il ne se mueve point; et soit ta lieeure a la racine dou dent si qu’il ne puist eschaper.	When the front teeth become loose, either due to impact or falling out, and the patient cannot press on what they bite without it moving, and treating them with constrictive medicines does not help; then they must be restrained with a gold thread, because silver threads turn green and rot, but gold never moves. And let the thread neither be too thick nor too thin, according to the size of the space between the teeth. If you wish to align the teeth, take the thread and place it double between two healthy teeth, then insert the loose tooth or teeth between them until you carefully reach another sound tooth on the other side; then continue covering with the thread back to where you started, and withdraw your hand skillfully and cautiously so that nothing moves. And let the knot be at the root of the tooth so it cannot escape.
Puis cope les chiés dou fil a unes tenailles, et les assemble, et les repont entre le dent sain, et le met ensi qu’il ne blece la lengue; et puis le laisse ensi estroit tant com il puet demorer, et s’il deslie, ou li filz ront, si l’estraint d’un autre fil; si demorrait et servira ensi tout son tens, et c’est li forme des dens et li figure de l’adrecement des II dens sains, et des II meus, si com tu vois:	Then cut the teeth of the wire with pliers, and join them together, placing them between healthy teeth so as not to hurt the tongue; then leave it as tight as possible until it can remain, and if it loosens or the wire breaks, tighten it with another wire; thus it will stay and serve in this manner for its entire time, and this is the form of the teeth and the arrangement of the two healthy teeth and the two bad ones, as you see:
Et quant li dent chiet, si lou remet on en son leu, de fres en fres, si com nos avons dit; et ne s’en entremette mie qui n’est saiges et soffrans, et aucune fois fait on la forme d’un dent d’os de vaiche, et lou met on au leu ou li defaute est, et l’estraint on si com nos avons dit, et demore et sert ensi lonc tens.	And when a tooth falls out, replace it in its place with a fresh one, as we have said; and do not interfere with someone who is not wise or skilled, and sometimes one makes the shape of a tooth from bone of a fish, and places it where the deficiency is, and tightens it as we have said, and it remains and serves for such a long time.
de coper lou liien de la lengue	To cut the ligament of the tongue
Aucune fois est cist liiens qui vient desoz la lengue ou naturez, que on naist ensi; ou par accident de plaie soudee; et li ovraiges est telz que tu oevre la bouche dou malaide, et ait sa teste en ton sain, et li lieve la lengue; puis cope lou liien nervous dou large, tant que li lengue soit desloie de son tenement, et se il i a duresce ou nout, et c’est de soudement de plaie, si i boute l’uncine et cope dou large celui liement; et garde que li fendure ne soit mie trop em parfont, por l’artere qui est desoz; et quant tu as fait, si leve le leu d’aigue rose et d’aisil, ou d’aigue froide, puis met desoz la lengue une tente de lin; et la teigne li malaides chescune nuit, que li leus ne puisse soder.	There is sometimes this ligament that comes from under the tongue either by nature at birth; or by accident of a wound that has healed; and the operation is such that you work on the mouth of the patient, and hold his head in your hand, and lift up the tongue; then cut the nervous ligament widely, until the tongue is separated from its attachment, and if there is hardness or knot, which is due to sudden healing of a wound, then use hooks and cut it extensively; and be careful that the incision is not too deep, for the artery which lies underneath; and when you have finished, raise the area with rose water and mallow juice, or cold water, then place under the tongue a pad of linen; and bandage the patient every night so that the wound does not heal.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si met sor le leu vitriole broiet; et se li sans te vaint, si le cauterize au cautere lentiginout, qui est boin a ceu; puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez,	And if bleeding occurs, place over the area vitriol ground; and if it affects the blood, cauterize with a light cautery, which is good for this; then treat it with other treatments until he is healthy,
et se tu lou vois de fusse color ou noir ou dur, si que li malaides ne lou sent, si n’i touchier point, car c’est chancre; et s’il est declinans a blenchor, et il i a moistor, si i giete l’oncine, et lou fent d’un spatumile subtil, et lou delivre d’une part et d’autre; et se li sans te vaint a ton ovraige, si met sus vitriole broiet tant qu’il soit estainchiez, puis revien a ton ovraige tant que tu traies tout fuer; puis leve lou leu d’aisil et de seil, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	and if you see it as a black or hard color and the patient does not feel it, do not touch it, for it is an ulcer; and if it declines towards phlegm and there is moisture, apply lancing and open it with a fine scalpel, and release it from both sides; and if the blood affects your work, place ground vitriol until it stops flowing, then return to your work as long as you heal completely; then lift the area gently and treat it with other treatments until he is healthy.
des apostemes de la gorge	abscesses of the throat
Aucune fois vient dedens la gorge boces qui sont apelees «godath», et les apele on proprement les II amandres, et quant tu les cures, si com nos avons dit en la division, et elles ne sont sanees, si pren garde: se c’est apostemes dur de petit sens et de fusse color, si ne lou touchier mie de fer.	Sometimes there come into the throat glands which are called "godath," and they are properly referred to as the two tonsils; and when you treat them, as we have said in the division, and if they are not healed, be careful: if these abscesses are hard with a small sensation and of dark color, do not touch them with iron.
Et s’il est rouges et li racine est grosse, si ne lou touchier mie de fer, ausi por lou decorrement de sanc; mais lou laisse tant qu’il soit meur, et adonques tu lou partiras, ou il rompirait par soi; et s’il est de blainche color reont, et li racine est subtilz, si aies apareilliet l’estrument por coper, mais regarde premierement se li apostemes chalz repose et est apaisiez.	And if they are red and the base is swollen, do not touch them with iron, also to prevent bleeding; but leave them until they become black, and then you will remove them, as they would naturally break apart; and if they are of white color and the base is fine, have your instrument ready to cut, but first check whether the abscess lies still and is calm.
Adonques fai seoir lou malaide devant lou soleil, et ses chiés soit en ton sain, et li oevre la bouche et lou preigne li serjans entre ses mains, et presse la lengue desoz a tout l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme; et soit d’argent ou d’arain subtil ausi com uns coutelz:	Then have the patient sit before the sun, and his head in your sight, and open his mouth and grasp the tongue between your hands, and press it down with all the instrument, which is of this form; and let it be of silver or fine brass like a knife:
Cant tu presses la lengue a tout cest estrument, et tu vois l’aposteme, si pren l’oncine et lou fiche en l’amandre, et la trai fuer au desus plus que tu pues; et trai aucune chose des toiles avec, puis la cope a l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme, que semble unes forces; et toutevoie li chief sont corbé, et l’un endroit l’autre, et sont molt agut, et est fait de fer inde ou d’andainne:	When you press the tongue with all this instrument, and you see an abscess, take a lancet and insert it into the almond, and pull out as far as you can; and remove some things from the cloth along with it, then cut it off with the instrument, which is of this form, resembling forceps; and nevertheless the heads are curved, and one part different from another, and they are very sharp, and made of iron or steel:
Et se tu n’as cest estrument present, si lou cope as tenailles, de coi ci est li forme:	And if you do not have this instrument at hand, cut it with pliers, of which here is the form:
Et soit trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part nom; et quant tu as copeit l’une des amandres, si cope l’autre selonc cele meisme maniere, et aprés l’incision gargarize li malaides aigue chaude, et aigue et aisil, et se decorremens de sanc avient, si gargarize li malaides aigue, ou escorces de pomes grenates soient cuites, ou fuelles de mirte, et semblans choses, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et aucune fois naissent en la gorge autres apostemes que les II amandres, si les cope donques ensi com les II amandres igament.	And let it be cutting on one side and named on the other; and when you have cut one of the glands, cut the other in the same manner, and after the incision, gargle the patient with hot water, and warm and soothing liquids, and if bleeding occurs, gargle the patient with water in which pomegranate peels or myrtle leaves are boiled, or similar things, until the blood is congealed; then treat him until he is healthy; and sometimes other abscesses appear in the throat besides the two glands, so cut them as you would the two glands equally.
Et je medicinai une femme d’un aposteme que li estoit neis dedens la gorge, c’est a savoir I aposteme de petit sens; et avoit jai bien pres close toute la gorge, si que li femme ne pooit expirer por le conduit qui estoit estoupez, et ne pooit ne mengier ne boivre, et fust morte s’elle demorast ensi I jor ou II.	And I treated a woman who had an abscess that was born inside her throat, which is to say the tonsillar abscess; and it had almost completely closed off the entire throat so that the woman could not exhale through the blocked conduit, nor eat or drink, and she would have died if she remained in this state for one or two days.
Et li apostemes estoit jai si montez qu’il avoit fuer mis II rains par les II pertuis dou neis.	And the abscess had risen so high that it had been pierced two inches through both passages of the nose.
Je hastai donques tantost, et fichai en l’un I oncine, puis lou traï fuers, et en traï grant porcion de bowe; puis refis autreteil en l’autre pertus dou neis, et li ovrai la bouche et li pressai la lengue; aprés fichai l’oncine en ces apostemes, et en copai une partie, et n’en issit fuers que un poc de sanc; et ensi fut destoupez li conduis de la gorge la femme, et comensa maintenant a boivre aigue et puis vin, et ne cessai de taillier de cel aposteme par lonc tens; et li apostemes recroissoit adés, et remplissoit lou leu que je avoie vuidiet, tant qu’il refut mout gros; adonques je l’engignai et lou cauterizai dedens la gorge: ensi demora sens croistre; et me partis de ces parties, et ne soi que Deus fist de li aprés moi.	Then I hurried and inserted a lancet into one side, then drew out a great quantity of pus; then I did the same on the other nasal passage, and opened her mouth and pressed her tongue; after that, I inserted the lancet into the abscesses and removed part of it, and only a little blood came out; thus, the throat conduit was cleared for the woman, and she now began to drink water and then wine, and I did not stop cutting into this abscess for a long time; and the abscess grew back quickly and filled up the place that I had emptied, until it became very large again; then I worked on it and cauterized it inside the throat: thus, it remained without growing further; and I left these parts behind, and do not know what God did for her after me.
de l’uve	of the eye(socket)
Quant reume dessent a l’uve, et elle est enflee et elle est longe, si est apelee «perpendiculaire»; et s’elle est desoz grosse et reonde, si est apelee «uve».	When rheum descends into the eye socket, and it is swollen and elongated, it is called "perpendicular"; and if it is swollen and round, it is called "eye".
Quant elle est curee si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, et tu vois que li chaus apostemes est apaisiez, et elle est subtilz, si covient que tu la copes; et celle qui est reonde assemblee et n’est mie longe; et elle est sanguine ou de fusse color ou noire, si covient que tu eschues l’incision de li.	When it is treated as we have said in the division, and the treatment does not help, and you see that the swelling has subsided but it remains subtle, then you must cut it; and if it is round and not elongated, and it is bloody or dusky colored or black, then you should avoid incision.
Car il i a grant peril sus lou malaide.	For there is great danger to the patient.
Il covient donques, quant tu la vois, selonc la maniere que j’ai dit, de sa blenchor et de sa longesce, que tu faices seoir le malaide devant lou soleil, et li presse la lengue a l’estrument dont nos avons fait la remembrance ci devant; puis fiche l’oncine en l’uve, et la trai desoz, et la cope a I des II estrumens que j’ai dit en l’incision des II amandres.	Therefore, when you see it, according to the manner that I have said, regarding its whiteness and length, you should seat the patient before the sun, and press the tongue with the instrument of which we have made mention previously; then place a needle in the eye socket, and draw it out from below, and cut at one of the two points where I have instructed for cutting between the two almonds.
Et covient que tu ne coper mie fuer que la superfluiteit qui est outre le termine natureil; car se tu en copes plus, si grieves a la voix, et a la parolle; et aprés l’incision, use de ceu que nos avons dit en l’incision des II amandres, et le cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And you should not cut any flesh beyond the excess that is beyond the natural boundary; for if you cut more, it harms the voice and speech; and after the incision, use what we have said about cutting the two glands, and treat it until it is healed.
Et se li malaides a paor dou coper, si covient que tu i use d’engien a la cauterization de li sens paor.	And if the patient fears the cutting, then you should use a cautery on the fearful sensation.
Et li maniere dou cautere si est aigue ague.	And the manner of the cautery is sharp like aqua fortis.
Et est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, et puis li presse la lengue a l’estrument que nos avons dit ou chapistre de cautere, et confis avec aigue vive chaus, si qu’elle ne soit mie trop espesse ne trop clere; et en emple le chevement de cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme:	And it is that the patient place their head in your lap, and then press the tongue with the instrument we have mentioned in the chapter on cautery, and apply it with sharp vinegar, so that it is not too thick or too clear; and use the edge of this instrument, which has the following form:
Et ait ou chief une cheveure ou om met la medecine, si com li chevemens d’une cuillier, et met l’estrument a tout la medicine sus l’uve; et li malaides soit gisans sus son costeit, si que li salive et li muscillaige corre de sa bouche de la medicine dedens, si qu’ele ne dessende a la gorge, et lou blece; puis tien ta main a tout la medicine et la presse sus l’uve, la quantiteit de la moitiet d’une houre, tant que tu la vois nercie et li mordications de la medicine soit apaisie; et se tu vues, pren coton et l’envoloupe sus aucun estrument, et moille lou coton en la medicine, et boute l’estrument a tout le couton en la cainne desus, tant que li coton s’aerde sus l’uve; et fai ceu sovent, tant que li cauteres soit parfais, puis la laisse elle seche, et chiet aprés IIII jors ou V Et se tu as mestier de rencomencier lou cautere de la medicine, si le rencomence, et aprés le cautere l’essue entor l’uve, de couton embut em burre, et mundifie ceu qui est entor de la medicine; et soit arosez d’aigue froide, et soit curez de gargarismes tant qu’il soit sanez.	And place on the head a piece of cloth where the medicine is applied, like the amount in one spoon, and put the instrument with all the medicine over the eye; and let the patient lie on their side so that saliva and mucus run from their mouth into the medicine, so it does not go down to the throat and close off; then hold your hand over all the medicine and press it onto the eye for half an hour, until you see it has settled and the tickling of the medicine is calm; and if you want, take cotton and wrap it around some instrument, and moisten the cotton in the medicine, and place the instrument with the cotton on top of the eyelid, so that the cotton adheres to the eye; and do this often until the cautery is complete, then leave it to dry, and after four or five days, if you need to start the cautery again with the medicine, restart it; and after the cautery wipe around the eye with cotton wrapped in butter, and clean what is around the medicine; and rinse it with cold water and gargle until they are well.
Ceste cure est plus save de l’incision, ne que li cautere; s’elle est curee de fumigation selonc ceste maniere, pren calament et ysope et origanum et rue et camomille et avronne et semblans herbes, et les assemble toutes ou aucunes d’eles en I pot, et i met aisil, et fai bullir; et li potz soit bien gluez de fort terre, et enmi le pot ait I estrument cheveit selonc ceste maniere:	This cure is better than incision or cautery; if it is treated by fumigation according to this method, take calamint and hyssop and origanum and rue and chamomile and wormwood and similar herbs, and put them all together or some of them in one pot, and add salt, and boil; and the pot should be well sealed with thick clay, and inside the pot have an instrument pointed according to this manner:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, et soit li uns des chiés boutez en la bouche dou malaide tant que li vapor monte a l’uve par la caine, tant que li uve soit mortifie; aprés lou rencomence sovent, tant que li uve seche, et garde que tu ne faices ceu au comencement de l’avenement de l’aposteme chaut, car plusors choses i avienent; et ne faire mie ceu fuer que a la declination d’aposteme chaut.	And it should be made of silver or brass, and place one end in the patient's mouth so that the vapor rises to the eye through the duct until the abscess is deadened; after this, repeat often, until the abscess dries up, and take care not to do this at the beginning of the onset of a hot abscess, for many things can happen; and do not attempt this unless there is a decline in the condition of a hot abscess.
Et se cist estrument n’est presens, si pren une caine et met dedens lou chief une craiffe d’uef, si que li bouche au malaide n’ait mie trop chaut; car li craiffe d’uef ne lait mie la vapor grever la bouche, et c’est bone cure ensamble salut.	And if this instrument is not present, take a chain and place inside the head an eggshell, so that the mouth of the patient does not become too hot; for the eggshell does not let the vapor weigh down the mouth, and it is a good remedy together with safety.
Maintes fois s’aert a la gorge os ou espinee de poisson, ou aucune chose; si covient donc que tu traies ceu que tu pues veoir, et li presse la lengue au soleil a tout l’estrument, si que tu voies mues la chose; et ceu que ne t’apert mie et est reponus en la gorge, covient que tu faices vomir le malaide ainsois que li viande soit cuite en l’estomac; par aventure si istra li chose aerse par le vomissement; ou li malaides englutisse une piece d’esponge, ou une piece de navel, ou une racine de laitue, ou I morceil de pain sec; et lie a l’esponge I fil, et puis la transglutisse; et quant elle venra au leu, si s’aerdra, et puis trairas fuer; et s’elle ne vient fuer de ceu que nos avons dit, si pren I estrument de plonc selonc ceste forme:	Many times a fish bone or some other object gets stuck in the throat. Therefore, you must extract what you can see and press the tongue with a tool to make the object visible; and for what is not apparent and lodged deep in the throat, you must induce vomiting in the patient as if the food were cooked in the stomach; perhaps this will expel the foreign object by vomiting; or the patient swallows a piece of sponge, or a piece of navel cloth, or a lettuce root, or a small piece of dry bread; and tie a thread to the sponge, then swallow it; when it reaches the place where the object is stuck, it will adhere, and you can pull out the foreign body with force; and if these methods do not work as mentioned above, take this instrument made of lead according to this form:
Et soit li estrumens corbés au chief si qu’il puist plus legierement entrer en la gorge, et ait le chief en haut leveit; et warde que tu ne touchier l’epiglote, que li tous ne li viegne, ne ne bouter mie l’os dedens; et mues vaut que li malaides i boute l’estrument, por ceu qu’il seit mues ou li chose est aerse; si la boute aval, ou il la traie fuer a tout l’estrument igalment, tant qu’elle soit fuer.	And let the instrument be curved at the head so that it can more easily enter the throat, and have the head raised high; and beware that you do not touch the epiglottis, lest breathing be obstructed, nor push the bone inside; and move the patient to put in the instrument, so that they may be moved where the thing is loose; if pushed down, or pulled up entirely, evenly, until it is fully inside.
de la sansue de la gorge	of the blood from the throat
Aucune fois est medicinee li sansue, si com j’ai dit en la division, par la cure de medicines; et quant ceu ne profite mie, adonques regarde en la gorge dou malaide au soleil, puis que tu li presses la lengue a l’estrument que je t’ai dit.	Sometimes the blood is treated, as I said in the division, by the cure of medicines; and when this does not help, then look into the patient's throat in the sunlight, after you press their tongue with the instrument that I told you about.
Et se tu vois la sansue, si la trai a tout I petit uncine, ou as tenailles subtilz que valent a ceu.	And if you see the blood, draw it out completely with a small hook, or with fine forceps suitable for this purpose.
Et se ceu ne vaut, si pren une caine chevee, et la boute en la gorge dou malaide, puis boute ou chevement de la caine I fer chaut, et fai ce sovent.	And if that does not work, take a hooked cane and insert it into the patient's throat, then place a hot iron at the hook of the cane, and do this frequently.
Et se teigne li malaides d’aigue toute jor.	And if the patient is constantly bleeding.
puis pren plein I voirre d’aigue froide, et oevre la bouche, et la giete ens sens englutir, et la mueve a sa main sovent; et si tost com li sansue sent l’aigue, si chiet.	Then take a full glass of cold water, and pour it into the mouth, and let them swallow it; move their hand frequently so they can drink as soon as possible; and as soon as the blood tastes the water, it will stop.
Et s’elle ne chiet si com nos avons dit, si subfumige lou malaide d’asefetide, a l’estrument que j’ai dit en la fumigation de l’uve; fai ceu maintes fois, car elle cherra sens targier.	And if it does not stop as we have said, then suffume the patient with asafoetida using the instrument I mentioned for the fumigation of the eye; do this many times, for it will stop without delay.
Et li maniere de la fumigation si est que tu preignes I pot ou il ait charbons vis, et soit li pos covert d’un coverseil perciet en mileu, et en celui pertus soit li chiés de l’estrument; puis i giete ta fumigation, et li malaides mette lou chief de la cainne en sa bouche, et cloie la bouche, si que li fumee n’en isse mie, mais viegne jusc’a la sansue; et la sansue cherra maintenant, et s’elle ne chiet, si rencomence la fumigation par maintes fois; et soffre li malaides soif, et menjuce choses salees et als, et ne boive point d’aigue; et adonques li iert mestier qu’elle isse fuer par cest governement.	And the method of fumigation is that you take one pot in which there are live coals, and cover it with a sieve pierced in the middle, and through that aperture place the head of the instrument; then throw your fumigation into it, and have the patient put his chin on top of it, and close the mouth so that no smoke escapes but goes straight to the blood; and now the blood will fall out, and if it does not fall out, restart the fumigation multiple times; and allow the patient thirst, and drink salty things and ashes, and do not let them drink water; and then by this governance it is necessary for it to come forth.
Et li forme de l’estrument a coi on trait la sansue, si est, quant on la puet veoir, semblans a tenailles corbés por mues entrer en la gorge; et ait semblance au bec de soigne, et i ait asperiteit de lime, si que ceu qu’elle prent, elle ne puet lassier; et vez ci la forme:	And the form of the instrument with which one treats the blood when it can be seen is like curved tongs for entering into the throat; and it resembles a bird's beak, and there are ridges like a file so that what it grasps cannot be released; and here you see its form:
li chapistres des apostemes	the chapter on abscesses
Mout de semblances d’aposteme sont, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient ci aprés d’un et d’autre en cest livre, et sont diver en perforation et en taille; et c’est en II manieres dont l’une est en sa semblance meisme, et de ceu qu’il tient moistor.	There are many types of abscesses, according to what the memory brings back later in this book, and they differ in perforation and size; and this is in two ways, one of which is in its form itself, and from those that it holds moisture.
Et li seconde maniere si est por les leus ou il sont au cors.	And the second way is for the places where they are on the body.
car li apostemes dou chief est autres que cil dou fondement, et li apostemes dou leu charnut est autres que cil qui vient en jointures, et chescuns ait son jugement en l’uevre.	for abscesses of the head are different from those of the buttocks, and abscesses of the flesh are different from those that come in joints, and each has its judgment in the work.
Et si a apostemes c’on ne doit mie percier, tant que li bowe est meure selonc son acomplissement; et si a de telz qu’il covient percier quant il sont crut, et ne meurent mie selonc lor acomplissement, si com aposteme qui sont delez jointures.	And there are abscesses that one must not pierce until the pus is dead according to its completion; and there are some that should be pierced when they are hard, and do not die off according to their completion, such as abscesses near joints.
Car quant apostemes vient delez jointures, et on le laisse tant qu’il est porris entor, par aventure si sont corrumput li liien et li nerf de la jointure, par coi ce est cause de contraction en celui membre.	For when abscesses come near the joints, and one lets it remain until it is rotten around, by chance the ligament and nerve of the joint are corrupted, which is the cause of contraction in that limb.
Ou li aposteme est delez lou membre principel, et se tu tardes la perforation tant qu’il soit meurez, si nuira au membre principeil; ou il est delez lou fondement, si le perce on ainsois qu’il soit meurs; et ne covient mie que tu perces aposteme crut sens digestion acomplie, fuers que celui qui est delez lou fondement, qu’il ne porrisse em parfont, et soit alongiez dedens, et i viegne fistule; et ne puisse saner en grant termine.	When the abscess is near the principal limb, and if you delay the incision until it is dead, it will harm the principal limb; when it is near the fundament, pierce it similarly before it becomes dead; and it must not be that you pierce an unripe abscess without complete digestion, except for that which is near the fundament, lest it should rot entirely and become prolonged internally, and a fistula comes forth; and cannot heal in a long time.
Et covient que tu saiches l’oure de la perforation de l’aposteme qui est meur selonc l’acomplissement, et c’est quant li dolor est apaisie, et li departemens de la fievre, et l’amenuisement de la dolor et de la roujor, et dou debatement et de l’aguisement dou chief de l’aposteme, et les autres signes; et covient que tu faices seoir la perforation ou plus dependant leu de l’aposteme, et la ou il apert mues; et soit li perforation dou lonc dou cors, et se li apostemes est as mains ou as piez, ou en jointures et au ners et as arteres, et en toz leus igalz ou il n’a point de ploieure.	And it must be that you know the time for the incision of the abscess that is dead according to its completion, and this is when the pain is abated, and the departure of the fever, and the diminishment of the pain and redness, and the softening and sharpening of the head of the abscess, and other signs; and it must be that you make the incision where the dependence lies in the location of the abscess, and where it appears to have changed; and let the incision follow along the length of the body, and if the abscess is on the hands or feet, at joints, nerves, arteries, and all places equally where there is no joint.
En ces que ploient, par selonc celui membre.	In cases of bleeding, according to that member.
Et quant apostemes est en leu charnut, si vaut mues que tu laisses la perforation tant qu’il soit confermez en digestion acomplie, si com nos avons dit.	And when an abscess is in the flesh, it is better to wait until it is confirmed to be fully digested before performing puncture, as we have said.
Car se tu lou perces devant ceu, si iert alongiez li cors dou venim de lui, et est plains de mout d’ordure; et par aventure endurcissent les levres et li parfondetez de lui.	For if you puncture it before then, the venom will spread throughout the body, and it will be full of much filth; and by chance, its lips and depths may harden.
Et si a aucun aposteme que sont perciet selonc le large dou cors, selonc ceu que li membres en ait mestier.	And if there is an abscess that needs to be punctured according to the width of the body, depending on what the limb requires.
Et covient que tu amenistres em petis apostemes, petis pertus; et en grans apostemes, grans pertus, et maintes fendures selonc la semblance de la grandor de l’aposteme; et si a de tels apostemes ou il covient chever lou keur, et coper; quant il est jai devenus ausi com I drapelz, et est amortis, si covient faire ausi com on fait as bubes: et si a de telz que sont fendut en III angles, et si a de telz dont on cope ausi com la fuelle de mirte, si com apostemes des angres; et si a de telz ou on fait une reonde taille, et autres tailles et semblant copeure.	And you should treat small abscesses with small punctures; and large abscesses with larger punctures, and many incisions according to the size of the abscess; and for such abscesses that require slicing open or cutting off; when they have become hard like flags, and are swollen, then it is necessary to act as with boils: and there are some that are cut into three angles, and others that are cut like a boxwood leaf, as in case of abscesses from anger; and there are those where one makes a round incision, and other cuts similar to this.
Cil qui n’ont point de chief, si com aposteme souef superficial, il covient que tu lou perces plainnement; et covient quant li apostemes est gros, et il a coillit grant bowe, et tu lou perces, si ne traire mie toute la bowe en celle houre, mais en trai une partie; puis estoupe l’aposteme jusc’a l’autre jor, puis en trai aucune chose derechief; fai ceu par maintes fois de greit en greit, tant que li bowe isse toute; meismement se li malaides est de foible vertut, ou femme portans, ou petis enfes, ou viez hons decrepites.	Those who do not have a head, such as a superficial abscess, you must pierce completely; and when the abscess is large and has collected much pus, if you pierce it, do not draw out all the pus at that time, but draw out some of it; then plug up the abscess until the next day, then draw out something again; do this little by little over several times gradually, until all the pus comes out; similarly if the patient is weak in constitution, or a pregnant woman, or small children, or old men who are infirm.
Car li esperis tressaut aucune fois avec l’issue de la bowe, que par aventure muert li malaides, et tu ne t’en persois.	For the patient may sometimes gasp when the pus comes out, which might cause the patient to die, and you would not be blamed for it.
Eschuez donques cest chapistre par grant cautele, et quant tu as perciet ton aposteme, si essue la plaie, et regarde se li plaie de l’aposteme est petite; et se c’est une tailleure plainne, si amenistre tentes de lin ou de viez coton; et se c’est uns grans apostemes, et il i a mout de pertus, si covient que tu boutes en chescun une tente si qu’ele viegne l’une contre l’autre; et se tu as copeit en l’aposteme une partie dou cuir, et tu l’as cheveit entor, si covient que tu l’emplisses de viel couton ou de rasure de dras de lin sens moistor, et le lie jusc’au tier jor; puis l’oste, et le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	Avoid therefore this chapter with great caution, and when you have punctured your abscess, wash the wound, and observe if the abscess wound is small; and if it is a smooth incision, then bring lint or old cotton; and if there are large abscesses, and there are many openings, then you must place in each one a tent so that they come against each other; and if you have cut into the abscess part of the skin, and you have stitched around it, then you must fill it with old lint or linen shreds without moisture, and bandage until the third day; then remove it, and treat it with ointment until it is healed.
Et se decorremens de sanc avient a ton ovraige, si amenistre aigue froide et aisil, et moille I drapeil, et met sor le leu decorrant par maintes fois.	And if bleeding occurs during your work, then bring cold water and herbs, and wet the cloth with it, and apply it to the bleeding area repeatedly.
Et se li decorremens de sanc persevere, se i amenistre governement et cure, et les poudres que j’ai dit em mains leus en cest livre, et se c’est ou tens d’iver, et li leus ou li apostemes est est mout nervous, si couvient que tu mettes sus tentes et drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile chaut; et se c’est en esteit, et li leus est charnus, si covient que tu mes sus drapelz moilliez en aigue et en oile, ou en vin et en oile froit, jusc’au tier jor, si com nos avons dit; et puis deslie l’aposteme et l’essue et le cure, si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the bleeding persists, administer treatment and care, and use the powders that I have mentioned earlier in this book, and if it is winter, and the area where the abscess is very nervous, then you must place tents and cloths soaked in wine and hot oil; and if it is summer, and the area is fleshy, then you should place cloths soaked in water and cold oil, or in wine and cold oil, until the third day, as we have said; and then loosen the abscess and dry it and cure it as needed until it is healed.
Et ceu covient il conoistre universement en cures des apostemes: or vos ai dit coment on doit aler avant as cures des apostemes, et vez ci le chapistre.	And you must know universally in the treatment of abscesses: I have told you how one should proceed with the treatment of abscesses, and here is the chapter.
des soros	of sweats
Ou keur dou chief vienent petis apostemes, et sont manieres de nous que sont en toiles, ausi com li josier d’une geline, et mout en i a de semblances.	For small boils on the head come in various forms, like the pattern of a gooseberry, and there are many similarities.
Il en i a de gras et de telz ou il a moistor ausi com poulz; et si a de telz qui sont dur et pierous au taillier, et n’i a point de doutance se li artere n’i fait contraire.	Some are fatty and like those that contain moisture as if they were pus; and there are some that are hard and stony to the touch, and there is no doubt about them unless an artery opposes.
Et li ovraiges de la taille si est que tu esprueve a tout I estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», de coi li forme vient ci aprés, quel chose il contient.	And the work of the loin is such that you should test all the instruments called "entromissoire," of which the forms come next, what they contain.
Car s’il contient moistor, si lou fent par desus dou lonc.	For if it contains moisture, then cut it open from above along its length.
Et quant li moistor est vuidie, si escorche sens rien laissier la peil qui contient celle moistor, car il revient adés quant on i laisse rien; puis plonge coton en oignement egiptien, s’il est presens; se ceu non, en aigue et en seil, et en emple la plaie, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor; et ceu corront ceu qui est demorez dou nit.	And when the moisture is evacuated, carefully scrape away without leaving any skin that contains this moisture, for it returns quickly if anything is left; then soak cotton in Egyptian ointment, if it is available; if not, use water and wine, and apply it to the wound, and leave it until the next day; and do what remains at night.
Et pues rencomence lou coton, si com devant, le second jor, et lou tier, tant que tu saiches bien qu’il ne demoure point dou nit; puis cure la plaie d’oignement a ceu convenauble, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And then restart the cotton, as before, on the second day, and the third, until you are sure that nothing remains at night; then treat the wound with appropriate ointment until it is healed.
Et se li apostemes tient I nout gras, si le cope selonc ceste forme, dou lonc; et i giete tes oncines, et l’escorche de toutes pars, et met toute ta cure de traire fuer la cotte ou il gist; et se li artere te fait contraire, si fai ceu que je t’ai dit aprés.	And if the abscess remains deep and fatty, cut it according to this form, lengthwise; then apply your poultices, and scrape it from all sides, and put all your effort into draining it from where it lies; and if an artery opposes you, do as I told you afterward.
Et ausi fai de l’aposteme s’il est pierous, et dou taillier et dou curer si com je t’ai dit.	And do the same for the abscess if it is stony, and cutting and curing as I have told you.
Et li taille sus l’aposteme pierous et le moiste, si est plus legiere, car il sont de poc de sanc.	And when you cut into the stony and moist abscess, it is easier, for they contain little blood.
Et si a aucuns de ces apostemes ou chief ou il n’a point de moistor, et de ces fut I apostemes que je copai ou chief d’une vielle femme; et trovai l’aposteme ausi com une piere xourde, aspre et blainche, et ne pooit brisier; et s’on en eust ferut aucun, on li eust ausi bien fait plaie com d’une piere.	And if some of these abscesses occur at the head where there is no moisture, and among them were the abscesses that I treated on an old woman's head; and I found the abscess like a hard stone, rough and white, and it could not be broken; and if one had struck with it, it would have caused as much injury as a stone.
En autres apostemes venans ou chief, fuer que ces qui vienent as chief des enfans et as racines des oreilles, li overture si soit toz jors au plus dependant leu, por mues issir la bowe; et les cure si com il covient.	In other abscesses that occur at the head, especially those that come at the heads of children and at the roots of the ears, the incision should always be made as low as possible to allow the pus to escape; and treat them as is appropriate.
des scrophules	scrofulous glands
Maintes fois avienent cist aposteme au col, et desoz les asseles, et ens angres, et aucune fois vienent autre part ou cors, et sont mout, et sont enjanrees l’une avec l’autre.	These abscesses often occur in the neck, and sometimes near glands, and in armpits, and at other times they appear elsewhere on the body, and are very large, growing one upon another.
Et chescune scrophule est proprement dedens sa cote, si com li nout et li aposteme dou chief, si com nos avons dit; et les semblances de ces scrophules sont maintes.	And each scrofulous gland is properly within its own area, such as the one in the neck and the head abscess, as we have said; and there are many types of these scrofulous glands.
Il i a de teles que contienent moistor, et si a de malignes qui ne vuellent obeir a santeit.	There are some that contain moisture, and there are others that are malignant and do not want to obey treatment.
en celle donques que tu vois de bone disposition au tochier, et est semblans a la color dou cors, et muet de chescune part et n’est mie aerse as ners dou col ne a l’artere ne au conduit, et n’est mie parfonde; si covient que tu la copes par desus, et l’escorche de chescune partie, et estent les II levres dou keur as oncines, se tu en as mestier, si com nos avons dit en apostemes dou chief; et la trai poc et poc, et soies seur que tu ne coper lou nerf ne la voine, et ne soit mie li spatumile agus ne trenchans, que li mains n’eschaipe, et ne voise trop avant, que tu ne coper mie ceu que tu ne dois.	In the one that you see has a good disposition upon touch, and it resembles the color of the skin, and is soft on all sides and does not adhere to the nerves of the neck or the artery or the conduit, and is not deep; then you should cut it above, and peel off the skin from each part, and spread apart the two edges of the wound with forceps if you need them, as we have said about head abscesses; and cut little by little, and be sure that you do not cut the nerve or the vein, and do not make the incision too sharp or cutting, so your hand does not slip, and do not go too far in, lest you cut what should not be cut.
Et se tu copes la voinne ou l’artere, et ceu ne te laisse ovrer, si met en la plaie vitriole broiet, ou aucunes poudres que restainchent sanc, et estraint la plaie; et la laisse tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et soit amollie li plaie, et encomence a porrir.	And if you cut the vein or artery, and it does not allow you to work on it, put in the wound vitriol ground up, or some powders that constrict blood, and hold the wound; and leave it until the abscess is calmed, and the wound is softened, and then begin to treat it.
Et quant li sans est estainchiez, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que tu l’acomplisses; puis quier a ton doit indice s’il i demoure nules petites scrophules, si les cope et les munde.	And when the blood is constricted, return to your work until you complete it; then search for any small scrofulas that remain, cut them out, and clean them.
Et s’il a en la racine de la scrophule voinne grant, si ne covient mie que tu copes celle scrophule en sa racine, mais la lie d’un fil double fort, et la laisse cheoir par li, sens nuisement; puis emple la plaie de viel coton plongiet en oignement egiptien, puis la cure.	And if there is a large vein at the root of the scrofula, you must not cut that scrofula at its root, but tie it with a double strong thread, and let it fall naturally without harm; then fill the wound with old cotton soaked in Egyptian ointment, then treat it.
Et se tu copes toute la scrophule, si covient que tu assembles les II levres de la plaie, et les cout maintenant, puis qu’il n’i a point demoreit de superfluiteit por la grandor de la scrophule.	And if you cut out the whole boil, then you must bring together the two edges of the wound and sew them now, since there is no excess tissue due to the size of the boil.
si covient que tu entendes a coper la racine de li, et traire fuer, et la cout si com nos avons dit.	And you must focus on cutting the root of it, pulling out the core, and sewing as we have said.
Celles scrophules que tienent superfluiteit, perce lai ou il apert meure; et la perce ensi com celle devant dite, en dependant, puis i amenistre tentes avec oignement et semblans choses, si qu’elle corrompe ceu qui est demorez de la corruption; et quant li plaie est bien mundee, si la cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	For boils that contain excess tissue, pierce where it appears to be most dead; and treat the puncture as previously described, draining, then apply poultices and similar treatments so that the remaining corruption is cleansed; and when the wound is well cleaned, treat with healing ointments until it is healthy.
de squinance	Of scabies
Li ancien dirent et parlerent de la tailleure de la gorge; mais je ne vis onques en nostre terre qui la feist, et c’est li escripture de lor parole.	The ancients spoke and wrote about cutting the throat; but I have never seen anyone do it in our land, and this is the writing of their words.
A ces qui ont squinance, il covient que li fendure de la gorge qui est apelee «epiglote» soit eschuee; et c’on ne faice aide par ceu, por ceu que toutes les voines et li pormon dou malaide sont a ces qui ont aposteme chaut en la bouche, ou en la gorge ou en II amandres.	For those who have squint, it is necessary to remove the fissure of the throat which is called "epiglottis"; and one should not assist with this, because all the veins and flesh of the patient are affected in those who have a hot abscess in the mouth, or in the throat, or in both tonsils.
Quant li maladie est en la chenal dou pormon, il covient coper l’epiglote por fuir la perdition qui vient de l’estranglement.	When the illness is in the windpipe channel, it is necessary to cut the epiglottis to avoid the danger of strangulation.
Il covient donques, quant nos volons fendre l’epiglote, que nos le fendons desoz III cercles ou IIII une petite fendure dou travers, entre les II cercles ou par la quantiteit de la fendure dou syfac, ne mie en la cartillaige; et cil leus si est covenaubles a la section de l’epiglote qu’il n’i a point de char, et li vasseil sont lonc d’enqui.	Therefore, when we wish to cut the epiglottis, we must make a small incision across it within three or four circles, between two circles, and not in the cartilage; and those places are suitable for cutting the epiglottis where there is no flesh, and the vessels are long and straight.
Et se li maistres est paourous, si covient qu’il estende le cuir de la gorge a tout l’oncine, puis fende lou keur tant qu’il viegne a la cheneil; et eschue les vasselz de sanc, se tu vois aucune chose, et puis cope lou syfac, si com nos avons dit; et est demostrez par la section dou fleume de la cheneil ki saut fuer par le leu qui est rompus, et par la defaute de la voix; et laisse la plaie overte une piece.	And if the master is afraid, it is necessary that he stretches the skin of the throat to all the inch, then cuts the heart until it comes to the windpipe; and avoid the vessels of blood, if you see anything, and then cut the surface, as we have said; and this is demonstrated by the section of the phlegm in the windpipe which jumps forth from the place that is broken, and by the loss of voice; and leave the wound open for a while.
Et quant li houre est passee de coi on doute l’estranglement, assemble les II levres de la plaie dou keur, et la cout toute soule sens la cartillaige; puis aministre medicines qui font naistre char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when the hour has passed for which strangulation is feared, bring together the two lips of the wound of the heart, and stitch it all along to the cartilage; then administer medicines that promote flesh growth until it heals.
Albucasim dist c’on ne faice ce jusc’a tant que li gorge est toute estoupee, et li malaides est jugiez a mort, et li defaut li alaine.	Albucasim says that one should not do this until the throat is completely blocked, and the patient is judged to be dead, and the absence of breath occurs.
Adonques cope on l’epiglote por ceu que li malaides ne puet alener, et il respire par la plaie, et ensi est gardez de mort; et por ce commanderent li anciain a laissier la plaie overte tant que li malice de la maladie soit passee, et elle est passee en III jors ou en IIII Et adonques il comanderent a coudre la plaie et curer, tant qu’elle fut curee; et je vos dirai ceu que je vis.	Then cut the epiglottis because the patient cannot breathe, and they will then breathe through the wound, thus being saved from death; and for this reason, the ancients commanded to leave the wound open until the malice of the illness has passed, which takes three or four days. And then they commanded to sew up the wound and clean it until it was cleansed; and I will tell you what I saw.
Je vis que une damoisele prist I coutel, et le ficha en sa gorge, et copa partie des chenelz dou pormon; et je fui apelez por li curer, et la trovai ausi com morte.	I saw that a young lady took a knife and stuck it in her throat, cutting part of the windpipe; and I was called to clean her wound, and found her as if dead.
Je descovris la plaie, et trovai le sanc qui en estoit issus, et soi bien qu’elle n’avoit mie copeit voine ne conduit fuer que la gorge, et li vens issoit fuer par la plaie.	I examined the wound and found the blood that had come out, and realized that she had not cut any vein or vital organ, only her throat, and the flesh was protruding from the wound.
Je me hastai, et cousi la plaie, et la curai tant qu’elle fut sanee; et n’avint a la damoisele fuer qu’elle fut roge de voix, et revint aprés a sa disposition; por ceu di je que en la tailleure de l’epiglote n’ait mie paour.	I hurried and sewed up the wound, and treated it until it was healed; and there happened to the damsel no more than that her voice became hoarse, and she returned afterwards to her disposition; therefore I say that in the cutting of the epiglottis one need not fear.
de la grosse gorge	of the swollen throat
Cist apostemes est apelez «hernie de gorge», et est uns grans apostemes en color d’une jaisse, et est molt en femmes; et est selonc II manieres: naturez, et accidens; ou natureil n’a point d’engien.	This abscess is called a "hernia of the throat," and it is a large abscess in the color of a hazel nut, and it often occurs in women; and it comes in two manners: natural and accidental; the natural one does not have a core.
Et li accidens est selonc II manieres, de coi l’une est semblans a gras nous, et li autre maniere est semblans a aposteme qui vient de nous d’artere; et il i ait paour, et ne covient mie ovrer de feir fuers que en celi qui est petite, et le prueve et cerche a tout l’intromissoire: se tu le trueves ausi com I nout gras, et ne pent a nulle voine, si le cope, si com on cope les nous, et le trai a tout sa coife, s’il en i a point; et encerche bien tot, et le cure si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	And the accidental one comes in two manners, of which one is similar to fatty tissue, and the other manner is similar to an abscess that comes from an artery; and there is danger here, and it should not be operated upon except for the one that is small, and prove and search thoroughly throughout the interior: if you find it as fatty tissue and cannot reach any vein, then cut it out, as one would with a lump, and remove its entire covering, if there is any; and examine quickly and treat properly until it is perfectly healed.
des nous	from us
Maintes manieres de nous sont, dont je dirai toutes les semblances; et or covient que je die toute la difference qui est entre nout et issue.	Many ways are from us, of which I will say all the similarities; and now it is necessary for me to say all the differences that are between us and them.
Je dis que issue est chalors et fievre tenans, tant que li ebulicions est passee, et est acomplie li porriture; adonques repose li fievre et li chalor.	I say that the fever and heat persist until the ebullition is past, and the putrefaction is completed; then the fever and heat subside.
Avec lou nout n’a ne chalor ne fievre ne dolor, et contient I syfac, qui est ses propres sac et est selonc la color dou cors, et encomence ausi com une jaisse, et devient gros; et sont selonc ij semblances, ou grais, ou moiste, et mout de color sont si com j’ai dit en la division.	With us there is no heat nor fever nor pain, and it contains a swelling, which is its own sac and corresponds to the color of the skin, and begins like a pimple, and becomes large; and they are according to certain similarities, either hard or moist, and many colors are as I have said in the division.
Il covient, quant tu viens a la cure dou nout, que tu esprueves et l’enquier premierement a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», selonc ce que sa forme venra ou chapistre qui est aprés.	It is necessary when you come to the treatment of the nose that you test and inquire first about all the instruments which are called "entromissoire", according to what their form will be in the chapter which is after.
Et li maniere de l’inquisicion des apostemes des nous est que tu preignes ou plus moiste leu que tu trueves en l’aposteme, et torne tes dois poc et poc, tant que tu saiches que li estrumens ait perciet le keur, puis que ce soit selonc la grandor de l’aposteme; puis estrai l’entromissoire, et pren garde en ceu que saut fuer.	And the method of investigating abscesses of the nose is that you take at the moistest place that you find in the abscess, and turn your two fingers little by little, until you know that the instrument has pierced the core, according to the size of the abscess; then extract the entromissoire, and be careful not to use excessive force.
Se moistor corrans cort, queil color elle ait, si le fent si com j’ai dit des autres apostemes; et se aprés l’entromissoire nen vient moistor, saiches qu’il est gras, si le fent donques en croix, et le prent as pinceures, et l’escorche legierement de chescune part et warde la cotte ou il gist que tu la traies saine avec le nout; et se tu ne la pues traire saine, si la trai par pieces si qu’il n’i demoure rien.	If moisture comes out running when it is cut, whatever color it has, proceed as I have said for other abscesses; and if after the entromissoire no moisture comes out, know that it is fatty, then make a cross incision, take it with forceps, and lightly scrape from each side while watching the coat where it lies so you draw it off healthy with the nose; and if you cannot draw it off healthy, then draw it off in pieces so nothing remains.
Car s’il i demoure rien, si revient li nous par maintes fois; et s’il en demore un poc, et li sans te grieve, si emple la plaie d’aucunes poudres corrosives agues, et estraint la plaie, et met sus choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li nous est grans, si cout les II levres de la plaie, et le cure de ceu qui enjanre char.	For if anything remains there, the pus will return many times; and if a little remains, but the blood does not suffer from it, then apply to the wound some corrosive powder, and hold back the wound, and place hot things that calm down abscesses, and treat it with other treatments until it is healed; and if the pus is great, sew together both lips of the wound, and treat it as one who grows flesh.
et se li voine batans t’est contraire ou autre si te haste et emple le leu de vitriole broiet, et lou laisse liiet II jors ou III, tant que li plaie porrisse, et repose li ebulicion dou sanc; puis revien au coper ceu que i est demoreit dou nout.	and if the wound resists or is contrary to you, hurry and apply the place with broiled vitriol, and leave it for two days or three, until the wound purifies, and let the boiling of the blood rest; then return to copper those parts where pus remains.
Vez ci les formes des estrumens entromissoires, et sont de III manieres: grans et moien et petit; et s’en i a III quarrez qui sont apelez «albaret», et I qui est apelez «breb», et s’en i a de III manieres: grant, moien, et petit, por encerchier les apostemes de fistule; et sont ausi com les aguilles dont on cout les sorceles, et sont d’arain citrin, ou de fer, ou d’argent, et mues valent cil qui sont jaune, et sont plus esprovez de plonc noir por encerchier les corbeures de fistule; et sont de III manieres: grans, moiens, et petis, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce des pertus.	See here the forms of instruments used for probing, and they are of three kinds: large, medium, and small; and there are three square ones called "albaret," and one called "breb," which also come in three sizes: large, medium, and small, to encircle abscesses of fistulas; and they are like the needles used to stitch sorcerers, made of brass yellow, or iron, or silver, and those that are yellow are more valuable, and for encircling curved fistulas, black lead is more effective; and these also come in three sizes: large, medium, and small, according to the quantity of the width of the openings.
Les formes des oncines sont de mout de semblances, si com tu vois ci: grans, moiens, et petis; et si a oncines qui ont II corbeures de III manieres ausi; et si a oncines qui ont III corbeures, et sont ausi de III manieres; et si a oncines qui ont II corbeures, et oncines d’une corbeure soulement, et sont de III manieres; et tuit cist sont necessaire en lor leu.	The forms of hooks are of many likenesses, as you see here: large, medium, and small; and there are hooks that have two curves in three ways thusly; and there are hooks that have three curves, and they are also in three ways; and there are hooks that have two curves, and hooks with a single curve only, and they are in three ways; and all these are necessary in their place.
Li chief de ces a coi on fent sont trenchant, et de telz i a qui ne taillent mie fuer que d’une part, dont on escorche les nous, por ceu c’on ne cope la voine ne le nerf; et de ces intromissoires sont les alemeles reponues en mainches, si que li malaide ne s’en persoivent a l’overture des apostemes; et sont de III manieres: grant, petit, et moien, si com tu vois; et n’en use on mie fuer que en leu charnut, si com jambes, et bras, et mameles, et as angres, et en semblans leus; et aucune fois fait on I autre estrument petit, semblant a escorces de fistices, selonc ceste forme, a coi on estainche sanc:	The tip of these for cutting is sharp, and there are some that only cut from one side so as to strip the flesh, because thereby one does not sever the vein or nerve; and these intermediaries have lancets placed in handles so that the patient does not feel them at the opening of abscesses; and they are of three kinds: large, small, and medium-sized, as you see; and one uses them only in soft flesh such as legs, arms, breasts, and similar places; and sometimes one makes another instrument small, resembling the rind of a citron, according to this form, with which one stops blood:
et le met on aucune fois au leu qui saine a copement des voines, et as arteres, et aucune fois reont selonc ceste grant forme:	and it is sometimes placed at the site suitable for cutting veins, and arteries, and sometimes follows this large form:
Aucune fois enflent les mameles d’aucuns homes quant cil encomencent estre corrumput, tant qu’eles semblent mameles de feme; et demorent laides et enflees, et qui les vuet curer, si le covient soier selonc ceste forme des ceste ligne .b. jusques a .g.:	Sometimes the breasts of some men swell when they begin to be corrupted, so much that they seem like women's breasts; and remain ugly and swollen, and whoever wishes to treat them must follow this form from this line b to g:
puis escorche la graisse, et emple la plaie de medicine enjanrant char, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie a costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee; et se li mamele cline aval, et est amolie por sa grandor si com il avient as femmes, si la fent en II costelz desus, par II semblans fendures; de coi l’une soit tenans a l’autre a la fin de l’une et de l’autre, si que li plus grans ligne conteigne la menor selonc ceste forme, des ceste ligne .b. jusc’a la ligne .g.; puis escorche le cuir qui est entre les II levres, et oste la graisse, et i amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de costure et de poudres, et ceu qui est necessaire en la cure, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il n’est sanez, ou li incision n’est mie toute faite, por ceu que li malaides ne vuet reposer, ou por le decorrement de sanc, si covient que tu emplisses la plaie de coton moilliet en oignement corrosif; et le laisse tant qu’il menjuce le remenant et la graisse, puis le cure tant qu’il soit saneis.	Then scrape off the fat and apply medicine that promotes flesh healing to the wound, then bring together the two edges of the wound to suture it, and treat it until it is healed; if the breast droops down because of its size as happens with women, cut it in half above through two similar incisions, so that one side is connected to the other at both ends according to this form from line b to line g; then scrape off the skin between the two edges, remove the fat, and manage it as we have said regarding suturing and powders necessary for healing until it is healed; if it does not heal or the incision has not been completely made because the patient does not want to rest or due to bleeding, you must fill the wound with cotton soaked in a corrosive ointment; leave it until it consumes the remainder and the fat, then treat it until it is healed.
des apostemes des asselles	abscesses of the buttocks
Cist apostemes que vienent desoz les asseles sont manieres de scrophules dures ou il ait cotes, et s’en i a que contienent moistor.	These abscesses that appear beneath the buttocks are hard forms of scrofula with edges, and there are some that contain moisture.
Cil donques qui contienent moistor covient qu’il soient copez selonc ceste forme, des la ligne .b. jusc’a la ligne .g.:	Those that contain moisture should be incised according to this form, from line .b. to line .g.:
Et quant toute li bowe qui est en l’aposteme est vuidie, si emple la plaie de viel coton, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor, puis oste tout le coton, et cure d’oignement avenant a ceu tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when all the pus in the abscess is drained, fill the wound with old cotton, and leave it until the next day, then remove all the cotton, and treat it with ointment appropriate for healing until it is healed.
Et se li apostemes est de semblances de scrophules, si le fent si com nos avons dit en fendures des scrophules, et se li plaie rent bowe, si amenistre cautere si com nos avons dit devant.	And if the abscess resembles a scrofula, then incise it as we have said about incisions for scrofulas, and if the wound discharges pus, then treat it with cautery as we have previously stated.
de la routure de l’artere	Of the rupture of the artery
Quant li artere est route, et li cuir est soudez qui est sus, si en vient maintes fois apostemes, et tout aussi avient il a la voine enflee et aposteme; et si le conoist on ensi quant c’est por l’artere, si est li apostemes lons em parfont; et quant tu le sens a tes dois, si sens I estraignement; et quant c’est por la voine, si est reons defuer aparans; et c’est folie de coper cest aposteme, et meismement quant il est desoz les asseles et as angres et ou col et em mout d’autres leus, et est mout grans.	When the artery is ruptured and the skin above it is sealed, abscesses often occur; similarly, this happens with a swollen vein and an abscess. And if you recognize it as being due to the artery, the abscess will be long and deep; and when you feel it with your fingers, you sense tightness; and when it is due to the vein, it appears soft and diffuse; and it is foolish to cut this abscess, especially when it is below the armpits, at the angles, on the neck, and in many other places, and it is very large.
