Il covient donques eschuir la cure de fer, et celui qui est a chief covient eschuir ausi, et en celui qui est d’enfleure d’artere fent par desus le cuir dou lonc; puis oevre la taille as oncines, et depart bellement l’artere des toiles, tant qu’ele soit descoverte; puis boute desoz li une aguille, et la fai percier jusc’a l’autre costeit, et estraint l’artere d’un fil double en II leus, selonc ceu que je t’ai ensigniet en l’estraction des II arteres qui sont en temples; puis point le leu qui est entre les II liens d’un intromissoire tant que li sans en isse qui i est, et soit deliiez li aposteme; puis amenistre la cure que enjanre bowe, tant que li liien chient; puis cure ceu d’oignement avenant a ceu, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li apostemes est por la taille de la voinne, si covient que tu teignes a ta main ceu que tu pues de l’aposteme a tout le cuir, puis boute l’aguille desoz le leu que tu tiens a ta main, et la fai percier, et i ait I fil double, si que tu le trais de l’autre costeit; puis lie l’aposteme, si com je t’ai dit, ou liien de l’une de II pars as II chiés dou fil; et se tu doutes que li filz n’isse fuer, si i reboute une autre aguille a tout I fil desoz tout l’aposteme a l’incision de la premiere aguille, et estraint les filz en IIII leus; puis cope l’aposteme tant que li superfluitez en isse, puis cope la superfluiteit dou keur et laisse ceu qui est liiez; puis met sus I drapeil moilliet en vin et en oile, puis li amenistre cures de tentes et d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	It is necessary to avoid treatment with iron in such cases, and one who suffers from swelling of the artery should also be avoided; for those suffering from a swollen artery, make an incision above the skin along its length; then work carefully around the arteries using hooks, and separate the artery from the surrounding tissues until it is fully exposed; then insert a needle below the area you are holding, piercing through to the other side, and tie the artery with a double thread in two places as I have taught you for extracting the two arteries in the temples; then puncture the area between the two ties with an interosseous needle so that blood comes out from there, and loosen the abscess; then apply the remedy derived from bovine urine until the ties come loose; if the abscess is due to a vein injury, use your hand to mark the extent of the abscess on the skin, then insert the needle below where you marked with your hand, piercing through, placing a double thread underneath across the entire abscess near the first needle's incision point; then tie the abscess as I have instructed using two threads from either side of the stitches; if there is doubt about whether the threads will come loose, reinsert another needle along the full length of the abscess at the initial needle’s insertion point and secure both threads in four places; then cut open the abscess until excess fluid drains out, and remove any superfluous heart tissue while leaving what remains tied; finally apply a moist dressing made from wine and oil, and administer treatments using tents and ointments until it heals.
des apostemes des ners	abscesses of the nerves
Ausi com aposteme vienent en l’artere et en la voine, vienent aposteme as ners quant il sont ferut, ou par trop grant travail, et semblans choses.	Just as abscesses occur in the artery and vein, abscesses also occur in the nerves when they are injured, or from excessive labor, and similar things.
Et ceu avient plus sovent as adjutoires et as dois et en toz leus ou il ait jointures, et c’est I grief apostemes, et sa color semble la color dou cors, et est em plusors dispositions sens dolor; et quant on l’estraint forment, si sent li malaides dolor, et n’est mie em parfont dou cors, mais desoz lou keur; et muet bien de toutes pars, et ne va ne avant ne arrier, ne desoz ne desus, et celui qui est en jointures ne covient mie coper par fer: par aventure i vanroit contraction; et cil qui est ou chief ou ou front, fent le cuir au spatumile.	And this happens more often in the shoulders and elbows and at all places where there are joints, and these are severe abscesses, and their color resembles the color of the flesh, and they cause a great deal of pain; and when one presses them firmly, the patient feels pain, but it is not throughout the body, but rather near the heart; and it moves in no direction, neither forward nor backward, nor up or down, and those that are in joints must not be cut with an instrument: perhaps there would be a contraction; and for those that are on the head or forehead, make an incision in the skin with a spatula.
Se li apostemes est petis, si le tien a unes tenailles, et le cope en sa racine; et s’il est grans, si le sospent a l’oncine, et l’escorche, puis l’oste et assemble la plaie a la costure, et lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	If the abscess is small, hold it with pliers and cut it at its root; and if it is large, suspend it on a hook, then scrape it, remove it, and stitch up the wound until it heals.
des grosses boces pendans	large hanging mouths
Aucune fois avient en ventres et ne mie autre part thelul, et est une maladie qui est apelee «funge» par la semblance d’aus, et est li racine subtilz, et li chiez gros; et en i a de petis et de mout grans; et je vis I home qui en avoit II ou ventre qui estoient plus semblans a funges que ai autre chose, et n’i avoit point de difference, et estoient blanc, et avoient menue racine, et estoient jai fendut, et en corroit adés moistor.	Sometimes it occurs in the abdomen and nowhere else, and it is a disease called "fungus" due to its resemblance to such things, and the root is subtle, and the growths are large; there are small ones and very large ones; I saw a person who had two of these on their abdomen that were more like fungi than anything else, with no difference, they were white, had fine roots, and were jagged, and moisture corroded them quickly.
Je les copai et trovai en l’un XVIII onces pesant, et en l’autre VI З., et li ovraiges en l’incision si est que tu regardes se li malaides est moistes, et li color de l’artelul est blainche et moiste et de subtil racine; si le cope au spatumile large, et soient en ta presence li cautere au feu.	I weighed them and found one to be eighteen ounces heavy, and the other six, and in the work of cutting open it is that you observe if the patient is moist, and the color of the artery is white and moist and of fine texture; cut with a broad spatula, and have the fire cautery ready at hand.
Car au taillier vient maintes fois trop grans decorremens de sanc, et se li sans te vaint, si te haste donques dou cauterizer; et se tu vois le malaide espoanteit et paourous de l’incision dou fer, si prent I fil de plonc bien fait, et en lie l’artelul si com nos avons dit, et le laisse II jors; et puis le restraint, et ne cesser d’estraindre lou fil de plonc tant qu’il cope l’artelul, et chiece par lui sens travail; et se les racines sont grosses, si a paour au coper meismement por le ventre, mais tu em pues bien coper la moitiet, puis le cauterize qu’il ne reviegne; puis cure la plaie, et garde que tu ne coper le thelul qui est de fuxe color et de povre sens et de lait regart.	For when cutting there often comes excessive bleeding, and if the blood runs too freely, then hasten quickly to cauterize; and if you see the patient frightened and fearful of the iron incision, take a well-made linen thread, tie it around the artery as we have said, and leave it for two days; then remove it, but continue to press on the linen thread while cutting the artery, and proceed cautiously; and if the roots are thick, be cautious about cutting them entirely, but you can cut half of it, then cauterize so that it does not regrow; then treat the wound, and be careful not to cut the tendon which is red in color and of poor sensation and milk-like appearance.
Car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, et je venrai a la cure de chancre ci aprés.	For this is an embedded abscess, and I will come to the treatment of ulcers shortly thereafter.
quant li boude ist fuer	when the wound becomes hot
Se li apparance de la boude vient par cautere de plaie ou de fendure de syfac, et est sus le ventre et en ist aucuns des bouez, si com il avient en autres routures, ou de sanc qui cort de voines ou d’arteres selonc ceu qui est devant, ou de ventositeit; et se c’est par la routure dou syfac et par l’issue dou bouel, si est li color de l’aposteme semblans a la color dou cors, et est legiere chose sens dolor, et apert de diverse issue.	If the appearance of the wound comes from a cautery on a wound or tear on the surface, and it is on the abdomen and some boils appear there, as happens in other ruptures, whether from blood that flows from veins or arteries depending on what is before, or from gas; and if this is due to a rupture of the surface and an issue from the belly, then the color of the abscess resembles the color of the skin, it is a light matter without pain, and appears through various outlets.
Et se c’est por l’issue de l’intestine, adonques est il plus divers, et quant on le presse a ses dois si se repont, et puis revient, et par aventure si est sarrez, et agrandist mout a l’entree dou bain et por fort travail.	And if this is due to the issue from the intestine, then it becomes more diverse, and when one presses on both sides, it swells up, and then returns, and perhaps it is congested, and greatly enlarges at the entrance of the bath and for hard work.
Et se c’est por moistor, c’est legiere chose, et apert bien quant tu le presses a ta main, ne ne constraint mie; et se c’est por sanc, si apert par ces signes li apostemes gros et dur, et est fichiez selonc une quantiteit; et se c’est por ventositeit, si est souef au tochier, et li ovraiges si est que tu regarde se li apparance est por le sanc de l’artere, ou de la voine, ou ventositeit.	And if it is due to moisture, it is a light matter, and becomes clear when you press it with your hand, as it does not resist; and if it is due to blood, it becomes apparent through these signs of large and hard abscesses, which are fixed according to quantity; and if it is due to windiness, it is soft upon touch, and the work is that you observe whether the appearance is from arterial blood, or vein blood, or windiness.
Si covient que tu laisses la cure.	It is necessary that you leave the treatment.
Car il en a doutance et paor, si com je t’ai dit ou chapistre des apostemes, por l’artere et por la voine.	For there is doubt and fear about it, as I told you in the chapter on abscesses, regarding the artery and the vein.
Et se li apparance est por l’intestine ou lou boueil, si covient que tu comandes au malaide qu’il teigne son alaine, et soit estendus tout drois, puis seigne d’enche tout entor la boude; puis le comande a gesir sovin entre tes mains, puis va entor le leu que tu as signiet a tout le spatumile, puis estent la moitiet de l’aposteme au desus a tout le grant uncine; puis le lie entor d’un fil fort, ou d’une corde de fort soie fermement, et soit li nous dou liien assolz; puis oevre la moitiet de l’aposteme estendut sus le liien, et i boute ton doit indice, et quier l’intestine; se tu le trueves pris dou liien, si le deslie, et boute l’intestine au defuer dou ventre; et se tu trueves le boueil, si le prent a l’oncine, et en cope la superfluiteit; et se li artere te fait contraire, ou li voine, si vai belement entor, puis revien a ton ovraige et pren II aguilles, et i boute II fors filz, et boute les II aguilles entor ceu que tu as fait en crois que tu feis percier; puis estrain l’aposteme en IIII leus sus les aguilles, et se tu vues, oste les aguilles, et laisse lou leu tant qu’il porrisse, et chiece li char morte par soi; ou tu la cope quant elle iert subtiliie et porrie, puis le cure de ceu qu’il covient, et cheve l’aposteme si com nos avons dit; et estrai le sanc ou la moistor que tu trueves, puis cure le leu de ceu qu’il couvient, et soude le leu.	And if the appearance is from the intestine or the bladder, it is necessary that you instruct the patient to hold their breath, and lie completely straight, then make a full incision around the abscess; then command them to rest quietly between your hands, then work all around the place where you have marked for the entire spatumile, then extend half of the abscess above to the large uncinate forceps; then tie it all around with a strong thread or a firm silk cord; then work the half of the abscess extended on the thread, and put your index finger in, seek the intestine; if you find it caught by the thread, untie it, and push the intestine out of the belly; and if you find the bladder, take it with the forceps, and cut off the excess; and if the artery or vein opposes you, go gently around, then return to your work and take two needles, put two strands out, and place the two needles around where you have done piercing; then pull the abscess in four places over the needles, and if you wish, remove the needles, leaving the place until it rots, and cut off the dead flesh by itself; when it is fine and rotten, cut it away as we have said; then extract the blood or moisture that you find, cure the wound according to what is necessary, and close the wound.
dou chancre	of the ulcer/gangrene
Nos avons dit en la division les semblances de chancre, et coment on i doit ovrer par medicines, et coment on doit eschuer la cure de fer; et disons le chancre enjanreit en la marris, et grant cautele a en la cure, et dirent li ancien que quant chancres est en leu ou on le puet raier si com chancre qui est em mameles, et en la cuixe, et en semblans leus, et le doit tout oster quant il est en l’encomencement; et quant il est grans et anciens, si ne covient mie que tu l’aproches, car je n’en poi onques nul saner; ne nulz n’en sana onques devant moi.	We have said in the division about the likenesses of ulcers/gangrene, and how one should treat them with medicines, and how one should avoid treatment with iron; and we say that an ulcer/gangrene often arises from a boil, and there is great caution in its cure, and the ancients said that when ulcers are in places where they can be lanced such as those on breasts, and on the thigh, and in similar places, one should remove them entirely when they are in their beginning; but when they are large and old, it does not suit to approach them, for I have never seen any heal from them; nor have any ever healed before me.
Et li ovraiges, quant il est en leu ou on le puet oster, si com nos avons dit, est que tu purge aucune fois le malaide de cole noire; puis le fai sainier s’il ait manifeste repletion, puis afaite le malaide I boin leu por faire l’ovraige; puis giete tes oncines ou chancre, et le cheve de toutes pars, et l’oste de toutes pars sens rien laissier; et laisse corre le sanc tout fuer, et espreint bien le leu a ta main ou a aucune chose, et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire de l’incision de l’artere ou de la voine, si le cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the treatment, when it is in a place where it can be removed as we have said, is that you purge the patient of black bile at times; then make him fast if he has obvious overeating, then prepare the patient properly for the procedure; then apply your lancets to the ulcer/gangrene and remove all hair around it entirely without leaving anything behind; and let the blood flow freely until it stops on its own; then press the area well with your hand or some object, and if the bleeding from the wound is against the incision of an artery or vein, cauterize until the bleeding ceases; then treat further as necessary until he is healed.
de ydropisie	Of hydropsy
Nos avons jai dit en la division les semblances d’idropisie, et en queil maniere li assemblee de l’aigue est faite, et les signes de chescune semblance, et la cure qui est faite par medicines, et cele qui est curee par fer: si est eclites soulement; et ne doit on touchier de fer en ces II semblances: c’est a savoir, tympanites et yposarche, car c’est mortelz chose; donques quant tu medicines ceste semblance de ydropisie qui est apelee «eclites» de medicines, et li cure ne profite, si regarde se li malaides est foibles, ou s’il ait autre maladie que ydropisie, si com toust et solution de ventre et semblans choses; si n’i touchier de fer, car il i a doutance; et se tu vois le malaide de fort vertut, et il n’a autre maladie que ydropisie soulement, et il n’est mie trop jones ne trop vielz, si dois ensi ovrer: lieve le malaide droit sus tes mains, et li ministres presse le ventre em boutant l’aigue a la plus basse partie dou pis, puis pren le spatumile espinous selonc ceste forme:	We have already described in the division the similarities of hydropsy, and how the accumulation of water is formed, and the signs of each type, and the cure that is performed with medicine, and that which is cured by iron: only swelling is mentioned; one should not use iron on these two types: namely tympanites and yposarche, for it is a deadly practice. Therefore, when you treat this form of hydropsy called "swelling" with medicines, and the treatment does not help, check if the patient is weak, or if they have another illness besides hydropsy, such as coughing and abdominal discharge and similar conditions; do not use iron then, because there is doubt. And if you see that the patient is strong in constitution, and he has no other ailment but hydropsy alone, and he is neither too young nor too old, then proceed thus: lift the patient straight up into your hands, and let the attendants press on his belly to force out the water to the lower part of the hip, then take the spatumile according to this form:
Et soit trenchans de II pars.	And let there be cutting from two sides.
a pointe, et toutevoie ne soit mie si entrans qu’il puist venir jusc’a l’intestine quant on le fiche ens, et ne le puist blecier; puis regarde se li ydropisie est enjanree devers les intestines: si covient que tu fendes ensus de la boude III dois droit desoz sus lou poignil; et se li ydropisie est por la maladie dou foie, si soit ta fendure au senestre de la boude III dois; et se c’est por la miuce, si soit a destre, et ne covient mie que li malaides gise sus la fendure que les superfluitez ne corrent a celui foible leu; puis perce tout le cuir a l’estrument, et le boute, et lieve ta main a tout le spatumile entre le cuir et le syfac ausi com en escorchant a la quantiteit d’une ungle ou enqui entor; puis perce lou syfac tant que li spatumile viegne au leu vuit, et c’est li leus de l’aigue, puis le trai fuer, et i boute cest estrument de coi ci est li forme:	With a point and let it not enter so deeply that it can reach the intestines when inserted; then observe if the hydropsy is towards the intestines: you should cut three fingers above the pubis from below upwards on the left side; and if it is due to liver disease, cut on the left side of the pubis three fingers wide; and if it is because of mucus, cut on the right side; and let not the patient lie over the incision so that superfluities do not run to a weak spot; then perforate the skin with the instrument and apply it, lift your hand for all the spatumile between the skin and the tissue as much as in flaying about an inch around; then penetrate the tissue until the spatumile comes to the desired place, which is where the water is, then pull straight out, and insert this instrument of which here is the form:
Et est semblans a une caine d’argent subtil, et est d’arain ou d’archaut legier, et a en la partie desoz I petit pertus; et ou costeit d’une part, III pertus; et II d’autre part, et I d’autre; et est li chiés tailliez si com une penne, et c’est li forme de l’incision dont li escrivains taille la penne:	And it is similar to a thin silver chain, and it is made of copper or light brass, and has in the middle part one small hole; and on one side, three holes; and two on another side, and one on yet another; and the head is shaped like a feather quill, and this is the form of the incision that the writer makes when cutting the quill:
au chief desus est li alemele, si que quant li estrumens vient a l’aigue, si dessent maintenant sus l’estrument; vuide la donques la moitiet ou la tierce part, car se tu en vuides plus qu’il ne covient en celle houre, par aventure si muert li malaides por la resolution de son esperit de l’arme, ou il chiet paumez, ou il aproche a la mort; mais en vuide selonc la quantiteit de sa vertut, et selonc ceu que les dispositions de la vertut dou malaide signifient, et ses poulz; puis trai l’estrument et retien l’aigue, et elle est retenue maintenant por le keur qui estoupe le pertus qui est sus le syfac, de coi j’ai parleit, que tu perces selonc ceste maniere; puis rencomence l’estrument l’autre jor, se tu vois le malaide soffrant ceu, et trai de l’aigue une petite quantiteit; fai ce aucun jor, et te garde de foloier tant qu’il ni demore mais c’un poc d’aigue.	At the top is the alembic, so that when the instrument comes to the liquid, it now descends upon the instrument; empty then half or a third of it, for if you empty more than what is appropriate at that hour, perhaps the patient will die from the resolution of his spirit due to the weapon, or falls unconscious, or approaches death; but empty according to the quantity of its potency, and according to how the dispositions of the patient's vertu indicate, and his pulses; then draw the instrument and retain the liquid, and it is now retained by the heart that stops up the hole which is on the surface, about which I have spoken, that you pierce in this manner; then restart the instrument another day if you see the patient suffering from it, and draw off a small quantity of the liquid; do this for some days, and beware not to overdo it but leave just a little bit of the liquid.
Et se tu doutes sus le malaide, et tu i lais mout d’aigue, si le cure de la sepulture ou sablon chaut, et par mout sueir ou bain et au soleil, et se teigne de boivre; et le cure de medicines desiccatives tant qu’il soit sanez, et cauterize sus l’estomac et sus lou foie et sus l’esplen aprés l’estraction de l’aigue, si com j’ai dit devant.	And if you doubt about the patient, and leave much moisture, then treat with the grave or hot sand, and by much sweating or bathing in the sun, and have them abstain from drinking; and treat with drying medicines until he is healthy, and cauterize on the stomach and liver and spleen after extracting the moisture, as I said before.
de l’estopement de la verge	about the numbness of the penis
Aucune fois naissent enfant qui n’ont point de pertus en la verge, ou li pertus est petis, ou il n’est mie en son leu.	Sometimes children are born who have no opening in the penis, or the opening is small, or it is not in its proper place.
Si le covient tantost qu’il n’aist percier a tout I spatumile molt subtil selonc ceste forme:	It is necessary to pierce it immediately with a very fine spatula according to this form:
puis met ou pertus I clo subtil de plonc, et le lie et le tien ensi III jors ou IIII et quant il vuet faire urine, si soit ostez li clos, et faice urine, et puis li remet; et par aventure nen i couvient point, car li urine qui vient fuer ne lou laisse close.	Then place a fine cloth over the opening and keep it there for three or four days, and when he wishes to urinate, remove the cloth, allow him to urinate, and then replace it; and perhaps it may not be necessary, because the urine that comes out does not leave the cloth closed.
Cil de cui li pertus est petis, si est medicinez dou clo de plonc, si com nos avons dit, si s’eslargera.	He whose opening is small should be treated with the cloth of flax as we have said, and it will enlarge.
Cil qui n’ont mie le pertus en lor leu sont bleciet, car aucun naissent qui ont le pertus au chief de la verge, por coi il ne puient pissier avant s’il ne lievent lor verge en haut; et ne pueent enjanrer por ceu que li matiere ne puet venir jusc’a la marris, et c’est une male maladie.	Those who do not have the opening in its place are afflicted, for some are born with the opening at the head of the penis, so they cannot urinate unless they lift their penis upwards; and they cannot copulate because the matter cannot reach the testicles, and this is a serious illness.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos, puies estent le chief de la verge et le cope ausi com la taille d’une penne, si ke li pertus chiece em mileu, si com il covient; et te garde de decorrement de sanc qui i vient maintes fois, et s’il avient, si l’estainche de ceu qui estainche sanc, et cure la plaie tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the manner of the work is that the patient lies supine on his back, then place the rod under the head and as with the width of a pen’s feather, so that the hole fits exactly in the middle, as it should; and be wary of blood loss which happens often, and if it occurs, stop it with what stops blood, and treat the wound until he is healed.
des pustules de la verge	pimples on the penis
Maintes fois vienent cist albathe en la verge, et est une apparance de char laide; et en i a malignes et non malignes; si covient que tu les preignes a I oncine subtil, et les cope et munde toutes, puis met sus coton moilliet en oignement egiptien; puis le cure d’oignement diafinicon tant qu’il soit sanez.	Many times these blisters appear on the penis, and it is an unpleasant appearance of flesh; and there are both malignant and non-malignant ones; you must pierce them with a fine lancet, and clean and treat them all, then apply cotton soaked in Egyptian ointment; then cure them with diafinicon ointment until he is healed.
Et se li albathe est maligne, de pute color et depuant, si covient que tu i amenistres cautere.	And if the ulcer is malignant, of putrid color and foul-smelling, then you must apply a cautery to it.
Quant tu l’as copeit, et se li albathe est en som la verge, et en ait partie dedens la peil et partie defuer, si covient que tu oste l’albathe qui est dedens premier; et quant il est soudez, si le cure defuer.	When you have cut it, and if the ulcer is deep within the flesh, with part inside the skin and part outside, then you must remove the part of the ulcer that is inside first; and when it is adhered, treat what is outside.
Car quant tu le cures ensamble, si n’est mie asseurez li chiez de la verge qu’il ne soit perciez, et vient noiror et corruption en son la verge et ou coion; si covient chever tout ceu qui est noir et corrumput, puis lie sus l’emplaustre de miel et de farine qui soit fait d’escorce de poumes grenates et de veces, puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	For when you treat it all at once, the flesh of the ulcer is not secure and may be perforated, leading to blackening and corruption in the ulcer and the testicle; you must excise everything that is black and corrupted, then apply a plaster made from pomegranate rind and flax, then continue treating it with other methods until it is healed.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si amenistre le cautere lunaire selonc ceste forme:	And if bleeding occurs, then treat with a lunar cautery according to this form:
Li cauteres si aide as II dispositions ensamble: c’est asavoir, au decorrement de sanc, et a la corruption; et se li chiés de la verge est corrumpus et retrais, si covient que tu boutes ou conduit de la verge une cainne de plonc, et pisse li malaides parmi; et quant li pelz iert aerse au chief de la verge qui avient a ces qui n’ont mie esteit circoncis, ou il avient por plaie ou por aposteme, si covient donques que tu l’escorches a I estrument cheveit, tant que li liiens soit desliiez, et soit delivrez li chiez de la verge de toutes pars; et se c’est grief chose de deviser ceu, si covient que tu l’escorches a I spatumile aucun poc dou chief de la verge et de la peil; puis dessevre belement entre II, et i met I subtil drapeil de lin moilliet an aigue froide, qu’il n’aerse derechief.	The cautery helps with two conditions simultaneously: namely, bleeding and corruption; and if the head of the penis is corrupted and retracted, then it is necessary to insert a tube of lead into its conduit, through which the patient urinates; and when hair grows at the head of the penis, which happens in those who have not been circumcised, whether due to injury or abscess, then you must burn it with an instrument that has a sharp tip until the ligament is loosened, and release the head of the penis completely from all sides; and if it is difficult to describe this, then you should burn it slightly at the top of the penis and skin with a spatula, then gently separate them, and place a fine piece of moist linen cloth in cold water between them so that it does not grow again.
de la circoncision	Of circumcision
Circoncision n’est mie desliemens de continuation si com les autres plaies; toutevoie quant nos faison ceste oevre de nostre volenteit, et proprement as enfans, si est mestier que nos faisiens la millor oevre, et la plus legiere a salut.	Circumcision is not like the separation of continuity as other wounds are; nevertheless, when we perform this work by our will, and especially on children, it is necessary that we do the best work, and the least painful for safety.
Je dis que li ancien ne dirent mie la circoncision de lor enfans, car il n’en usent mie en lor loi, et n’en avons mais que ceu que nos avons aquis par experiment.	I say that the ancients did not speak of circumcision for their children, because they did not practice it in their law, and we have only what we have acquired through experience.
Car j’ai veut la plus grant partie des maistres et des sainors qui faisoient circumcision entor I dal, et as forces, et a tout une novacule; si fuioit li keurs car il i a II toiles, et par aventure si cope on celi desus et demore celle desoz.	For I have seen the majority of masters and seniors who performed circumcision around the glans, and forcefully, and in one swift action; it was dangerous because there are two layers, and perhaps they cut through the outer layer but left the inner.
Or la recovient coper, et est li dolor double, et a la mundification qui est dou dal n’est mie asseuree li pointe dou membre; et a la mundification de l’ungle par aventure eschaipe li fer, et corront l’uevre, et maintes fois naissent ensi qu’il n’ont mestier de mundification et je l’ai veut.	Now it must be cut back again, and the pain is doubled, and in the cleaning of the wound that is deep there is no certainty about the tip of the limb; and when cleaning under a nail by chance the tool may slip, and ruin the work, and many times they arise such that they do not need cleansing and I have seen this.
De la mondification qui est faite as forces a tout le liien de fil ai je troveit la bonteit de l’experiment, car les forces taillent justement ausi bien desus com desoz.	Of the cleansing that is done with force to the entire limb of thread I have found the goodness of the experiment, for the force cuts precisely both above and below.
Car quant tu presses ta main, si tailles igalment en I tout soul tens; mais que li filz soit bien estrois entor lou cuir; et soit li maniere dou premier ovraige si est que tu faices penser l’enfant, s’il entent, que tu ne li fais fuer que liier le fil entor la verge tant soulement, et pues le fai esjoir en toutes les manieres que tu pues; puis le fai ester entre tes mains tout droit, et repont les forces entre tes mains ou desoz tes piez que li enfes ne les voie, ne aucun des estrumens; puis boute ta main a la verge et souffle ou keur, et la trai en haut tant que li chiés de la verge soit ens; puis la mundifie bien de l’ordure qui i est assemblee, puis lie le leu signiet d’un fil double, puis la lie desoz I poc a I autre liien; et la tien as II dois par la seconde lieeure au pouchet et au doit indice, et cope entre les II liiens, puis lieve le keur desus hastanment et trai le chief de la verge; puis laisse corre le sanc poc et poc, car c’est li muedres; et met poudre sus et sus la poudre I drapeil glueit d’un moieuf d’uef cuit destempreit d’aigue rose, confit avec oile roset boin et fres, et lou laisse sus jusc’a l’autre jor, et le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	For when you press your hand, cut equally in one single motion; but ensure the thread is tight around the skin. The method of the first procedure should be such that if the child understands, he thinks you are only tying the thread around the shaft merely for fun; then make him laugh and enjoy in all ways possible; then hold his hands straight between yours, and move your hands or feet with force where the child cannot see, nor any instruments; then bring your hand to the shaft and blow on it, and pull it upwards until the head of the shaft is embedded; then clean thoroughly of any accumulated debris, then tie a double knot at that spot, then secure below the pouch and at the second index; cut between the two threads, then lift the bloodletting area quickly and pull the head of the shaft; then let the blood flow drop by drop, for this is the safest method; place powder upon it and over the powder place a small piece of cloth glued with a beaten egg yolk mixed with rose water, preserved with good fresh oil of roses, and leave it there until the next day, and treat it in another way until it is healed.
Li forme des forces a la mundification si est ceste: li dui chiés soient tenves et soient trenchans, et soient li chiés ausi grant com li mainche igalment:	The form of the instruments for cleansing is thus: the two heads should be blunt and should have cutting edges, and the heads as large as the handle evenly.
li error de la mundification si est quant li keurs dedens fuit a l’incision; donques il covient que tu l’estendes a ton ungle, ainsois que li leus faice aposteme; et le cope igalment, et se tu ne lou pues tenir a ton ungle, si le tien as tenailles, et puis le cope.	The error in cleansing is when the pus inside goes to the incision; then it is necessary that you extend it to your nail, just as one would an abscessed boil; and cut it evenly, and if you cannot hold it to your nail, then hold it with forceps, and then cut it.
Et s’il trespassent III jors, et ceu qui est desoz la verge est enflez, si le laisse tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et l’escorche legierement; si le cope si com tu pues mues, et te garde de la partie de la verge, ce ne li nuira niant.	And if they pass three days, and that which is below the shaft is swollen, leave it until the abscess is sufficiently abated, and gently scrape the skin; then cut as you can move it, and be careful of the part of the shaft, so it does no harm.
Cure donques le leu de choses soudans plaie de poudre, que nos avons dit ou traitier des poudres, et s’on cope dou keur outre mesure, et il va au desus, si ne nuira point; cure le donques, si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Treat then the site of things with powder for wounds, as we have said in the chapter on powders, and if one cuts into the heart too much, and it goes beyond measure, it will not harm; treat it then as we have said until he is healed.
dou retenement de l’urine	from the retention of urine
Li retenue de l’urine si est d’opilation de piere, ou de sanc congeleit, ou de bowe, ou de char nee, ou de semblans choses, que nos avons dit en la division; et se li urine n’est desliie , et tu vois estre la retenue por la piere qui est jai ou col de la vessie, si covient que li malaides soit corbés sus ses genoulz; et li soient mis li piez sor le dos, et estende son ventre de la partie desus lou dos, et restraigne li malaides s’alainne tant com il puet; et adonques est constrains li colz de la vessie a l’expression de la piere au desus, por coi li urine est desliie e; et s’elle ne vient, si com nos avons dit, et li malaides sent grant dolor, si covient que tu i aministres extraction a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «siringue», de coi ci est li forme: et soit d’argent subtilz legiere chevee, si com li penne d’un oiseil; et soit li caine d’une palme de lonc et demie, et soit subtilz au chief.	The retention of urine is due to the obstruction by a stone, or congealed blood, or pus, or dead tissue, or similar things, as we have mentioned in the division; and if the urine does not flow freely, and you see that the retention is because of a stone which is lodged at the neck of the bladder, then it is necessary for the patient to be seated on his knees; and place his feet on his back, and extend his belly from above the back, and have the patient pull his thighs as much as he can; and thus the neck of the bladder is constrained to express the stone upwards, which makes the urine flow freely; and if it does not come out, as we said, and the patient feels great pain, then you must administer extraction with all the instruments called "syringe," here is its form: it should be made of fine light silver, like a feather of an eagle; and let the tube be one palm in length and half, and let it be fine at the tip.
Et li maniere de l’issue de l’urine si est que tu pren I fil double, et lie au chief I poc de laine ou de couton, et boute le chief dou fil dedens la siringue; et cope la superfluiteit de la lainne et le boute jusc’au chief de la siringue, puis oint la siringue d’oile ou de burre et d’aubin d’uef, et fai seoir le malaide sus I siege, et li arose la vessie et la verge d’oile moiste et d’oile d’olive et d’aigue tede; puis met legierement la siringue en la verge, tant qu’elle viegne a la racine de la verge, puis double la verge desus devers la boude; puis boute la siringue avant jusc’a la vessie, et la sente li malaides venir jusc’a la chose vuide, et ceu n’est mie fait selonc cest ordre fuer que por ceu que li conduis ou elle vait est tors; puis estent le fil a tout la laine poc et poc, et li urine en suit la laine, puis l’estrai fuer, et fai corre l’urine; et rencomence la siringue tant que li vessie soit vuidie, et soit aligiez li malaides.	And the method for urination is that you take double thread and tie at the top a piece of wool or cotton, and put the end of the thread inside the syringe; then cut the excess wool and push it up to the top of the syringe, then smear the syringe with oil or butter and egg yolk alum; then have the patient sit on a chair, and massage the bladder and penis with moist olive oil and cold water; then gently insert the syringe into the penis until it reaches the base of the penis, then bend the penis upwards towards the body; then push the syringe forward up to the bladder, and feel the patient’s urine coming out until it reaches the empty place, and this is not done according to this order unless for what leads where it goes wrong; then stretch the thread all the way through the pieces of wool piece by piece, and the urine follows the wool, then pull it out firmly, and let the urine flow; and repeat with the syringe until the bladder is empty, and relieve the patient.
des maladies de la vessie	diseases of the bladder
Quant escorcheures ou sanc vient en la vessie, ou porriture i est assemblee, et tu i vues distiller aigues et medicines, si fai a tout l’estrument qui est apellé «clepsedre», et c’est li forme:	When pus or blood comes to the bladder, and putrefaction is assembled there, and you wish to introduce liquids and medicines, use all the instruments which are called "clepsydre," and this is its form:
Elle est close, et si a III pertus: II d’une part, et I d’autre, si com tu vois; et li leus chevez par coi li medicine cort soit telz qu’il estoupe bien la verge sens adition, si c’on em puisse traire la moistor, et bouter quant mestier est; et quant tu vues giter tes medicines en la vessie, met le chief dou keusteur en la moistor, et trai au traiant qui est ens; si trairas la moistor au kesteur, et puis reboute fort le traiant ens; si entrera li moistors ens, et venra a la vessie maintenant, si que li malaides la sentira; et c’est li forme dou clistere subtil dont on clisterize la vessie: si est ci:	It is closed and has III openings: II from one side, and I from the other, as you see; and the place where the medicine comes out should be such that it stops up well the tube without addition, so that no moisture can come out, and pour in when necessary; and when you wish to introduce your medicines into the bladder, put the head of the catheter in the moisture, and draw with the drawer which is inside; thus, you will draw the moisture to the catheter, and then push firmly the drawer back in; thereby, the moisture will enter inside and reach the bladder now, so that the patient feels it; and this is the form of the subtle enema with which one irrigates the bladder: here it is:
Et est d’argent ou d’archaut, et est li chiés plus haut; et desoz a I sein ou li liiens chiet; puis pren une vessie de mouton et i met la moistor dont tu vues clisterizer la vessie, puis la lie entre les II seins forment d’un boin fil double, et chaufe I poc celle moistor sus le feu; puis boute le chief dou clistere en la verge, puis estrain ta main sus la vessie a tout la moistor avenanment, tant que li malaides sente que celle moistor est jai venue a la vessie; et se tu n’as la vessie, si pren une piece de parchemin, et en fai I cercle, et le perce rondement entor; puis boute I fil fort en ces pertus, puis assemble le cercle si com on assemble I dal, et met dedens ceu que tu vues d’oile et de moistor et d’aigue, et le lie en l’estrument; et fai si com tu as fait de la vessie, de presser a ta main tant que li moistor veigne a la vessie.	And it is of silver or brass, and the head is higher; and behind the chest where the string hangs; then take a sheep's bladder and put in the water with which you wish to enema the bladder, then tie between the two breasts firmly with a strong double thread, and heat the pot of this water over the fire; then put the head of the enema into the tube, then squeeze your hand on the bladder gradually until the patient feels that the water has come to the bladder; and if you do not have the bladder, take a piece of parchment, and make a circle, and pierce it roundly around; then insert the string tightly in these holes, then join the circle as one joins a tile, and put inside what you wish of oil and water and liquid, and tie it to the instrument; and do as you did with the bladder, squeezing your hand until the water comes to the bladder.
de la piere	of the stone
Nos avons jai dit en la division les manieres de piere, et l’estraction ensamble medicines; et ai dit la difference entre la piere enjanree as rains, et toz les signes, et en queil piere on doit ovrer de taille; et en la vessie, et en la verge; et je le vos dirai apertement et briément.	We have already discussed in the division the methods of stones and their extraction along with medicines; and I have stated the difference between a stone formed in the kidneys, and all the signs, and when one should operate on a stone; and in the bladder, and in the penis; and I will tell you openly and briefly.
Je dis que li piere qui est enjanree en la vessie si avient plus sovent as enfans, et c’est signe que li aigue saut de la vessie semblans a aigue en sa subtiliteit; et i apert harene, et graite li malaides sa verge, et li pent maintes fois, et puis enroidist; et a mout de ces saut li fondemens; et est legiere li sanation des enfans jusqu’il ont IIII ans, et est mout grief en viellars, et est as jones moiene, a ces qui sont entre jonesce et viellece; et est li cure plus legiere de ces qui ont la piere grans, que de ces qui l’ont petite.	I say that the stone which is formed in the bladder happens more often to children, and this is a sign that the urine jumps from the bladder similar to acute conditions; and one can see hairiness, and the patient's penis becomes irritated, and he suffers many times, and then it reddens; and much of these jumps lead to foundational issues; and healing for children until they are four years old is easier, but it is very difficult in older people, and for young adults it is moderate, those who are between youth and old age; and the treatment for those with large stones is lighter than for those with small ones.
Et quant nos venons a la cure, si couvient premier mundifier le malaide per clistere, por traire tout le fiens qui est as intestines.	And when we come to the treatment, it is necessary first to purify the patient with an enema, to draw out all the feces that are in the intestines.
Car il encombre aucune fois a querir la piere.	For it sometimes obstructs in seeking to remove the stone.
Puis prenez le malaide par les piez, et lou deboutez et movez au desoz, si que li piere dessende au parfont de la vessie, et saille aucune fois dou leu haut; puis le fai seoir entre tes mains appareilliet, et ses mains soient desoz ses cuisses, si que li vessie soit toute declinans aval; puis la quier et la touche dedens; se tu sens la piere en l’espaice, si te haste maintenant de taillier sus la piere.	Then take the patient by the feet and raise him up and move him back so that the stone descends to the bottom of the bladder, and sometimes comes from a high place; then make him sit between your hands prepared, and his hands should be behind his thighs so that the bladder is fully inclined downward; then seek it and touch inside; if you feel the stone in the space, now quickly cut into the stone.
Et s’elle ne chiet au touchier dou tout, si moille ton doi indice d’oile de la main senestre, se li malaides est enfes, ou ton doi moien, se li malaides est jovencelz acomplis; et le boute en son fondement, et quier la piere, et quant tu la sens a ton doi, si l’amoine au col de la vessie; puis presse sus a ton doi, et la boute au defuer lai ou tu vues taillier.	And if it does not fall when touched entirely, moisten your index finger with oil from the left hand, if the patient is male, or your middle finger, if the patient is a fully grown female; and insert it into his/her anus, and seek the stone, and when you feel it with your finger, push it to the neck of the bladder; then press on your finger, and bring it out where you wish to cut.
Et comande au ministre qu’il presse la vessie a sa main, et li comande qu’il estende a sa main destre les coions en haut, et a sa main senestre oste le cuir qui est desoz les coions en la partie ou on fait la taille; puis i boute le spatumile copant, de coi ce est li forme:	And instruct the assistant to press the bladder with their hand, and command them to extend their right hand over the testicles, and with their left hand remove the skin which is underneath the testicles in the part where one makes an incision; then place the spatula cutting, of which this is the form:
Et fent entre ceu qui est entre les coions et le fondement, ne mie em mileu mais au costeit de la naige senestre; et soit drois sus la piere, et tes dois soit adés ou fondement, et soit li taille dou traver si qu’ele soit large par defuer, et dedens estroite, selonc la quantiteit de la piere, ne mie trop grans; par aventure la presse si li dois qui est ou fondement, qu’elle saut fuer sens travail; et saiches qu’il i a teil piere ou il a angles, et marges: si est griés a issir; et si a teil qui est souez, semblans a une glant, et reonde, dont li issue est legiere.	And make an incision between the testicles and the anus, not in the middle but on the side of the left thigh; and it should be straight over the stone, and its ends should be close to the anus, and the cut should be wide at the top and narrow inside according to the size of the stone, so that pressing does not cause the lower part near the anus to jump out without effort; and know that there are some stones with angles and edges: it is difficult to remove; and there are those that lie deep, like a clover leaf, round, whose exit is easy.
A celi donques ou il a angles et marge, fai la taille plus grant; et s’elle ne saut, si covient que tu estraignes sus as tenailles qui sont ausi com une lime au chief, por mues estraindre la piere si qu’elle n’eschaipe; ou tu boute desoz li I estrument subtil corbé au chief; et se tu ne la pues engignier ensi, si eslarge I poc lou pertus, et se li sans decort, si l’estrainche de vitriole; et s’il i a plus d’une piere, si boute premier la plus grant au col de la vessie, puis cope sus, puis le trai fuer, et les petites aprés s’il en i a plusors.	For those who have corners and margins, make the incision larger; and if it does not work, you must hold with pliers that are like a file at the top to grip the stone so that it does not escape; or place below the instrument curved at the top; and if you cannot manage it thus, enlarge the hole slightly, and if blood comes out, seal it with vitriol; and if there is more than one stone, first push the largest into the bladder neck, then cut above, then pull it out forcefully, and the smaller ones afterward if there are several.
Et s’elle est mout grans, si la covient soier, et faire plus grant plaie.	And if it is very large, you must observe it and make a larger incision.
Car II choses avienent au malaide: ou il muert, ou li urine vient adés par lai que li leus ne puet souder; mais toutevoie t’efforce dou traire, ou dou debrisier as tenailles, tant que tu la traies par pieces; et quant tu as acomplit ton oevre, si emple la plaie d’encens et d’aloe et de sanc de dragon, et l’estraint, et met par sus I drapeil moilliet en oile et en vin, ou en oile et en aigue rose et aigue froide, por apaisier l’aposteme chaut; puis resovine le malaide sus son col, et ne desliier lou lien jusc’au tier jor.	For two things happen to the patient: either he dies, or urine comes out immediately where the flesh cannot heal; but still try hard to pull it out, or use pliers to remove it piece by piece; and when you have completed your work, apply the wound with frankincense, aloes, and dragon's blood, then bandage it tightly with a moist cloth in oil and wine, or oil and rose water and cold water, to soothe the hot abscess; then lift the patient onto his shoulder, and do not loosen the binding until the third day.
Et quant tu le desliies, si arose mout bien lou leu d’oile et d’aigue, puis le cure d’oignement dyafinicon et d’oignement basilicon, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you release it, wash the area thoroughly with oil and water, then treat it with diafinicon ointment and basilicon ointment until it is healed.
Et se apostemes chaus vient en la plaie et corrosions, et congelemens de sanc en la vessie, et soit par ceu retenue li urine, qui est conue en teil maniere que sans saut avec l’urine: boutes donques ton doi en la plaie, et estrai celui sanc, car s’il i remaint, si corront la vessie, et la porrit; puis leve la plaie d’aigue et d’aisil et de seil, et li aide en toutes les manieres que tu seis, tant qu’il soit sanez; et covient que toutes les oures que tu le cures, que tu li lie les II cuisses, et assemble les medicines sus le leu.	And if abscesses and corrosions come in the wound, and coagulation of blood in the bladder, which causes retention of urine, known to occur in such a manner that without urination: pour then your hand into the wound and extract the blood, for if it remains there, it will corrupt the bladder; then cleanse the wound with water and herbs and wool, and assist it in all ways you know until it is healed; and it is necessary that every time you treat him, you tie his two thighs together, and apply the medicines to the area.
Et se li piere est petite, et ele est ou conduit de la verge, et fichie ens, et li urine ne puet issir; si le cure de ceu que je dis ainsois, que tu lou tailles maintes fois, est on escusez de la taille per ceste cure.	And if the stone is small, and it is in the channel of the penis, and lodged there, and the urine cannot pass; then treat this as I say thus, that you cut it many times, for this treatment excuses the cutting.
Je ai ja ce proveit ensi.	I have already tested this in this way.
Pren I foret de fer selonc ceste forme et soit a III angles fichiees en I tison:	Take an iron fork according to this form and have three prongs fixed in one handle:
puis pren I fil et lou lie entor la verge desoz la piere, si qu’ele ne puist venir arrier en la vessie; puis boute le foret en la verge legierement, tant qu’il viegne a la piere; et torne le foret a ta main en la piere poc et poc, tant que tu puisses percier la piere d’autre part; si venra tantost li urine, puis presse ta main sus ceu qui est demorez de la piere qui est dedens la verge.	Then take some thread and tie it around the penis below the stone, so that it cannot move back into the bladder; then gently insert the fork into the penis until it reaches the stone; and turn the fork with your hand on the stone little by little, until you can pierce the stone from the other side; then the urine will come forth soon, and press your hand on what remains of the stone that is inside the penis.
Si est tantost brisie, et saut fuer avec l’urine, et est garis li malaides; et se tu ne pues ce faire por aucune chose qui le deffent, si lie I fil desoz la piere et I autre desus, puis fent la verge endroit la piere entre les II liiens, puis l’estrai fuer, et deslie lou liien, et mundifie lou sanc congeleit qui est en la plaie; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	It is broken at once, and the urine comes forth with it, and the patient is cured; and if you cannot do this for some reason that prevents it, tie a thread below the stone and another above, then cut the penis directly through the stone between the two threads, then extract the urine, and untie the thread, and clean the congealed blood which is in the wound; and treat it until it is healed.
de la piere des femmes	of women's stones (referring to kidney stones or similar conditions)
Poc avient que piere soit enjanree en femmes, et s’il avient aucune fois, si est li cure grief, et est deffendut por III choses: l’une est que per aventure li femme est vierge; et li seconde est c’on ne puet trover femme bien saichant qui se descuevre as mires, meismement quant elle est caste.	It rarely happens that a stone forms in women, and when it does occur, the treatment is difficult, and it is forbidden for three reasons: one is that perhaps the woman is a virgin; and the second is that one cannot find a knowledgeable woman who will expose herself to doctors, especially if she is chaste.
Et li tierce maniere si est que par aventure on ne puet trover femme bien saichant en cest art de mains; et li quarte maniere si est que li piere de la femme si est plus em parfont que li piere de l’ome, por coi il i couvient faire plus parfonde taille, et grant paour i a. Et se necessitez semont a ceu, si covient que tu preignes une mieresse bien sachant, et a poines la trueve on, et se tu n’en trueves, point si quier I caste mire subtil; et li presente une baile bien saige en la vie des femmes, ou une femme qui saiche une partie de l’art, et li comande qu’ele faice ceu que tu li comandes de l’inquisicion de la piere; et regarde mout bien se li femme est vierge: adonques li covient bouter son doit ou fondement et querir la piere; et s’ele la trueve, si la constraigne desoz son doit, et li recomande qu’elle boute son doit ou con la malaide, et quiere et presse sa main senestre sus la vessie forment.	And the third manner is that by chance one cannot find a woman well knowing in this art of hands; and the fourth manner is that the stone of the woman is more emparfount than the stone of the man, why it behooves to make a deeper cut, and great fear there is. And if necessity mounts on thee, then it behooves that thou takest a midwife well knowing, and at pains one finds her, and if thou findest none, by no means seek a cunning leech; and the present one an honest woman in the life of women, or a woman who knows part of the art, and commandeth that she doth that which thou committest to her of the inquiry of the stone; and look well whether the woman is a virgin: then it behooves her to put her hand into the fundament and seek out the stone; and if she findeth it, then constraineth it beneath her hand, and commandeth that she putteth her hand in where the patient doth have pain, and seeketh and presseth her left hand on the bladder forcibly.
S’elle la trueve, si covient qu’elle la mueve de greit en greit des l’entree de la vessie jusque desoz, tant qu’elle viegne a la racine de la cuisse; puis cope sus la piere en la racine de la cuisse encontre le mileu dou con, lai ou il est mues apparilliet, et sent la piere en celle partie; et ne mueve son doi desus la piere ou desoz, et soit li taille au premier petite; puis boute lou rait en la taille, se tu sens la piere si acroi la plaie tant que li piere puisse issir fuer, et saiches que maintes manieres de pieres sont: c’est a savoir, petites et grans et aspres et souez, longes et reondes, et qui ont rains.	If she finds it, she must move it gradually from the entrance of the bladder down until she reaches the root of the thigh; then cut around the stone at the root of the thigh opposite the midpoint of the anus, where the stone is located and feel the stone in that area; and do not move her thumb above or below the stone, and make the incision initially small; then insert the probe into the incision, if you feel the stone enlarge the wound until the stone can come out; and know that there are many types of stones: namely small and large and rough and smooth, long and round, and those with edges.
si saiches les semblances por savoir l’issue.	and know the signs to understand the outcome.
Et se li sans te vaint, si met au leu vitriole broiet, et li tien une houre tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis revien a ton ovraige, tant que li piere soit fuer, et aies des estrumens que je t’ai dit en l’estraction de la piere as homes por toi aidier en ton oevre; et se li sans te vaint, et c’est de l’artere qui est copee, si met la poudre sus le leu et l’estrain de tentes et de bendelz, et ne rencomencier plus ceu, et laisse la piere et ne la traire mie, que par aventure morroit li malaide; puis cure la plaie.	And if the blood flows from there, apply powdered vitriol to the area and keep it for an hour until the bleeding stops; then return to your work until the stone is out, and have the instruments that I told you about for extracting stones from people to assist you in your work; and if the blood flows again, and this is from an artery that has been cut, apply powder of tents and bendelz to the site, do not restart the procedure, and leave the stone where it is without trying to remove it, as the patient might die; then treat the wound.
Et quant li chalor dou sanc est apaisie, et li leus porrist, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que li piere soit fuer.	And when the heat of the blood is appeased, and the swelling subsides, then return to your work, until the stone is expelled.
de hernie carnouse	of flesh hernia
Ramice aquouse n’est autre chose que assemblee de moistor ou blanc syfac, qui est desoz lou keur des coions, que contient l’uef; et est apelez «syfac», et aucune fois est proprement en la toile de l’uef, si c’on cuide que ce soit I autre oef; et c’est li cuir dou coion entre lou blanc syfac que nos avons dit; et ceu n’avient se poc non.	Aqueous retention is nothing other than a collection of moisture or white matter, which is separated from the heart of the testicle, containing the egg; and it is called "white matter," and sometimes it is properly within the membrane of the egg, so one thinks that it might be another egg; and this occurs in the skin of the testicle between the white matter we have mentioned; and this does not occur without pain.
Et li generation de cest ramice si est de foibleteit que vient as coions, et est espandue celle matiere.	And the formation of this aqueous retention is due to weakness that affects the testicles, and this matter spreads out.
Et aucune fois si vient de percussion sus les coions, et ceste moistor si a maintes colors: ou c’est color declinans a jaunice, ou c’est sans rouge, ou noir, ou aquous blans, et ce avient plus; et ce sont li signe de conoistre ceste assemblee, car s’elle est ou blanc syfac que nos avons dit, si est li apostemes reons, I poc lonc si com li figure d’un oef, et n’apert mie li coions, car il a moistor tout entor.	And sometimes it comes from percussion on the testicles, and this moisture has many colors: where its color declines to yellow, or it is without redness, or black, or aqueous white, and these things happen more; and these are the signs of recognizing this assembly, for if it is in the white pus we have mentioned, then the abscesses are numerous, I put long as the shape of an egg, and does not reveal the testicles, for it has moisture all around.
Et s’il a moistor en la propre toile, si est li apostemes reons avec une partie de l’uef, et por ceu pense on que c’est uns autres oef; et se li moistor est entre le cuir des coions et le blanc syfac, si le sent om bien; donques quant tu vues savoir la color de la moistor, si esprueve a tout l’intromissoire quarreit, de coi li forme est ci devant.	And if there is moisture in the proper tissue, then the abscesses are numerous with part of an egg, and for this reason one thinks it is another egg; and if the moisture is between the skin of the testicles and the white pus, then one can feel it well; therefore when you wish to know the color of the moisture, then try throughout the entire interspace, whose form is as described before.
Selonc ceu donques qui vient aprés l’intromissoire, juge de ceu qui est dedens.	According to what follows after the introduction, judge what is within.
Et quant nos la curons par fer, si covient que li malaides soit sainiez selonc som pooir et la repletion de son cors; puis le sovine sus son dos, sus une chose un poc haute, et met desoz lui mout de drapelz; puis sié sus sa senestre, et comande au ministre qu’il sié a destre, et estende la verge a l’un des II costelz dou keur des coions; puis pren le spatumile leit, et cope le cuir des coions parmi leu dou lonc jusque delez lou poignil, et soit ta fendure toute droite en devisant le cuir des coions jusc’a syfac blanc, et l’escorche subtilment selonc tom pooir; puis perce lou syfac plain d’aigue a I large pertus, et estrai toute l’aigue, et puis met tes oncines, et estent lou syfac amont; et ne touchier le keur des coions, mais que le syfac soulement; cope tout ou par pieces meismement le costeit de lui subtil, que se tu ne le copes bien saigement, si revenra li aigue; et se l’uef saut fuer a ton oevre, si le ramoinne en son leu quant tu avras acomplit l’uevre dou syfac; puis assemble les II leivres dou keur des coions a une costure, puis le cure si com les autres plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when we treat it with iron, the patient must be restrained as much as possible and according to the fullness of his body; then lay him on his back on something slightly raised, and put many cloths under him; then sit on his left side, and instruct the assistant to sit on the right, and extend the rod along one of the two ribs near the groin; then take the heated spatula and cut through the skin over the area from front to back until you reach the white membrane, cutting it all straight without damaging the underlying tissue; then pierce the membrane full of fluid with a wide opening, and remove all the liquid, then apply your forceps carefully, stretching out the membrane upwards; do not touch the organ itself, but only work on the membrane; cut through everything carefully in pieces, so if you don’t cut properly, the fluid will return; if the organ jumps during your work, gently put it back into place once you have completed the operation on the membrane; then sew together the two sides of the organ with a suture, and care for it as other wounds until it is healed.
Et se tu trueves l’uef corromput d’autre maladie, si covient que tu lies les vasselz que sont suspensoire, en doutant le decorrement de sanc; puis cope le coion a tout le suspensoire, et estrai l’uef, et le cure si com nos avons dit.	And if you find the egg corrupted by another disease, then it is necessary to tie the vessels that are suspensory, fearing the escape of blood; then cut the cord entirely along the suspensory part, and extract the egg, and treat it as we have said.
Et se aigue est assemblee en II parties ensamble, saiches que ce sont II ramices; si cope l’autre partie si com tu as fait la premiere igalment, puis essue lou sanc, et met en la plaie lainne moillie en oile roset; et met defuer autre laine moillie en vin et en oile, et met sus les II coions, et met desus drapelz doublés, et le lie sus a tout le liien qui est selonc ceste forme:	And if the fluid is collected in two parts together, know that these are two roots; then cut the other part as you did the first equally, then wipe the blood, and place on the wound flax soaked in rose oil; and cover with another layer of flax soaked in wine and oil, and put over it doubled cloths, and tie it up according to this form:
Puis pren II drapelz, et les emple de laine charpie selonc ceste semblance et soient assemblez par cousture en la gorle des braies, et li uns des chiés preigne sus le fondement jusc’au dos, et li autres a la partie dou poignil; et li autre dui chief sus les II angres, et soit toute assemblee li restreinture en la boucle dou braier; et aucune fois est medicinee ceste ramice de cautere en leu de taille de fer, et est que tu preignes I cautere cultellaire subtil, et cope le cuir des coions, et soit eschaufez si com nos avons dit, si que li syfac blanc que contient l’aigue est descovers; si pren lou cautere selonc ceste forme, et perce celui syfac as oncines, et l’escorche a cest subtil cautere chaut:	Then take two cloths, and wrap them with flax shreds according to this appearance and sew them together at the waist of the trousers, and one should cover from the fundament up to the back, and the other part toward the thigh; and both ends on the two sides, and let it be fastened around the constriction in the trouser loop; and sometimes this root is treated with cautery instead of iron cutting, and you should take a fine knife-shaped cautery, cut through the skin of the cord, and heat it as we have said, so that the white surface containing the fluid is exposed; then take the cautery according to this form, and puncture this surface with small incisions, and cauterize it with this fine hot instrument:
Et lou cope en toutes les manieres que tu pues, tant que tu esraiches tout; et garde que li feus ne touche l’uef; et saiches que ceste oevre est plus salve; et mues gardans de decorrement de sanc, et muedres que li ovraiges de taille; et se nulle chose te fait contraire, ou aposteme chaus ou decorremens de sanc ou autre chose, si cure ce qui te fait contraire, selonc ceu qui est devant dit.	And cut in all ways that you can, until you clean everything; and be careful that the fire does not touch the eye; and know that this work is safer; and move while guarding against bleeding, and do your work with precision; and if anything opposes you, whether it is an abscess or bleeding or something else, treat what opposes you according to what has been said before.
Et se li malaides est paourous, et ne vuet atendre cest ovraige por son horribleteit, si amenistre perforation, si com je te di, et est que quant tu es bien certains par les significations que nos avons dit que ramice aquouse est lai, si fai seoir le malaide sus I siege leveit; pues perce l’aposteme an la partie desoz a tout le spatumile large, et met la perforation dou lonc dou cors; et soit larges li pertus, si que toute li aigue corre fuer; puis met coton sus le leu, et le lie, et laisse por corre le remenant de l’aigue, puis le cure tant que li plaie soit sanee; et se li blainche toile ne laisse issir l’aigue en la bouche de la plaie, si covient que tu i boutes une penne ou l’estrument dont on trait l’aigue des ydropiques, de coi li forme est ci devant; et eslarge I poc la plaie, et saiches que li aigue revient, et est assemblee aprés VI mois ou enqui entor, et quant elle est assemblee si com devant, et ensi passera li malaides ses jors.	And if the patient is fearful and does not want to wait for this work due to its horror, then proceed with perforation as I tell you, and it is when you are certain by the signs we have mentioned that watery pus is there, make the patient sit on a raised seat; then pierce the abscess in the part below throughout the entire span of the area, and make the perforation along the length of the body; let the openings be wide so that all the fluid can flow out; then put cotton over the place and secure it, and leave it to drain the remaining fluid until the wound heals; if white cloth does not allow the fluid to exit from the mouth of the wound, you must insert a feather or an instrument used for treating the fluids in hydropics, as described before; enlarge the hole of the wound, and know that the fluid will return after about six months or around this time, and when it is gathered together as previously mentioned, then the patient will live their days.
de l’aposteme des coions	of the abscess of the testicles
Saiches que en la section de ceste ramice a paor em plusors dispositions, por coi il me semble que mues vaut c’on la laisse; et je vos dirai l’ovraige et les semblances de l’aposteme.	Know that in the section of this branch there are many fearful conditions, for which it seems best to leave it as is; and I will tell you about the work and similarities of the abscess.
Je dis donques que maint aposteme vienent ou cors, et meismement as coions; et c’est par mout de cas.	I say then that many abscesses occur in the body, especially in the testicles; and this happens for various reasons.
C’est a savoir par superfluiteit aigre et ague, qui est espandue as coions, ou de percussion; et est li color de l’aposteme selonc la color dou cors; et ne trueve point de dolor, et est aposteme grief; et par aventure est uns apostemes griés paourous et pierous, et de fuxe color, et aucune fois vient de nout d’artere, ou d’enfleure de voine.	This is to know by excess of sharp and cold moisture spread in the testicles, or from impact; and the color of the abscess corresponds to the color of the skin; and there is no pain, and it is a serious abscess; and sometimes an abscess can be frightful and stony, and of a red color, and at times it comes from blockage of an artery or swelling of a vein.
Quant c’est par nout d’artere, si est conus par la disposition d’aposteme chaut, quant tu la presses a tes dois; et ne covient mie que tu i touches.	When it is from an artery, it is known by the hot disposition of an abscess when you press it with your fingers; and it must not be touched.
Cil qui est fais d’enfleure de voine est conus par sa disposition a l’expression dou touchement des dois, et puet om bien faire la taille sus ceste semblance, et sus les autres chars; et est que tu cope lou keur des coions, puis estent l’uef en haut, et le trai fuer dou blanc syfac, et delivre lou suspensoire de toutes pars de l’uef.	One who is suffering from a swollen vein is known by its disposition in the expression of touch with your fingers, and one can properly treat this condition based on this appearance, as well as others; and it is that you cut the groin area, then place an egg at the top, and draw out the white substance from the surface, and free the suspensory ligament around the egg.
Se li uef est ja sodez avec ces chars nees, si covient donques que tu traies l’uef, et lou cope; et s’il est aers au syfac, ou en ceu qui est dedens les vasselz, si covient que tu delivre toute celle tenve, et la cope reondement.	If the egg is already swollen with these new tissues, then it is necessary that you draw out the egg and cut it; and if it is raised on the surface or within the vessels, then it is necessary to free all of this swelling and cut it roundly.
Et se li naissance de la char est ou leu derrier, si covient que tu la copes toute, et estrai l’uef, si com nous avons dit.	And if the birth of the flesh is at the back, then you must cut it all away, and extract the eye, as we have said.
Et quant tes ovraiges est acomplis, si emple la plaie de laine moillie en oile roset et en vin, puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when your work is complete, apply the wound with wet wool in rose oil and wine, then treat it with other treatments until it is healed.
de l’aposteme des coions	of the abscess of the testicles
Cis est uns apostemes envoloupez d’un envoloupement semblant a I borjon, avec le mollifiement des coions, et se muet li malaides griement quant il vait; et li cure de ceste maladie si est bien pres ausi paourouse com ceste ci devant, et toutevoie nos vos dirons l’ovraige de li, selonc ceu que li ancien firent.	This is an abscess wrapped in a covering similar to the scrotum, with softening of the testicles, and the patient suffers greatly when he moves; and the treatment for this disease is as difficult as the one before, yet we will tell you about it according to what the ancients did.
Il covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide sus I siege aleveit, puis li boute le suspensoire des coions aval a tes dois, a tout le vasseil qui sont prochien a la verge, et les teigne li maistres, et les estende forment; puis cope au spatumile trenchant large dou traver endroit les vasselz, tant qu’il soient descovert, et puis escorche de chescune part, si com nos avons dit en l’estraction des arteres qui sont en temples; puis i fiche une aguille ou il ait I fil double, et le lie au premier leu ou li vis est venue, et le lie derechief a l’autre chief; puis les cope em mileu droitement, selonc la longesce dou cors, et en trai les moistors corrumpues; puis cure la plaie si com les autres ou on enjanre bowe, si que aucun vassel chiecent que norrissent l’un des coions; car par ceu n’i vient point de mal, et se a toz les vasselz vient vis, si covient traire les coions a tout les vasselz; si que li oes ne perde son norrissement por l’incision des vasselz, et sechent et ne se puient aidier.	It is necessary that you seat the patient on a raised chair, then place the suspensory of the testicles down to your hands, on all the vessels which are close to the penis, and hold them firmly, and stretch them forcefully; then cut with a wide sharp spatula across the vessels until they are exposed, and then skin off from each side as we have said in the extraction of arteries that are in temples; then place an awl where there is double thread, and tie it at the first spot where the vein has come out, and tie it again at the other end; then cut them straight down the middle according to the length of the body, and draw out the corrupted moisture; then treat the wound as with others where a graft is engrafted, so that some vessels may fall which nourish one of the testicles; for by this no harm comes, and if all the vessels come together, it is necessary to pull the testicles up to all the vessels; so that the testicle does not lose its nourishment due to the incision of the vessels, and they dry up and cannot be helped.
de la routure dou syfac	of the fracture of the cheekbone
Li avenemens de ceste ramice si est par la section que vient ou syfac, ou l’estension sus le ventre en la partie des angres, por coi li intestine dessendent de celle routure a l’un des coions; et ceste routure est ou dou syfac, ou de l’estension de li, et vienent ces II manieres de mout de causes: ou de percussion, ou de saut, ou de braire, ou de levement de grief faix, et par semblans choses; et li signes quant c’est de l’estension dou syfac, si est qu’il avient poc et poc, en lonc tens, et ne vient mie soudainnement; et est li apostemes igalz jusque vers le parfont, por ceu que li syfac apresse l’intestine.	The occurrence of this rupture is through the section that comes from the cheekbone, or by extension on the abdomen in the area of the groins, due to which the intestines descend from that fracture to one of the thighs; and this rupture is either from the cheekbone itself, or from its extension, and these two manners come from many causes: such as impact, jumping, straining, lifting heavy loads, and similar things; and the signs when it is an extension of the cheekbone are that they occur little by little over a long period, and do not happen suddenly; and the abscesses are equal up to the base, because the cheekbone presses on the intestines.
Et li signes est quant c’est de la section dou syfac, qu’elle fait venir a l’encomencement dolor soudaine, et est li apostemes divers apparans, desoz le cuir pres, et c’est por l’issue de l’intestine et le cors au defuer dou syfac.	And the signs when it is from the section of the cheekbone are that they cause a sudden pain at the beginning, and the abscesses appear differently, near the skin, because of the exit of the intestine and the body pulling away from the cheekbone.
Et aucune fois dessent li cirbes avec l’intestine, et est retenus enqui, et fait grant dolor soffrir au malaide, meismement quant il est pressez.	And sometimes the intestines descend with the bowel, and it is retained inside, causing great pain for the patient, especially when it is compressed.
Et en ces cures de fer a paor, por coi il s’en covient eschuir.	And in these iron treatments there is fear, for which one should avoid them.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que tu comande ou malaide qu’il ramoine l’intestine a sa main au dedens en la plaie, s’il i puet rentreir; puis soit sovinez sus son col. entre tes mains, et lieve les cuixes; puis estent le keur au desus, et cope tout le cuir des coions dou lonc; puis boute dedens les leivres de la taille uncines selonc ceu que tu en as mestier por ovrir la plaie, et soit telz que li oes em puist issir; puis escorche lou syfac que est desoz lou cuir des coions, tant que li blans syfac dur soit descovers de toutes pars; puis boute ton doi indice en ceu qui enseut lou coion, en ceu qui est entre lou blanc syfac qui est desoz lou cuir de l’uef, et entre lou secont syfac, et depart ceu qui est derrier l’uef, et entre lou secont syfac; et pues muef a la main destre dedens lou keur des coions, et estent lou blanc syfac en haut a ta main senestre, et lieve l’uef a tout lou syfac devers la taille; et comande au ministre qu’il estende l’uef en haut, et deslie ceu qui est aers derrier le liement; et quier a tes dois s’il a point de l’intestine envoloupeit ou blanc syfac dur, et se tu en trueves aucune chose, si le boute au ventre desoz; puis pren une aguille ou il ait I gros fil fait de X filz, et la boute en la derriere partie dou syfac, qui est aprés lou cuir des coions; aprés la taille, puis cope les chiés qui apperent des filz, tant qu’il i ait IIII filz; puis les assemble l’un sus l’autre en maniere de croix, et en lie lou syfac, dont nos avons dit qui est desoz lou cuir des coions, d’un fort liien de II pars; puis envoloupe les chiés des filz, et les lie forment de II pars, si que nuls des vasselz que les norrissent ne puissent entrer en ous, que aposteme chaus n’i viegne; et met derechief le liien selonc le premier liien lonc II dois de celui, et aprés ces II liiens laisse dou syfac qui est desoz lou keur des coions le grant d’un doi; et aprés tout l’autre selonc la rondesce que li euf porte; puis cope en la partie qui est desoz le cuir des coions, tant qui li sans corre, et li bowe, si com nos avons dit ci devant; puis amenistre laine moillie en oile, et met em plaies, et i amenistre le liien que nos avons dit.	And the method of work is that you instruct the patient to push his intestines back into the wound with his hand if it can be reinserted; then bind him tightly around his neck between your hands, and lift his thighs;
