then stretch his abdomen above, and cut all the skin from the genital area down to the pubic hair; then insert fingers according to what you need to open the wound, so that the testicles may emerge; then peel off the fatty tissue beneath the skin of the genitals until the hard white fat is uncovered on all sides; then put your index finger in between where the scrotum is, and separate it from the second layer, and detach what is behind the testicle, and between the second layer; and then move with your right hand inside the abdomen of the genital area, stretch the hard white fat upwards to your left hand, lift the testicle towards the waistline; and instruct the assistant to lift the testicle up, and release what is tied behind the bandage; and ask him if any part of the intestines are wrapped around the hard white fat, and if you find anything, put it back under the belly; then take a needle with a thick thread made of ten threads, and insert it at the rear end of the fatty tissue, which is after the skin of the genitals; after the waist, cut off the ends of the threads that show, so there are four threads left; then arrange them one on top of another in the shape of a cross, and tie the fatty tissue beneath the scrotum tightly from two sides; then wrap around the remaining thread ends, and tie it firmly from both sides, so no vessels can enter inside and cause an abscess; then place back the bandage according to the first long bandage by two fingers wide, and after these two bandages leave one finger width of fatty tissue beneath the scrotum exposed; and then cover all around as per the roundness of where the testicle is; then cut at the part below the skin of the genitals until it reaches the soft flesh, and the bowels, just as we mentioned earlier; then apply moistened wool in oil to the wounds, and place on top the bandage that we have described.
Et aucune fois est cauterizez li blans syfac que nos avons dit, aprés l’incision, par doutance de decorrement de sanc.	And sometimes the pale surface we have mentioned is cauterized after the incision, due to fear of blood loss.
Car ce avient maintes fois, et laisse le liien tant qu’il chiece per lui; et s’il tarde au cheoir, si soit arosez d’aigue chaude, et met sus ceu que nos avons dit, tant qu’il chiece; puis cure la plaie d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	For this often happens, and leave the ligament until it falls off by itself; and if it delays in falling, soak it with hot water, and place what we have mentioned until it falls off; then treat the wound with another treatment, until it is completely healed.
de hernie carnouse	of flesh hernia
En ceste ramice ne vis je onques nul qui osast faire la cure par fer.	In this branch, I have never seen anyone dare to treat it with iron.
Et li ancien dirent qu’ele est faite si com li ramice qui est ensamble la vis, en teil maniere que tu lie les vasselz, aprés la taille sus ous legierement au desoz; puis cope em mi, et cure l’aposteme de ceu qui oevre, tant que li vasselz chient; et le cure si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the ancients said that it is done like the branch that is along the vein, in such a way that you tie the vessels, above the waist lightly on the back; then cut into it, and treat the abscess with what is needed, until the vessels release; and treat it as we have said, until it is healed.
Aucune fois vient routure ens angres, si com nos avons dit, et apert li leus; et ne dessent nulz des intestines as coions, et s’il en i dessent, c’est poc, et repaire toutes houres; et toutevoie s’il demoure trop en cest point, si croit li plaie ou syphac, tant que li intestine dessent; et ceu avient par l’estension dou syfac qui est as angres, si com nos avons dit, car il est estendus, puis est mollifiez et enflez li leus et apert; et li cure si est par cautere, si com nos avons devant dit; et aucune fois est curee par fer en ceste maniere: et est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos entre tes mains, puis cope le leu de la routure enfleit dou large selonc la quantiteit de III dois; et puis estrai le syfac qui est desoz le cuir que l’ensuet, puis pren lou rait et lou met sor le leu apparant dou syfac; et lou presse au parfont dou ventre, puis cout les II leus apparans dou syfac sus lou chief dou rait, et cout l’un et l’autre; puis estrai le chief dou rait, et ne coper point dou syfac ne n’estendre l’uef n’autre chose, si com je t’ai fait savoir en la cure de la ramice des intestines; puis le cure par la cure des plaies.	Sometimes a rupture occurs in the groin area, as we have said, and the place becomes apparent; and no part of the intestines descends to the thighs, but if they do descend, it is serious and requires immediate care at all times; however, if it remains for too long in this state, the wound or syphace grows so much that the intestines may descend; and this happens due to the extension of the syphace which is near the groin area, as we have said, because it becomes stretched out, then softened and swollen; and the treatment for this is by cautery, as we have mentioned before; sometimes it is treated with a knife in this manner: the patient lies on their back between your hands, then you cut around the swollen area of about three fingers wide; then remove the syphace which is under the skin following that, take the thread and place it over the visible part of the syphace; press firmly against the belly, then stitch both sides of the wound onto the head of the thread; pull out the head of the thread without cutting the syphace or spreading the egg or any other thing, as I have told you in the treatment of the prolapse of the intestines; finally treat it according to the method for treating wounds.
Et quant tu copes les filz, si le mundefie et cure la plaie, tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And when you cut the threads, heal and treat the wound until it is healed.
Li syfac est constrains, et n’a point d’apparance en la routure, et li cauteres est muedres en cest leu, et plus prochiens a salut.	The suture is tight, and there is no appearance of it in the rupture, and the cauterizations are soft in this place, and closer to healing.
de l’amollissement dou cuir des coions	of the softening of the skin of the testicles
Maintes fois est amollis li cuirs des coions en aucuns homes, por ceu que les chars que sont dedens sont mollifiees, et est lait a veoir; et est mestier, quant on le vuet curer, c’on faice gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et li cope le cuir qui est mollifiez sus le cuir natureil; puis assemble les II levres a une costure, et se tu vues, cout premier la superfluiteit dou cuir mollifiiez a III costures ou IIII fermement; puis cope entre les costures, et lou cure si com les autres plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez, et chient li fil.	The skin of the testicles is often softened in some men because the tissues inside are softened and appear milky; and when one wants to treat it, make the patient lie on his back, then cut the soft skin over the natural skin; then sew together the two lips at a seam, and if you wish, stitch the excess of the soft skin into three or four seams firmly; then cut between the seams, and treat it like other wounds until it is healed, and remove the thread.
dou chastrement	of the punishment
Saiches que chastremens est escomeniez en nostre loi, et por ceu il me plairoit que je n’en parlasse mie en cest livre; et n’est necessaires fuer que por II manieres: dont l’une est que li mires en saiche respondre quant on li demandera, et en saiche la cure; et li autre, por ceu que nos avons sovent mestier de chastrement d’aucunes bestes por nos aidier, si com de bouc et de mouton et de chait et d’autres bestes.	You know that castration is forbidden by our law, and for that reason I would prefer not to speak of it in this book; yet it is necessary for two reasons: one is knowing how to respond when asked about it and understanding the treatment; the other is that we often need to castrate certain animals to help us, such as goats and sheep and cats and other beasts.
Je dis donques que chastremens est fais selonc II manieres: ou par atraction, ou par fendure.	I say then that castration is performed in two ways: either by traction or by cutting.
En celle que nos faisons par attraction, faisons nos seoir la beste en aigue chaude, tant que li coion soient mollifiez et pendant; puis les preing a ta main, tant qu’il soient remis et que tu ne les sentes plus.	In the method we perform by traction, we have the animal sit in hot water until the testicles are softened and hanging down; then hold them with your hand until they are retracted and you no longer feel their weight.
Du chastrement de taille: covient que tu teignes la beste, et li presse le cuir des coions a ta main senestre, puis lie le suspensoire, et cope sus chescun oef a I cop, quant tu les avras bien escorchiez; et i laisse aucun poc dou syfac et lou subtil syfac qui est sor les vasselz; et ceste maniere de chastrement est muedre que cele qui est faite par attraction, por ceu que a l’atraction demoure par aventure aucune chose des coions, par coi li beste desire luxure; puis cure la plaie tant qu’ele soit sanee.	Of the castration of animals: it is necessary that you castrate the beast, and press the skin on its testicles with your left hand, then tie the suspensory bandage, and cut each testicle in one stroke after you have well skinned them; and leave some of the fatty substance and the fine fat which is over the vessels; and this method of castration is gentler than that done by traction, because with traction there may remain parts of the testicles, due to which the animal desires lust; then treat the wound until it heals.
des hermofrodites	Of hermaphrodites
Hermofrodie est selonc II manieres as homes: l’une si est que entre les II coions apert ausi com li figure de la nature d’une femme, ou il ait poil, et aucunes fois en cort li urine.	A hermaphrodite is in two ways for men: one is that between the two testicles it has the shape of a woman's anatomy, with hair, and sometimes even a vagina.
Et li autre maniere si est en femmes, et ait sus lou poignil ausi com une verge et II coions.	And the other manner is for women, and place on the finger as thick as a rod and two eggs.
Et li cure de l’ome et de la fame si est que tu copes les chars ajostees toutes, et les cure si com autres plaies; en la seconde maniere, des homes dont li urine saut par lou cuir des coions, si n’a point de cure.	And the treatment for a man and a woman is that you cut away all the affected flesh, and treat it as other wounds; in the second manner, for men whose urine sprays through the skin of their testicles, there is no treatment.
de la tentigene	of tension or strain
Tentigene est une chars ajostee sus la partie natureil, tant qu’elle est trop laide a veoir; et aucunes femmes l’ont ausi grant com une main, et c’est li cure.	Tentigene is a swelling on the natural part, so much so that it looks very bad; and some women have it as large as a hand, and this is its treatment.
Il covient que tu teignes la superfluiteit de la tentigene a ta main ou as oncines, et la cope legierement; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne, puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et a une autre char que naist a la bouche de la marris, et l’emple, et par aventure saut fuer, et est selonc la semblance d’une kowe, et por ceu l’apelerent li ancien «maladie kowee».	You should soak the excess of the tentigene in your hand with onions and cut it lightly; do not go too deep so that no blood comes out, then treat it as you would other wounds until it is healed; and for another part that appears at the mouth of the vagina, remove it, and sometimes it may become inflamed, resembling a cow's condition, hence why the ancients called it "cow sickness.
Si covient que tu la copes, si com nos avons dit la tentigene, et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	It is necessary that you treat it as we have said about tendinitis, and care for it until it is healed.
de erratique	Of erratic/erratic nature
Erratique si est quant li nature de la femme n’est mie percie, ou li pertus est petis; et est naturez par naissance, ou accidens par maladie que venue i est; ou c’est par char ajostee, ou dou syfac subtil ou espés, et est fais em parfont en la marris, ou en costez, ou desoz, ou que soit; et deffent le concevoir, et l’enfantement, et par aventure les flors a avoir; et li connoissance de ceu si est par le regart de la baile.	It is erratic when the nature of a woman cannot be perceived, or when the passage is small; and it is naturally so from birth, or due to an accident caused by illness; or due to thick or fine membranes attached; and it forms perfectly in the womb, or in the ribs, or elsewhere; and it prevents conception and childbirth, and perhaps menstruation as well; and knowledge of this is determined by examining the condition.
Se li estoupemens est prochiens apparans, si quier a tes dois ou au rait.	If constipation is closely apparent, then use either of my two methods or the right one.
S’il est dou syfac subtil, et il est prochiens as II leivres, si te haste, et la ront ensi: met tes II dois indices ensamble, et li femme soit sus son dos, espandues ses jambes; puis estent les II leivres forment, tant que li subtilz syfac soit rons, et soit overs li estoupemens; puis pren laine, et la moille en oile, et la met sus le leu, et gise li femme a home chescun jor, si qu’il ne puist souder.	If it is a subtle syphilitic sore and it is close to the two books, hurry and proceed as follows: place your two fingers together, and have the woman lie on her back with her legs spread; then stretch the two books firmly, so that the subtle sore lies flat over the swelling; then take linen, and moisten it in oil, and apply it to the area; then let the woman rest each day, so she may not sweat.
Et se li syfac est dur et espés, si covient que tu lou copes au spatumile semblant a foille de mirte.	And if the sore is hard and thick, then you should cut it with a scalpel resembling a myrtle leaf.
Se li estoupemens est de char nee, si la sospent a l’oncine et la cope; et aies les medicines estainchans sanc, si com acaice, sanc de dragon, encens, ensamble abun d’uef; puis amenistre une caine de plonc large, si que li plaie ne puisse souder; et ensi soit longement, et li amenistre une tente de lin sec; puis soit curez d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	If the swelling is of flesh growth, suspend it and cut it off; and have medicines that draw out blood, such as vinegar, dragon's blood, incense, mixed with an abundance of egg white; then cover the wound with a piece of cloth to prevent it from healing over too quickly; and keep it covered for a long time, and dress the wound with a dry bandage of linen; then treat it with other treatments until it is healed.
Et quant en la marris vient char nee, si la covient coper selonc ceste maniere, se ce n’est apostemes enchancrez.	And when flesh becomes corrupted in a wound, it must be cut according to this manner, except for deeply seated abscesses.
Car a l’aposteme enchancreit qui est en la marris, ne doit on touchier de feir.	For in the deeply seated abscess that is in the wound, one should not attempt to cut it open.
des emorroides	of hemorrhoids
Emorroydes sont overtures de voines dont sans cort acostumeement, et quant les emorroydes sont vielles si devienent thelul; et nos avons jai dit en la division les semblances d’aus, et les signes, et je dirai ci celles qui resoivent curation.	Hemorrhoids are protrusions of veins that often become accustomed without care, and when hemorrhoids are old they become hard; and we have already described their appearances and signs in the division, and here I will say those which can be cured.
Je di que les emorroides et li thelul, quant il sont em parfont en la marris, et il n’aperent au sentir, si n’est mie li cure par fer.	I say that when hemorrhoids and hard growths are thoroughly embedded in the wound and do not respond to sensation, they cannot be cured by cautery.
Cil qui sont a la bouche de la marris, c’on puet sentir, sont cil c’on puet curer.	Those who have a sore on their mouth, which can be felt, are those who can be treated by cleaning.
Il covient donques que tu mettes la femme en une maison froide, puis estent l’altelul as tenailles, et le cope en ses racines, puis poudre sus medicines restraignans sanc, si com acaice et sanc de dragon et encens, et semblans choses; puis boute ses piez a la paroit une houre, puis la met en aigue froide; et se decorremens de sanc i vient, si la fai seoir en une decoction de sumac et d’escorce de pomes grenates et de gales et de semblans choses, et puis pren farine d’orge, et la confis avec miel et aisil, et en fai I emplaustre sus son dos.	Therefore, you must place the woman in a cold room, then remove the altar with tongs, and cut it off at its roots; then apply medicinal powders that constrict blood, such as acacia, dragon's blood, and incense, and similar things. Then bind her feet to the wall for an hour, then immerse her in cold water; if there is a discharge of blood, seat her in a decoction of sumac bark and pomegranate peel and gallnuts and similar things, and then take oatmeal flour, mix it with honey and grease, and make a plaster to apply to her back.
Et se il estainche, c’est boin.	And if it stops flowing, that is good.
Se ceu non, se li fai aerdre ventouses au dos et as mameles sens ferir; puis pren lainne, et la moille en jus de plantain ou en jus d’aglentier avec vin viel, et fai aerdre au leu.	If not, then apply cupping to the back and breasts without injuring them; then take flax, and soak it in plantain juice or oak bark juice with old wine, and apply it to the affected area.
Et quant li aposteme repose, si cure lou leu d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez; et celle qui est apelee «albathir» est rouge, et est semblans a I chief aspre, si le covient coper si com j’ai dit le thelul; et puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when the abscess rests, treat the area with ointment until it is healed; and what is called "albathir" is red, similar to a hard head, so it must be cut as I have said about the thuluth; then treat it until it is healed.
des apostemes de la marris	For abscesses of the flesh
Maintes manieres d’aposteme vienent en la marris, si com chancre et aposteme pierous et herpes et estiomenes et fistules et emorroides et aposteme chaut, et plusors autres maladies que j’ai dit en la division.	Many types of abscesses occur in the flesh, such as cankers and stone abscesses and herpes and ulcers and fistulas and hemorrhoids and hot abscesses, and many other diseases that I have mentioned in the division.
Il covient donques que je die en cest traitier l’aposteme chaut qui vient en la marris, qui n’est mie des apostemes que coillent bowe; et se tu vues savoir l’ovraige de fer, si regarde se li apostemes est agus en l’encomencement de sa venue, et plain de chalor et de fievre, et s’il devient rouge se tu le pues veoir.	It is necessary then that I speak in this treatise of the hot abscess which comes to the buttocks, which is not one of those that are collected by urine; and if you wish to know the work of iron, look to see if the abscess is sharp at the beginning of its arrival, and full of heat and fever, and if it becomes red if you can see it.
Adonques ne te haster mie de percier, mais lou fais meurer tant que li dolor soit apaisie; et puis fai seoir lou malaide sus I siege, et ait II petis sieges ou il se cline, et apoie sus son dos et assemble ses piez as parties defuer la jambe; et soient ses cuixes espandues, et mette ses braz desoz ses genous, et les lie bien d’un boin liien; puis succe li baille devers lou destre costeit, et i amenistre l’estrument dont on oevre la bouche de la marris, de coi ci aprés vient li forme; et covient que quant tu i vues amenistrer cest estrument, que tu fiches le rait premier ens por savoir la parfondeté de la marris, si que ceu qui entre ens de l’estrument n’i viegne plus em parfont qu’il ne doit, et qu’il ne blece la malaide; et se li estrumens est plus grans, si covient covrir la parfondesce de la marris de drapelz, si que li estrumens ne li grieve; et covient qu’il mette le cornet de l’estrument au desus, et qu’il teigne l’estrument.	Then do not hurry to pierce it, but let it die down until the pain is alleviated; and then make the patient sit on a chair, and give him two small chairs where he can lean, and support his back and bring together his feet from under the thigh; and let his thighs be spread out, and put his arms below his knees, and tie them well with a good bandage; then take the cup towards the right side, and there administer the instrument for working on the buttock, of which the form follows hereafter; and it is necessary that when you wish to administer this instrument, you fix the first point inside to know the depth of the buttocks so that what enters into the instrument does not go deeper than it should, and does not hurt the patient; and if the instrument is larger, then cover the depth of the buttocks with cloths, so that the instrument does not irritate them; and it is necessary that he place the cone of the instrument at the top, and that you hold the instrument.
Et quant li apostemes apert, et on lou fent a la main mol, si le covient coper au chief, au spatumile leit; et quant li bowe est vuidie, si covient que tu mettes en la plaie tentes moillies en oile roset, ou en oile vert sec; et met la tente fuer de la plaie au parfont de la marris, et met par defuer sus la marris et sus le poignil lainne nette moillie en aigue ou malves soient cuites; puis le cure aprés II jors d’oignement avenant a ceu, tant qu’il soit sanez; et aucune fois leve on la marris et la plaie par clistere d’aigue et de miel, et puis d’aigue ou racines de lis et aristologe longe soient cuites; puis reveigne a l’oignement.	And when the abscess is open, and it is cut with the hand gently, then you must cut off its head at the spatumile line; and when the pus is emptied, then you should place in the wound moist cloths soaked in rose oil or green oil that has been rendered; and put a cloth around the wound and above the poultice, and place below the poultice and over the bandage clean wool moistened with water or mallows that have been cooked; then treat it after two days of ointment application as appropriate, until it is healed; and sometimes lift the poultice and the wound by enema of water and honey, and then of water in which roots of lilies and artemisia are boiled for a long time; then return to applying ointments.
Et se li plaie est reponue en la marris, si covient que tu te gardes de cuire de fer, mais cure la si com nos avons dit en la division.	And if the wound is covered with a poultice, then you should avoid treating it with iron, but treat it as we have said in the section.
de l’enfantement	Of childbirth
Mestier est premier a la baile qu’elle conoisse la figure de l’enfantement natureil, et li signes si est quant tu vois la femme apresser aval, et desire odorer l’ar: adonques se haste li enfes de fuer issir; adonc saiches que cil enfantemens est selonc la figure natureil, et est li issue soz son chief, et li secondine avec lui; et quant tu vois ces signes, si covient presser legierement son ventre, si que li enfes isse tost; car quant il dessent sus son chief, si ist li secondine avec lui, et est mondee li marris de ses superfluitez par bone mundification; et cist qui vient autrement ne vient mie naturelment.	It is necessary first for the midwife to know the figure of natural childbirth, and the signs are when you see the woman press downward and desire to smell the air: then the child hastens to come out. At that moment, you know that this childbirth follows the natural form, and the exit is under its head, with the afterbirth coming with it; and when you see these signs, gently press her belly so that the child comes out quickly, for as it descends with its head, the afterbirth comes with it, and the child is properly cleansed of its excesses through good care. And those who come in another manner do not come naturally.
Car il vient aucune fois sus ses piez, et vient fuer li cors ou li chiés, et les mains, ou il vient sus son ventre, ou sovin, et est convertis par aventure sor son col, et par autres figures malvaises; si est mestier a la baile qu’elle soit saige et subtilz en ces choses, et se warse d’error et de decevement, et je vos mostrerai toutes les figures coment on li doit aidier.	For sometimes it comes upon its feet, and the body or head faces upwards, or the hands come out, or even on its belly or side, and it may turn around by chance onto its neck, and in other bad positions; thus it is necessary for the midwife to be wise and subtle in these matters, and guard against error and deception, and I will show you all the figures of how one should assist them.
Se li enfes vient sus son chief par issue natureil, et li femme enfante griement, et li vertus de li est foible, si la fai seoir sus une selle, ou les femmes la tienent; et arose sa nature d’oile ou fenugreic soit cuit, et puis boute li baile entre ses dois le petit spatumile dont ci est li forme:	If the child comes out naturally above its head, and the woman gives birth with difficulty, and if her strength is weak, then let her sit on a stool, where women usually sit; and prepare an emollient of oil or fenugreek boiled, and then place between her two thighs a small spatula shaped like this:
et fende la secondine, et cope a son ungle tant que li moistors qui est ens corre fuers; et preint lou ventre de la femme tant que li enfes dessende, et s’il ne dessent, si covient clisterizer la femme de muscillaige de fenugrec avec oile de sisament; puis la fai preindre et esternuer de condisi, et tien sa bouche et son neis une houre: si istra maintenant l’enfes.	and cut the membrane, and slice it to the nail so that the moisture inside comes out; and press the woman's belly until the child descends, and if it does not descend, then it is necessary to give her an enema of fenugreek mastic with sesame oil; then make her sniff and sneeze at condisi, and hold her mouth and nose for one hour: now the child will come out.
Et se les II mains issent fuer, si covient que tu les ramoinne legierement poc et poc; et s’elles n’i puent entrer, si met la femme sus I siege, et li lieve les piés en haut; puis deboute le siege sus terre, et teigne on la femme, qu’elle ne chiece au deboutement; et se li mains n’i puet entrer, et li enfes muert, si li cope les mains au couteil qui est ci devant mis, et estrai l’enfant, et ramoine igalment.	And if the two hands exit forcefully, it is necessary that you reset them gently bit by bit; and if they cannot enter, place the woman on a chair, and lift her feet up high; then raise the chair off the ground, and support the woman so she does not fall when standing up; and if the hands still cannot enter, and the child dies, cut the hands with the knife that is placed here before, and extract the child, and reset them evenly.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus ses piés	of delivering the child onto her feet
Quant li enfes vient sus ses piez, si lou covient bouter en haut; et puis le torne poc et poc, tant qu’il soit igalz; puis preigne I des piez et l’estende poc et poc.	When the child is brought onto its feet, it should be lifted up; then turn it little by little until it is upright; then take one of its feet and stretch it little by little.
Cant il saut jusc’as cuixes, si la comande a preindre, et la fai esternuer de condisi; si saut fuer, se Deus vuet.	When it jumps to the thighs, command it to be taken, and make it sneeze with conditi; if it jumps further, as God wills.
Et s’il n’ist fuer si com nos avons dit, si le torne poc et poc, tant qu’il soit selonc la figure natureil.	And if it does not go as we have said, turn it little by little until it is in its natural position.
Car adonques ist il legierement.	For then it moves easily.
Et s’il ne vient fuer si com nos avons, dit si pren muscillaige de altee, et oile de sisament, et gomme fondue, et broie tout en I mortier; et met sus la nature de la femme dedens et defuer cest oignement, puis la fai seoir en aigue tede jusque desoz les costelz; et quant elle est moillifie desoz, se li fai I coliere de mirre, et li met desoz, et li laisse une houre; puis la fai seoir sus I siege, puis la fai esternuer et estraint sa bouche et son neis, et li preint le ventre legierement, car li enfes saut maintenant.	And if it does not come as we have said, take mastic of aloes, oil of cumin, and melted gum, and grind all in a mortar; then place the woman's nature inside and outside this ointment, then have her sit in warm water up to below her ribs; when she is moistened below, apply a poultice of myrrh and put it there, and leave it for an hour; then have her sit on the seat, then make her sneeze and hold her mouth and nose, and gently press her abdomen, for now the child jumps.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus ses genous	of the issue of the child upon its knees
Quant li enfes vient en ceste forme, si i mette li baile ses mains poc et poc; puis soit sovinee sus son col, et li pendent li piez aval, et soit gisans sor I lit; et plie ses mains poc et poc, et puis li preint les mains sus lou ventre, et li oste les cussins desoz, tant qu’elle soit appareillie aval; et se li enfes ne saut, si pren ses piez et li muef forment, puis li muef lou ventre amont, puis i boute tes mains; et ewe l’enfant poc et poc; et comande a la femme qu’elle se preigne tant que li enfes isse.	When the child comes in this form, place its hands bit by bit; then lift it on its neck, and let its feet hang down, and have it lying on the bed; and bend its hands bit by bit, and then hold its hands on the belly, and remove the cushions underneath, until it is prepared to go down; and if the child does not jump, take its feet and move them apart, then lift up the belly, then put your hands in; and let the child go bit by bit; and command the woman to hold herself as much as the child comes out.
de l’issue de l’enfant qui vient dou large une main pendant	of the issue of the child that comes with one hand hanging out
I covient engignier a ramener la main: s’on ne la puet ramener, si fai lever la femme, et aler; s’elle ne puet aler, si la fai gesir sus I lit, et li deboute les jambes forment; puis amenistre lou muscillaige que j’ai conteit; et s’elle n’enfante, si la fai seoir sus I siege, puis estudie au rameneir la main; et ewe l’enfant selonc la figure natureil, et la fai esternuer, et li comande qu’elle se preigne tant que li enfes isse fuer.	It is necessary for the surgeon to attempt to return the arm: if it cannot be returned, make the woman stand and walk; if she cannot walk, have her lie on the bed with her legs straight; then administer the muscillaginous preparation that I described; and if she does not give birth, have her sit on a chair, then study how to return the arm; and according to the natural appearance of the child, make her sneeze, and instruct her to grip tightly until the baby comes out.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus son col, et ait espandues ses mains, et sa faice tornee devers lou dos sa mere	from the birth of the child on its neck, and have her spread out her hands, and her face turned towards her mother's back
I covient que li baile teigne sa main, puis le torne poc et poc, et l’ewe legierement; et quant il est igalz, si met sus la nature muscillaige de altee et oile, si com nos avons dit, puis li comande qu’elle se mueve poc et poc; et quant tu avras ce fait, si la fai seoir sus I siege, et li comande k’elle se preigne; et la fai esternuer.	It is necessary for the surgeon to hold her hand, then turn it little by little, and do so gently; and when it is straightened, apply the natural muscillaginous preparation of altitude and oil as we have said, then instruct her to move little by little; and when you have done this, have her sit on a chair, and tell her to grip tightly; and make her sneeze.
de ceste meisme maniere a tout la secondine	In the same manner for the entire second part
Quant il vient fuer en ceste maniere a tout la secondine, si cope la secondine a ton ungle, tant que li moistors soit vuidie; et se li enfes pent sus sa faice et sus son col, si la cope des la boude, qu’elle ne soit retenue, et muere li enfes; puis boute l’enfant dedens, tant que tu l’aies mis si com il covient, et comande a la femme qu’elle se preigne aucune fois: adonques si istra legierement.	When it comes to applying heat in this manner to the entire second part, cut the second part at your fingernail until the moisture is emptied; and if the fetus moves up on its face and neck, cut from the mouth so that it is not restrained, and move the fetus; then insert the child as needed, and instruct the woman to hold herself: then gently extract.
de l’issue des gemelz	about the birth of twins
Saiches que gemeil naissent maintes fois, et aucune fois en naissent III ou IIII; et ceu n’est mie estrainge chose, et poc avient.	You should know that twins are often born, and sometimes three or four are born; this is not a strange thing, and it occasionally happens.
Dui sont estrainge chose, et ne vivent mie, se poc nom; je sai ceu, qu’il soient multipliiet, et sont desevrez par lou syfac qui les devise, qui est liiez a la boude; et aucune fois issent ausi naturelment com uns tous sous, si com nos avons dit.	Two are strange things, and do not live, if the name may be given; I know that they are multiplied, and are separated by the upper surface which divides them, which is attached to the bud; and sometimes they emerge as naturally as all others, as we have said.
Et s’il issent griement, si la cure si com nos avons dit, et soit li baile subtilz, et faice tost et legierement ceu qu’elle fait; et faice ensi com il vaut mues a salut.	And if they emerge severely, then treat them as we have said, and let the nurse be subtle, and do quickly and gently what she does; and act as it is worth for healing.
de plusors enfans	of many children
Aucune fois sont formez en la marris I ou II ou III ou IIII ou V ou VI ou VII, ou plusors jusc’a XV, et sont tout formeit en forme d’enfant par le mesurement dou saige glorious, et couvient que li baile saiche tout ceu, car par aventure semblans chose li avient; si faice selonc ceu qu’il covient.	Sometimes they are formed in the month I or II or III or IV or V or VI or VII, or more until XV, and are completely formed in the form of a child according to the measurement of the sage glorious, and it is necessary that the nurse knows all this, because similar things may happen; do as is appropriate.
de l’enfant mort	of the dead child
Quant tu cures la femme de l’enfant mort ou ventre, si com j’ai dit en la division, et il ne vient fuers, et tu es constrains d’ovraige de mains; si covient que tu saiches se li femme est de saine vertut, et n’ait accident ou elle ait paor de mort; si covient que li femme soit sovinee sus son dos, et soit ses chiés enclins aval, et les jambes levees; et li ministre la teigne de II pars, ou elle soit liie au lit si qu’elle ne soit traite au dessendement de l’enfant; puis frotez la bouche de la marris d’oiles moistes avec muscillaige de altee et de fenugrec et semence de lin, puis oigne li baile ses mains de ces oiles et de ces muscillaiges; puis les boute en la marris legierement, puis quiere I leu ou elle boute les oncines que soient covenaubles a ceu, et pren warde se li enfes est apparilliez qu’il dessende sus son chief; si fiche les oncines en ses eulz ou en son col ou en sa bouche ou en som palais ou desoz la barbe ou en la forcele ou pres des costez, et se li dessendemens est sus piez, se li fiche ou poignil et as costes moienes; et covient qu’il teigne l’oncine a sa main destre, et mette la corbeure entre ses dois de la senestre main, et li boute a tout sa main legierement, et fiche l’oncine en aucun de ces leus que nos avons dit, tant qu’il viegne a la chose vuide; et c’est li forme de l’oncine:	When you treat a woman of a dead child in her womb, as I said in the division, and it does not come out, and you are constrained to work by hand; it is necessary that you know if the woman has healthy strength, and does not have an accident where she fears death; it is necessary that the woman be laid on her back, and her thighs bent downwards, and her legs raised; then the assistant takes hold of two parts, or she lies on the bed such that they are not treated downward from the child; then rub her mouth with marish oil moistened with muscillaige of hellebore and fenugreek and flax seed, then anoint her hands with these oils and these muscillaiges; then gently place them in the marish, then seek one place where she can insert the hooks that are suitable for this, and pay attention if the child is prepared to come down on its head; then insert the hooks into its eyes or neck or mouth or palate or below the chin or under the jawbone or near the ribs, and if the descent is from feet, insert it at the navel and around the middle ribs; and you must hold the hook in your right hand, and place the curve between the two fingers of your left hand, and gently push with all your hand, and insert the hook into any of these places that we have mentioned until something comes out empty; and this is the form of the hook:
puis fiche encontre I autre oncine, ou le tier se tu en as mestier, si que li estractions soit igalz; et puis l’estent igalment en movant d’une part et d’autre, por mues issir, et soit li oncines dentez por mues tenir, si com ci est li forme:	Then insert against the other lancet, or the third if you need it, so that the extraction is equal; and then spread equally by moving from one side to the other, to allow blood to flow out, and let the lancets be toothed to hold the blood, as shown in this figure:
Et s’il en demoure une partie, si oigne li baile aucuns de ses dois d’oile, et les boute en celle partie, et traie l’autre partie; et s’il en i demoure point, si met cest oncine ou plus haut leu, et fai ceu tant qu’il s’en isse tout fuers.	And if any part remains, anoint the area with some of his oil on one side, and pour it into that part, and draw out the other part; and if there is still any left, place this lancet higher up, and do so until everything comes out completely.
Et se l’une mains vient devant l’autre, et il ne puet ramener por l’estreignement, si covient que tu envoloupes sus I drapeil, tant qu’il isse tote; puis la cope en la jointure de la plante ou au coute, et ensi covient que tu faices en l’autre main, et as II piés.	And if one hand comes before the other and he cannot bring it back for grasping, you must wrap above the finger until it all comes out; then cut at the joint of the knuckle or at the side, and thus you must do the same with the other hand, and both feet.
Et se li chiés de l’enfant est gros et il est estrois en l’issue, ou il ait ou chief aigue assemblee, si covient que tu boute le spatumile espinous entre tes dois, et fent le chief et estrai l’aigue; ou tu la ront a l’estrument qui est apelez «almidach», de coi li forme vient avec les estrumens ou chapistre qui est aprés cestui; et ensi meisme faice se li enfes a grant chief naturelment; et puis traie fuer les osses as tenailles, et se li chiés saut fuer et il estraint a la forcele, si soit fendus, tant que li moistors qui est ou pis issue fuer; et s’elle ne puet issir, si le cope par pieces au mues que tu pues; et s’il est enflez au ventre ou desoz les costez, si covient que tu lou perces tant que li moistors corre.	And if the head of the child is large and it is tight in the passage, or there is a feverish gathering on the head, then you must insert the spatumile spine between your two fingers, and cut open the head and remove the fluid; or you shave it with the instrument called "almidach", which comes with the forms along with the instruments in the chapter that follows this one; and do the same if the child has a large head naturally; and then pull out the bones with pincers, and if the head jumps forward and is stuck to the forcele, cut it as far as the moisture in the passage must flow; and if it cannot come out, cut it piece by piece until you can reach where it is blocked; and if it is swollen in the belly or inside the ribs, then you must pierce it so that the fluid runs.
Et se li enfes est sus ses piez, si est li attraction legiere, et li adrecemens a la bouche de la marris est legier.	And if the child is on its feet, then the traction is light, and the adjustment to the mouth of the socket is light.
Et s’il est estrois au ventre ou au pis, si couvient que tu l’estraies a I drapeil envoloupeit sus la main; et fent le ventre ou le pis, tant que li moistors qui i est corre; et se li autre membre sont osteit, et li chiez demoure, si boute li baile sa main em parfont de la marris, et le traie jusc’a la bouche de la marris; puis i boute I oncine ou II, et le trai fuer; et se li bouche de la marris est retrecie por aposteme chaut qui i est venus, si n’i covient mie travillier, ains covient amenistrer choses moistes et grasses; et li amenistre emplaustres, et siece en aigue mollifians et amoistans.	And if it is tight in the abdomen or breast, then you must stretch it with a sling wrapped around the hand; and cut into the abdomen or breast until the moisture that is there runs out; and if another limb is removed, and the head remains, then he should put his hand properly in the socket, and pull up to the mouth of the socket; then insert one finger or two, and push forcefully; and if the mouth of the socket is narrowed due to a hot abscess that has come there, it is not necessary to work on it, but rather to treat with moist and fatty things; and the treatment should be plasters, and apply them with water that softens and moisturizes.
Et se li enfes est sus son costeit, et tu le pues mettre igal, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit en l’enfant vif; et s’on nen ait pooir, si lou trai fuer par pieces, et n’i laissier rien de la secondine.	And if the child is on its side, and you can make it even, then minister as we have said in the living child; and if one has no power over it, then draw out what remains piece by piece, and leave nothing of the second skin.
Et quant tu avras ce fait, se li amenistre ceu que nos avons dit ens apostemes chaus que vienent en la marris; et se decorremens de sanc vient, si soit mise en aigue restraignant, et li amenistre autres cures.	And when you have done this, treat it as we have said for large abscesses that come with swelling; and if bleeding occurs, apply cold compresses, and then administer other treatments.
Et je vis une femme en cui ventre uns enfes avoit esteit mors, puis consut I autre sus celui, et refut mors li autres.	And I saw a woman in whom the fetus in her womb had died, then another was conceived afterwards, and that one too was stillborn.
Aprés lonc tens li vint uns apostemes en la boude, et enfla tant qu’il ovrit, et comensa a grant porreture.	After a long time, she developed an abscess in her breast, which swelled so much that it burst, and began to fester severely.
je fui apelez a la cure, et i pensai lonc tens, et ne pot soder li plaie.	I was called to treat it, and I thought for a long time, and could not heal the wound.
Je mis sus emplaustre de fort attraction, et en issit uns os, et aprés aucuns jors uns autres.	I applied an adhesive plaster, and out came a bone, and after several days another one.
Je me mervillai mout, por ceu c’ou ventre n’a point d’os.	I was very amazed, because there are no bones in the abdomen.
Si pensai que c’estoit des os d’un enfant mort.	I thought that they were the bones of a dead child.
Je quis la plaie, et en traï mains os, tant que li femme fut em millor point; et vesquit li femme lonc tens ensi, et issoit adés un poc de bowe dou leu; et je n’ai recordeit cest chapistre fuer que por ceu que, quant li maistres trueve une estrainge chose, qu’il i saiche mettre aide.	I examined the wound and extracted many bones until the woman was at her best point; and I kept the woman for a long time in this condition, and she would still emit a little pus from the site; and I have remembered this chapter only because when masters encounter an unusual thing, they should seek to understand it.
dou ramener la marris a son leu	to return the joint to its place
Ci aprés vient li forme dou pressor, a coi on ewe les livres; et a II tornans as II chiés des II liiens.	Here follows the form of the binder, which the books have; and to two turns at the two shoulders of the two limbs.
Toutevoie, li cornes soit plus subtilz dou restrictoire, et soit fais de ebene ou de bux; et soit li bouche dou fust I doi de large, et li marge des arbres I doit, et de lonc une palme et demi; et enmi les II liemens soient dui ajostemens de cest meisme fust, qui soient fermeit en l’un et en l’autre, de demi palme de lonc ou un poc plus; et cist dui ajostement sont bouteit en la bouche de la marris por ovrir quant on torne les II cornes.	Nevertheless, the horns should be more subtle than the restrictor, and should be made of ebony or boxwood; and the mouth of the shaft should be two fingers wide, and the margin of the trees one finger, and a length of one palm and a half; and within the two limbs there should be two joints of the same wood, which are firmly placed in each, about half a palm long or a little more; and these two joints are inserted into the mouth of the joint to open when turning the two horns.
Une autre forme, a sa semblance plus subtilz et plus legiere, soit faite de fust de ebene ou de bux, selonc la semblance des tenailles; et ait as II chiés II ajostemens, si com tu vois, d’une palme de lonc, et II dois de large; et quant tu vues ovrir la marris a tout l’estrument, si fai seoir la femme sor I lit, les piez pendant et les jambes overtes, puis boute les II ajostemens ajostez ensamble en la marris, et tien le chief de l’estrument desoz entre ses cuixes; puis oevre ta main a tout l’estrument, si com tu as fait as tenailles igalment, selonc la quantiteit que tu vues ovrir la bouche de la marris, tant que li baile faice ceu qu’elle vuet.	Another form, similar but more subtle and lighter, should be made of ebony wood or boxwood according to the resemblance of the tongs; and let it have two heads with two attachments as you see, one palm long and two fingers wide; then when you wish to open the vagina fully with all the instrument, make the woman sit on a bed, her feet hanging down and legs spread apart, then insert the two attachments together into the vagina, and hold the head of the instrument below between her thighs; then work your hand along all the instrument equally as you did with the tongs according to the quantity that you wish to open the mouth of the vagina, until she gives face what she wants.
Cist estrument sont tuit sormontez, et sont multiplies lor semblances; et quant li mires les ait apareilliez, tant est plus hastans li oevre, et plus haute as homes por lor quantiteit.	These instruments are all equipped with heads, and their forms vary; and when the doctors have them prepared, they become more efficient in their work, and higher in esteem among people for their quality.
Si ne despire mie l’estrument que tu ne l’aies apparelliet, car lor necessitez n’est mie escusauble.	Do not despise the instrument because you have not prepared it, for their needs are not excusable.
Quant li secondine est retenue a l’enfantement, si covient que tu comandes a la malaide qu’ele reteigne son alaine, et puis la fai esternuer de condisi, et li estraint tes mains a la bouche et au neis; et s’elle saut per ceu, bien est.	When the afterbirth is retained during childbirth, you must instruct the patient to hold her breath, and then make her sneeze forcefully; and press your hands over her mouth and nose; if she struggles because of this, so be it.
Se ceu non, si prent I pot, et fai I pertus ou cuvercle, et i met herbes que puissent ovrir la bouche de la marris, si com calament, rue, anis, camomille, cassialigne et centoire; toutes ces herbes, ou aucunes d’eles, soient cuites ou pot en aigue sus le feu; puis met une caine ou pertus dou pot, et l’autre chief en la bouche de la marris, et la teigne tant que li vapors viegne dedens la marris; puis la fai esternuer, si com nos avons dit.	If not, take a pot and make holes in its lid, then place herbs that can open the mouth of the mare inside it, such as calamint, rue, anise, chamomile, savory, and centaury; all these herbs or some of them should be boiled or steeped in water over the fire; then put one end of a tube into the pot hole, and the other end into the mare's mouth, and hold it tightly so that the vapor enters inside the mare; then make her sneeze as we have said.
Si saut li secondine hastanment.	The second joint jumps quickly.
Et s’elle remaint aprés ceste cure, et n’ist mie fuer, si comande a la baile qu’ele moille sa main senestre en oile de sesement ou en muscillaige de altee, et puis la boute en la nature, et quiere la secondine; et quant elle l’avra trovee, si la preigne et l’estende poc et poc droitement, si que li marris ne chiece a l’estraction; mais la covient movoir legierement a destre et a senestre, et puis traie; si venra et se desaerdra.	And if it remains after this treatment and does not move as desired, command the patient to moisten her left hand in linseed oil or murtilla juice, and then place it on the area naturally, and seek the second joint; when she has found it, grasp it and extend it little by little straightly so that no part breaks during extraction; but it must be moved gently from side to side, and then pulled; it will come out and disengage.
Et se li bouche de la marris est jai estrecie, nos avons dit la cure d’esternuer, et de fumigation des herbes; et s’elle n’ist de tout ceu que nos avons dit, si garde que tu ne foloies au traire; mais il couvient que ceu qui est a la bouche de la marris, que tu le lies a la cuixe de la femme, puis la clisterize d’oignement tetrafarmaçon; si la porrira et remettra, et venra fuer; mais toutevoie, quant elle porrist si en vient male odor au stomac et au chief, et blece la malaide.	And if the end of the broken part is tightly closed, we have mentioned the treatment of sneezing and fumigation with herbs; and if it does not move despite all that we have said, be careful not to forcibly pull it; but what is at the end of the broken part should be tied to the woman's thigh, then administer a clisterium made of tetrafarmacos ointment; this will purge and reset, and it will come out; however, if after purging there comes an unpleasant odor to the stomach and head, it will displease the patient.
Si covient donques fumigations covenaubles a ceu: aucun des anciens ont esproveit fumigation de cresson et de figues seches.	Therefore, appropriate fumigations are necessary for these conditions: some of the ancients have found it effective to use fumigation with cress and dried figs.
Li forme de l’estrument a coi on fumige la femme a la retenue des flors et de la secondine si est ceste:	The form of the instrument used to fumigate the woman for retaining her flowers and secondine is as follows:
Et est de voirre semblant a une caine, et met on le chief subtil en la nature, et les chiés larges sus le feu; et soit li fumigations sus les charbons, et la teigne tant qu’elle soit gastee, et rencomence une autre.	It is made of glass, resembling a tube, with the narrow end inserted into the body, and the wider ends over the fire; and place the fumigation over the charcoal, and let the smoke be inhaled until it is exhausted, then begin again with another.
de percier lou fondement	to pierce the fundament
Maint enfant naissent qui n’ont mie le fondement perciet, ains l’ait estoupeit uns subtilz syfac: si covient donques a la baile qu’ele perce celui syfac a son doit, et ne lou perce mie de spatumile agut, et garse le lacement qu’elle ne le touche; puis met sus lainne moillie en vin et en oile, puis la cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	Many children are born who do not have the fundament pierced, instead it is plugged with a fine sphincter: therefore, the midwife must pierce that sphincter at its proper place, and should not do so hastily with an awl, but carefully to avoid injuring it; then apply wool soaked in wine and oil, followed by ointment until it heals.
Et se tu doutes qu’il ne restoupe, si met ou pertus une caine de plonc, et li laisse mains jors, et soit ostee quant li enfes vuet aler en chambres.	And if you doubt that he will keep it still, place a chain through the ring, and leave his hands bound for a day, and remove it when the child wishes to go to chambers.
Et aucune fois vient cist estoupemens de soudement de plaie ou d’aposteme; si covient coper celui soudement: si soit curez, si com nos avons dit de la caine de plonc.	And sometimes this obstruction comes from the sudden closure of a wound or abscess; then it is necessary to cut that closure: let it be treated as we have said about the chain of lead.
de la fistule dou fondement	of the fistula of the anus
Fistules qui vienent desoz le fondement sont nodation, et groissor que vienent delez lou fondement defuer, ou en l’espaice des II parties, si a une fistule ou plusors; et quant celle nodation est anciene, si aoeuvre, et encort moistor awouse blainche ou subtilz bowe, et aucune fois sont ces fistule persans; et sont conues par ceu qu’il en ist ou egestion ou ventositeit quant li malaide fait egestion, et par aventure en saut uns vers.	Fistulas that come from inside the anus are nodations, and those that come near the anus to defecate or in the space between the two parts may have one fistula or more; and when this nodation is old, it works, and at times moisture comes out white or subtle bowe, and sometimes these fistulas are persistent; they are known by what comes out during egestion or flatulence when the patient defecates, and perhaps a worm might come out.
Et si a fistules que percent jusc’a la vessie, et jusc’a la moitiet de la verge; et parvienent jusc’a la jointure de la cuixe, et jusc’a nout de la kowe.	And if there are fistulas that penetrate to the bladder, and up to half of the shaft; and reach to the joint of the thigh, and to the root of the knee.
Et ensi conoist on la fistule persant au fondement, et ne mie persant: et est que tu boutes ton doi indice ou fondement, et boute une aguille subtil d’arain ou de fer en la fistule quant il n’i a tortuositeit.	And thus one knows whether the fistula penetrates to the rectum or not: and this is done by inserting your index finger into the rectum, and inserting a fine needle of linen or iron into the fistula when there is no curvature.
Et s’il ait tortuositeit, si i boute une tente de plonc subtil, ou I poil de cheval, tant que tu sentes la tente ou le poil a ton doit; et se tu ne le sens, et il ne vient dou pertus egestion ne ventositeit ne ver, si com nos avons dit: saiches qu’elle ne perce mie; si te haste dou curer.	And if there is curvature, then insert a probe of fine wax or horsehair until you feel the probe or hair with your finger; and if you do not feel it, and no passage leads to flatulence, wind, or feces, as we have said: you know that it does not penetrate; therefore hasten to treat.
Et quant li fistule est persans jusc’a la vessie ou jusc’a conduit de l’urine, si en saut li urine, et ne puet soudeir par medicines.	And when the fistula reaches to the bladder or to the conduit of urine, then urination occurs, and cannot be stopped by medicine.
S’elle est percie jusc’a la jointure de la cuixe, si est li tente venans jusc’au leu; s’il n’i a tortuositeit et li invention de la dolor entor, si est qu’il en ist adés bowe, et n’i vaut medicine ne soudement par oignement; et en ces fistules persans n’a point de cure fuer que labor, et vaniteit des folz mires qui s’en entremettent.	If it reaches to the joint of the thigh, then swelling comes up to that place; if there is no tortuosity and pain around, then it will quickly become an abscess, and neither medicine nor treatment by ointment helps; and in these penetrating fistulas there is no cure other than surgery, and foolish doctors who intervene with ineffective methods.
En celle qui n’est mie persans et n’est mie anciene, a esperance de saniteit par fer, si com j’ai esproveit, et est que li malaides gise entre tes mains sus son dos; et li lieve les jambes jusque sus ses cuixes, et ait ses cuixes enclinees a son ventre; puis boute une tente d’arain, ou de plonc s’il i a tortuositeit, tant que tu saiches ou li tente vient.	In the case that is not penetrating and is not old, there is hope for healing by iron, as I have experienced, and it is that the patient lies on their back; lift their legs up to their thighs, and let their knees incline towards their stomach; then apply a lead tent or of linen if there is tortuosity, until you know where the swelling is.
Se li malaides la sent entor le fondement, si covient que tu i boutes ton doi indice, se sens adonques que li tente l’ait perciet; et soit descoverte ou tu sens entre ton doit le syfac ou la char, adonques saiches qu’elle est persans; si n’i travillier mie c’on ne la puet saner.	If the patient feels it around the fundament, then you must insert your index finger there; if you then feel that the tent has been pierced; and where you feel between your finger the surface or flesh, then you know it is perforated; do not tamper with it as it cannot be healed.
On dist toutevoie c’on em puet bien saner aucuns, mais ce avient poc; et li aide c’on i fait, si est c’on eschaufe le cautere subtil selonc la largesce de la fistule, si com il est devant dit; et le boute tout chaut en la fistule, tant qu’il viegne delez le fondement; et faice ceu II fois ou III, tant que tu saiches que ces chars fautrees soient arses, qui sont semblant a une penne d’oiseil; et puis le cure de tentes moillies em burre, tant que celle chars isse fuer, puis le cure d’oignement enjanrant char et soudant.	It is said that one can often heal certain conditions well, but this happens rarely; and the help one provides involves heating the cautery finely according to the width of the fistula, as was previously mentioned; and insert it very hot into the fistula, until it reaches near the fundament; do this two or three times until you know that the diseased tissues are burned, which look like a feather from a bird; then treat with moistened tents in butter until the flesh grows back, then apply an ointment that promotes healing and unites tissue.
S’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien.	If he is thus healthy, it is well.
Se ceu, nom autrement ne puet estre sanez; et se li tente entre, et ne perce jusc’au doit qui est ou fondement, et a entre ton doi et la tente une coverture espesse de char ou de syfac, et tu vois la fistule a ceu qui enseut la coverture dou keur; si le cope des l’encomencement de la fistule, et boute adés avant la tente, et pues le cautere aprés, tant qu’il viegne au chief de la tente; et sera delivré li tente, et cherra; puis mondefie celles chars fautrees que semblent une penne d’oisel, et n’en remaigne niant.	If he cannot be healthy otherwise; and if the fistula enters but does not penetrate to the bottom which is at the foundation, and there is a thick covering of flesh or tissue between the bottom and the fistula, and you see the fistula on him who is under this covering of the heart; cut from the beginning of the fistula, then push forward through the fistula, and apply the cautery afterward until it reaches the head of the fistula; and he will be freed from the fistula which will fall out; then clean away the damaged flesh that looks like a bird's feather, and leave nothing remaining.
Et si li sans te vaint, et cort entre toi et l’uevre, si le cauterize de feu ou de medicine ague.	And if the blood fails you, and cuts between you and the work, then cauterize with fire or with astringent medication.
Car li cauteres de feu assemble II bones choses: c’est a savoir, l’arsure de ces chars ajostees, et l’esteinchement de sanc et la sechor de la moistor; puis le cure de tentes moillies em burre ou en choz broiez, tant que li leus giete bowe, et isse fuer li chars arse en la bowe; puis cure la plaie des oignemens soudans enjanrans dure char, et sont les medicines seches.	For the fire cautery unites two good things: that is to say, the burning of the flesh adhering, and the stopping of blood and drying of moisture; then treat with bandages soaked in butter or similar substances until the wound produces pus, and the flesh burned in the pus; then treat the wound with ointments consisting of hard ingredients, and these medicines are dry.
Car quant il est restoree, si est sanee et ne revient mie.	For when it is restored, it is healed and does not return.
Et se fistule vient jusc’a parfont dou fondement, et est esloigniez dou cors, se li boute ton doi ou fondement, et enquier ceu.	And if a fistula comes up from the depths of the fundament, and is distant from the body, then pierce it at the fundament, and examine it.
Se tu sens la tente, et entre II est li toile ou li syfac ou chars, ou il est pres a percier, si n’i ait fuers que voie de fiance et d’esperance, par l’aministrement de l’une des III manieres: ou tu le cauterizes si com nos avons dit, ou tu le cope jusc’a fons, ou se tu pues si i met tentes et cure si com premier; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, que tu ne coper le tenement qui tient le fondement, et viegne li egestions par lai sens volenteit; puis le cure, si com nos avons dit; par aventure si sera sanez, ou tu esloigne celle coverture et la munde puis qu’elle est copee delez lou fondement, ou par tente ou par autre estrument apointé; puis mondefie cele char fautree qui est en la plaie, tant com tu pues; puis estudie a restorer la plaie, et a demorer la fistule en la partie defuers le fondement: si iert plus legiere chose au malaide.	If you feel the tent, and between two it is the tissue or flesh where it is close to piercing, there must be no doubt in believing and hoping, by means of one of the three methods: either you cauterize it as we have said, or you cut it down to the base, or if you can place bandages and treat it as initially; do not go too deep so that you do not cut into the tissue holding the fundament, and let the evacuation occur according to your will; then treat it as we have said; perhaps it will heal, or remove the covering which is cut around the fundament, either by bandage or with another appropriate instrument; then clean the diseased flesh in the wound as much as you can; then study to restore the wound and keep the fistula outside the fundament: this will be a lighter matter for the patient.
Et aucune fois sont fistules selonc ceste maniere: et est quant tu boutes la tente en la fistule, et elle est ou costeit dou fondement delez lou cuir desus, si pren une tente percie au chief selonc ceste forme:	And sometimes there are fistulas in this manner: and when you insert the probe into the fistula, and it is at the bottom of the foundation near the skin above, take a probe perforated at the tip according to this form:
Et i boute I fil tort en II, et boute la tente a tout le fil en la fistule tant qu’il soit au chief.	And insert the thread twisted into two parts, and insert the probe along the entire length of the thread into the fistula until it reaches the tip.
S’elle est persans en la marge dou fondement dedens, adonc estrai lou fil de celui pertus, ensi que tu boutes ton doi ou fondement; et trai le chief dou fil, et assemble les II chiés ensamble, et estraint l’un a l’autre, et le laisse I jor ou II; et le restraint aucune fois, tant que li filz cope ces chars que sont entre dous, et chiecent; puis cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit soudee et sanee.	If it is perpendicular in the margin of the foundation inside, then extract the thread from that opening, such that you place your finger on the foundation; and pull the tip of the thread, and join the two ends together, and hold them tight to each other, and leave it for one day or two; and tighten it occasionally, until the thread cuts through the tissues between them and they close; then treat the wound until it is sealed and healed.
Se li fistule ne perce, si la fai percier en toutes les manieres que tu pues, s’ele n’est trop em parfont.	If the fistula does not open, pierce it in all ways that you can, if it is not too deep.
Car il ne covient mie faire por le lacement coper si em parfont, et puis le cure, si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	For it is not appropriate to make an incision too deep for the displacement and then treat it as we have said, until it is healed.
Li forme dou spatumile espinous dont on fent la fistule si est mout agus d’une, part et trenchans; et d’autre part non, por ceu c’on ne cope mie ceu c’on ne doit mie copeir, si com tu vois ci:	The form of the spatumile spine where one makes the fistula is very sharp on one side and cutting; and not so on the other side, because one must not cut what should not be cut, as you see here:
des emorroydes	for hemorrhoids
Emorrydes sont selonc II manieres: ou elles sont dedens le fondement, ausi com grain de resin, et s’en i a petites et grans, et en cort adés sanc, et s’en i a une ou plusors, et sont defuer le fondement et au chief dou fondement; mais celles qui sont defuer si ont poc de moistor, et encort adés ou un poc d’aigue citrine ou un poc de sanc, et ont la color dou cors; et li cure de ces qui les ont dedens le fondement, si est que tu comandes au malaide qu’il s’espreigne por aleir en chambres, tant que li fondemens li isse fuer, et c’aperent li filz; si te haste, et le pent as tenailles, ou tu le tien a ton ungle, puis le cope en ses racines; et se li uncine ne les pueent tenir por ses moistors, si les prent a I drapeil, ou a couton, ou d’une piece de chamelot; et les estrai a tes dois, puis les cope, et poudre desus aucunes chaudes poudres que soient en leu de cautere; ou tu les cauterize si com il est dit ou chapistre de cautere, pues les cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li fondemens ne puet issir, si clisterize le malaide de clistere mordant et aspre por laver ceu qui est ou fondement, si qu’il puist issir apertement; cant li malaides se preint, et se li fil sont fuer dou fondement, si est li cure legiere; et est que tu les preignes a ton ungle ou as tenailles, et les cope, puis les cure si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez, et qu’il redoute l’incision par fer.	Hemorrhoids are of two kinds: those inside the anus, like grains of resin, and they can be small or large, and there is blood in them; and there may be one or several, some near the anus and others at the top of the anus. But those that are farther away have less moisture, and sometimes contain a little yellow liquid or blood, and their color matches the skin. The treatment for these inside the anus is to instruct the patient to abstain from food so that the hemorrhoids can come out easily; if they do not, grasp them with your fingernail, then cut them at the base; if the nails cannot hold due to moisture, use a cloth or cotton or piece of camel hair to grip and pull them out, then cut them off and apply some warm powder used for cauterization. Then cauterize as described in the cautery chapter, and treat further until healed; if the anus cannot be made to open, give an enema that is harsh and rough to clean what is inside the anus so it can come out freely. If the patient is diligent and the threads have come out of the anus, the treatment will be easier; grasp them with your fingernail or forceps, cut them off, and treat as we have said until healed, and avoid cutting with iron instruments.
Si covient que tu amenistre la costure selonc ceste maniere: pren I fil tort, et le boute en une aguille, et puis trai le fil au desus et fai percier l’aguille d’autre part, et torne les II chiez dou fil desoz l’aguille, et si soit dou large; et estraint le fil forment, puis noe le fil, et estrai l’aguille, et fai ensi de toz les autres, et en laisse I por corre la superfluiteit dou sanc; puis met sus le fondement I drapeil moilliet en oile roset ou en cerote, et met sus le fondement, et comande au malaide k’il repose; et puis le laisse tant qu’il chiecent, et quant il seront cheut, si les cure d’oignement et d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	So you must treat the sutures in this manner: take twisted thread and put it on a needle, then pull the thread from above and pierce the needle from another part, and turn both ends of the thread under the needle, and make them wide; and firmly tighten the thread, then knot the thread, and remove the needle, and do so for all others, leaving one to drain excess blood; then place a moistened piece of cloth in rose oil or cerate on the foundation, and place it over the foundation, and instruct the patient to rest; and then leave them until they dry, and when they have dried, cure them with ointment and other treatments until they are healthy.
dou sechement dou fiens ou fondement	from the dryness of the bowels or foundation
Maintes fois avient sechement de fiens en l’intestine, et par constrignement de nature, et quant li maladie est vielle et medicine n’i vaut.	Often there is dryness of feces in the intestines, and by compulsion of nature, and when the illness is old and medicine does not avail.
Si covient que tu reses a la point d’un spatumile ou a ton ungle l’escorce desus, qui ne le laisse a moistir; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sodez si com il covient; et s’il ne puet soder, si rencomence la rasure plus fort que devant, tant qu’il saine mout, et soit escorchiez; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	You should scrape with the point of a scalpel or your nail on the surface above it, without letting it become moist; then clean until it is dry as needed; and if it cannot be dried, continue scraping more forcefully than before, until it bleeds much and becomes scraped; then clean until it is healed.
dou fremit	with trembling
Formice est une petite apparance fautree antor le cors, et va mout em parfont; et aucune fois la trueve li frois, et le sent on ausi comme mort de fremit, et vient en tout le cors, et plus as mains que autre part.	Formice is a small rash that appears on the body and spreads very quickly; sometimes cold causes it, and one feels it like being dead from trembling, and it comes throughout the whole body, and more in the hands than elsewhere.
Et li cure si est que tu pren une cainne d’une penne d’oie, ou une penne de vultul fort, et met celle caine sus le fremit, tant que li cercles porpreigne le fremit tot entor; puis torne ta main a tout la cainne tant que tu copes tout entor le fremit, et le met em parfont, et esraiche le fremit de ses racines.	And the treatment is that you take a quill from a goose's wing or a strong vulture feather, and place this quill over the swelling so that the circles completely encircle the swelling; then turn your hand around the entire quill until you cut all around the swelling, and place it perfectly flat, and excise the swelling from its roots.
Et se tu vues, si fai ceu d’une caine d’arain ou de fer selonc ceste forme, et soit subtilz desoz et traians desus:	And if you wish, do this with a thread of linen or iron according to this form, and let it be fine underneath and drawn over:
ne mie perciet, por mues tenir au doi, et mues presser Et se tu vues, si cauterize lou fremit, si com il est devant ou chapistre de cautere.	do not pierce it, to hold the threads in place and press them, And if you wish, cauterize the swelling as described in the chapter on cautery.
de la forme dou clistere	of the form of the enema
Aucune fois fait on clistere d’argent ou d’archaut, ou d’arain fondut ou mailliet; et aucune fois fait on de ces estrumens petis et grans, selonc ces a cui il sont amenistrez.	Sometimes a enema is made of silver or sorrel, or of melted silk or barley; and sometimes these instruments are made small and large, according to those to whom they are administered.
Cil donques c’on amenistre en la cure des enfans et qui sont foible et dolorous, sont petis.	Those who are treated in the care of children and those who are weak and in pain are small.
Li forme dou clistere petit et grant si est desus large, ou li ventres est liiez selonc ceste maniere:	The form of the enema, small and large, is as follows, or the belly is bandaged in this manner:
et i ait une desevrance ou li ventres soit liiez, si com tu vois, et li chiez soit dedens perciez; et ait a l’un des costez II pertus, et en l’autre I; et soit li ventres ou om met les medicines d’une vessie de beste ou de parchemin, et soit perciez tout entor de menus pertus, et ait entre chescun pertus I doit d’espaice, puis boute en ces pertus I fil fort de fil crut tort en X ou enqui entor, et assemble le ventre si com est une chievre; et quant li medicine est dedens, si la lie a l’estrument devant d’un fil fort, puis clisterize; et c’est li forme dou cercle:	and there should be a space where the belly is bandaged as you see, and the center should be pierced; and have two holes on one side and one on the other; and let the belly where the medicine is placed be made of an animal bladder or parchment, and pierce it all around with small holes, and leave one finger's width between each hole, then insert a strong raw thread twisted ten times around, and secure the belly as if it were a goat; and when the medicine is inside, tie it to the instrument with a strong thread, then administer the enema; and this is the form of the circle:
Et soit li medicine ne trop chaude ne trop froide, et oint le chief dou clistere d’oile ou d’aubun d’uef, ou de semblant chose, puis le boute ens legierement; puis l’espreigne li ministres a ses II mains ensamble, tant qu’il soit toz vuis, puis estrai lou clistere, et lieve li malaides ses jambes a la paroit, et se li medicine vuet issir, si la teigne tant com il puet; et s’il dort une nuit atot, si est plus grans aide.	And let the medicine not be too hot nor too cold, and anoint the head with a poultice of oil or oak leaf juice, or something similar, then press it on gently; then stretch the patient's arms with both hands until they are fully extended, then remove the poultice, and raise the patient's legs against the wall, and if the medicine needs to come out, let it stay as long as possible; and if he sleeps a whole night straight, there is greater help.
Et se tu le clisterizes em maladie de decorrement de ventre, et li medicine se haste d’issir, si le rencomence tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you give him an enema in a disease of diarrhea, and the medicine comes out too quickly, then repeat it until he is well.
Et se li emorroide sont ou fondement, ou aposteme, si soit li clistere ausi subtilz com por I enfant; et c’est li forme dou clistere subtil sus coi li cuir soit estraint:	And if the hemorrhoids are at the fundament or an abscess, then the enema should be as fine as for a child; and this is the form of the fine enema in which the skin is stretched:
des plaies	of wounds
Nos avons jai dit en la division la cure des plaies; or vos dirons les cures de mains et de medicine, selonc l’acomplissement.	We have already mentioned in the division the treatment of wounds; now we will tell you about the treatments by hand and with medicine, according to the completion.
Je dis que les plaies sont diverses selonc ceu qu’elles sont faites, et selonc les leus ou les plaies sont faites, et de coi elles sont faites.	I say that wounds vary according to how they are made, and according to the places where the wounds are made, and from what they are made.
Les choses par coi plaies sont faites sont par gitement de piere, et taille d’espee et de couteil, ou de lance ou de fust ou de siette, ou de semblans choses; ou que sont faites selonc les leus dou cors, si com plaie que chiet sus le col, ou sus le chief, ou le peis, ou le ventre, ou le foie, et semblans membres; et je vos dirai la cure de chescune plaie, et encomencerai as plaies dou chief simples, car li remenbrance venra en son chapistre.	The things by which wounds are made are due to the falling of stones, and cutting with a sword or knife, or spear or staff or arrow, or similar things; they are made according to the places on the body, such as a wound that falls on the neck, or head, or foot, or belly, or liver, and other members; and I will tell you the treatment for each wound, starting with simple head wounds, because the memory will come in its chapter.
Je dis que quant simple plaie vient ou chief, et li os n’est brisiez, si pren garde se c’est de gitement de piere ou de semblans choses, et li cuir est toutevoie rompus et est li plaie grans, et tu doutes levement d’aposteme chaut: si le fai tantost sainier de la cephalique meismement s’il vient poc de sanc de la plaie, et soit li sainie au contraire de la partie navree; et eschuisse li malaides repletion de vin et de viandes grosses.	I say that when a simple wound comes to the head and the bone is not broken, be careful if it is from falling of stones or similar things, and the skin is completely torn and the wound large, and you fear the development of a hot abscess: then I apply immediately a cephalic dressing if there is little blood coming from the wound, and let the dressing be on the opposite side of the injured part; and avoid the patient overindulgence in wine and heavy foods.
Et s’il ne vuet sainier, si soit amenuisie sa viande, et ne boive point de vin, ne ne menjuce point de char; et met sor la plaie, se apostemes chaus i vient, coton moilliet en oile roset soulement, ou en vin stiptice; et s’il n’i a aposteme chaut, si met sus la plaie, s’elle est fresche a tout son sanc, et elle n’est muee par l’air, poudre, que je dirai un poc ci aprés; et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucuns oignemens, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if he does not want to be bled, then let his meat be reduced, and let him drink no wine, nor eat any flesh; and place on the wound, if hot abscesses come there, cotton soaked in rose oil only, or in astringent wine; and if there is no hot abscess, and the wound is fresh with all its blood and has not been exposed to air, apply powder which I will mention a little later; and if it becomes inflamed from exposure to air, then put on some ointments until it heals.
Et se li plaie est grans si com de tailleure d’espee et de semblans, et les levres ne se pueent assembler par tentes, si les assemble par cousture, si com je dirai as plaies dou ventre, de la costure.	And if the wound is large like a sword cut and similar, and the edges cannot be brought together by suturing, then join them by stitching, as I will explain for belly wounds, of the suture.
Se li plaie est descoverte de l’os, et pent, et ne tient mais que a un poc, si le cope; puis cure la plaie de medicine, et restoure char dure en leu de cuir, et comande au malaide a mengier grosses viandes, si com testes et froment cuit, ausi com poulz, et semblans choses.	If the wound is exposed bone, and is thin, and only holds together at one point, then cut it; then treat the wound with medicine, and restore hard flesh in place of skin, and instruct the patient to eat hearty foods, such as brains and cooked wheat, as well as pulse, and similar things.
Et se tu trueves ou cuir porriture, et il n’aert a l’os, si cope lou porrit tot, et giete fuer, puis le cure; et se il ait artere en la plaie ou voine, dont sans cort, et il ne puet estainchier par medicines, si quier l’artere, et se tu la trueves desloie, si la lie d’un fil; et se ceu ne profite mie, si la cauterize.
