And if you find putrid skin in the wound that adheres to the bone, then cut out all the rotten flesh and apply poultices, then treat it; and if there is an artery or vein in the wound that cannot be staunched with medicine, then ligature it, and if you find it dislocated, tie it back with a thread; and if this does not help, cauterize it.
Et se ces plaies sont petites et simples, si est li cure legiere: et est que tu mettes ens ceste poudre qui soude ainsois que li ars l’ait muee.	And if these wounds are small and simple, then the treatment is light: it is that you put into this powder which heals as soon as the burn has peeled off.
Et li maniere de la poudre si est: pren encens une partie; sanc de dragon II parties; chalz vive III parties, et le poudre subtilment, et emple la plaie, et l’estraint forment, tant qu’elle s’aerse bien et se joigne a tout son sanc; et puis la lie bien, et la laisse sens desliier, s’elle n’enfle; car on n’oste la madicine tant qu’ele soit sanee.	And the method for the powder is as follows: take incense one part; dragon's blood two parts; live charcoal three parts, and finely grind the powder, then apply it to the wound, and press firmly until it adheres well and joins with all its blood; then bind it tightly, and do not loosen it if it does not swell; for you should not remove the medicine until it is healed.
Et aucune fois fait on ceu de chalz soulement, quant on n’ait l’encens ne lou sanc de dragon, mais que li ars n’ait muee la plaie.	And sometimes one does this with charcoal alone, when there is no incense or dragon's blood available, but the burn has peeled off the wound.
Et se li ars ait mueit la plaie, meismement en esteit, si n’i met om mie ceste poudre; mais met sus aucuns oignemens digestis, ou poulz de farine d’orge faites d’aigue et de miel, tant qu’ele giete bowe; puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the wound has moved, especially in summer, do not put this powder on it; but apply some digestible ointments, or a poultice made of oatmeal with water and honey, until it discharges pus; then treat it with other remedies until it is healed.
Et se li brisure d’os vient avec la plaie, et elle est petite, si l’estrai as pinceures subtilz; et je vos dirai ci aprés les brisures dou chief.	And if the bone fracture comes with the wound, and it is small, then extract it with fine forceps; and I will tell you afterwards about fractures of the head.
de la plaie dou col	of the wound of the neck
Se plaie vient ou col et elle est simple, si n’a point de difference entre li et celi dou chief, mais se li ners dou col ou li artere est copee.	If the wound is on the neck and it is simple, there is no difference from that of the head, but if the nerve of the neck or the artery is cut.
Se c’est li ners, si n’i a autre engien que laissier la cure, et n’i mettre nulle chose restraignant, car il nuit as ners et les fait retraire; et ne mettre sus la plaie rien froit, car li substance des ners est froide, et li continuation d’aus si est avec le cerveil, qui est li plus haus membres; mais soit li medicine souez, si com chalz lavee en aigue douce, et mellee avec oile roset, et cucie lavee ausi en aigue douce, et autres pieres de mine selonc ceste maniere, et oignemens moistes.	If it is the nerve, then there is no other remedy but to leave it untreated and not apply anything constricting, for it harms the nerves and makes them withdraw; nor should anything cold be applied to the wound, because the substance of the nerves is cold, and their continuation is with the brain, which is the highest part of the body; but let the medicine be warm, such as hot water mixed with sweet water, and rose oil, and boiled linseed in sweet water, and other mineral stones according to this manner, and moist ointments.
Et se li plaie est grans, si la cout et lie de bendes, puis la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the wound is large, then sew and bind it with bandages, then treat it until it is healed.
Et se les plaies sont parfondes et ele est chevee et pleinne de bowe, si la perce ou plus bas leu; et se li artere est copee, et decorremens de sanc en vient, si la desoivre, et la loie, et la cauterize se mestier est; et se li espinee de la gorge est copee, ou li keurs, et li conduiz est gardez, par coi la viande va, si cout le keur sus la cainne de la gorge, et ne touchier la gorge mais la remet selonc sa figure naturel; et puis l’estraint avenanment, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le cure d’oignemens desechans tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li plaie a fait empression en l’os, si la quier; et s’il i a pieces d’os, si les trai fuers toz se tu pues, et ces que tu ne pues avoir, si laisse tant que li plaie porrisse, et soit desevree et aligie li issue; et se li plaie est fresche, si poudre sus la poudre que j’ai dit.	And if the wounds are deep and filled with pus, then puncture it where it is lowest; and if an artery is cut and bleeding occurs, then open it, bind it, and cauterize it if necessary; and if a spine in the throat is cut or the neck is injured, by which the flesh passes through, sew the wound on the neck over the windpipe without touching the throat, and place it back according to its natural shape; then bandage it securely, and leave it for several days, then treat it with drying ointments until it heals; and if the injury has caused a depression in the bone, then graft it; and if there are pieces of bone, remove them cleanly as much as you can, and leave those you cannot reach to rot and clear the passage; and if the wound is fresh, sprinkle on the powder that I mentioned.
Et s’il a en la plaie os et il i a fistule, si la cure ensi com j’ai dit en son chapistre.	And if there is bone in the wound and there is an abscess, treat it as I have said in its chapter.
de la plaie de lance ou de coutel	of a lance or knife wound
Se c’est cop de lance ou de coutel, et li plaie est parfonde, si regarde se de la plaie saut ventositez cant li malaides alainne: saiches adonques que li plaie est mortelz; et s’elle n’est parfonde, et elle est fresche a tout son sanc, si n’i mettre mie a la premiere houre la poudre, ne ne la liier mie por le sanc que ne demorse em parfont, et reviegne au cuer, et ocie lou malaide; mais i met oignement atractif, et le lie II fois le jor; et se tu n’as oignement, si met en la plaie viel coton por succier fuers la moistor, et fai dormir le malaide sus la plaie III jors, ou IIII, ou plusors; si n’i venra mie spasme, ne tremor male de cuer n’estraingnemens d’alainne; et quant tu vois les bones dispositions, si saiches que li plaie est sauve.	If it is a lance or knife wound and the wound is deep, then look to see if the wound emits air when the patient breathes: if so, you know that the wound is mortal; but if it is not deep and the blood flows freely throughout, do not apply powder at the first hour, nor bind it for fear of stopping fresh blood from flowing out, which could reach the heart and kill the patient; instead, use an adhesive ointment, and bandage it twice a day. If you have no ointment, place old cotton in the wound to absorb moisture, and let the patient sleep near the wound three days or four or more; thus there will be no spasm, no tremor, nor strangulation of breath; and when you see good signs, then you know that the wound is safe.
Cure la donques de tentes et d’autres cures, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’elle ne puet saner, et oevre, adés saiches que il i a fistule; si la cure si com on doit.	Treat it then with tents and other treatments until he is healed; and if she cannot heal him, and you operate, then know that there is a fistula; treat it as one should.
Et se li plaie est d’incision d’espee ou de coutel, et elle est simple, ou pis ou au dos, si la cure de ceu qui est devant; s’elle est grans, de cousture; et s’elle est petite, de poudre, et s’elle est empressee en l’os, et en a copeit pieces, si quier la plaie, et les trai fuers s’il sont desevrez; et s’il ne sont desevrez, si laisse porrir la plaie, si aligera li estractions; et des autres plaies as autres membres est li jugemens si com nos avons dit.	And if the wound is from a sword or knife cut, and it is simple, whether on the front or back, treat it like any other; if it is large, by stitching; if small, with powder; and if it presses into the bone, and chips of bone are present, then probe the wound, and draw out loose pieces; and if they are not loose, let the wound heal open, which will ease the extraction; and for wounds on other members judgment is as we have said.
dou derrompement dou ventre	from the rupture of the abdomen
Li derompemens dou ventre est grans et moiens et petis; de la grant plaie saut aucune fois li intestine, ou li ners des intestines, par coi li intromission d’aus; et li costure est plus malaisie, et aucune fois vaut pis li petite plaie que li grans, por ceu c’on remet plus a poinnes les intestines en, s’on ne les i remet de chaut en chaut; por ce que li intestine enflent tantost qu’il sentent le froit, si rentrent plus a poinnes, et por ceu vaut mues li moieinne plaie, por ceu c’on ramoine mues l’intestine a son leu que as autres II Et saiches que li routure dou ventre est selonc IIII manieres: les II costures communes avienent en la costure dou ventre, et li costure des autres plaies dou cors et II autres costures propres sont communes as autres plaies; et toutevoie elles sont plus propres avec la costure dou ventre, et je dirai une chescune et declairerai.	The rupture of the belly is great and medium and small; from the large wound sometimes the intestines come out, or the nerves of the intestines, which causes an intestinal perforation; and suturing is more difficult, and sometimes a smaller wound is worse than a larger one because if the intestines are not replaced gradually they become swollen immediately upon feeling cold, thus entering deeper, and for this reason a smaller rupture may be more severe because it is easier to replace the intestines in their place compared to other two. And know that belly ruptures occur according to four manners: the two common sutures happen with the abdominal suture, and the sutures of other wounds on the body and another two specific sutures are common to other wounds; yet they are more appropriate with the abdominal suture, and I will describe each one and explain.
Je di que quant li plaie est petite, et aucune chose de l’intestine ist fuer, et griés chose est dou remettre, ceu est par l’une des II manieres: ou por la petitece de la plaie, si com nos avons dit, ou por ce que li intestine est enflez por le froit.	I say that when the wound is small, and something of the intestine comes out, and it is difficult to replace, this is done by one of two methods: either because of the smallness of the wound, as we have said, or because the intestines are swollen due to cold.
Et quant il est frois, eschaufez lou en teil maniere: moillie une esponge ou I mol drapeil en aigue tede soulement, ou tu cuis en aigue squinant et cipre et spique, et arose l’intestine tant que li enfleure soit ostee; et aucune fois fait ce vins restraingnans, et est muedre que awe soule por desenfler.	And when it is cold, warm it in this manner: moisten a sponge or piece of cloth in hot water only, or boil it in water with squinants and cypress and spikenard, and rinse the intestines until the swelling subsides; and sometimes use constricting wine, which helps to reduce the swelling.
Et quant tu vois l’enfleure departir, si amoiste l’intestine d’aigue ou altee et malves soient cuites, car par ceu est aligie li entree a poc de chose; et s’il n’i puet entrer, si fent un poc la plaie a l’estrument de coi on cope les emorroydes; et li premiere cure est muedre que li taille, que nus n’i doit taillier sens grant necessiteit n’i ait; et c’est li estrumens por le fendre: si trenche dedens en la corbeure et defuer non, et vez ci la forme:	And when you see the swelling depart, moisten the intestines with water in which hellebore and mallows have been boiled, for this gradually opens up the entry; and if it cannot enter, make a small incision in the wound with the instrument used to cut hemorrhoids; and the first treatment is such that one should not cut without great necessity; and here is the form of the instrument: cut inwardly along the curvature and do not go deeper, as shown here.
Et quant li plaie est enlargie, et li intestine saut fuer, si le remet arer selonc la forme naturel en son leu propre, se tu en as pooir, car ce vaut mues.	And when the wound is enlarged, and the intestines jump out, place them back in their natural form in their proper place, if you have the power to do so, for that is better.
Quant li plaie est large, et elle est en la partie desoz lou ventre, si covient que tu faices gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et met ses jambes plus haut que son chief; et s’elle est en la partie desoz le ventre, si met le chief et le pis plus haut que les parties desoz, et ausi se li routure dou ventre est en l’une des II parties si met t’entente en ceu que li partie navree soit plus haute que li autre; et ensi covient amenistrer ceu que je dis en plaies grans et moienes.	When the wound is large, and it is in the back part of the belly, you should make the patient lie on his back, with his legs higher than his head; and if it is in the front part of the belly, raise the head and feet higher than the middle parts, and similarly if there is a rupture of the abdomen in one of the two parts, raise the injured part higher than the other; and thus should be treated what I say about large and medium wounds.
Es plaies petites met ceu que t’est apparilliet, puis aies entre tes mains I ministre pitous ki teigne toute la routure a sa main, et assemble les levres; et c’est la maniere commune de costures, et est que tu preignes une aguille ou plusors, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce de la plaie, puis laisse des le chief de la plaie I doi d’espaice, et i fiche une aguille ou il ait I boin fil fort; et perce les II chiés dou cuir avec les II chiés dou siphac, qui est desoz le cuir dedens, tant que tu la faices percier de celle partie, et assemble les II chief dou siphac les IIII ensamble; puis l’estrain d’un fil double entor l’aguille de II pars, puis assemble les II chiés de la plaie avenanment, et puis laisse I doi d’espaice, et i fiche une autre aguille; puis la lie dou fil si com tu as fait la premiere aguille, et ne cesser de ceu faire selonc ceu que tu as mestier des aguilles, tant que toute li plaie soit restrainte; et soient les aguilles moienes, entre subtilz et grosses, car les aguilles subtilz copent toute la char, et les trop grosses si ne pueent mie bien entrer: por ceu covient qu’elles soient moienes; et ne covient mie bouter les aguilles trop au defuer de la char et dou cuir, k’elles ne copent et oevrent la plaie devant la soudure; et puis cope les chiés des aguilles, qu’elles ne blecent lou malaide au dormir, et i met tentes ou drapelz au chiés des aguilles por mues tenir, et les laisse tant que li plaie soit soudee; et ceste maniere de costure as aguilles est plus covenauble en petites plaies, car il i soffist une aguille ou II Li seconde costure si est commune, et est que tu assemble les II chiés dou cuir et les II chiés dou syfac ensamble a une aguille ou il ait I fort fil moien; et quant tu avras perciez ces chiez toz IIII ensamble, si ramoinne l’aguille a la partie ou tu as encomenciet, en la maniere c’on cout les dras; et met d’espaice entre chescune costure la grossece d’un menor doi; ceste costure sevent li home, et je cousi une plaie c’uns hons avoit ou ventre, qui estoit navrez d’un coutel, et estoit li plaie plus d’une palme de grant, et issoit des intestines bien II palmes de grant, et estoit li plaie enmi le ventre.	In small wounds apply what is appropriate, then hold in your hands one minister who can cover the entire wound with their hand and bring together the edges; this is the common method of suturing, where you take a needle or several needles according to the width of the wound, leaving about an inch from the edge of the wound, and insert a needle with sturdy thread at that point; and pierce both sides of the skin with two points inside the subcutaneous layer so that it is thoroughly pierced from one side to the other, bringing together the four corners; then draw the double thread around the needle from both sides, and bring together the two edges of the wound gradually, leaving another inch between them before inserting another needle; then tie the knot as you did with the first needle, and continue doing this according to your need for needles until the entire wound is closed; and let the needles be medium-sized, neither too thin nor too thick, because thin needles cut through all the flesh, and thick ones cannot enter properly: thus they should be of moderate size; do not insert the needles too far from the flesh and skin, so as not to damage the wound before it heals; then trim the ends of the needles so that they do not prick the patient when sleeping, and place small pieces of cloth or thread at the ends to hold them in place, leaving them until the wound is healed; this method of suturing with needles is more suitable for small wounds. A second common method is where you bring together both sides of the skin and subcutaneous tissue on one needle with a sturdy medium-sized thread; when you have pierced these corners all four at once, pull the needle back to the starting point in the manner used to sew cloth; leave an inch between each suture; this technique is known by people. I stitched up a wound that a man had on his belly, which was cut with a knife, and the wound was more than one palm wide, with intestines protruding about two palms wide, located right in the middle of the abdomen.
Je li ramenai l’intestine puis k’il ot esteit XXIIII houres fuer, et fut li plaie soudee jusc’a XV jors, et le curai, et fut sanez.	I returned the intestine to its place after it had been outside for twenty-four hours, and the wound was sealed up until fifteen days, and I treated it, and he was well.
Et li mire l’avoient jugiet qu’il morroit, et ce fut miracle; et ne le curai mie d’oignement, car je estoie en I leu ou on n’en trovoit point, ne nule medicines; et metoie sens plus sus la plaie coton viel II fois le jor, et le lavoie d’aigue de miel tant qu’il fut sanez.	And the physicians had judged that he would die, and it was a miracle; and I did not treat him with ointment, for I was in a place where none could be found, nor any medicines; and I placed old cotton on the wound twice a day, and washed it with honey water until he was well.
Or vos dirai les II propres manieres de cousture: pren l’aguille, et la boute des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens; quant elle a perciet le keur de droit en droit, si lai le chief dou siphac ou cousteit ou tu as bouteit l’aguille, et la fai percier d’autre part des la partie dedens jusc’a celi defuer; et li entendemens de ceste costure si est que tu cous ausi com li peletier font les pelz, et que tu laisses une fois le syfac d’une part, et le reprent d’autre, tant que li costure soit toute acomplie.	Now I will tell you the two proper methods of suturing: take the needle, and pierce from the outer part to the inner; when it has pierced the tissue straight through, lay the head of the suture where you have inserted the needle, and make it pierce again from the inner part outwards; and the understanding of this stitch is that you sew as tailors do with skins, and leave one time the thread on one side, and take it up again on the other, until the entire seam is completed.
Li seconde maniere de costure, que Galiens dist proprement, si est si com aucun font, qui assemblent les II parties ensamble naturelment, et apploient l’un des chief dou syfac a l’autre chief, en teil maniere: fiche une aguille ou chief dou mirach prochiene, et fai percier celui leu soulement, et laisse les II chiés dou syfac; puis torne l’aguille, et la fai percier des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, as II chiés dou syfac; puis fai percier l’un et l’autre des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, en II autres chiés dou mirach que sont on l’autre costeit; et c’est li muedre maniere de costure et li plus commune.	The second method of stitching, which Galen describes properly, is as follows: some people join the two parts naturally together and connect one end of the suture to the other end in such a way: insert a needle at the nearest apex, pierce only that point, and leave both ends of the suture; then turn the needle and pass it from the outer part to the inner part through the two points of the suture; then pierce one and the other from the outer part to the inner part through two other apices on the opposite side; this is the muddied method of stitching and the most common.
Galiens si dist ceste parolle, et aucun le tesmoignent, c’on doit coudre le ventre a II aguilles, ou il ait fil en chescune; et doit on bouter l’une aguille d’une part, et l’autre d’autre, en la maniere de ces qui cousent corroies; et saiches que quant li routure est enmi lou ventre, si est li cousture plus griez que des autres leus dou ventre.	Galen says this and some attest that one should stitch the abdomen with two needles, each having thread; one needle should be inserted from one side and the other from the opposite side, in the manner of those who sew belts; and note that when the rupture is inside the abdomen, the stitching is more difficult than for other areas of the abdomen.
Li jugemens de la plaie si est telz com li jugemens des autres plaies: et est que quant tu trueves la plaie fresche a tout son sanc, ainsois que li ars l’ait muee, si remet arer l’intestine, et lou cout; puis met sus la poudre enjanrant char, et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucun oignement que soit present, tant que li plaie bowe; et chicent li fil, et soient soudez li sifac, et li mirach; puis cure la plaie si com les autres, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu n’as medicines, si met sus, tantost qu’ele comance a giter bowe, coton viel, et le remue II fois le jor tant k’il soit sanez.	The judgment of the wound is such as the judgment of other wounds: and it is that when you find the wound fresh with all its blood, as if the burn had moved it, then reset the intestines, and sew; then apply a powder to heal flesh, and if the burn has moved it, then apply any ointment that is present until the wound starts to close; and stitch the wound, and let the edges stick together and join; then treat the wound as with others until it is healed; and if you do not have medicines, then put on old cotton as soon as it begins to discharge pus, twice a day until it is healed.
Car tu n’as mestier d’autre medicine en plusors dispositions cant les plaies sont simples; et se tu doutes que li plaie ne faice communiteit as membres principelz, si covient ke tu moilles lainne legiere en oile de tempree chalor, ou en oile roset, et la met entor les angres, et desoz les asselles; et s’il sent dolor ou porriture en bouelz, et maintes fois avient, si les clisterize de vin noir tede, et meismement se li porriture vient jusc’a l’intestine; et le perce dedens, et saiches que quant c’est li gros intestines, si est plus legier a saner que li petis.	For you do not need other medicine in many cases where the wounds are simple; and if you doubt that the wound will cause harm to principal members, then it is necessary that you moisten light wool in warm oil, or rose oil, and place it around the angles, and below the armpits; and if there is pain or putrefaction in bowels, which often happens, then administer an enema of cooked black wine, especially if the putrefaction reaches the intestines; and pierce inside, and know that when it is the large intestine, it heals more easily than the small.
Li intestine qui est apelez «jeun» ne puet saner quant il est navrez, et c’est por la planteit des voinnes que i sont, et por la subtiliteit de tout le cors, et l’aprochement de sa nature des ners.	The intestine called "jejunum" cannot heal when it is pierced, and this is due to the smallness of the veins that are there, and the subtlety of the whole body, and the proximity of its nature to the nerves.
Et si li zirbe saut de la plaie, si le remet arrier ausi com l’intestine, tandis qu’il est fres; et s’il est vielz et devenus vers ou noir, si covient que tu lies le leu qui est noir, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne, car il i a voinnes et arteres; puis cope ceu qui est entre le liien, et met les II chiés pendans des la partie desoz la plaie jusque defuer por aligier l’estraction quant li zirbes chiet, et li plaie bowe.	And if the spleen jumps out of the wound, put it back as you would with the intestine, while it is fresh; and if it is old and has turned black or green, then tie off the area that is discolored to prevent blood from seeping through, because there are veins and arteries there; then cut around where you will tie it, and hang the two ends below the wound so that when the spleen falls out again, it eases its extraction, and the wound heals.
de la routure dou boueil	Of the fracture of the eye socket
Quant li intestine est rons, et li plaie est petite, si la puet on restorer en aucuns homes, por ceu que je vis que uns hons fut navrez ou ventre d’une lance; et estoit li plaie au destre de l’estomac, et fut envillie et devint fistule, et en issoit li egestion et li ventositez; je i mis cure selonc ceu que je poi, et ne cessai de subtilier tant qu’il fut sanez, et li leus soudez.	When the intestines are punctured and the wound is small, it can sometimes be repaired in some people, as I saw a man pierced in the belly with a lance; and the wound was on the right side of the stomach, and became inflamed and turned into a fistula, from which came out feces and gas; I applied treatment according to what I could, and did not stop suturing until he was healed, and the flesh sealed.
Et quant je le vis souder, je doutai que li malaides n’eust mal en son ventre; et il n’i ot point de mal, mais demora en millors dispositions, et menjans et bevans; et dirent aucun experimentors que quant il a petite plaie en l’intestine, qu’il doit estre liiez en teil maniere: pren fremis a grans testes, puis assemble les levres de la plaie, et quant li fremis ait overte la bouche, si la met sus les II levres, si qu’elle estraigne sa bouche sus; et puis li cope la teste, et ce se tient si qu’il ne puet desliier, puis met I autre fremit aprés en celle maniere que devant, tant que li plaie soit toute porprise; et cout la plaie.	And when I saw it sealing, I feared the patient might have pain in his belly; but he had no discomfort and improved in disposition, eating and drinking. And some experienced practitioners say that for a small wound in the intestines, one should treat it as follows: take thread with large eyes, then bring together the edges of the wound, and when the needle opens its eye, place it over the two edges so they clamp onto it; then tie off the end securely, and proceed to place another needle after this manner until the entire wound is closed; then sew up the wound.
Cil chief si s’aerdent en l’intestine, et ne vient nulle nuisance au malaide, et se puet on liier l’intestine d’un fil subtil qui est copez de l’intestine d’une beste, en teil maniere: pren le chief de cest fil d’intestine que soit mout descharnez, et puis lie au chief de cest fil I fil de lin subtil tort, puis boute le fil en l’aguille, et en cout l’intestine, et le ramoinne en la routure; et ceste maniere de costure de fremis nen est fuers que selonc la voie de fiance et d’esperance; et se li plaie est grans et large, meismement quant elle est en l’un des grailes intestines, si n’i a engien ne santeit, fuer que subtiliteit.	If the head of the intestine becomes inflamed but causes no harm to the patient, it can be ligated with a fine thread that matches the thickness of an animal's intestine in this way: take the tip of this intestinal thread and strip it bare, then twist a fine linen thread around its tip, put the thread through the needle, and stitch the intestine closed; and this method of stitching is not different from trust and hope; and if the wound is large and wide, especially when it is in one of the great intestines, there is no remedy or safety except for subtlety.
de fistule ou qu’ele soit	of a fistula wherever it may be located
Saiches que toute plaie ou aposteme, quant il enveillist, si est apelee universement «fistule», et meismement quant elle est chevee et rent bowe.	Know that any wound or abscess, when it comes to a head, is generally called a "fistula," and especially when it is drained and becomes hollow.
Et fistule est selonc la verteit nodation fautree dure et blainche, ou on ne sent dolor, et est ausi chevee com li penne d’un oiseil; et aucune fois en saut clere bowe, et autre fois espesse; aucune fois poc, et autre fois assez; et je en ai jai parleit en la division des plaies, que toute plaie que n’est sanee, et il n’i a char, ce n’est fuers que par une des VIIII causes: c’est a savoir, par la petitece dou sanc ou cors; ou por sa malice; ou por ceu qu’il i a char dure dedens, et sus les levres, que n’i laisse naistre char; ou il i a trop de bowe; ou li leus est porris, et li matiere est de male qualiteit; ou li medicine n’est mie bone en la cure; ou por ceu que li corruption est maniere de pestilence; ou por la proprieteit en la region est tardive li digestion, et tarde li santeit, et enflee par nature; ou il i a voinnes ou os: et j’ai ja mostreit toutes ces causes, et les signes, et les cures de medicines en la division.	And a fistula is according to the truth an abnormal knot hard and white, where one does not feel pain, and it is also feathered like the quill of a bird; and sometimes it flows clear fluid, and other times thick; sometimes it is small, and other times enough; and I have already spoken in the division of wounds that any wound which is not healed, and there is no flesh, except for one of the VIII causes: namely, due to the smallness of the blood or body; or because of its malice; or where there is hard flesh inside, and on the edges, leaving no room for new flesh to grow; or it has too much fluid; or the place is rotten, and the matter is poor quality; or the medicine in treatment is not good; or due to corruption being akin to plague; or because of the nature of the region having late digestion, and delayed healing, and swollen by nature; or there are veins in the bones: and I have already shown all these causes, signs, and remedies for medicines in the division.
Or covient que je te faice a savoir la cure de fistule qui est faite par oevre de mains.	Now I shall inform you of the treatment for a fistula which is done by manual work.
Saiches que fistule avient en tous membres dou cors; car il i a fistules que vienent as grans voines, et as arteres, et as ners, ou au syfac, ou a l’intestine, ou a la vessie, ou a aucunes des costes, ou a l’espinee dou dos, ou a aucune jointe des mains ou des piez; et si a teil que vient a la proprieteit dou membre principeil, et as semblans leus.	Know that fistulas can occur in all parts of the body; for there are fistulas that come from large veins, and arteries, and nerves, or on the surface, or in the intestine, or in the bladder, or in some of the ribs, or in the spine, or in any joint of the hands or feet; and some affect the main property of the limb, and similar places.
Et toutes les fistules que sont de ceste maniere sont de grief sanation, et n’i a fors que labour, et ignorance; et se il i a aucune fistule que ne veigne mie jusc’a leu que j’ai dit, et tu as fiance de la cure, et tu la vues conoistre, si pren une tente d’arain ou de fer, se li fistule est droite, si la quier; et se li fistule est torte, si la cerche d’une subtil tente de plonc, car li plons se ploie mues entor la tortuositeit; et se li fistule a mains pertus et tu ne la pues mie bien cerchier par tentes, si la clisterize par l’un des pertus, car la moistors si cort d’un pertus a autre, et la mundifie; puis la quier saigement a ton pooir, que tu conoisses s’il i a os ou nerf, et est chevee em parfont, et demande bien au malaide de la dolor qu’il sent au presser de ta main, et le leu ou il la sent; et quant tu savras vraiement le leu ou elle est, et s’elle est loing de jointure, ou de nerf, ou d’artere ou de voine, ou en aucuns des leus que je t’ai dit, si la cope selonc ceu que je t’ai dit, et oste fuer la fautreure et les chars corrumpues que sont dedens; et puis la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee, et se li fistule est bien parfonde de droit endroit, si covient que tu copes em parfont, tant com tu pues, puis i met tentes moillies en medicine ague, et les boute jusc’au chief de la fistule, tant que li medicine corrode la superfluiteit qui est demoree au fons; et puis i met oignemens enjanrans sainne char, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il n’est sanez par ceu, si le cauterize si com nos avons dit, et se li os est corrompus de la fistule, si le cope.	And all the fistulas of this kind are difficult to heal, and there is no cure other than surgery and ignorance; and if there is any fistula that does not reach the places I mentioned, and you have confidence in its treatment, and want to know it, take a probe made of brass or iron, if the fistula is straight, then insert it; and if the fistula is curved, use a delicate probe made of lead, because lead bends easily around curves; and if the fistula has multiple openings and you cannot properly explore with probes, irrigate through one of the openings, as moisture quickly passes from one opening to another, and clean it; then gently press your hand to find out if there are bones or nerves, and feel precisely where it is, and carefully ask the patient about the pain they feel when you press, and where they feel it; and once you truly know where it is, and whether it is far from a joint, nerve, artery, vein, or in any of the places I mentioned, then cut according to what I have said, and remove all the pus and corrupted flesh inside; and continue treating until it heals, and if the fistula is deeply straight, you must cut deeply as much as possible, then place wet probes soaked in astringent medicine into its depths, so that the medicine dissolves the remaining excess at the bottom; and then apply healing ointments to regenerate new tissue until it is healed; and if it does not heal by this method, cauterize it as we have described, and if the bone has been corrupted by the fistula, remove it.
Se voinne ou ners ne te greve ou membres principelz, si com nos avons dit; et se li os est descovers, et il i a corruption et noiror, si lou reis tant que li corruption soit toute ostee, puis le cure de choses enjanrans char tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il n’est sanez, et rent bowe si com devant, saiches que tu n’es mie alez jusc’a font: si descuevre et quier tant que tu soies au fons, et oste toute la corruption, puis restore le leu; et s’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien.	If a vein or nerve does not cause trouble in the principal members as we have said; and if the bone is exposed, and there is corruption and blackness, remove it until all corruption is gone, then treat with substances that heal flesh until it is healthy; and if it is not healthy, and you need to go deeper, expose and search until you reach the bottom, and remove all corruption, then restore the place; and if it is thus healthy, that is well.
Se ceu non, saiches que la corruption est trop en parfont, que tu n’i pues avenir; si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier a nature; et s’il i a i petit os corrumput, et tu le pues traire as tenailles, si l’estrai a I estrument covenauble a ceu, et s’il i a maint os, si les trai trestoz, ne n’en laissier nes un; et se li moistor te fait contraire, et il n’i a error ne paour, si cope et moistor et char, et delivre les os.	If not, know that the corruption is too deep for you to reach; there is no other remedy but to leave it to nature; and if there is a small corrupt bone, and you can pull it with pincers, extract it with suitable instruments, and if there are many bones, remove them all without leaving any; and if the moisture opposes you, and there is no mistake or fear, cut through flesh and bone, and free the bones.
Et se tu ne les pues oster a une houre, si met sus la plaie chose enjanrant porriture, et laisse tant que li leus soit porris entor les os, et adonc si avront plus legierement les os; et se c’est uns grans os, si com de jambe ou de cuisse, si reis tant soulement la corruption tant que li noiror soit toute ostee, puis restoure la plaie; et s’il en i a grant partie dou corrumput, et vient jusc’a mole de l’os; si le covient soier et coper tout jusc’a la corruption, et puis le cure tant qu’il soit soudez; et je te dirai d’une fistule qui avint I home en sa jambe, si que tu i preignes exemple et aide en ton ovraige.	And if you cannot remove them in one hour, place on the wound something that generates putrefaction, and leave it until the flesh is rotten around the bones; then they will have more easily the bones. And if it is a large bone, such as from a leg or thigh, reduce only the corruption so that all blackness is removed, then restore the wound; and if there is much of the corrupted part coming to the bone tissue; you must scrape and cut away all the corruption, and then treat it until it heals. And I will tell you about a fistula that happened in a man's leg, so that you may take an example and aid in your work.
Il fut I jovencelz entor XXX ans, qui ot une dolor en sa jambe d’une cause que vint dedens le cors, tant que les matieres vinrent a la jambe, et fut enflee d’un gros aposteme, et n’ot point de cause defuer por ovrir; mais li mire par lor folie ovrerent tant sus que li apostemes ovri, et en corroient mout de matieres, et devint fistule, et i vint mout de pertus que tuit gitoient bowe et moistor dou cors; et maint mire i mirent cure entor II ans, et n’i ot nul saige en l’art de mains, tant que je i fui apelez, et vi sa jambe et les medicines dont on le curoit, et ceu que corroit par les pertus a grant cors; et devenoit rouges li cors dou jouvenceil, et avoit color citrine.	There was a young man around thirty years old who had pain in his leg due to something that came inside the body, until the matter reached the leg and it swelled with an abscess which had no reason to burst; but the doctors, through their folly, cut so much on top of it that they opened the abscesses and let out a lot of matter, causing it to become a fistula with many openings where all pus and body moisture went; and many doctors treated him for two years without any skilled hand in the art, until I was called to it, and saw his leg and the medicines used to treat him, as well as what came out through the openings into his large body; and the young man's skin turned red and had a citrine color.
Je boutai une tente en l’un de ces pertus, et puis cerchai toz les pertus, et trovai que li uns venoit encontre l’autre de toutes les parties de la jambe.	I pitched a tent in one of these holes, and then searched all the holes, and found that they came together from all parts of the leg.
Je me hastai donques, et copai en l’un des pertus tant que je descovri une partie de l’os, et le trovai corrumput et perciet, et venoit li corruption jusc’a l’os dedens; je soiai ceu qui m’aparissoit de l’os corrumput, et cuidai qu’il n’i eust autre corruption, fuer que celi que je ostai; et comensai a restourer la plaie de medicines sodans par lonc tens, et ne pot souder; et puis rencomensai, et descovri l’os si com devant, et trovai la corruption continuee en l’os, et la soiai, et puis l’ostai, et me penai de souder le leu; mais je ne pou tant que je copai entor une palme de l’os, et le traï fuer a tout son mole, puis le restourai de medicines; et il fut sanez et soudez hastanment, et ne covint plus rencomencier l’ovraige fors por la foibleté dou malaide, qui ne pooit soffrir, et por la paour de mort que je avoie de lui.	I then hurried and cut into one of the holes until I discovered a part of the bone, which was corrupted and perforated, and the corruption reached deep inside the bone; I removed what appeared to be corrupted bone, thinking there would be no further corruption beyond what I had taken out; and I began to treat the wound with medicines for a long time, but it could not heal; then I started over again, cut into the bone as before, and found the corruption continuing in the bone, so I removed it, and tried to mend the place; but no matter how much I worked around one palm's length of the bone, down to its marrow, after treating with medicines, it healed quickly and firmly, except for restarting the work due to the patient’s weakness, which could not endure it, and my fear of death.
Car por l’evacuation sanglotoit sovent, mais il fut sanez entierement, et nasquit en leu de l’os une char dure, et fut de bone disposition et n’ot point de nuisement ne de contraire dou tout en tout, ne a l’aleir ne a venir.	For often there was an evacuation of blood, but he remained entirely healthy, and in the place of the bone grew a hard tissue, and he had good health and suffered no harm or contraindication whatsoever, neither going nor coming.
Et se li os est brisiez en aucun leu dou cors, si le covient soier en ceste maniere: pren I liien, et l’estrain au chief de l’os qui apert, et comande aucun k’il l’estende en haut; et met I autre lien de lainne plus gros dou premier liien, et le lie sus la char qui est desor l’os, et estent le chief, si que tu traies la char corrumpue au desoz, et descuevre la char sus le leu ou tu vues soier, que li soie ne blece la char; et met I tison ou une tauble desoz l’os por mues coper la char corrumpue; et covient tant soier com on puet veoir et sentir la corruption, et soier ancor autre fois.	And if the bone is broken in any place of the body, it must be treated in this manner: take a linen bandage, and stretch it over the part of the bone that is visible, and have someone hold it taut; then take another thicker linen bandage and wrap it around the flesh covering the bone, stretching it so you draw the corrupted flesh inward, and expose the flesh where you wish to treat, ensuring the salve does not harm the flesh; place a cautery or a tablet under the bone to cut away the corrupted flesh; and one must continue treating until one can see and feel that all corruption is gone, and repeat this process.
Et se li os est corrumpus, et n’apert mie, et li corruptions est en mileu ou en une partie, si descuevre la char toute; puis met I tison desoz, et puis soie des l’une partie a l’autre la corruption, et soit li soieure dou lonc de la corruption I poc, si com nos avons dit; et se li corruptions est en la jointure, si cope la jointure corrumpue, et soie l’os ou elle contient de l’autre part; et se li corruptions est en la continuation des II jointes, si n’i a autre angien que dou coper; et se li corruptions est ou poignil de la main, ou ou poignil dou piet, si est mout fort celle chose, mais toutevoie il covient que tu enquieres celle corrosion, coment elle t’apert; et la mundifie en toutes les manieres que tu pues, mais que li voine ou li nerf ne te faicent contraire; et saiches que li incisoire et les soies por coper ces os sont maintes, selonc l’assise des os et l’aparance d’ous, et lor grossece et lor subtiliteit, et lor grandor et lor petitece, et lor duresce; et por ceu covient il apareillier a chescune semblance d’ovraige son estrument; et saiches que l’uevre te moustrera l’estrument dont tu avras mestier, selonc la conissance de cest art, et le tesmoignaige des manieres des maladies; si porpense l’estrument dont tu as mestier selonc ceu qu’il le covient.	And if the bone is corrupted and it does not appear clearly, and the corruption is in the middle or in a part of it, then uncover all the flesh; then place an ember underneath, and then scrape the corruption from one side to the other along the length of the corruption as we have said; and if the corruption is at the joint, then cut out the corrupted joint and scrape the bone on the opposite side; and if the corruption is in the continuation between two joints, there is no way but to cut it; and if the corruption is at the finger or toe joint, that thing is very strong, but still you must investigate this corrosion as it appears to you; and cleanse it in all possible ways, but do not let veins or nerves hinder you; and know that the instruments for cutting these bones vary according to the position of the bones and their appearance, their thickness and fineness, their size and smallness, their hardness; and therefore it is necessary to prepare an instrument suitable for each kind of work; and know that your work will show you the tool you need according to the knowledge of this art and the testimony of various diseases; therefore consider the tool you need based on what is appropriate.
dou feu	of fire
Li chiés porrissent ou par cause dedens, ou par cause defuer; et quant tu avras medicinee celle corrosion par la cure des medicines, et il ne profitent mie, si covient coper celui membre jusques au leu ou li corrosion vient, si que li malaides eschaipe par ceu de la mort, ou par la malice, qui est plus grans, de la defaute dou membre; et li signes si est que li membres devient noir, si qu’il semble qu’il soit ars dou feu, et porrist aprés la noiror, pues va celle corrosions de membre em membre, et prent par tout le cors; si te haste dou coper, et se c’est par la percussion d’aucunes venimouses bestes, si com scorpion de mer et wivre et semblans, se li corrosion est au chief dou doi, si le cope, et ne li doner mie espaice de venir jusc’a la main.	The head may rot from within or due to external causes; and when you have treated that corruption with medicine but it does not improve, then you must amputate the limb up to where the corrosion begins so that the patient escapes either death or the greater malice of losing a limb; and the signs are that the limb turns black as if burned by fire, and it rots after turning black, spreading from one limb to another throughout the body; therefore hurry with the amputation, and if this is due to the bite of venomous creatures such as sea scorpions or vipers and similar ones, and if the corruption reaches the head of the arm, then amputate it and do not give it space to reach the hand.
Et s’elle vient jusc’a la main, si la cope a la jointe, si que la corrosion ne viegne jusc’a bras; et s’elle vient au bras, si le cope au coute; et s’elle passe le coute, c’est li mors, et n’i vaut amenistremens fuers que li quantitez de sa vertut; et tot ensi fai quant li corrosion vient ou piet: s’elle vient en la premiere jointe, si la cope aprés l’autre jointe; et s’elle vient ou piet, si cope tout le piet; et s’elle monte en la jambe, si cope a la jointure dou genoil; et s’elle vient desus le genoil, si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier le malaide a mort; et li maniere dou coper ou dou soier le membre si est que tu le lie desus et desoz, et estende uns menistres l’un des liiens aval, et uns autres ministres l’autre liien amont, et tu dessevre la char qui est entre les II liiens a I spatumile large, tant que li os soit descovers; puis le cope ou soie, et met de chescune part I drapeil de lin, si que li soie ne touche le leu sain, et viegne au malaide autre lesion et aposteme chaus.	And if it comes to the hand, cover at the joint, so that the corrosion does not reach the arm; and if it comes to the arm, cut with a knife; and if it passes the knife, death is certain, and there are no remedies except for the quantity of its virtue; and do this exactly when the corrosion reaches the foot: if it comes to the first joint, cover after the second joint; and if it comes to the foot, cover the whole foot; and if it climbs up the leg, cover at the knee joint; and if it comes above the knee, there is no other remedy but to leave the patient to die; and the manner of cutting or covering the limb is that you bind above and below, and extend one minister with a string downwards, and another minister upwards, and separate the flesh which is between the two strings at one finger's breadth wide until the bone is uncovered; then cut or cover, and place on each side a piece of linen so that the dressing does not touch healthy skin, and cause no other injury or abscess to the patient.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient quant tu oevres, si cauterize le leu hastanment, ou tu met sus aucunes poudres restraignans; puis revien a ta medicine tant qu’elle soit acomplie, puis lie le membre navreit d’un liien covenauble, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et je te conterai k’il avint a I home en som piet: il li avint une noiror qui sembloit arsure de feu, et celle corrosion vint premier en son doi dou piet, tant qu’elle porprist tout le piet; et quant li hons vit la corrosion, si se hasta de coper le piet, et fut sanez; et lonc tens aprés li revint li corrosion ou doi de la main, et il vint a moi, et je li mis sus choses repercussives aprés la mundification dou cors, et ne pot cesser li corrosions; et il vot que je li copasse la main, et je ne vou, que je avoie esperance de repercuter la matiere; et doutai ausi que se je tailloie sa main, qu’il ne morist, car li vertus de l’ome estoit foible; et il se despera toz, et revint en sa terre, et se hasta de coper sa main, et fut sanez; et je n’ai ceu conteit fuers que por ceu c’on faice autreteil, s’on en a mestier.	And if bleeding occurs when you treat it, cauterize the area quickly or apply some constricting powders; then return to your medicine until it is complete, and bind the injured limb with a suitable bandage, and care for it until it heals; and I will tell you what happened to one man: he had a blackness that seemed like a burn from fire, and this corrosion first appeared on his big toe, spreading over the entire foot; when the man saw the corrosion, he hurried to amputate his foot and healed; after a long time, the corrosion returned to his thumb, and he came to me, and I applied counter-irritants after cleansing his body, but could not stop the corrosion; he wanted me to cut off his hand, but I refused because I hoped to repel the matter; I also feared that if I cut his hand, he would die, as his constitution was weak; he became desperate and returned home, hurriedly amputated his hand, and healed; and I have no other content than for such cases where there is a need.
Aucune fois vient aposteme en leu charnut, et demore si longement qu’il fait grant assemblee de bowe; et puis ront et perce, et en saut li bowe, et demoure li leus vuis, ausi com uns vasselz; et li cuir qui est desus est ausi subtilz com I drapelz deliiez, et ne corront mie jusc’a l’os, ne jusc’au nerf, et telz maladie si est apelee «sain», et n’est mie apelee «fistule»; mais s’elle est si alongie qu’elle viegne jusc’a l’os em parfont, si est apelee «fistule»; et li cuire si est que tu cope celui cuir tout entor, et meismement quant il est subtilz, ausi com uns drapelz; et ne s’aert mie por sa corruption.	Sometimes an abscess appears in the flesh and persists so long that it accumulates a great deal of pus; then it bursts and drains, leaving behind a cavity similar to a vessel; and the skin above is as thin as fine linen, not extending to the bone or nerve; such a condition is called "sinus" and is not called "fistula"; but if it extends so far that it reaches the bone in depth, then it is called "fistula"; and you should cut around this skin entirely, similarly when it is thin like linen; and it does not change due to its corruption.
Et se tu as fiance que li cuirs s’aerde, et li corruption n’est mie en parfont, et li cuir est espés de char, si le cure de clistere ensi: regarde se li seins est grans, et li bowe qui en ist est de puant odor, adonques le clisterize de medicine egiptiaine qui est ensi faite: prenez aisil, et oile, et litargire, igalment, et metez cuire en I vassel au feu, tant que li medicine soit rouge, et deviegne ausi espesse com miel; et puis pren de ceu selonc ta necessiteit, et le font en aigue et en miel, et en clisterize lou sein, et estraint le pertus; et laisse la medicine ens par II houres, puis l’estrai en espreignant; fai ce mout de fois, tant que li seins soit mondefiiez, et soit ostee li puor; et aucune fois est clisterizeis d’aigue de cendres, quant ceste medicine n’est presens, et est que tu preignes cendres de fust de vigne, et giete aigue desus, puis la coule, et en clisterize, tant que tu saiches que li seins est bien mondez; et se li malaides ne le puet soffrir, ne la medicine egiptiaine ne l’aigue de cendres, si le clisterize d’aigue et de miel ou il ait un poc de litargire broiet; ou tu la clistirize de miel et de vin melleit, que li mielz ait proprieteit de mundifiier et de laver, et li vins fait aerdre le sain; et quant tu as ce fait, et tu as fiance que li seins est bien mundifiiez, si le clisterize de ceu que fait naistre char en li, et est que tu preignes emplaustre diafinit, et le font avec oile roset et en vin; ou tu le clisterize d’aucunes medicines et d’oignemens, dont j’ai dit les proprietez ou traitier des oignemens; et se li pertus dou sein est petis, et li cainne dou clistere n’i puet entrer, si l’eslarge d’un fer un poc, et met ens une tente de l’oignement egiptiein, ou oignement basilicon, tant k’il soit eslargiez; et se li plaie est trop large, si la cout et i laisse tant soulement I leu ou li clistere puisse entrer, et se li pertus que giete bowe est au desus, si le cope ou plus bas leu que i est.	And if you believe that the skin will heal and the corruption is not deep, and the skin is thick with flesh, then treat it with an enema in this way: check if the breast is large, and the pus coming from it has a foul odor, then give an enema of Egyptian medicine made thus: take myrrh, oil, and litharge equally, put copper in a vessel over fire until the medicine turns red and becomes as thick as honey; then take this according to your need, mix with water and honey, and administer the breast enema, restraining the anus; leave the medicine inside for two hours, then expel it by straining; do this many times until the breast is cleaned, and the foulness removed; sometimes you give an enema of ash water when this medicine is not present, which involves taking vine wood ashes, pouring water over them, filtering it, and administering as an enema until you know the breast is well cleansed; if the patient cannot tolerate either the Egyptian medicine or the ash water, then administer an enema of water and honey mixed with a small amount of ground litharge; or give an enema of honey and wine mixed, where the honey has the property to clean and wash, while the wine helps heal the wound; once you have done this, and believe the breast is well cleansed, give an enema of medicine that promotes tissue growth, such as a diaphoretic plaster made with rose oil and in wine; or use some medicines and ointments whose properties I have discussed in treating ointments; if the anus opening for pus discharge is small and the catheter cannot enter, enlarge it slightly with an iron instrument, then place an Egyptian ointment cloth or a basilicon ointment over it until it is sufficiently enlarged; if the wound is too large, sew it up leaving only one spot where the enema can be inserted; if the pus discharge opening is higher, cut it lower down where it is.
Car quant li bowe est en parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char; et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues, si appareille en tel maniere que li bowe corre au plus bas leu que i est, car quant li bowe est parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues, si apareille en teil maniere: que li bowe corre legierement aval, et n’i lassier rien de la bowe; et pren medicines consolidatives por mettre sor le sain, et estent sus I drapeil de lin que cuevre tout le sain; puis cope as forces endroit le pertus dou sein I poc plus large dou premier, pues estent oignement souef sus I autre drapel selonc la quantiteit dou pertus, et le met sus le pertus dou sain por aligier la bowe, et n’oster mie le grant drapeil fuers que aprés maint jor une fois; et celui qui est sor le pertus dou sein, oste sovent por oster la bowe, et saiches ceu que corra de la bowe, se c’est venin ou poc ou assez, ou digeste, ou indigeste; et pren warde se li patiens sent dolor ou nom, et s’il i a aposteme ou non, et quant ta medicine s’est en teil maniere estendue et tu vois la nature que saut sus le pertus dou sain, si saiches que li seins s’aert ja, et aproche li santez; et puis le deslie le matin, ou le tier jor, et quant tu delies la plaie, si chainge I autre drapeil, et renovele l’oignement.	For when the bowe (swelling or tumor) is deep, it does not allow flesh to regenerate; and if you cannot cut beneath the breast as desired, prepare it in such a way that the bowe flows downward to the lowest place where it is; for when the bowe is deep, it does not allow flesh to regenerate, and if you cannot cut beneath the breast as desired, prepare it in this manner: that the bowe flows gently downwards, leaving nothing of the bowe; then apply medicines that consolidate over the wound, and cover all the wound with a linen cloth; then cut around the force of the opening of the wound a little wider than the first, place an ointment under another piece of cloth according to the size of the wound opening, and put it on the wound opening to alleviate the bowe, and do not remove the large cloth until after several days once; and that which is on the wound opening, often remove to remove the bowe, and examine what flows from the bowe, whether it is venomous or a little or enough, or digestible or undigestible; take care if the patient feels pain or numbness, and whether there is an abscess or not, and when your medicine has been applied in this manner and you see that nature works over the wound opening, then know that the bowe starts to heal and approach health; and then untie it in the morning or on the third day, and when you untie the wound, change another cloth, and renew the ointment.
Et se li seins giete bowe indigeste aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie.	And if the stomach throws up undigested food after many days, know that the stomach does not settle.
Et se venins subtilz cort aprés lonc tens, si ne te desperer mie de la santeit, car li santez aproche.	And if subtle poisons affect after a long time, do not despair of recovery, for health is near.
Car il i a homes cui tarde enjanremens de char en ses plaies, et de ces que font le contraire; et se bowe indigeste saut dou sein aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie; et se li seins tarde d’aerdre, et est porloigniez, si ajoste medicines sechans moistes en substance et seches en vertut, si com oignement diafinit, car il i a grant partie de vitriole, et c’est li derriene medicine; pren oignement dyafinit, et le font avec oile roset, et l’arose de viel vin igal en substance; puis le confit et en use; et ceu meisme fait mielz cuit engroissiez, quant oignemens dyafinit n’est presens, ou tu pren mirre et aloen et encens, et le broie, et le poudre sus le miel quant il est sor le feu; et puis en glue I drapel, et l’estent sor le sein, et aucune fois i aministre on aristologe longe, et racines de lis celeste, qui est ausi com farine de veces et centoire; et en use de simples ou de compostes: broie les, et en fai poudre, et met sus le miel que j’ai dit, et en use; et se li cure est alongie, et n’est curez par ceste cure, adonc saiches que la corruptions est em parfont, et fait empression en l’os, ou as membres durs, ou as liemens; si le cure de la cure de fistule, si com nos avons dit ci devant.	For there are those to whom the healing of meat in their wounds takes time, and others who do the opposite; and if undigested food comes up from the stomach after many days, know that the stomach does not settle; and if digestion is delayed and prolonged, add drying medicines in substance and drying in virtue, such as a diaphoretic ointment, for it contains much vitriol, and this is the last medicine; take a diaphoretic ointment made with rose oil, and rinse it with equal parts of old wine; then boil it and use it; and this same method works better when thickened, when no diaphoretic ointment is present: take myrrh and aloes and incense, and grind them, and powder them over the honey while it is on the fire; then glue a small piece of cloth to it, and apply it to the stomach; sometimes administer an aromatic long strip, and roots of celestial lilies, which are like wheat flour and centaury; use simples or compounds: grind them, make powder, mix with the honey I mentioned, and use; and if the cure is prolonged and not healed by this treatment, then know that corruption has set in, affecting bones, hard members, or ligaments; treat it according to the fistula cure as we have said before.
de l’aposteme de l’ungle	of the abscess of the nail
Panarice est un aposteme que naist desoz l’ungle dou pouchiet de la main, ou dou piet, ou par aventure naist en autres dois; et quant il est envielliez, et on n’i prent garde, si i vient I aposteme chaus, et corront et giete bowe tant qu’elle corront la racine de l’ungle, et par aventure la corront toute; et vient li corrosions jusc’a l’os, tant qu’il i vient dolor puant, et est li chiés dou doi larges, et est li color fuxe.	Panaritis is an abscess that arises beneath the nail of the hand or foot, or occasionally on other fingers; and when it ages and no care is taken, a soft abscess comes, running and discharging pus until it reaches the root of the nail, and sometimes it runs all the way through; and corrosion reaches to the bone, causing foul-smelling pain, and the head of the finger becomes wide, and its color turns bad.
Quant tu le cures si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, si covient que tu copes a i. fer toute la superfluiteit qui est demoree de l’ungle, puis cauterize la plaie aprés.	When you treat it as we have said in the section, and the treatment is of no use, then you must cut away all the excess that remains from the nail, then cauterize the wound afterwards.
Li cauteres est mout grans aide se li os est sains, et li ungle est sainne; et se li ungle apresse la char ens, et l’encomence a poindre, et la blece, si covient que tu mettes lou rait desoz l’ungle que point la char, et la boute en haut, et cope celi char subtilment et legierement, et met sus le remenant de la char medicines ardans et corrosives por oster tout; puis le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	The cautery is a great help if the bone is sound and the nail is healthy; and if the nail presses into the flesh, and it begins to hurt, and swells, then you must place the edge under the nail that is pressing on the flesh, and lift it up, and cut away that part of the flesh carefully and lightly, and apply the rest of the remaining flesh with burning and corrosive medicines to remove everything; then cure it with ointments until it is healed.
Et se li corrosion est en l’os, si le cope, et trai fuer, car tant com li os corrumpus i est, si ne puet saner; et se tu vois le doi corrumpre, si le cope en I des nous si com il est devant dit, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il est ferus, et boutez, et il sent grant dolor, si covient que tu le sainnes premier; puis cope l’ungle dou spatumile agut en taillant de travers desus, et warde que li taille ne viegne jusc’a la char qui est desoz l’ungle, car li malaides sentiroit trop grant dolor; et s’il avient, si met chose sus qui apaise.	And if the corrosion is in the bone, then cut it out and use force, for as long as the corrupted part of the bone remains, it cannot heal; and if you see that the bone is damaged, then cut it off as previously described, and treat it until it heals; and if it is pierced and there is great pain, then first stop the bleeding; then carefully cut the nail diagonally across, being careful not to cut into the flesh beneath the nail, for this would cause too much pain; and if it happens, apply something that soothes.
la dolor dou sourdoit de la main	the pain of the stiffness of the hand
Li dois ajostez qui naist en mains d’aucuns homes par aventure est toz charnus, et par aventure i a teil ou il a osses, et aucune fois i a ungle, et aucun d’aus naissent en la racine de la jointure, ou li naissance est en aucuns nous des dois.	The second bone that is born in the hands of some men is entirely flesh, and sometimes there are bones, and at times it has a nail, and some of them are born at the root of the joint, where the birthplace is in some people's case.
Cil qui naist en aucune nout dou doi ne se muet, et cil qui naist a la jointure dou doi, par aventure se muet; la taille de celui qui est charnus si est legiere, en teil maniere: taille le en sa racine d’un large spatumile.	Those who are born with any knot in the finger do not move, and those who are born at the joint of the finger sometimes move; the size of the one that is flesh is very small, in such a way: measure it from its root with a broad spatula.
Cil qui naist en la racine de la jointure si est grief a curer: si te tien dou coper.	Those who are born at the root of the joint are difficult to treat: be careful when cutting them.
En celui qui naist ou doit au derrien nout, si covient que tu copes premier la char reondement jusc’a l’os, puis cope l’os a une soie convenable a ceu, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	In the one who is born or should be at the rear end, you must first cut the flesh roundly until the bone, then cut the bone in a single stroke suitable for him, then treat it until it is healed.
Li soudemens que vient as dois ensamble vient par naissance, ou par soudement de plaie, ou par arsure de feu, ou par semblans choses.	The swelling that comes to the two together comes by birth, or by inflammatory reaction of a wound, or by burning with fire, or by similar things.
Si couvient que tu copes celle soudeure, si que li doit repairent selonc lor formes naturelz; puis met entre dous tentes ou drapelz moilliez en oile roset, qu’il ne se soudent; ou tu met entre dous pieces de plonc subtilz, tant que li leus soit soudez, si com il covient.	You must cut that swelling so that the parts repair according to their natural forms; then place between two cloths or moistened towels in rose oil, so they do not swell again; or you can place between two pieces of fine wool, until the wound is sealed as it should be.
Se soudemens vient a aucun de ses dois avec la paume, si cope celle sodure si com il covient.	If swelling comes to either of the two with the palm, then cut that swelling as it should be done.
des vils	of worms
Vis sont voinnes grosses envoloupees pleines de superfluitez melancoliouses, que vienent em plusors membres dou cors; et plus avient en jambes de ces qui vont a piet et qui travaillent et portent, que a autres.	Veins are thick and wrapped, full of melancholic excesses, which occur in many parts of the body; and they happen more often in the legs of those who walk and carry burdens than in others.
Il covient donques que tu li aministres aucune fois espurgement de cole, et puis le saine de la basilique.	It is necessary then that you administer an enema at times, and then treat them with basilicon salve.
Li cure de fer si est selonc II manieres: l’une est c’on les cope, et traie on fuer le sanc noir; et li autre maniere si est que tu lieves la voinne, et la trai toute fuer.	The treatment with iron is according to two methods: one is that you cut and draw out the black blood; and the other method is that you open the vein and draw it all out.
Li taille si est selonc ceste maniere: arose li premier la jambe d’aigue chaude mout fort, tant que li gros sans soit subtiliiez, puis estrain la jambe dou malaide des desus la cuixe jusc’a la partie desoz le genoil; puis cope la voinne en I leu, ou en II ou en III, d’une taille large, puis eslieve et trair fuer le sanc noir a ta main, des l’un chief jusc’a l’autre, tant que tant de sans en isse com li vertus dou malaide puet soffrir; et puis la lie, et li comande qu’il se teigne de viandes enjanrant cole noire; et recomence l’evacuation et la sainie quant les voinnes sont plainnes, et nuist au malaide.	The procedure for bleeding is as follows: first wash the leg with very hot water until the thick blood becomes thin, then strain the patient's leg from above the thigh to below the knee; then cut the vein in one place or two or three, making a wide incision, then lift and draw out the black blood with your hand, from one end to the other, as much blood as the patient can tolerate; then bandage it, and instruct them to eat foods that promote bowel movement; and repeat the evacuation and treatment when the veins are full again, and do not harm the patient.
Li alevemens de li est selonc ceste maniere: reis la jambe dou malaide, s’il i a mout de poil, puis le met ou bain, et li arose la jambe d’aigue chaude tant qu’elle deviegne rouge, et enflent les voinnes; et se tu n’as point de baing, si le chaufe au feu, et puis le cope endroit la voinne dou lonc au chief dou genoil, ou en la partie desoz a la cheville; puis aoevre le cuir a l’oncine, et escorche la voinne de chescune part, tant qu’ele apere quant on la sent; et on la voit rouge et noire, et quant elle entre ou cuir si semble ausi com une corde blainche; puis boute le rait desoz, tant qu’ele soit alevee dou cuir, et puis la pent a l’oncine legier, puis le cope en I autre leu ensus III dois; puis escorche le cuir sus la voinne tant qu’ele apere, puis la lieve au rais, si com tu as fait, et la pent a un autre uncine, si com tu as fait premiers; puis cope une autre taille, ou plusors se tu en as mestier, puis la lieve, et la cope au doi dou piet, puis la trai et lieve jusc’a la seconde taille; puis l’estrai de taille en taille, tant qu’elle isse toute fuer, puis la cope; et se tu ne la pues traire et lever, si i boute une aguille a tout I fil fort double, et la lie et la trai, et i boute desoz I rait, et torne ta main d’une part et d’autre, tant qu’il en isse; et garde qu’elle ne cope, car s’elle cope, si ne la puet on traire ne lever, et en vient nuisement au malaide; et quant tu l’as toute traite, si met sor le leu de la plaie laine moillie en vin et en oile roset; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	The lifting of the vein is done in this manner: raise the patient's leg, if there is much hair, then place it in a bath, and wash the leg with hot water until it becomes red and the veins swell; and if you have no bath, warm it by fire, and then cut along the vein from the shin to the knee, or at the part below the ankle; then work the skin with the scalpel, and strip the vein on each side until it feels taut when touched; and it appears red and black, and when it enters the skin it seems like a white cord; then lift the vein under the skin as much as possible, and then press it gently with an uncine, as you did before; then make another incision above three fingers width; then strip the skin over the vein until it feels taut, then lift it again as you did previously, and press it with a different uncine, as you did earlier; then cut another length or more if needed, then lift it, and cut at the toe joint, then draw and lift up to the second incision; then pull from one length to the next until it is all lifted out, then cut; and if you cannot draw and lift it, put a needle through the entire double thread, tie and pull it, and place a reed underneath, move your hand back and forth until it comes free; and beware that it does not tear, for if it tears, it cannot be drawn or lifted, which is harmful to the patient; when you have finished pulling it all out, put wool soaked in wine and rose oil on the wound site; treat the wound until the patient is healed.
Et se li vis est contraite et torte et envoloupee ensamble, et ele n’est mie droite, si com nos avons dit, si covient que tu la fendes tortement, mais ne la coper mie; et la trai si com nos avons devant dit.	And if the vein is constricted and twisted and wrapped together, and it is not straight, as we have said, then you must cut it sharply, but do not sever it; and draw it out as we have previously stated.
Li forme dou fer dont on cope la vis si est corbes, et ne trenche mie, qu’il ne cope la voinne; et est de grosse corbeure, car s’il estoit subtilz, si coperoit la voine, mais soit gros si com nos avons dit, et ci est li forme:	The shape of the iron with which one cuts the vein is curved and does not cut, so as not to sever the vein; it has a thick curve, for if it were fine, it would cut the vein, but it should be thick as we have said, and this is its shape:
de la voinne civile	of the civil vein
Ceste voinne est enjanree en jambes, en chaudes parties ou il ne naist herbes ne arbre, et en terre ou il n’a point de moistor; et par aventure naist autre part qu’en jambes, et ceu avient de la porriture que vient desoz le cuir, si com il vient dedens le cors serpens et vers, enjanrez entre cuir et char.	This vein arises in the legs, in warm parts where no herbs or trees grow, and in dry ground that lacks moisture; and it may arise elsewhere than in the legs, and this happens due to putrefaction beneath the skin, as it occurs inside the body as worms and vermin, arising between the skin and flesh.
Et se li signes de l’encomencement de ceste voinne si est qu’il vient en la jambe une tres grans enflammation, puis se chainge li leus, et comence li voinne fors issir, ausi com une racine d’une plante.	And if the signs of the beginning of this vein are that there comes a very large inflammation in the leg, then the location changes, and the vein begins to come out, like the root of a plant.
Quant li chiés apert, si covient que tu envoloupes entor une piece de plonc des une З et demi jusc’a II З., et la noe, et laisse le plonc pendant a la jambe, et totes les fois qu’il en ist point au defuer, si l’envoloupe entor le plonc, et la nowe; et s’elle est trop longe, si en cope une partie, et envoloupe le remenant, et ne la coper mie en sa racine, tant qu’elle soit toute issue; car se tu la copes, si rentre en la char, et fait venir aposteme et porriture ou leu, et male maladie; por la queil chose il covient qu’elle soit traite poc et poc jusc’a chief, et n’en remaigne rien ou cors; et est aucune fois ceste voinne quant elle est traite de V paumes de lonc, ou de X, et uns hons vint ja a moi, a cui elle issit de X paumes de long, et quant tu la copes, si boute I rais ou pertus, et la perce jusc’a fons, si que tout en isse; et soit vuidie li matiere qui est dedens, et amenistre au leu medicines enjanrans porriture aucun jor, puis le cure si com les apostemes.	When the vein is open, you must wrap it around a piece of linen one and a half to two fingers wide, tie it up, and let the linen hang from the leg; every time there is a point where it starts to protrude, wrap it around the linen and tie it again. If it is too long, cut off part of it and wrap the remaining part, but do not cut it at its root until it is completely out; because if you cut it, it will re-enter the flesh and cause an abscess and putrefaction in that place, leading to a bad illness. Therefore, treat this vein little by little until there is nothing left on the body; sometimes this vein can be five palms long when treated or ten palms, as one patient of mine had it come out ten palms long, and when you cut it, pus comes out from one hole or perforation, so pierce it to its depth so that everything comes out; empty the matter inside, then apply medicines to expel putrefaction for a few days, and then treat it as you would an abscess.
Et aucune fois a ceste voinne mains rains, et meismement quant elle apert en la jointure dou piet, ou ou piet, et i vient mout de pertus, et dont il saut rains; cure le donques si com nos avons dit devant.	And sometimes this vein is deeper, especially when it appears in the ankle joint, or at the foot, and there is much perforation, and thus it bleeds heavily; treat it then as we have said before.
des vers qui naissent entre cuir et char	worms that are born between the skin and flesh
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «maladie de buef», por ceu qu’elle avient maintes fois as bués, et est un petis vers qui naist entre cuir et char, et va par tout le cors montant et dessendant, et le sent om bien a l’aler de membre en membre, tant qu’il desront le cuir ou il vait, et saut fuer; et est enjanrez de porriture d’aucunes humors, si com vienent vers et serpens et lumbris et ascarides ou ventre; et doute on de son malice, car quant il va par le cors, et il monte au chief, et il vient a l’oil, par aventure rentre, et destruit l’oil; et ceu avient maintes fois.	This disease is called in our land "the buffalo disease," because it often affects buffaloes, and it is a small worm that is born between the skin and flesh, and travels throughout the body moving up and down, and one can feel its movement well as it moves from limb to limb, until it breaks through the skin where it goes, causing pain; and it is engendered by putrid matter of certain humors, just as worms, serpents, lice, and ascarids come from the intestines; and there is fear of its malice, because when it travels throughout the body, and rises to the head, and comes to the eye, sometimes it enters, and destroys the eye; and this happens often.
Quant tu le vues curer et traire, si ne puet on fuers que quant il vait: si covient donques que tu lies le leu desus et desoz d’un fort liien bien estroitement, puis cope sus et le trai fuer, et se li vers est em parfont en la char, et tu ne le trueves, si le cauterize de feu sus, tant qu’il muire; et li plus grans nuisemens que il fait, si est qu’il corront l’oil, si com nos avons dit; et se tu le vois venir ou chief pres de l’oil, si estraint desoz lui le sorcil forment, puis cope sus, et le trai fuer; et covient user le malaide de mundifiement de cors de medicines solutives por les males humors porries, et se warse de viandes enjanrans porriture.	When you see it necessary to cure and drain it, one cannot do so while it is flowing: therefore, you must bind the area above and below with a strong tight bandage, then cut into it and drain it forcefully; if the vein is deep in the flesh and you cannot find it, cauterize it with fire until it stops bleeding; and the greatest harm it causes is that it can corrupt the eye, as we have said; and if you see it coming near the eye on the head, bind the eyelid firmly below it, then cut into it, and drain it forcefully; and the patient must use purgatives of medicines to dissolve bad humors and abstain from foods that cause putrefaction.
de la dolor qui vient de ventositeit	of the pain that comes from windiness
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «vakirir», et est une dolor que vient en aucuns membres, et pues se mue de membre en membre; et je vis ceu que je vos di.	This disease is called "vakirir" in our land, and it is a pain that comes to certain limbs, and then moves from limb to limb; and I have seen what I tell you.
Je fui apelez a une femme malaide, et me descovrit som bras, et vis une petite enfleure en la voinne dou brais; et I poc aprés, li vis monter ausi com un ver a l’espaule, plus tost que nulle chose, ausi com vif argent quant il cort de leu a autre; li dolor se departit de celui leu, et se ficha en l’espaule, et puis un poc aprés corrut par tout le cors, tant qu’ele vint en l’autre brais; puis me contait qu’elle tornioit adés entor le cors, si com je la vis.
