I was called to a sick woman, and she showed me her arm, where I saw a small swelling in the vein of the arm; and shortly after, I saw it rise as quickly as a worm to the shoulder, faster than anything, like quicksilver when it flows from one place to another; the pain departed from that spot and settled in the shoulder, and then a short while later spread throughout her body until it reached the other arm; then she told me that it circled around her body very quickly, as I saw.
Je me mervillai mout coment elle se movoit ensi de membre em membre, car je n’avoie onques veut ceste maladie selonc ceste maniere.	I marveled greatly at how it moved from limb to limb, for I had never seen this disease behave in such a manner.
Toutevoie, je avoie veut maint que bien avoient veut movoir dolor de leu a autre, mais je ne l’avoie mie veut, si com je le vis en la femme; et je me pensai que c’estoit por ceu que li femme avoit sec cors, et les voinnes descovertes, et por ceu apparoit celle ventositez constrainte; et n’aperent mie selonc ceste raison a ces qui sont delicious, et qui ont moistes cors et voinnes reponues.	However, I have seen many who wanted to move pain from one place to another, but I did not want it so, as I saw in the woman; and I thought that this was because the woman had dry flesh, and veins uncovered, and for this reason this windiness appears constrained; and they do not appear according to this reasoning with those who are fat, and who have moist bodies and veins covered.
Et quant tu vues curer ceste maladie, et li malaides sent celle dolor, s’elle t’apert si com nos avons dit, si la lie desus et desoz hastanment, et puis cope sus tant que cele ventositez constrainte au leu isse fuer; et cauterize le leu; et se tu ne la vois a tes eulz, si le cure de ceu qui deboute les ventositez, si com pilules fetides, et pilules de serapin, et semblans autres.	And when you want to treat this disease and the patient feels this pain, if it appears as we have said, then lift it up quickly and then cut into it until that constrained windiness leaves its place; and cauterize the spot; and if you do not see it with your eyes, then treat it from those who expel winds, such as foul pills, and pilules of serapion, and similar others.
des saiettes	of arrows
Les saiettes sont diverses, selonc lor semblances et selonc les leus dou cors ou elles chient.	Arrows vary according to their forms and the parts of the body where they penetrate.
Li diversitez de lor si est qu’il i a de celles qui ont grans pointes, et petites, et chevees, et soudees; et de celles qui ont II angles, et de celz qui ont lengues, et de celles ou il a pieces; et celle qui chiet en aucun membre si chiet selonc II manieres: ou en membre principeil cheveit, si com cerveil, cuer, foie, pormon, rains, intestine, vessie, et semblans membres.	The variety of arrows is such that there are those with large tips, small tips, barbed tips, and fixed tips; and there are those with two angles, and some have tongues, and others have pieces; and when an arrow penetrates any limb, it does so in two ways: either it penetrates a principal member, such as the brain, heart, liver, spleen, ribs, intestines, bladder, and similar members.
Quant elle chiet donques en aucun leu de ces membres, et li signe de mort, que je te dirai ci aprés, t’aperent: si covient que tu te warses de l’estraction de ceste saiette, car li mors vient aprés en plusors dispositions; et quant cist mal signe ne t’aperent mie, et li saiette n’est mie em parfont, si la trai, et cure la plaie.	When it penetrates any part of these members, and the signs of death, which I will tell you now, become apparent: then you must be wary about extracting this arrow, for death often follows in many cases; but when these signs do not appear, and the arrow is not deeply seated, then remove it and treat the wound.
Et li signe dou cerveil quant li saiette i chiet et perce l’os, et saut li syfac fuer qui est sus le cerveil, est quant scotomie et sode et esvertin et roujor ens eulz, et enflammation et roujor de lengue, et spasme et permixtion d’entendement, et vomissemens de cole; et per aventure ist sans fuer des narines, ou des oreilles; et par aventure pert la parole et la voix; et saut de la plaie moistor blanche semblant a poulz, et en saut ausi com bruee de char; et se cist signe t’aperent, si te tien de la cure, et trai la saiette s’elle n’est ens.	And the signs of the brain when an arrow falls and pierces the bone, and strikes the dura mater which is above the brain, are scotoma and stupor and vertigo and redness in the eyes, and inflammation and redness of the tongue, and spasms and confusion of understanding, and vomiting of bile; and by chance it may issue without strength from the nostrils or ears; and by chance speech and voice may be lost; and there may ooze out from the wound white moisture like pus, and also as a stream of flesh; and if these signs appear to you, then hold back from treatment, and draw out the arrow if it is within.
Li signe de la siette quant elle chiet ou cuer, sont qu’elle est pres de la mamele senestre, et sent ausi com s’elle estoit fichie en chose dure, ne mie vuide; et par aventure li siette se muet ausi com li poulz, et en cort noir sanc, et vient froidor et suor froide, et sincope: saiches adonc sens doute ke li mors dessent.	The signs of the arrow when it falls into the heart are that it is near the left mammary area, and it feels as if it were fixed in something hard, not empty; and by chance the arrow moves like pus, and forms black blood, and coldness and cold sweat come, and syncope: you then know without doubt that death follows.
Et li signe de la saiette que nevre lou pormon est que sans plains d’escume saut de la plaie, et li gorge enfle, et li malaides mue color, et sospire haut et quiert le froit ar.	And the sign of the arrow that pierces the throat is that foamless phlegm spouts from the wound, and the throat swells, and the patient changes color, and sighs loudly and seeks cold air.
Et se li saiette chiet en la coverture dou pis, si est delez les petites costes; et giete grant alainne et grant dolor et sospire; et li muevent tuit li membre des espaules.	And if the arrow strikes in the cover of the hip, it is among the small ribs; and causes great pain and great suffering and sighing; and all the shoulder members move.
Et se li saiette chiet ou stomac, par aventure si saut de la plaie aucune chose de la viande indigeste.	And if the arrow strikes in the stomach, by chance something of undigested meat may spout from the wound.
Et se li saiette chiet ou ventre, et en saut point de fien par l’intestine rout, si n’a point d’esperance en la cure, ne en l’estraction de la saiette.	And if the arrow strikes in the belly, and no sign of it can be felt through the intestines, there is no hope for treatment, nor for the extraction of the arrow.
Et se li saiette chiet en la vessie, et li urine en saut et vient defuer, et li malaides sent fort dolor: saiches que li plaie est mortelz.	And if the arrow falls into the bladder, and the urine jumps out and comes to flow, and the patient feels great pain: know that the wound is mortal.
Li autre membre, si com li faice et li colz et li gorge et li espaule et li adjutoire et li espinee dou dos et li forcele et li cuixe et les jambes, et li membre semblant, sont sauf selonc plusors dispositions.	The other limb, such as the face and neck and throat and shoulder and joint and spine of the back and rib and thigh and legs, and similar limbs, are safe according to many positions.
Quant li saiette est en lou nerf ou l’artere, et elle n’est venimouse, si com je vos dirai qu’il m’avint, por ceu que vos faciez autretel.	When the arrow is in the nerve or artery, and it is not venomous, as I will tell you that it happened to me, for which reason you should do otherwise.
Il avint a I home c’une saiette li chut ou larmier en la racine dou neis: je la tentai, et la traï d’autre part desoz la graisse de l’oreille, et fut sanez sens nusement.	It happened to a man that an arrow fell into his helmet at the root of his nose: I felt it and drew it out from the other side beneath the fat of the ear, and he was safe without injury.
Et traï a un jeu une saiette que li chut en la graisse de l’oil desoz la papiere desoz, et li saiette estoit reponue, et n’en poi ataindre que la pointe devers lou fust, et estoit li saiette grans d’un arc turcois, a tout I fer legier sens oreilles; li jeus fut sanez, et ne li vint nulz mavais accidens.	And he pulled out an arrow that had pierced the fat under the eye membrane below, and the arrow was embedded, and only the tip towards the shaft could be reached, and the arrow was large from a Turkish bow, made entirely of light iron without wings; the patient remained healthy, and no bad accidents occurred.
Et traï une saiette de la gorge a un crestien, et estoit li saiette arabique a oreilles: je soiai les barbions, et subtiliai tant que je la traï, et fut sanez li crestiens.	And he pulled an arrow from the throat of a Christian, and the arrow was Arabian with wings: I felt the barbs, and carefully extracted it as much as possible, and the Christian remained healthy.
Et traï une saiette a I home, que li estoit cheue ou ventre, et pensai qu’il moroit; et puis qu’il ot passez XXX jors, si ne mua point sa disposition; je taillai sus la saiette, et l’engignai, et la traï fuer, et n’ot point de mavais accident.	And he pulled an arrow from a man who had it lodged in his abdomen, and I thought he would die; but after thirty days had passed, there was no change in his condition; I incised around the arrow, disinfected it, forcefully extracted it, and he suffered no bad consequences.
Et si vis I home cui une saiette chut ou dos, et fut li plaie soudee sus; et demora li saiette dedens li, et ne chainja point ses dispositions naturez, ne ne trova nuisement en aucune de ses oevres naturelz.	And if you wish to treat a man who has an arrow embedded in his back, and the wound is sealed over; and the arrow remains inside him, and he does not change any of his natural dispositions, nor finds harm in any of his natural functions.
Et vis I autre homme, cui il chut une saiette en sa faice, et fut soudee li plaie; et demora ensi sens soffrir grant dolor; et mout d’autres semblans.	And if you wish to treat another man who has an arrow shot into his face, and the wound is sealed over; and it remains thus without him suffering great pain; and many other similar cases.
Et traï une saiette a I home des princes le roi, que li estoit cheue enmi lou neiz, et estoit un poc declinans a la destre partie; et estoit li saiette toute reponue Je fui apelez a la cure aprés ceu qu’elle fut cheue III jors.	And I treated an arrow that was embedded in the head of one of the king's princes, which was lodged between his ears, and it was slightly inclined towards the right side; and the arrowhead was completely bent. I was called to treat him three days after it had struck.
Si trovai la plaie mult estroite.	I found the wound very narrow.
Je la quis a tout une subtil tente, et ne la sentis mie; et il sentoit pointure et dolor desoz sa destre oreille.	I examined it thoroughly and felt nothing; yet he experienced pain and tenderness behind his right ear.
Je pensai que c’estoit de la pointe de la saiette Je mis sus lou leu emplaustre atratifet digestif, por ceu que li leus n’enflast; et m’aparut li leus de la saiette.	I thought it was from the tip of the arrow. I applied a poultice that is both absorptive and digestive to prevent swelling; then the place where the arrow had entered became apparent.
Je i mis l’emplaustre mains jors, et resouda li plaie derechief, et demora ensi li malaides lonc tens, tant qu’il sentit la saiette I jor dedens son neis; et il le me dist.	I applied the poultice for several days, and then reopened the wound, and the patient remained in this condition for a long time until he felt the arrow one day inside his nose; and he told me about it.
Je mis sus la plaie medicine ague corrosive par mains jors, tant qu’elle fut overte, et la tentai, et sentis le chief de la saiette qui s’aerdoit au leu; puis ajostai en l’overture de la plaie par celle medicine ague, tant que li chiés de la saiette m’aparut visablement; et trespassa bien li termines entor IIII mois, et puis eslarja si li plaie que je i boutai les tenailles, et le meus d’une part et d’autre, et ne pot issir; adonques ne cessai de subtiliier et d’engignier de manieres d’estrumens, tant que je la pris I jor as tenailles bien faites, selonc ceu que sa forme venra en la fin de cest chapistre, tant que je la traï, et restourai la plaie.	I applied a corrosive medicine to the wound for several days until it was open, and I examined it, feeling the tip of the arrow that was lodged there; then I used the same corrosive medicine to enlarge the opening in the wound until the head of the arrow became visible; and after about four months, I widened the edges around the wound so much that I could place pincers inside from both sides, but it would not come out; therefore, I did not stop trying various methods and instruments until one day I extracted it with well-made pincers, according to what will be described at the end of this chapter, and then closed the wound.
Et li mire jugent que li cartillaige dou nez ne puet restorer: je la restourai adonques, et fut soudee li plaie, et fut sanez li malaides entierement.	And the doctor judges that the nasal cartilage cannot be restored: I then repaired it, and the wound was sealed, and the patient was entirely healthy.
Or t’ai dit la qualiteit de l’estraction d’aucunes saiettes, si que tu mettes ta cure sus ceu que je ne dis mie, car li livres ne puet mie tout porprendre; mais li saiges maistres compere sus bien poc grant chose, et sus ceu que li est present et defaillant, trueve nueve oevre, et nuef estrument, au dessendement des choses estrainges qui avienent en cest art.	I have told you about the quality of extracting some arrows, so that you do not put your care into what I do not say, for books cannot contain everything; but wise masters compare well with great matters, and with what is present and lacking, they find new work, and new instruments, in descending things strange that happen in this art.
Je dis que les saiettes n’issent des membres ou elles sont fichies fuer que selonc II manieres: ou par lou leu ou elles entrent, ou par d’autre part; et celle que saut fuer par lai ou elle entre, c’est saiette entrans en leus charnus, et saut fuer aucune fois maintenant.	I say that arrows exit from the members where they are embedded in two ways: either from the place where they entered, or from another part; and those that come out from where they entered, are penetrating arrows, and sometimes they come out immediately.
Et s’elle ne saut maintenant, si la laisse tant que li chars soit porrie entor, et soit alegie li issue; et ausi s’elle est fichie en l’os, et elle ne puet issir, si la laisse ensi aucuns jors, et la muef chescun jor; et adonques elle saut, et s’elle ne saut, si perce entor a tout I foret subtil, tant que li leus entor soit eslargiez, et puis la trai.	And if it does not come out now, leave it until the flesh around it is rotted and the exit is widened; and likewise if it is lodged in the bone, and cannot come out, leave it thus for some days, and soften it each day; then it will come out, and if it does not come out, cut around it with a fine point, until the flesh around it is enlarged, and then draw it out.
Et se li saiette est fichie en l’os dou chief, et vait jusc’a l’un des ventres dou cerveil, et aucuns des accidens que j’ai dit apert au malaide: si ne la traire mie, mais la laisse tant qu’elle soit igalz aprés aucuns jors, car se li saiette vient jusc’a syfac, c’est li mors.	And if the arrow is lodged in the bone of the head and goes to one of the ventricles of the brain, and some of the accidents that I have mentioned are apparent to the patient: do not draw it out, but leave it for a few days until it is even, because if the arrow reaches the sinus, it is death.
Et se li saiette n’est fichie fuer qu’en l’os soulement, et ne vient jusc’a syfac, et demoure li malaides aucuns jors sens mavais accident, si l’engigne dou traire.	And if the arrow is not embedded deeper than just in the bone, and does not reach the surface, and the patient remains for some days without any adverse event, then one should attempt to remove it.
Et s’elle est mout fichie ensi et ne puet issir fuer, si i aministre tareres entor, si com je t’ai dit; puis cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it is deeply embedded and cannot be removed, then administer therapeutics around it, as I have told you; then treat the area until it is healed.
Et se li saiette est reponue en leu dou cors si c’on ne la puisse veoir, si la quier a tout la tente; et se tu la sens, si la trai a aucun estrument covenauble; et se tu ne pues por l’estrecement de la plaie, et por la parfondesce de la saiette, et il n’i a os ne nerf ne voine, si la fens tant que li plaie soit grans; et trai la saiette se tu pues, et s’il ait en la saiette oreilles a coi elle tient, si oste la char qui est ens fichie de II pars au mues que tu pues, et puis brise ou ploie les oreilles de la saiette, tant que tu la puisses traire; et subtilie bien que tu ne brisier la saiette, que tu la trairoies plus griement.	And if the arrow is lodged in the body where it cannot be seen, search throughout the wound area; and if you feel it, remove it with any suitable instrument; and if you cannot due to the tightness of the wound and the depth of the arrow, and there are no bones or nerves or veins, enlarge the wound so that it is large enough; and remove the arrow if you can, and if it has barbs by which it holds fast, cut away the flesh from both sides as far as you can reach, then break or bend the barbs until you can extract it; and be careful not to break the arrow, which would make removal more difficult.
Et se tu ne pues a une fois, si la lai jusque li leus entor soit porris, puis la trai, car li estraction iert alegie.	And if you cannot do it all at once, leave it until the area around the wound is healed, then draw it out, for the extraction will be easier.
Et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de la cure en son chapistre; et te warde de l’incision dou nerf et de la voinne, et met engien coment tu pues mues traire la saiette sens peril, ou tost ou tart, ou fermement ou belement; et met le malaide selonc la forme qu’il estoit quant li saiette li chut ens, car c’est li plus grans aide que i soit, et se tu ne pues, si lou met selonc ceu que li signe lou te mostrent.	And if the flow of blood is contrary to you, then treat it as we have described in its chapter; and beware of cutting the nerve and the vein, and place the arrow so that you can safely remove the arrow without risk, quickly or slowly, firmly or gently; and position the patient according to how he was when the arrow struck him, for this is the greatest help there can be, and if you cannot, then place it as the signs indicate.
Li saiette que vient fuer d’autre part, ou il apert aucune chose de li, ou li cuir est enflez endroit si c’on le voit ou sent aparamment: taille donques sus, tant que les tenailles i puissent prendre, et puis l’estrai: si saut fuer maintenant.	The arrow that comes from another part, where something of it is visible, or the skin is swollen in such a way that it can be seen or felt clearly: cut above it until pliers can grasp it, and then extract it: do this now.
Et s’elle est retenue en l’os, si tornoie ta main rondement, tant qu’elle entre en l’os, et eslarge l’os, puis la trai.	And if it is held in the bone, turn your hand circularly until it enters the bone, and widen the bone, then draw it out.
Et s’elle ne puet issir, si la laisse encor, et puis rencomence l’estraction tant qu’elle isse fuer; et se li fust de la saiette i est, se le boute a tout le fust; et se li fust chiet, et tu vues aministrer boutement, si i aministre I estrument cheveit, si que li pointe de la saiette entre en la cheveure de l’estrument; et puis boute fuer, et se li saiette est chevee, se i boute I estrument a pointe entrant ens, por alegier l’estraction.	And if it cannot come out, leave it there and then restart the extraction until it comes out; and if the shaft of the arrow is still there, cut off everything except the tip; and if the shaft breaks, and you wish to administer a probe, then administer an instrument with a hole, so that the point of the arrow enters the hole in the instrument; and then push firmly, and if the arrow has been removed, then use an instrument with a sharp entry for easier extraction.
Et se li saiette est entouchie, si covient que tu copes toute la char entor ou li venins est, se tu pues, puis cure la plaie si com il couvient.	And if the arrow is touched, then you must cut away all the flesh around where the wound is, if you can, and then treat the wound as necessary.
Et se li saiette chiet ou peis ou au ventre ou a la vessie ou au costeit, et elle est prochiene, et tu pues coper sus, se i cope; et te garde de coper la voinne et lou nerf, et puis l’estrai, et puis cout la plaie, se mestier est; et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And if the arrow falls in the foot or in the belly or bladder or side, and it is near, then cut above if you can; and beware of cutting the vein and nerve, then extract it, and then stitch the wound if necessary; and treat until it heals.
Li forme des tenailles dont on trait les saiettes sont semblans au bec d’oiseil, et vez ci la forme:	The form of the forceps used to treat arrows is similar to the beak of a bird, and see here the shape:
Et en sont mout de manieres: grans, moienes, et petites, selonc la quantitei de la saiette.	And there are many kinds: large, medium, and small, according to the size of the arrow.
Li forme dou boutant cheveit est ausi com li penne d’un oisel, por bouter a la pointe de la saiette, si com ci est li forme:	The shape of the needle used to pierce hair is also like the feather of a bird, to pierce at the tip of the arrow, as shown here is the shape:
li forme des tenailles por bouter et por sachier si est ci:	the form of the tongs for inserting and holding is as follows:
des voinnes dou cors communes	of common veins of the body
Des voinnes dont on se saine sont XXXI, de coi il a ou chef XVI, c’est a savoir: II batans qui sont aprés les oreilles, qui sont apelees les dous «herbech»; et les II arteres qui sont en II temples apparans; et II voines que sont en II larmiers des II eulz, que sont apelees «aspires»; et li voine que est emmi le front; et li voinne que est au chief dou neis; et les II guindeges qui sont ou col; et les II voinnes que sont en levres desus de la bouche, et ce sont les voines que sont apelees «augeherich»; et II voinnes que sont desoz la lengue.	There are thirty-one veins from which one can bleed to cure, sixteen of which are in the head: two beating ones behind the ears, called the "herbech"; and the two arteries that appear on each temple; and the two veins in the lacrimal bones under each eye, called "aspires"; and the vein in the forehead; and the vein at the top of the nose; and the two jugulars in the neck; and the two veins in the upper lip, which are called "augeherich"; and the two veins below the tongue.
Les voinnes dont on saine communement sont V en chescun bras: l’une est li cephalique, et est dou senestre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou chief»; et li moiene est apelee «faste», et est composte de la cephalique et de la basilique, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou cuer»; et li basilique si est ou destre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gent «voinne dou ventre», et est sus le foscile, et est celle dont on saine, qui apert manifestement sus le pouchet.	The veins from which one commonly bleeds are V in each arm: one is the cephalic, and it is on the left side, and the lay people call it "vein of the head"; and the middle one is called "faste," and is composed of the cephalic and basilic, and the lay people call it "vein of the heart"; and the basilic is on the right side, and the lay people call it "vein of the belly," and it is above the fossa, and this is the one from which one commonly bleeds, which appears manifestly on the pouchet.
Et li salvatelle est li voine qui est entre l’auriculaire et l’anulaire, et si a II rains; et en la jambe et ou piet sont III voinnes: l’une si est desoz la corbeure dou pochet dou senestre costeit, et li seconde sophene qui est a la cheville dou destre costeit; et li voine qui est apelee «nesse», que est en la cheville de l’autre costei; et en l’autre jambe sont III voinnes desoz celles.	And the savior vein is the one that is between the little finger and the ring finger, and it has two branches; and in the leg and foot there are three veins: one is below the bend of the left ankle, and the second sophene which is at the right ankle; and the vein called "nesse," which is at the other ankle; and in the other leg are three veins beneath those.
Li sainie des voinnes que sont aprés les oreilles si aide as catharres anciens, et a emigraine; et li qualiteis dou sainier, si com je te dis, et est que tu reises lou chief dou malaide, et frote lou leu ou les voinnes sont d’un drap aspre; puis estrigne li malaides son col a une vis, tant que les II voinnes aperent derrier les oreilles en II leus dependens dou chief: quier les donques a ton doi, et ou tu sens lou poulz desoz ton doi, si seigne d’enche; puis pren la lancette, et la boute par desoz la voine jusc’a l’os, puis lieve ta main a tout la voinne amont, et cope et lou cuir et la voinne bien II dois dou traver, et fai issir dou sanc tant que tu vues; puis l’estrain et lie, tant qu’ele soit sanee; et j’ai ja dit l’incision et le cautere ou premier livre.	The bloodletting of the veins that are behind the ears helps with chronic catarrhs and migraine headaches; and the quality of this bloodletting, as I told you, is to tilt the patient's head back, then rub the area where the veins are with a rough cloth; then tighten the patient’s neck with a tourniquet so that the two veins behind the ears appear in two places dependent on the head: hold them down with your thumb, and where you feel the pulse beneath your thumb, make an incision there; take the lancet and insert it below the vein up to the bone, then lift your hand along the entire length of the vein upwards, cutting both the skin and the vein well two fingers wide apart, letting out as much blood as you wish; then tie off and bandage them until they are healed; I have already mentioned incision and cautery in the first book.
Li sainie des II arteres que sont en II temples, si vaut a emigrainne anciene, et sode, et obtalmie acostumee, et au cors des larmes agues as eulz; et li qualitez dou sainier si est si com je dis: et est que li malaides estraigne son col, tant que les II voinnes aperent apertement; et sent lou polz desoz ton doi, et puis seigne d’enche; puis lieve lou keur sus la voinne en haut a ton doi indice, et boute la lancette desoz, et lieve la voine en haut, et la cope, si com tu as fait en II autres voinnes, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit; puis deslie lou malaide, et met ton doi sus la voine une houre, puis met sus coton; et puis la lie forment, et la laisse tant qu’elle soit sanee; et nos en avons jai parleit et de lor copement et de lor estraction, ou comencement dou livre.	The bloodletting from the two arteries that are in the two temples is good for chronic migraine, severe headache, habitual ophthalmia, and excessive aqueous humor in the eyes; and the quality of the bloodletting is as I say: it is that the patient tightens his neck so that the two veins appear clearly; then feel the pulse below your thumb, and then prick with a lancet; lift the vein above on your thumb index, and insert the lancet below, and raise the vein above, and cut, just as you did in the other two veins, and let the blood flow according to your necessity; then untie the patient, and place your hand on the vein for an hour, then put cotton over it; then tie it up properly, and leave it until it is healed; and we have already spoken about their cutting and extraction at the beginning of the book.
Li sainie de la voine dou front si vaut autant com li sainie de la cephalique as maladies de la faice ancienes, et a emigraine, et a roujor; et li qualitez si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant, tant que li voine apere; puis pren l’estrument qui est apelez «fosseur», dont ci est li forme:	The vein of the forehead is worth as much as the cephalic vein in ancient face diseases and for migraines and redness; and its quality is that the patient strains their neck by twisting it until the vein appears swollen; then take the instrument called "digger," here is its form:
Et met la pointe sus la voinne, et fier sus de ta main, ou d’autre chose, et laisse dou sanc issir selonc la quantiteit que tu vues; puis delie au malaide le col, et lie la voine tant qu’elle soit saneel et aucune fois l’uevre on d’un flaime large.	And place the point on the vein, and press with your hand or something else, and let blood flow according to the quantity you wish; then release the patient's neck, and tie off the vein until it is secure, and sometimes use a wide flame.
Toutevoie, il ne covient mie que li flaimes soit trop agus; et le saine de travers, car li os est pres, et par aventure brise li flaimes quant il est subtilz.	Nevertheless, it is not appropriate for the flame to be too sharp; and the vein runs sideways, because the bone is close by, and by chance may break when it is thin.
Li sainie des II voines que sont en II larmiers si aide as eulz, et a la tigne, et a la roujor, et a l’oriuel en l’oil, et as maladies de la faice; et li qualitez de lor sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant d’aucun liien, si com devant; puis le saine, et soit li sainie dou traver, un poc dou lonc dou flaime un poc large, car il n’i a point de char.	The blood from the two veins that are in the two lacrimal bones aids in treating the eyes, and for eyelid problems, and for redness, and for ulceration in the eye, and for ailments of the face; and the quality of their treatment is such that the patient strains his neck by twisting with some kind of ligature, as mentioned before; then he treats it, and let the treatment be done across, a bit along the length of the flame a bit wide, because there is no flesh.
Et se li flaimes est subtilz, par aventure si brise; puis fai corre dou sanc, tant com tu en as mestier, et puis lie sus couton, et le lie bien.	And if the flame is fine, it may break; then let the blood flow, as much as you need, and then cover with a cloth, and bind well.
Li sainie de la voine dou neis si vaut a ague, et a sode forsenee, et a maladies de faice, si com emigraine et roujor que vient en la faice, et meimement quant elle est anciene; et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estrigne son col, puis estrain son neis a ta main senestre, et pren lou flaime subtil lonc, et le fiche emmi la levre en l’espaice qui est entre les II narines, car li voinne n’apert mie bien enqui, et li sans comencera maintenant a corre; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit, puis la lie une nuit, car elle est mout tost restoree; et c’est li forme dou flaime:	The treatment with the vein from the nose is effective for fever, and for severe headache, and for face ailments such as migraine and redness that comes in the face, especially if it is old; and the quality of this treatment is that the patient strains his neck, then pinches his nose with your left hand, and take a fine long flame, and insert it between the lips in the space between the two nostrils, because the vein does not open well otherwise, and the blood will now start to flow; do not go too deep, and let the blood flow according to your need, then bind it for one night, as it is quickly restored; and this is the shape of the flame:
Li sainie des II guindeges si aide a l’estrecement de l’alainne, et a l’encomencement de meselerie, et a mout de maladies, et a empetigine, et a corrodens, et a herpes, et estiomenes; et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col desoz l’une et l’autre, si com nos avons dit; et soit li maistres estans sus lou chief dou malaide, et li malaides siece sus I siege, puis saine la voine dou lonc un poc largement, puis trai dou sanc tempreement, ou tant com mestier est; puis refai autreteil en l’autre voinne, puis deslie lou liien, et estraint andous les voines moienement, que li malaides n’estrangle; et le laisse jusc’au matin, que li plaie soit sanee.	The salve of the two figs helps in constricting the vagina, and at the beginning of mixing ingredients, and for many diseases, and for impetigo, and corrosives, and herpes, and erythemas; and the quality of the salve is that the patient tightens his neck under one and the other, as we have said; and let the master be standing over the head of the patient, and the patient sit on a chair, then apply the vein of the long slightly wide, then draw blood moderately, as much as needed; then do it again in the other vein, then undo the bandage, and bind both veins moderately so that the patient does not strangle; and leave it until morning, when the wound is healed.
de la sainie des leivres	of the salve of the leaves
Li sainie des voinnes des levres desus si aident a cole en la bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et fendures de levres, et dou neis et entor.	The bleeding of the veins above the lips helps in the coagulation in the mouth, and for the corruption of gums, and splits of the lips, and nose and around.
Et li qualitez de la sainie si est de faire seoir lou malaide devant toi, et estraint son col si com j’ai dit; puis torne la levre, et regarde as II voinnes, dont l’une est a la destre levre et li autre a la senestre, et les conoist on par ceu qu’elles sont noires, et par ceu que entor elles a voines menues noires: cope donques l’une et l’autre, et se tu ne les conois, et tu en es en doutance, si cope la plus grosse de chescune part, et tout ausi fai des II voinnes que sont desus et desoz, car c’est une meisme maniere.	And the qualities of the bleeding are to have the patient sit before you, and hold his neck as I said; then turn the lip, and look at the two veins, one on the right lip and the other on the left, and recognize them by their black color and by the small black veins around them: therefore cut both of them, and if you do not know them and are in doubt, cut the largest from each side, and do likewise for the two veins above and below, because it is the same method.
de la sainie desoz la lengue	Remove the tongue from the socket
Li sainie des voinnes que sont desoz la lengue si aide aprés la sainie de la cephalique, et c’est a l’estrecement de la gorge, et as maladies de l’uve, et as maladies de la bouche; et li qualitez dou sainier si est que li malaides siece entre tes mains devant lou soleil, et li lieve la lengue, et regarde desoz en chescun costeit une voinne noire: saine donques l’une et l’autre, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car desoz sont les arteres.	The treatment of the veins that are behind the tongue follows after the treatment of the cephalic area, which is at the constriction of the throat, and for eye diseases, and mouth ailments; and the qualities of the healer are such that the patient urinates into your hands in front of the sun, and you lift the tongue up, and look underneath on each side there is a black vein: treat then one and the other, but do not go too deep, because below are the arteries.
Les voinnes dou coute dont on saine communement sont sainies selonc II manieres: ou em poignant a tout I flaime mirtin large, ou olivaire subtil si com coutez trenchans, et est apelez «anesil»; et sont large et subtil selonc la largesce et l’estrecement des voinnes.	The veins of the forearm that are typically treated are treated in two ways: by piercing with a broad flame-like cautery or an olive-shaped fine one like cutting knives, and it is called "anesil"; and they are wide and fine according to the width and narrowness of the veins.
Li forme dou flaime mirtin si est mout renommee, et est large si com tu vois:	The form of the flame of fire is very famous, and it is as wide as you see:
Et ait mestier por ovrir les voinnes chevees plaines de gros sanc apparent, et que contienent gros sanc et trouble; et c’est li forme dou flaime olivaire:	And it is necessary to open veins that are full of thick visible blood, and which contain thick and turbid blood; and this is the form of the olive flame:
et est plus subtilz apointé, et est por sainier les voinnes subtilz, ou il a subtil sanc citrin.	and it is finer in shape, and is for bleeding fine veins, where there is fine yellow blood.
Li sainie de la basilique, qui est une de ces voinnes, si aide as maladies que sont desoz la gorge, et ou col, et ou peis, et ou ventre; et covient au sainor qu’il saine saigement, et qu’il se warse de l’artere qui est desoz.	The basilic vein, which is one of these veins, helps with diseases that are below the throat, and in the neck, and in the chest, and in the abdomen; and it is necessary for the physician to bleed carefully, and to avoid the artery that is underneath.
Et s’il cope l’arterre, et decorremens de sanc vient, si le covient estainchier, si com j’ai dit; et ne doit mie estre poignans li flaime, mais taillans si com anesil.	And if he cuts the artery and blood flow comes out, it must be stopped as I have said; and should not be pressing on the flame but cutting as before.
Et se li basilique n’apert manifestement, si covient que tu l’estrainges, et chainge une autre; ou tu quieres aucun rain de li, ou tu saine en leu de li la voinne emmi le bras: elle apert manifestement; et la cope au flaime anesil, si com nos avons dit.	And if the basilica does not appear clearly, then you must remove it and change another one; or take some rain from it, or heal in its place a vein in the arm: it appears clearly; and cut with the flame as before, as we have said.
Et se tu vues conoistre le leu de la sainie, si covient ainsois que tu estraignes lou bras, que tu touches le leu tant que tu conoisses le poulz; puis signe le leu d’enche, et puis lie lou bras, et cope la voine dou flaime anesil; et warde que tu ne ferir en l’artere quant tu vois le leu enfleit, car c’est de l’artere: eschui la donques.	And if you wish to know the place of the incision, then you must first remove the arm and touch the area until you feel the pulse; then mark the spot on the bone, and then tie up the arm, and cut the vein with the flame as before; and be careful not to injure the artery when you see the area swollen, for it is the artery: avoid it then.
Et se tu vois saillir en haut ausi com l’urine d’un enfant, et li sans est rouges et subtilz, saiches que c’est sans de l’artere: haste toi donques, et met ton doi sus longement, puis oste ton doi se li sans estainche, que maintes fois avient; se lie lou bras, et laisse ensi, et ne lou mueve li malaides; et soit sus paour, et ne lou mueve tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you see it flowing upwards like the urine of a child, and the blood is red and thin, know that it is arterial blood: hurry then, and place your hand for a long time, then remove your hand if the bleeding stops, which often happens; bind the arm, and leave it thus, and do not move the patient; and be afraid, and do not move the patient until he is healed.
Et se li sans n’est estainchiez, et il te vaint, et li medicine ne t’est presens, si cope l’artere s’elle apert, car li chief de li retraient; et estainche li sans.	And if the bleeding does not stop, and you are forced to, and no medicines are present, then cut the artery if it is visible, for its end can be pressed back; and stop the bleeding.
Et pren une escorce de fistice, et la fent, et pren l’une des moitiez et lie sus bien jusc’a l’autre jor; se li sans estainche, c’est bien; se ce non, si le cure, si com nos avons dit, des poudres qui estainchent sanc; et li estainchemens n’est mie griés em plusors dispositions por le petit leu de la plaie, et la possance dou liien dou bras.	And take a piece of flax bark, and cut it, and take one half and bind it well until the next day; if the bleeding stops, that is good; if not, treat it as we have said with powders that stop blood; and the bandaging does no harm in many conditions due to the small area of the wound, and the strength of the binding on the arm.
Li sainie de la voinne em mileu si aide qu’elle trait sanc dou chief desus, et dou cors desoz, por ceu qu’elle est composte de la basilique et de la cephalique, si com nos avons dit; et covient au sainor qu’il se warse por lou nerf qui est desoz, et s’il point trop em parfont, et il trueve lou nerf, et il enfle et li santez soit griés, et par aventure ne puet saner; et cist nerf apert mult de fois, et s’il n’apert en aucuns homes por sa subtiliteit, si covient que tu lou saines de l’estrument anesil; et eschui lou nerf a ton pooir.	The incision of the vein in the middle helps to let blood flow from the head above and from the body below, because it is composed of the basilic and cephalic veins, as we have said; and it is necessary for the surgeon to protect himself against the nerve that is below, and if he pierces too deeply, and finds the nerve, it swells and the patient will be in great pain, and perhaps cannot heal; this nerve appears many times, and if it does not appear in some people because of its subtlety, then you must treat it with an instrument called anesil; and avoid the nerve to the best of your ability.
Et se il a voinne entre les II ners, si la fent dou lonc.	And if there is a vein between the two nerves, then make the incision along its length.
Li sainie de la cephalique si aide, qu’ele atrait sanc dou chief, et aide as eulz; et covient sainier em poignant au flaime olivaire ou au flaime mirtin, car c’est li plus sauve de toutes les voinnes, car il n’a desoz li ne nerf ne artere.	The cephalic vein helps to draw blood from the head and aids the eyes; it should be punctured with an olive leaf needle or a myrtle leaf needle, for this is the safest of all veins, as there are no nerves or arteries nearby.
Toutevoie, covient querir lou plus legier leu, et ne grieve rien s’on faut la premiere fois, et on rencomence; et par aventure enfle li leus a aucuns homes, cant on faut la premiere fois, mais il ne grieve rien.	Always seek the most delicate spot, and it does not harm if one must puncture for the first time, and then try again; and sometimes the spots swell in some people when punctured for the first time, but it does no harm.
La qualitez de la sainie si est selonc ta pensee.	The quality of the vein is as you think.
Li premiere chose que tu dois savoir de sainier, si est que sainie n’est amenistree fuer que por garder santeit, et por eschuir les maladies a venir; et soit li sainie faite en l’une des III voinnes que sont ou coute: c’est a savoir, cephalique, faste, et basilique; et se doit on sainier en l’encomencement de prientens a geun, et en autompne et en yver aprés mengier, quant li signe de repletion aperent; et se doit on sainier le premier jor ou le tier, aprés II houres ou III dou jor.	The first thing you must know about bleeding is that it should not be done except to maintain health and to prevent future illnesses; and one should bleed in one of the three veins mentioned: namely, cephalic, facial, and basilic; and one should bleed at the beginning of prayer time on Mondays, and in autumn and winter after eating, when signs of repletion appear; and one should bleed either on the first day or the third, two hours or three after the day begins.
Li sainie qui est aministree as maladies n’a point d’oure determinee, mais que quant besoing est de jor ou de nut, en toutes houres et en toz tens; et ne covient mie sainier les enfans jusc’a XIIII ans, ne femme portant fuer que des lou quart mois jusc’a septime.	The physician who treats diseases has no fixed hour determined for them, but rather whenever the need arises day or night, at all hours and in all seasons; and it is not proper to treat children until they are fourteen years old, nor women carrying a fetus from the fourth month until the seventh.
Ne ne se doient mie sainier li viel qui ont passez LX ans.	And one should not treat the elderly who have passed sixty years.
Et quant aucuns se vuet sainier, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient k’il mondefie les intestines d’un clistere legier, s’il a mout de fiens retenut, si que les voines n’atraient des intestines les superfluitez porries nuisans as membres principelz; ne ne se saine mie cil qui est trop saolez de viandes, ne qui est yvres, tant k’il en soit fuer, ne ydropiques; et se warse on de sainier aprés colique passion, et vomissement, et decorrement de ventre, et multipliement d’abiter a femme, et de traval, de veiller et de juner, et ceu que tot la vertu, ou par chose de l’arme ou dou cors; puis subtilie les humors, se li sans est gros, par viandes et par bevraiges et par medicines, se tu en as lou poir; puis entre ou bain, s’aucune chose ne lou deffent, por subtiliier lou sanc, et te saine de la voinne dou pis entor la tierce, si com nos avons dit; et te garde celui jor de travail, et de poinne, et de luxure, et de semblans choses; et soies liez et joians, et soit li sainieres plus haut que cil cui on saine, et li frote lou bras II fois ou III, puis estraigne lou liien desus moienement, car quant il est trop estrois ou poc, si ne puet corre li sans; et puis le frote le leu as mains, tant que les voines enflent, et les sente on; puis moille li sainieres le flaime d’un poc d’oile viel, puis mette son doit de sa main senestre sus celle voinne desoz lou leu un poc ou il vuet sainier, que li voinne ne fue et faille au ferir.	And when someone wishes to be bled, in whatever manner it may be, they must first cleanse their intestines with a mild enema if there is much retained feces so that the veins do not attract superfluous harmful substances from the intestines to the principal limbs; nor should one bleed those who are overly full of food, nor drunkards, whether they are pregnant or not, nor hydropics; and one does not bleed after colic pain, vomiting, diarrhea, excessive sexual activity, labor, staying awake, and feasting; then purify the humors if the blood is thick, with foods and drinks and medicines, if you have the power to do so; then take a bath, unless anything prevents it, to refine the blood, and bleed from the vein around the elbow, as we have said; and on that day keep away from labor, exertion, lust, and similar things; be happy and joyful, and let the physician be higher than the one being bled, and rub his arm two or three times, then loosen the bandage moderately, for if it is too tight, blood cannot flow freely; then feel the vein with your hands until they swell and can be felt; then moisten the lancet with a little old oil, place your left hand on the vein below where you wish to bleed so that the vein does not move when pricked.
Car il i a voinnes que fuient ausi com cordes au sainier, et si a de telz que sont plainnes de ventositeit, si que quant on met sus le flaime, si retrait a flaime, et ne puet ovrir li voinne, et ensi est on de ceus; et s’il aoevre la voinne, si est li plaie trop estroite, por ceu si covient que li sainieres soit avisez en ces choses.	For there are veins that behave like strings to the surgeon, and some are full of airiness, so when one applies the flame, it withdraws from the heat, and thus the vein cannot be opened; and if one operates on the vein, the wound is too narrow, therefore it is necessary for surgeons to be cautious in these matters.
Et se li voine oevre la premiere fois, c’est boin; se ceu non, si rencomence ancor un poc desoz celui leu ou sus hastanment, se li leus n’est enflez.	And if the vein is opened the first time, it is good; if not, then begin again a bit below that place quickly, unless the area is swollen.
Et se li leus est enflez, et li malaides s’espoante, se li laisse I jor ou II, et ne liier mie le bras: par aventure i venra apostemes chaus; ne n’entre ou bain, puis rencomence la sainie s’elle li plait; et se li pertuis est petis, ou li sans cort subtilment et tu doutes qu’il n’isse mie tant de sanc com tu vues, si fier en celui pertuis meisme a tout le flaime droitement; et l’uevre un poc hastanment, ainsois que li leus soit enflez; car ceu avient maintes fois, quant li plaie est petite.	And if the area is swollen and the patient is frightened, let them rest for one or two days and do not bind the arm: perhaps an abscess will come safely; nor enter a bath, then resume the procedure if it pleases them; and if the opening is small, place the cautery directly over it with all the flame; work quickly so that the area becomes swollen; for this often happens when the wound is small.
Se tu vois le leu enfleit, si ne rencomencier mie la sainie, et met sus un poc de lie d’oile, car elle alige lou cors dou sanc, et est muedre en cest leu li lie que li oile; et ensi aministre la lie de oile en chescune sainie que tu saines les voines, por estanchier lou cours dou sanc; et ceu meisme fait triaicle et bowe d’eus, quant on le met sus le leu; si subtilie li sans et s’espart quant il est trop gros.	If you see the area swollen, do not restart the bleeding, and apply a poultice of oil, for it lightens the body of blood, and at this place the poultice of oil is soft; and thus administer the poultice of oil each time you bleed the veins to stop the flow of blood; and this same treatment applies when applying triacle and bandages, when they are placed on the area; it subtly thins and disperses the blood when it is too thick.
Et s’il i vient uns apostemes gros, qui avient maintes fois, meismement quant il n’est sainiez fuer que a celi fois ou li overture de la voinne est petite, si te haste, et met sus le leu esponge moillie en aigue et en seil un poc chaut, et l’estraint une houre; et covient que tu faices ceu aprés l’issue dou sanc de la voinne, et s’il demoure au leu aprés aucuns jors aucune noiror ou verdor, si ne li nuist mie; et se tu vues, met sus aucune chose de aloes ou de mirre remise en jus de calament, monstastre, ou semblant.	And if a large abscess comes, which happens many times, especially when bleeding is not done forcefully at the time of vein opening, hurry and place an sponge moistened in warm water and vinegar on the area for one hour; and you must do this after the blood flows from the vein, and if any black or green discoloration remains after some days, it will do no harm; and if you wish, apply something like aloes or myrrh dissolved in juice of calamint, mastix, or similar.
Et maintes fois avient aposteme et aparance a la sainie de la basilique: met donques ta main sus, et se tu trueves le leu mol a la compression de la main, si est celle aparance male.	And often an abscess and swelling occur at the base of the skull: place then your hand upon it, and if you find the spot soft under the pressure of the hand, that appearance is bad.
Eschui donques que tu ne mettes sus aucune chose de ceu que nos avons dit, car par aventure en cort sans de l’artere; mais li fai I emplaustre sec por endurcir le leu, puis le cure d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Avoid placing anything of what we have said above, for fear of cutting into an artery; but apply a dry poultice to harden the area, then treat it with another treatment until it is healed.
Et trai a chescun dou sanc selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu, et de la color dou sanc.	And draw out the blood from each according to the quantity of its virtue and the color of the blood.
Car se li sans est noir, si en laisse issir tant qu’il soit rouges; et se tu lou vois gros, si lou laisse tant qu’il soit subtiliiez; et s’il est trop chaus, si le laisse refroidier.	For if the blood is black, let it flow until it becomes red; and if you see it thick, let it flow until it becomes thin; and if it is too warm, let it cool down.
Et covient a celui qui est plains et fors, et ait mestier d’estraction de sanc, c’on li faice plus large plaie, et soit li flaimes larges; et a celui qui est foibles, fai le contraire, et le covient sainier poc et sovent, et le doit on sainier en taillant de travers, ne mie en poignant; et ceste maniere de sainie est sauve de decorrement de sanc et de copement de nerf, et vaut mues que li sainie dou lonc ne dou large.	And it is appropriate for one who is healthy and strong, and needs bloodletting, to make a wider incision, and let the flow be wide; and for one who is weak, do the opposite, and it is fitting to bleed them less often but more gently, and this should be done by cutting across, not piercing; and this method of bloodletting is safe from fainting due to excessive bleeding and damaging nerves, and is worth much more than long or wide incisions.
Et a celui cui li cors faut a la sainie, covient doner pain moilliet en jus de pomes grenates; s’il est eschaufez, si trai dou sanc III fois ou IIII Et s’il est de froide complexion, si menjuce devant la sainie pain moilliet en sirop muzé, ou en sirop de miel aromatique avec espices, si com poivre, canelle, gingibre, et chiches, et sirop bien odorant.	And for one whose body needs nourishment before bloodletting, give them moist bread in pomegranate juice; if they are overheated, let them drink three or four times. And if they have a cold constitution, give them moist bread in muscat syrup, or aromatic honey syrup with spices such as pepper, cinnamon, ginger, and chickpeas, along with well-aromatic syrup before bloodletting.
Et s’il paume a la sainie, aprés l’issue de mout de sanc, si covient qu’il hume brouet de char, et sirop odorant subtil, et use des autres choses que nos avons dit en la division ou chapistre de sincope, por l’evacuation de voinne.	And if he faints after losing a lot of blood, it is necessary for him to drink broth of meat, and fragrant syrup, and use other things that we have said in the section or chapter on syncope, for the evacuation of veins.
Et s’il vuet esventer som bras, et sainier autre fois, si covient, quant il est afoiblis par grant sainie, k’il se saine poc et poc, selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu continueement.	And if he wishes to bleed his arm and let blood again, it is necessary, when he is weakened by heavy bleeding, that he lets blood little by little, according to the amount of his continued strength.
Et qui vuet esventer som bras aprés la premiere sainie, et il a cors fort, si se saine VII houres aprés la premiere sainie, ou aprés la nuevime houre.	And who wishes to bleed his arm after the first bleeding, and he has a strong body, should let blood seven hours after the first bleeding, or after the ninth hour.
Et qui se vuet sainier d’autre part, si se doit sainier lou secont jor ou le tier.	And who wishes to let blood from another place should do so on the second day or the third.
Car il a mout de sanc dedens le cors qui est ja eschaufez, et fait venir fievre; si en covient traire grant quantiteit, et eslargir le pertus tant qu’il chiece em pameson; puis que tu rewardes toutes les conditions de sainie, et met ta main sus som poulz quant il saine, que li mors ne viegne en leu de pameson, et ceu avient maintes fois, quant li sainieres est negligens; et ne covient mie quant tu vues desliier lou bras, et faire issir sanc la seconde fois, et li pertus est clos, que tu presses forment sus; ne s’il est corbes, qu’il estende lou bras hastanment, car ce seroit malz; mais le laisse tant qu’il saine la seconde fois; ou tu i point a la pointe dou flaime, tant que li sans qui est congelez a pertus de la voinne isse fuer, et met sus I poc de seil remis en aigue, et presse sus legierement.	For there is much blood within the body which is already heated, and it causes fever; thus a large quantity must be drawn off, and the passage widened until it bleeds freely; when you observe all the conditions for safety, place your hand on the pulse as soon as the bleeding starts, so death does not occur from fainting, and this happens often when the bloodletter is negligent; nor should you press firmly upon it if you want to release the arm and draw blood again, with the passage closed, nor should you extend the arm quickly if it is curved, for that would be worse; but leave it until the second bleeding starts; or prick at the point of the flame so that the frozen blood in the vein opening dislodges, place a little salt dissolved in water over it, and press lightly upon it.
Et se li voine est enflee, si la laisse et ne l’estreindre mie, tant que li aposteme soit apaisiez.	And if the vein is swollen, leave it and do not bind it, until the abscess is appeased.
Et se necessitez est dou traire dou sanc la seconde fois, si le saine en celui leu meisme, ou en un autre voinne, ou en l’autre bras.	And if it is necessary to draw blood a second time, do so from the same vein, or from another vein, or from the other arm.
Li voinne emmi le bras est sainie en leu de la voine dou chief por ceu qu’elle est composte.	The vein in the arm is bled instead of the head vein because it is composed appropriately.
Et li maniere de la sainie si est que li malaides boute sa main en aigue chaude, tant que li foscile soit rouges; puis soit liiéz moienement, si que li voinne apere bien, puis le saine maintenant dou travers, ne mie dou large ne dou lonc; et soit li pertus larges, et soit sainiez bien pres de la jointe de la main, et se sans n’en puet issir, si remet la main en aigue chaude, et laisse corre lou sanc en l’aigue, tant que tu en aies assez; et se c’est en esteit, si ne rebouter mie la main en aigue chaude, car on l’i met plus en yver que en esteit; et li sainie de ceste voine est plus sauve de toutes autres voinnes, qu’il n’i a ne artere ne nerf.	And the method of bleeding is that the patient puts their hand in hot water until it turns red; then bind it moderately so that the vein becomes firm, and now bleed through the middle, not across its width or length; make the incision wide and close to the joint of the hand, and if blood does not come out, put the hand back into hot water, and let the blood run in the water until you have enough; and if this is done in summer, do not put the hand in hot water again, for it is used more often in winter than in summer; and bleeding from this vein is safer than all other veins, as there are no artery or nerve nearby.
Li sainie de la salvatele de la main destre si vaut a toutes les maladies dou foie, et c’est li maniere: estrain la main, et boute en aigue chaude, tant que li voinne soit enflee, si c’on la voie; et se la saine de travers, et se tu la copes dou tout en tout, si ne grieve rien; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car li nerf sont desoz toz desnuez de char, et puis remet la main en aigue chaude, se li sans est congelez en la plaie, et n’en puet issir.	The treatment of the right hand salve is worth for all diseases of the liver, and this is the manner: pull out the hand, and put it in hot water, until the veins are swollen if you can see them; and if the vein runs obliquely, and if you cut it completely through, nothing will hurt; and do not go too deep, for the nerves are below entirely bare of flesh, and then put the hand back into hot water, if the blood is congealed in the wound, and it cannot come out.
Et quant tu avras trait dou sanc tant com mestier t’est, si met sus la voinne oile et seil por souder hastanment, et ensi fai de chescun rain.	And when you have drained the blood as much as is necessary, put on the vein oil and wax to seal it quickly, and do this for each vein.
Li sainie de li en la main senestre si vaut a la maladie de la mice, et fai tout ausi com je t’ai dit devers destre.	The treatment of the left hand is for the disease of the spleen, and do it exactly as I told you for the right.
Li sainie de la sophene si vaut a toutes les maladies que sont desoz le cors, si com maladies de la marris, et retenement de flors, et maladie des rains, et des cuixes et des jambes ancienes, et semblans maladies.	The salve of the sophene is effective against all diseases that are below the body, such as ailments of the thighs, retention of urine, disease of the legs and knees, and old diseases of the hips and legs, and similar illnesses.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides boute som piet en aigue chaude, et frote sus la voinne tant qu’elle pere, et lie desus la jointure dou piet; et li voinne si est a la cheville, et par desus lou piet en vont mout de rains; saine la donques ou plus large rain, ou a la cheville, que mues vaut.	And the quality of its salve is that the patient dips their foot in hot water, and rubs it on the vein until it becomes soft, and applies it above the joint of the foot; and if the vein is at the ankle, and there are many veins running up the foot, apply it to the widest vein, or at the ankle, which is most effective.
Et se tu la saines sus lou piet, si te warde des ners qui sont desoz, et la saine de traver ausi com en copant; et soit li flaimes anesil.	And if you apply the salve on the foot, be careful of the nerves that are below, and apply it across as when cutting; let the application be gentle.
Et se li sans n’en puet issir, si remet lou piet en l’aigue, et laisse bien vuidier la voine.	And if the blood cannot come out, place the foot in warm water, and let the vein be opened properly.
Et se li sainieres faut la premiere fois, si rencomence la seconde au desus un poc, car li leus est salz; ne ne douter de nerf, si com nos avons dit, et ensi fai de la sophene de l’autre piet igalment.	And if the incision is insufficient the first time, then make it again a little higher up, for the place is salty; do not worry about nerves, as we have said, and do this equally with the sole of the other foot.
Li leus de la voinne sciatique est a la cheville de fuer, et sa sainie vaut a la dolor de la hainche, quant c’est por sanc chaut.	The site of the sciatic vein is at the ankle on the inner side, and its incision relieves hip pain when it is due to hot blood.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides entre ou bain, et estraigne desus la cheville IIII dois en tordant, car autrement n’apert li voinne; et s’elle apert, si le saine en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et en traversant; et vaut mues que tu la copes, car li leus est saus, et elle est mout reponue a mains homes.	And the quality of its incision is such that the patient enters the bath, and presses above the ankle four fingers by twisting, for otherwise the vein does not appear; and if it appears, then cut it in all ways you can, and across; and it is better to cauterize it, for the site is deep, and it tends to reappear on many people.
Et se tu ne la trueves, si saine aucun rain de li qui apert ou dos dou piet, et vers lou petit doi, et te warde des ners; et fai tant corre dou sanc que tu vues, et puis deslie lou lien, et met sus coton et l’estraint; ele est maintenant sanee.	And if you do not find it, take a piece of linen from the area that is on the back of the foot and towards the little toe, and be careful of the nerves; and let the blood flow as much as you wish, and then loosen the bandage, and put cotton on and bind it; it is now healed.
des sainies de ventouse	cupping treatments
Ventouses sont fait de cornes, ou d’arain, ou de voirre; et ventosation si est faite selonc II manieres: ou par ferir et atraire sanc, ou sens ferir.	Cupping instruments are made of horns, linen, or glass; and cupping is performed in two ways: one by drawing blood, the other without drawing blood.
Et ceste ventosation qui est sens ferir si est selonc II manieres: ou elle est a tout feu, ou sens feu; et ventosation qui est faite par ferir et par estraction de sanc si est faite en XIIII leus dou cors, de coi li uns est tout en som le chief; et li autres est emmi le col; et II autres en II costeis dou col; et li ventouse desoz lou menton; et li ventouse des II espaules; et li ventouse sus les crupies; et les ventouses emmi les II bras; et les ventouses des II jambes; et les ventouses des II chevilles; et li ventosation ne trait point de sanc, fuer que des menues voinnes que sont esparses en la char, et por ceu n’en afoiblist om mie, si com on fait de sainie de voinne; et ne covient mie qu’elle soit aministree, ne a tout feu ne sens feu, en aucune maladie qui vient de repletion, tant que toz li cors soit vuidiez.	And this cupping without drawing blood is performed in two ways: either with heat or without heat; and the cupping that involves drawing blood is done at fourteen locations on the body: one on the top of the head; another around the neck; two others on each side of the neck; one below the chin; two on the shoulders; two above the buttocks; two in each arm; two in each leg; and two on each ankle. This type of cupping does not draw much blood, only from small veins scattered throughout the flesh, and therefore it does not weaken a person as venesection does; and it should not be administered with or without heat in any disease caused by excess, until all parts of the body are emptied.
Et se par necessiteit de maladies covient ventoser, ou por acostumances, si l’amenistrons chescune houre en l’encomencement dou mois, ou en la fin, et emmi et en chescun tens; car il i a de telz qui, quant il ont mestier de ventoser, si ont pesant chief; et si a telz qui truevent repletion et roujor en lor faice, et en lor chief, et au col, et tenebrour as eulz; et telz qui truevent une goute de sanc en lor bouche, et ont enflee la lengue, et raichent sanc; et si i a de telz qui songent, et voient par nut sanc et navrez et mors et semblans choses.	And if due to the necessity of diseases it is necessary to bleed, or by custom, we shall do so each hour at the beginning of the month, or at the end, and likewise in every period; for there are those who, when they need bleeding, have a heavy head; and there are those who feel bloated and redness on their face, and on their head, and neck, and darkness in their eyes; and there are those who see blood droplets in their mouth, and have swelling of the tongue, and cough up blood; and there are those who dream, and see by night blood and wounded and dead and similar things.
Et quant nos voions ces signes, et meismement quant c’est emmi lou mois, nos lou commandons a ventoser aprés III houres dou jor.	And when we see these signs, especially at the same time each month, we instruct them to bleed after three hours of the day.
Li sainie de la muze si aide a la grieteit dou chief … que vient as eulz, et ne covient mie que ce soit aprés l’evacuation de tout lou cors; et ceste ventosation si est en leu de la sainie de la cephalique, et ne covient mie que cil qui est de froide complexion en use, ou qui ait chatharre, car ce lor fait mout grant nuisement; et por ceu ne covient mie que li veillart en usent, ne qui ont ou chief froides maladies.	The massage of the temples helps with headaches … that come from the eyes, and should not be done after the evacuation of all the body; and this ventilation is instead like the massage of the cephalic region, and those with a cold complexion should not use it, nor those who have catarrh, because it causes them great harm; and therefore it is not suitable for the elderly to use it, nor for those who suffer from cold diseases in the head.
Et cil qui s’en saine sovent, si devient oblious, et por ce covient mettre la ventouse un poc plus aval par la doutance d’obliance.	And those who become frequently relieved by it, may become forgetful, and therefore the cupping should be placed a bit lower due to the risk of forgetfulness.
Li ventosation emmi le col est en leu de la sainie dou chief et de la basilique, et por ceu vaut elle a l’estrecement dou pis, et a fendure de la chenal dou pormon, et a toust, et a repletion; et la covient poc bouter, car s’elle tient trop fermement, si enjanre obliance ou stomac et ou cuer.	Cupping on the neck is like the massage of the head and the basilic region, and therefore it is beneficial for tightness in the chest, rib fractures, coughing, and bloating; but it should be applied gently, as if it holds too firmly, it may cause forgetfulness or indigestion in the stomach and heart.
Li ventosations as II costelz dou col si vaut as dolors dou chief, et obtalmie et emigrainne, et a l’estranglement, et a la dolor as racines des dens, et est en leu de la sainie de la basilique; et covient que tu comandes au sainor qu’il espresse sa main au mettre, qu’il ne cope l’artere, et ne veigne decorremens de sanc.	The ventosation between the two ribs of the neck is effective for headaches, and for optic nerve pain and migraines, and for choking, and for pain at the roots of the teeth, and it is in the place of the basilica bone; and you must instruct the healer to press his hand when applying it, that he does not cut the artery, and there should be no bleeding.
Li ventosations desoz lou menton si vaut a maladie de bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et semblans maladies qui sont en la bouche; et est en leu des sainies des II levres.	The ventosation below the chin is effective for mouth diseases, and for gum decay, and similar ailments that are in the mouth; and it is at the place of the bones of the two lips.
Li ventosations des espaules vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de remplissement.	The ventosation of the shoulders is effective for diseases that come from heat and swelling.
Li ventosations des coutes si vaut autant com des III voinnes dou bras, car elle atrait sanc de ces grosses voinnes; et comande au sainor qu’il ne fiere mie trop em parfont, car li leus est nus de char, et sait desoz ners et arteres.	The venesection of the arms is worth as much as that of three veins of the arm, because it attracts blood from these large veins; and instruct the physician not to cut too deeply, for the flesh is thin there, and near nerves and arteries.
Li ventouse qui est sus la croupe si vaut as emoroydes dou fondement, et as maladies desoz, et covient que li ventouse soit grans, et soit d’arain, qu’elle a mestier de bien traire; et par aventure, s’elle estoit subtilz, si briseroit; et i fai grans plaies.	The venesection on the buttocks is worth as much as hemorrhoids of the anus, and for diseases underneath, it should be large, made of iron, needing to draw well; and perhaps if it were delicate, it would break; and it causes large wounds.
Les ventouses des jambes si sainent apertement, car elles atraient sanc de tout le cors, et valent as dolors ancienes des rains, et de la marris, et de la vessie, et ramoinnent les flors; et sont en leu des II sophenes, et des II chevilles, et toutevoie elles afoiblissent lou cors aprés lonc us, et font venir paumison em plusors dispositions.	The venesections of the legs are very effective, for they attract blood from the entire body, and are worth for pains of old age, and of the kidneys, and of the bladder, and reset flows; and they are at the place of the two thighs, and of the two ankles, and overall they weaken the body after long use, and cause fainting in various conditions.
Li maniere de mettre la ventouse si est que tu la mettes premier vuide, et succe tempreement, et la met hastanment, et remue igalment, et ne cesser de ceu faire, tant que tu voies lou leu rouge et enfleit, et apere li roujor dou sanc; puis fier, et remet les ventouses, et pren warde en la disposition des cors, car il i a telz qui ont tanre char, et clers porez: si covient ferir une fois soulement, et covient faire larges plaies, et un poc parfondes; et suce legierement.	The way to apply the cupping vessel is that you place it first empty, then tempering, and put it quickly, moving evenly, and do not stop doing this until you see the spot red and swollen, and after a while, fix them, and replace the cups, and take care in the condition of the flesh, for there are some who have tender flesh, and clear pores: so you should strike once only, and it is necessary to make large wounds, and somewhat deep; and suck lightly.
Et se li sans est gros, si couvient ferir II fois: la premiere fois por subtiliier la voie dou sanc gros.	And if the blood is thick, you should strike twice: the first time to make the blood flow thinner.
Et se li sans est tres espés, si covient ferir la tierce fois; et quant nos volons traire dou sanc poc et poc, si nos soffist soulement une fois.	And if the blood is very thick, you should strike a third time; and when we wish to draw a little blood at a time, we do it only once.
Et se nos volons mout de sanc, si rencomensons sovent; et se li sans est espés, si fier em parfont, et li termines si est que li keurs soit perciez soudement, et couvient a celui qui a gros cuir et dur, et qui ont estrois porelz, que tu oignes les leus des ventouses d’oile aperitif et dissolutif: se c’est en esteit, d’oile violet, ou d’oile d’amandres douces, ou d’oile de semence de cucurbite; et se c’est en yveir, d’oile de cresson, ou de lis, ou de camomille, ou autre semblant.	And if we bleed much, we often resume it; and if the blood is thick, then apply fir to it thoroughly, and its end must be that the veins are pierced suddenly, and for those who have thick skin and hard pores, you should anoint the places with suction cup oil that is stimulating and dissolving: if it is in summer, violet oil, or sweet almond oil, or cucumber seed oil; and if it is in winter, cress oil, or lily oil, or chamomile oil, or similar.
Et se li superfluitez est grosse et froide, si pren oile amaratin, ou de balsamite, ou oile d’anet, et les semblans.	And if the excess is thick and cold, then take marjoram oil, or balsam oil, or anise oil, and similar.
Et se cil cui on saine a tendre char et larges porelz, se n’i covient mettre point d’oile, mais le covient laver aprés la ventosation d’aigue rose, ou d’aigue froide, ou d’aigue de morelle, ou d’aigue de cucurbite, ou d’aigue de porcelainne, ou autre semblant.	And if the one to whom treatment is given has tender flesh and large pores, no oil should be applied, but it is necessary to wash after ventosity with rose water, or cold water, or mulberry water, or cucumber water, or porcelain water, or similar.
Et cil qui a mout de moistor, si se leve d’aisil, ou d’aigue de mirte, et de sumac, et de semblans choses.	And those who have much moisture should rise from a bath of myrtle water, or sumac water, and similar things.
Et cil qui ont grosses superfluitez se levent de vin viel, ou d’aigue de seuc, ou de decoction d’anet ou de camomile, ou d’autres semblans; et ne se covient mie sainier de ventouse devant le bain ne em bain, mais aprés lou bain une houre ou II; et ne dorme mie aprés la ventosacion, et covient k’il se warse, quant il se doit ventoser et quant il est ventosez.	And those who have large excesses should rise from old wine, or fig water, or decoction of anise or chamomile, or similar; and it is not appropriate to bleed with a cupping glass before the bath nor in the bath, but after the bath for one hour or two; and do not sleep after ventosity, and they must wash when they should be cupped and when they are cupped.
Et warde se cil qui se saine est coleriques, et se li sans est trop agus et enflamez; si covient qu’il preigne choses froides, si com pomes grenates et endives et laitues a l’aisil, et semblans choses; et menjuce pucins, et char de chastron, et viandes moistes.	And beware if the one who is to be bled is choleric, and if the blood is too thick and inflamed; then he should take cold things, such as sour apples, endives, lettuce hearts, and similar things; and eat young birds, and castrated meat, and moist foods.
Et cil qui a froide complexion, si preigne syrop de miel, et vin odorant moien, qui est entre viel et noveil, et menjuce poc, et menjuce pucins et petis oiselz et pijons; et lou jor qu’il se ventousera, si doit plus boivre que mengier; et covient doner a aucuns homes aucune fois triaicle ou muscate devant la ventosacion, ou aprés, por conforter les membres principalz; et soit subtiliiez li sans, mais il ne covient mie que cil qui sont chaut le boivent.	And those with a cold complexion should take syrup of honey, and perfumed wine that is between old and new, and eat boiled foods, and eat young birds and small birds and pigeons; and on the day they will be bled, they should drink more than they eat; and sometimes it is appropriate to give certain people triacle or musk before bleeding, or after, to comfort the principal members; and the blood should be subtle, but those with a hot nature should not drink such things.
Les ventouses que sont mises sens ferir sont celles que sont mises sus lou foie, et sus la mice, et podagre, et sus lou ventre et la boude et les rains et la hainche, car cil membre ne soffrent mie ferir sus oulz, et ne le fait on fuer que por atraire sanc de membre em membre, si com nos mettons sus les mameles quant li neis sainne; por oster la viscositeit qui est au membre, si com nos metons ventouses sus le ventre et sus la boude por amenuisier le membre; et oste la dolor, quant il i a opilation ou piere, si oste par sa vertu atractive par aventure l’opilation, ou desaert la piere de son leu; et ensi fait ele quant on le met sus lou foie et sus la mice quant il i a ventositeit retenue, et ces ventouses sont aministrees vuides por sucier tant soulement; et aucune fois sont aministrees ensamble feu, et aucunes fois plainnes d’aigue tede, si com em maladies dou pleuresin, et en tel maniere c’on emplisse la ventouse d’aigue chaude soule, ou d’aigue ou il ait cuit herbes covenaubles a ceu.	The suction cups that are placed without piercing are those placed on the liver, and on the spleen, and for gout, and on the abdomen and belly and thighs and hip, because these limbs do not tolerate being pierced, and one does this only to draw blood from limb to limb, as we place them on the breasts when a child is nursing; to remove viscosity that is in the limb, just as we apply suction cups on the abdomen and on the stomach to reduce swelling; and it relieves pain when there is obstruction or stone, removing by its attractive power perhaps the obstruction, or displacing the stone from its place; and similarly, they act when placed on the liver and spleen where there is retained wind, and these suction cups are administered empty for sucking only; sometimes they are filled together with fire, and sometimes filled with warm water, as in cases of pleurisy, and in such a way that one fills the cup with hot water alone, or with water in which herbs suitable for this purpose have been cooked.
Li forme de la ventouse aministré a feu si est ci:	The form of the cupping vessel administered with fire is as follows:
Et ait II dois de large et demi palme de parfont, et ait ou costeit entor lou mileu I petit pertus, ausi com por bouter une aguille, et soit d’arain, souef devant si qu’ele ne blece lou malaide au mettre sus lou membre; et ait em mileu une verge de travers d’arain ou de fer, por mettre une chandoile emprise, et en soient et grans et petites selonc les maladies et l’eaige de ces qui les prenent; car les ventouses des enfans sont autres que des vielz, et des maigres que des gras.
