And it has two fingers wide and half a palm deep, and on the side there is one small hole, as if to fit a needle, and it should be made of brass, smooth so that it does not hurt the patient when applied to the limb; and in the middle there is a transverse rod of brass or iron, for placing a wick, and they are various sizes both large and small according to the diseases and age of those who use them; for the cupping vessels for children are different from those for the elderly, and for thin people than for fat ones.
Et doit on ensi mettre ceste ventouse sus lou membre: empren la chandoile de cire ou I linement, et le met emmi la ventouse au traver de la verge qui est emmi la ventouse, si que li clartez soit au fons de la ventouse qu’elle ne brule le malaide; et puis la met sus lou membre, et tes dois soit sus lou pertus que nos avons dit, si que quant on vuet, si en va li vapor, et oste on la ventouse; et emprent on le linement si com devant, et le rencomence sovent, se tu as mestier.	And one must place this cupping vessel on the limb thus: take the wick of wax or linen and put it in the cupping vessel across the rod that is inside the cupping vessel, so that the flame stays at the bottom of the cupping vessel and does not burn the patient; then place the cupping vessel on the limb, with your fingers over the hole we mentioned, so that when you want to, the vapor can escape and remove the cupping vessel; take the linen again as before, and repeat it often if needed.
En la ventouse donques qui est aministree em maladie de pleuresin, a tout aigue, n’a point de verge ne de pertus, et n’est amenistree fuer que quant ele est plaine d’aigue, et est mise sus lou membre tant soulement; et c’est li forme:	In the cupping treatment for pleurisy, which is applied in all cases of acute illness, there is no rod or hole, and it is not used except when it is full of liquid, and it is placed only on the limb; and this is the form:
Sansues ne sont amenistrees fuer que en membres ou on ne puet mettre ventouses por lour petitece, si com levres et gencives, et semblans leus; et en leus desnuez de char, si com doi ou neis, et autres semblans; et li qualitez de l’user si est que quant tu trueves sansues que sont en aigues douces nettes sens porreture, si les pren; et les met une nut en aigue douce, tant qu’elles soient famillouses, et n’aient rien en ventres; et puis soit sainiez de voinne et de ventouse, puis frote le membre tant k’il soit rouges, et met sus les sansues; et quant elles seront plainnes, et cherront, se c’est leu ou on puisse mettre ventouse, se li met, car ce vaut mout aprés.	Cupping should not be used except on limbs where cups cannot be applied due to their small size, such as the lips and gums, and similar areas; and in bare flesh spots like the eyes or nails, and other similar places; and the quality of use is that when you find cupping for mild cases without any impurities, take them; and place one in warm water until they are familiar, and have nothing inside; then cut a vein and apply cupping, rub the limb until it becomes red, and put on the cups; and when they are full and fall off, if it is an area where cups can be applied, apply them because this is very valuable afterwards.
Se ceu non, si leve le leu d’aisil, et puis d’aigue, mout bien, et puis l’espreint; et se li leus saine trop aprés lou cors des sansues, si moille I drapel de lin en aigue froide, et met sus, tant que li sans soit estenchiés; et se li sans est multipliez, si met sus vitriole broié, ou gales, et semblans choses, tant qu’il soit estenchiez; ou tu met sor le leu moitiez de feves pelees, et les laisse tant qu’elles s’aerdent au leu, si estanchera maintenant; et se tu en as de plus mestier, si pren autres sansues.	If not, lift the area and then apply cold water, very well, and then press it; and if the wound heals too quickly over the flesh, soak a linen cloth in cold water and place it on until the blood is absorbed; and if there are multiple wounds, put on ground vitriol or gall, and similar things, until they are absorbed; or you can apply half a pound of peeled beans to the area, let them dry there, and now it will stop bleeding; and if you need more remedies, take other herbs.
Et se les sansues ne se vuellent prendre, si frote le leu de sanc fres, ou tu i fiche une aguille tant que li sans en isse, et puis les met sus, et tantost com elles sentent lou sanc, si s’aerdent; et quant tu vues qu’elles chieent, si poudre sus un poc d’aloen et de seil broiet, ou de cendre, si cherront maintenant.	And if the wounds do not wish to be treated, rub the area with fresh blood, or place a needle there until the blood comes out, and then apply them, and as soon as they feel the blood, they will dry; and when you see that they are falling off, sprinkle some aloes and frankincense powder, or ash, and now they will fall.
Ci comence li livre des brisures	Here begins the book of fractures
Cist chapistres est maintes fois necessaires en l’art de medicine, et est restorement de brisure et de desaluement.	This chapter is often necessary in the art of medicine, and it pertains to the restoration of fractures and dislocations.
Saichiez, chier fil, que li fol mire se gietent de cest chapistre, qu’il ne virent onques nul des anciens livres, ne lettre n’en lurent; et por ceste cause est estraingie li science en nostre terre, car je n’en trovai onques nul boin; et n’en sai nient, fuer que par la science des anciens livres, ou j’ai tant estudiiet que je en ai traite la science, et par experiment, et par l’acostumance de ma vie; et je vos ai jai descrit en cest chapistre ceu qui est contenut, et l’ai abregié en la fin, et ai mostreit clerement les formes des estrumens que sont amenistrez, si com j’ai fait en ces II chapistres ci devant.	Know, dear son, that the foolish doctor falls away from this chapter, for they have never seen any of the ancient books or read any letters; and because of this reason, knowledge is strange in our land, for I have never found anyone good at it; and I know nothing except by the science of ancient books, where I have studied so much that I have treated the science, and through experience, and by the custom of my life; and I have clearly described in this chapter what is contained within, and have summarized at the end, and have shown clearly the forms of the instruments that are mentioned, as I have done in these two preceding chapters.
Il covient donques que nos disons ou prologue de cest livre les sommes de la parole et les chapistres ou li saiges met son entendement, et demore sus la verteit, si que cil qui sont esproveit saichent et aprenent cest art noble, et l’aprenent a autrui.	It is therefore necessary that we say in the prologue of this book the summaries of the speech and the chapters where the wise man puts his understanding, and remains on the truth, so that those who are experienced know and learn this noble art, and teach it to others.
Je dis que quant brisure ou dislocation ou torsions ou quasseure vient a aucun, si covient que tu te hastes de sainier lou malaide d’une part et d’autre, s’aucune chose ne lou te tot, si com foiblece de cors, ou enfes, ou viellars; ou se li tens n’est tres chaus, ou trop frois; et menjuce cholz frois, c’est a savoir froides joutes, et char d’oiseil et de chevril, et ne boive point de vin, ne menjuce nules grasses chars, et ne s’emplisse mie trop de viandes qui remplissent les voinnes de sanc, tant que tu n’aies doute d’aposteme chaut, ne d’espandement de matiere au membre; si reviegne li malaides a som premerain governement k’il a useit.	I say that when a fracture or dislocation or torsion or sprain comes to someone, it is necessary that you hurry to treat the patient from both sides, if nothing prevents it, such as weakness of body, children, or elderly; or if the time is not very warm, or too cold; and eat cool things, namely cold broth, and meat of birds and pork, and do not drink wine, nor eat any fatty meats, and do not overfill yourself with foods that fill the veins with blood, until you have no doubt about a hot abscess, nor spread of matter in the limb; so return to the patient's initial treatment if it has been effective.
Et quant li os brisiés comence a restourer, si covient que on norrisse le malaide de viandes que font gros norrissement, ou il ait viscositeit, si com froment cuit en aigue, et ris, et testes, et piez, et pance de vaiche, et oefz, et poissons fres, et gros vin, et semblans chose.	And when the broken bones begin to restore themselves, it is necessary to nourish the patient with foods that provide thick nutrition, which are viscous, such as boiled wheat in water, rice, and heads, feet, and belly of fish, and eggs, and fresh fish, and strong wine, and similar things.
Car a teil norrissement se reprent mues et plus tost li brisure.	For such nourishment promotes healing and the fracture heals more quickly.
Et saichiez que li os brisiez des vielz et des decrepites ne se pueent mie bien reprendre ne souder selonc lor nature por la sechor des membres, ne cil ausi qui sont trop tendre, si com os de petis enfans; mais n’a cure, ramoinne sus l’os brisiet I gros tenrons qui s’aert et joint le membre ensamble, tant qu’il enforce si com il fut devant; et ne li tot point de son oevre, et por ceu le covient norrir de grosses viandes, si com nos avons dit.	And know that broken bones of the old and infirm do not heal well or knit according to their nature due to the dryness of the limbs, nor those who are too tender, such as the bones of small children; but it does not matter, reset the bone on a thick splint which holds and joins the limb together until it strengthens as it was before; and do not let them eat much of their usual food, and for this reason they must be nourished with heavy foods, as we have said.
Et saiches que les briseures sont diverses em maintes manieres.	And know that fractures are diverse in many ways.
Car li brisure dou chief est autre que li brisure dou pis, ou de la jambe, et je vos dirai en cest chapistre toutes manieres de brisure.	For the fracture of the head is different from the fracture of the hip, or of the leg, and I will tell you in this chapter all kinds of fractures.
Car il i a brisure que vait a arvol, et autre en aguisant, si com li taille d’une penne por escrire.	For there is a fracture that goes to the bone, and another in sharpening, like the shaft of a quill for writing.
Et si a brisure avec plaie, et brisure a tout une petite fendure.	And there is a fracture with a wound, and a fracture that is just a small crack.
Et a chescune maniere ait son engien, et son estrument propre en la restauration, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient en son leu; et est conue li brisure de l’os par ceu que li leus est tors, et apert bien par defuer, et sone au presseir de la main; et quant il n’i a tortuositeit ne son au tochier, et li malaides ne sent mie grant dolor, se n’i a point de brisure; mais il puet bien avoir tortuositeit, ou fendure, ou petite brisure.	And each kind has its own treatment and proper instrument for restoration, according to what the memory brings forth in its place; and a bone fracture is known by the deformity of the limb, and is clearly evident by swelling, and sounds hollow when pressed with the fingers; and when there is no deformity or sound upon pressing, and the patient does not feel great pain, then there is no fracture; but it may well have a twist, or crack, or small fracture.
Si ne covient mie que tu lou mueves a la main, mais met sus medicines que vienent ci aprés, et puis l’estraint maintenant subtilment.	It is not necessary to move it with your hand, but apply the medicines that come next, and then press it now gently.
Et saiches que li brisure que vait en arvol, et sont les II parties desjointes, il les covient maintenant mettre a point igalment, ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne; et se apostemes chaulz i vient, si lou laisse aucun jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez; puis le met igal au mues que tu pues legierement et saigement, et saiches que li restauration de li est plus legiere que li restaurations de celi ou il ait pieces; puis l’estraint, si com il covient ci aprés.	And know that the fracture that goes into the bone, and where the two parts are disjoined, they must now be placed equally, as if smooth abscesses were to come; and if smooth abscesses do come, let it rest for some days until the abscess is eased; then set it equal when you can lightly and wisely; know that the restoration of this one is easier than those with pieces; then press it as should follow hereafter.
Et se en l’os a piéces brisies, si l’estent de II pars, se c’est mains ou piet, ou a ta main se c’est uns petis membres, ou a II cordes, ou a une corde et a ta main; et met le membre selonc sa figure natureil, si que quant les parties dou membre brisiet sont desevrees, si ramoinne par toz engiens les additions en lor leus au mues que tu pues, et garde que par ton ovraige ne viegne au malaide lesion ne doulor; et ajoste bien les II chiés des os selonc les millors formes.	And if there are pieces of a broken bone, hold it from two parts, whether it is the foot or hand, or with your hand for smaller members, or with two cords, or one cord and your hand; and place the member according to its natural shape, so that when the parts of the broken bone are separated, reset all additions in their places as you can, and ensure that your work does not cause injury or pain to the patient; and properly align the two ends of the bones according to the best forms.
Et le sent bien a la main s’il te semble k’il ne soit mie bien: si la dresce bellement, et ne l’estraindre mie trop, ne presser si com font cil qui i font venir par lor ovraige aposteme chaut et contraction au membre, si com nos avons veut maintes fois.	And you can feel with your hand if it seems to you that it is not right: then straighten it properly, and do not pull too hard, nor press so as to cause heat and contraction in the limb through their work, as we have seen many times.
Et quant li membres est a point, si chastie bien lou malaide qu’il ne lou mueve, ne en veillant ne en dormant, ne en tornant, ne en autre maniere; et warde bien que li membres soit si asseurez qu’il ne sente nule dolor.	And when the limb is properly set, instruct the patient well not to move it, neither while awake nor asleep, nor in turning, nor in any other way; and ensure that the limb is secured so that he does not feel any pain.
Car quant il sent nulle dolor, si n’est mie a point, et le covient mettre en teil disposition qu’il ne sent nule dolor; et te garde k’il soit mis droitement, que tortuositez n’i veigne quant il iert restorez; et li qualitez dou membre brisiet est selonc ceu que je te dis.	For when he feels any pain, it is not properly set, and you must put it in such a position that he does not feel any pain; and be careful that it is placed correctly so that no curvature arises when it is restored; and the quality of the broken limb depends on what I tell you.
Saiches que li membre brisiet sont divers em petitece et en grandor et en forme.	Know that broken limbs are diverse in smallness and largeness and in form.
Car il i a petis membres, si com brais et dois et semblans: si covient envoloupeir drapelz de lin molz et subtilz; et cil qui sont gros, si com cuixe et jambe: si covient envoloupeir d’un liien large et dur, car li larges liiens embraice tout le grant membre, et l’estraint de toutes pars igalment, si qu’il n’i a nule taiche; puis lie entor estoupes legieres, III tours ou IIII selonc lou membre, et estraint ta main un poc a tout le liien, puis vai au desus de la brisure et l’estraint moins, que la brisure puis esloigne un poc la brisure; et mollifie lou liien poc et poc, tant que tu preignes grant partie dou leu sain, puis repren I autre liien, et torne entor derechief sus lou leu brisiet; puis revai a la partie desoz de la brisure, et l’estraint moienement, ne mie trop fort ne trop molement, si com nos avons dit en la premiere lieure desus; puis met entre les liiens estoupes de lin ou drapelz, tant qu’il soit toz igalz, puis lie tout par desus I bendeil, et puis met tes esteles bien faites sus, s’il n’i a aposteme ou enfleure.	For there are small limbs such as arms and thighs: they should be wrapped in soft and thin linen cloths; and those that are large, such as the thigh and leg: they should be wrapped in wide and firm bandages, because wide bandages cover the entire large limb and bind it evenly so that no part is loose; then tie around light rollers three or four times according to the size of the limb, and press your hand slightly over the whole bandage, then go above the break and press less, allowing some space near the break; gradually loosen the bandages little by little until you cover a large portion of healthy tissue, then take another bandage, and wrap around again over the broken area; then tighten moderately below the break, neither too firmly nor too loosely, as we have said in the first chapter above; then place between the bandages linen or cloths so that everything is even, then tie it all up with a wide strip, and finally put on your well-made splints if there is no abscess or swelling.
Et s’il i a enfleure ou aposteme, si met sus chose apaisant aposteme chaut, et qui oste l’enfleure, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors; puis estrain sus tes esteles, et soient de moitiet d’une large cainne rese saigement, ou de fust dont on fait les clives, ou de rains de palme, et soient selonc ceste figure:	And if there is swelling or an abscess, apply a hot and soothing poultice that reduces the swelling, and leave it like this for several days; then incise over your stakes, which should be half as wide as one finger thick, or made of wood used to make clives, or palm ribs, and let them follow this shape:
mais il covient que li estele que om met sus la brisure soit un poc plus grosse et plus large que les autres; et soit ausi longe com il covient au membre de petitece ou de grandor; puis estraint sus les esteles ausi com tu as fait a la premiere lieure, puis lie desus un fil avenanment, si com en la premiere lieure sus la briseure; plus estroit est ensus, adés moins; et covient que li fil soient moien, ne trop gros ne trop menus, et soient de lin mol; car se li fil sont gros, si com j’ai veut des oevres des folz qui font lor lieures des cordes de linement tort, et c’est grant error, car li lieure ne puet estre igal s’il est trop subtilz, et ne covient mie qu’il ait entre chescune estele moins dou doi d’espaice.	but it is necessary that the stake placed over the fracture be a little thicker and wider than the others; and it should also be as long as needed for the limb whether small or large; then incise over the stakes as you did in the first dressing, then place a bandage on top of them, as was done with the first dressing on the fracture; tighter above, looser below; and the thread should be medium-sized, not too thick nor too thin, and should be soft linen; for if the threads are too thick, like those made by foolish people who use twisted linen cords for their dressings, it is a great error, because the dressing cannot be even if it is too fine, and there must be no less than two fingers of space between each stake.
Et se li malaides est navrez par les chiés des esteles aprés l’estrignement en leus sains, si met desoz elles estoupes de lin, ou lainne charpie, si qu’il ne se blece.	And if the patient is pierced by the tips of arrows after they are drawn from their wounds, place cotton plugs or linen strips beneath them so they do not pierce further.
Quant li plaie est avec la briseure, et li keurs est rompus, je en dirai la cure ci aprés.	When the wound is with the splinter, and the bone is broken, I will describe the treatment hereafter.
Et saiches qu’il ne covient mie estraindre d’esteles toz les membres brisiez le premier jor.	And you should know that it is not appropriate to extract all the splinters from broken limbs on the first day.
Car quant li membres est grans, se n’i covient mie mettre esteles fuer que aprés V jors ou VII, ou plus selonc ta seurteit d’aposteme chaut sorvenant; et vez ci la maniere des emplaustres anciiens por restorer brisure, dislocation, et torsion: et est que tu pren de la farine que se tient as parois dou molin, et la confis avec abun d’uef, et met ceste confection, ne trop clere ne trop espesse, et en use, et c’est li commune maniere de l’emplaustre restorant la brisure a plusors dispositions, et meismement as femmes et as petis enfans, car il n’est mie ne trop chas ne trop frois.	For when the limb is large, it is not appropriate to place splinters back in until after five days or seven, or more according to your judgment of a hot abscess that may occur; and here is the manner of ancient plasters for restoring fractures, dislocations, and twists: take flour that is kept near the mill walls, mix it abundantly with eggs, apply this preparation neither too thick nor too thin, and use it. This is the common method of the plaster used to restore fractures in various conditions, especially for women and children, as it is not overly hot or cold.
Autre maniere d’emplastre restorans la brisure et la dislocation et la torsion: pren З abareis et ladani et enule et asefetide et gomme arabique et mugat, ana X З.; mirre et aloes, ana V З.; alechil VIIII З.; et en fai poudre, et les melle avec aubun d’uef; se li complexion de l’ome est chaude, si use de cest emplaustre, car il est de bone composition, et restoure les os brisiés hastanment, et vaut a plusors homes.	Another way to make a plaster for restoring fractures, dislocations, and twists: take benzoin, storax, myrtle, asafoetida, gum arabic, mastic, ana X parts; myrrh and aloes, ana V parts; alembicated vinegar IX parts; and make powder, and mix with egg white; if the person's constitution is hot, use this plaster, for it is well composed, and quickly restores broken bones, and is suitable for many people.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a torsion: pren mugat et vismalve, ana X З.; mirre et aloes, ana VIIII З.; acaice VI З.; bolic armenic X З., et broie bien, et confit avec aigue ou abun d’uef, et l’aministre.	Another way to make a plaster for treating twists: take mastic and wormwood, ana X parts; myrrh and aloes, ana IX parts; acacia VI parts; Armenian bole X parts, and grind well, and cook with water or egg white, and apply.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a jointes et as os desevrez de lor leus, et apaise la dolor sorvenant, et le taille usent de l’os, et la briseure: pren lainne novele, et la moille en aisil et en oile cuit, et met sus lou leu.	Another method of plaster for joints and bones out of place, and to ease the pain arising, and the wear on the bone, and fractures: take new wool, and boil it in grease and oil, and apply it to the site.
Cist emplastres ne restoure mie, mais il est boins por apaisier d’aposteme chaut, et oste proprement les dolors.	This plaster does not heal, but it is good for soothing hot abscesses and properly relieves pain.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre qui restoure les os brisiez: pren foilles de figuier seches, et foilles de pavol terrestre, et broie ensamble, et fai emplaustre.	Another method of plaster to heal broken bones: take dried mulberry leaves and plantain leaves, and grind them together, then make a plaster.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a la restoration de la brisure de l’os et por amenusier lou remenant de l’aposteme.	Another method of plaster for the restoration of a broken bone and to reduce the remaining abscess.
Pren racine de vismalve, camomille, flors de violettes, farine de veces, de chescune une partie; et broie, et confis avec vin, et se li membres est eschaufez, se le confis avec aigue de coriandre moiste, ou d’aigue, et en use.	Take root of vervain, chamomile, violets, flour of oats, of each one part; and grind, and mix with wine, and if the member is heated, mix it with moist coriander water, or water, and use it.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre plus fors que li premier, quant aposteme dur vient a la restauration dou membre.	Another way of making an ointment stronger than the first one, when a hard abscess comes to the restoration of the limb.
Pren racines de vismalve, et semence de lin, balauste, mellilote, et sansuce, et flors de violetes et de camomille, de toutes ana une partie; et broie, et confit avec aigue de salz, ou aigue douce, ou avec vin, selonc la chalor du membre, et son repos.	Take roots of vervain, seeds of flax, hawthorn, melilot, and marshmallow, and flowers of violets and chamomile, of each one part; and grind, and mix with salt water, or sweet water, or with wine, according to the heat of the limb, and its rest.
Ypocras dist en son livre c’on ne mette sus lou membre brisiet por restorer fuer que cerote fait de cire et d’oile, et nulle autre chose plus, et dist qu’il soit entre dous ne trop molz ne trop durs.	Hippocrates states in his book that one should not place anything on a broken limb to restore strength except for cerotic wax made of wax and oil, and nothing else, and he says it should be neither too hard nor too soft.
Et il semble galien c’on doit mettre sus lou membre brisiet, por restoreir, choses seches un poc chaudes, si com mirre et aloes et encens et semblans choses, si com nos avons dit.	And Galen seems to suggest that for restoring a broken limb, dry and slightly warm things should be applied, such as myrrh, aloes, and incense, and similar items, as we have said.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a lesion et a dolor: pren mugath et chevolz d’omes decopez, ou pennes d’oiseil, et vismalve, et seil igalment, et les broie, et en fai emplaustre et lou lie.	Another way to make a plaster for injury and pain: take mastic, human hair, bird feathers, and vervain, in equal parts, grind them together, and make a plaster with it.
Et puis lou deslie un poc aprés, et pren garde se li malaides ne sent nule dolor, ne ne s’est meus li os de son leu; si ne lou deslie par mains jors Et se dolor vient au leu, ou prurite, sens repos ou enfleure, si te haste, et le deslie, et oste l’emplaustre maintenant; et pren drapeil legier, et esponge de mer moiste, et plonge en aigue, et en leve lou leu, tant que li prurite cesse, et soit apaisie li dolor; puis laisse reposer lou membre une houre, puis met sus lainne seche, moillie en aigue ou en oile roset, et lie sus une nut, tant que tu soies seur d’aposteme chaut; et repose li enflammation dou membre, et soit ostee li dolor, puis rencomence la lieure subtil, et un poc d’emplaustre, et ne l’estraindre mie si fort com devant; et subtilie tant qu’il soit sanez.	And then loosen it a bit after that, and be careful if the patient feels any pain or if the bone is not in its place; do not loosen it too soon. And if pain comes to the area, or itching, without rest or swelling, hurry up, and loosen it, and remove the plaster now; take a light cloth and a sponge soaked in sea water, dip it in water, and lift the area until the itching stops, and the pain is eased; then let the limb rest for an hour, then apply dry wool moistened with water or rose oil, and wrap it up on a pad, until you are sure of a hot abscess; and allow the inflammation of the limb to calm down, and when the pain has subsided, restart the gentle wrapping, and a bit of plaster, but do not press as tightly as before; and gently proceed until he is healed.
Et se tu vois que aposteme chaus et roujor et dolor et enfleure sont jai osteit dou tout, et tu as mestier d’emplaustre et de liien, si le rencomence, si com tu a fait premier igalment.	And if you see that the abscess is red and swollen and painful and has pus throughout, and you need to apply a poultice and bandage, then restart as you did first equally.
Et s’il ne vient au membre nient de ceu que nos avons dit, si ne le desliier fuer que aprés III jors ou IIII ou V ou VII; et aucune fois le laisse XX jors, selonc ce c’on voit, tant que li briseure s’aert, et aproche li ajostement de la char sus; adonques lou restraint plus que premier, et li engroisse sa viande, si com j’ai dit devant; et se tu vois lou leu sechier plus que mestier n’est, saiches que norrissemens n’i puet venir; arose lou donques d’aigue chaude tede, toutes les fois que tu lou deslies, et ce soit chescun tier jor, et eslaiche un poc la lieure; par cest ovraige donques cort li norrissemens au membre, et esmende hastanment ceu que font li fol mire, que restourent le membre tortement: c’est malvais, et si est ovraiges paourous, et je n’i voi autre chose que dou lassier et de l’ovrer droitement.	And if it does not come to the limb as we have said, do not release it before three days or four or five or seven; and sometimes leave it for twenty days, according to what you see, until the swelling subsides and the bone edges approach each other; then tighten it more than at first, and thicken its flesh, as I said before; and if you see that the place dries more than necessary, know that new tissue cannot come there; bathe it with warm water daily, every third day when you release it, and loosen the bandage a bit; thus by this work, prevent new growth in the limb, and correct quickly what foolish doctors do, who release the limb too soon: this is wrong, and such practices are dangerous, and I see no other remedy but to leave it and treat it correctly.
des diverses manieres de brisure	Of various ways of fractures
Maintes manieres de brisures sont, et diverses figures, et les causes sont destintees; car il a brisures que sont faites de percussion d’espee, et li colz oste tout l’os jusc’a syfac qui est desoz l’os, si com fait haiche ou fust; et por ceu est apelee ceste maniere de briseure «haichure».	There are many ways of fractures and various figures, and the causes are distinct; for there are fractures that are made by the impact of a sword, and the collarbone breaks all the bone up to the suture which is inside the bone, as if it were splitting wood or a staff; and this manner of fracture is called "haichure".
Ou li espee cope l’os par desus sens percier, et est apelee ceste maniere de brisure «absolue»; et est li plaie de ces II brisures grans ou petite.	When the sword strikes the bone from above without piercing it, this manner of fracture is called "absolute"; and the wound of these two fractures is large or small.
Et s’il i a percussion emboee, ou fendure ou de colz de piere, ou de cheoir sus piere, ou d’autres semblans.	And if there is an embedded impact, or a fissure from falling on stone, or from other similar incidents.
Et s’il a brisure persant, qui aproiche jusc’a la toile qui est desoz l’os, ou elle est sus l’os, et est ceste plaie ou grans ou petite.	And if there is a fracture that approaches the membrane under the bone, or is on the bone, and this wound is either large or small.
Et si a plaie qui est reponue en l’os ausi subtil com uns chevous, et est li fendure petite, et por ceu est apelee ceste brisure «capillaire»; et si la plaie qui est faite ou par ferir de piere, ou par cheoir, ou par semblant chose, et fait entrer la piece de l’os aval, et est li leus chevez si com font li chaudelier quant il fierent sus les chaudieres; si entre li piere dedens.	And if there is a wound in the bone as fine as a hair, and the crack is small, and for this reason it is called a "hairline fracture"; and if the injury is caused by hitting a stone, or falling, or similar things, and causes a piece of bone to enter below, and the place becomes rough like how blacksmiths shape pots; and stones can enter inside.
Et ceu avient plus a sous qui ont ou chief moistes os, si com chief d’enfant; et avient a toutes ces manieres de brisure que pieces menues en sont desevrees si com esteles; et je em parlerai en son leu.	And this happens more often in those who have moist bones in their head, such as the head of a child; and it occurs that in all these types of fractures small pieces are separated like splinters; and I will speak about them at their place.
Et conoissons toutes manieres de briseures par la detraction sus elles, et l’inquisition a tentes, et par la char corrumpue qui est sus.	And we recognize all manners of fractures by the depression on them, and the inquiry with probes, and by the corrupted flesh that is upon them.
Li semblance capillaire est conue par ceu que quant on a descovert l’os, et on frote enche sus, si apert li brisure noire.	The hairline fracture is known by this: when one has exposed the bone and rubbed it, the fracture appears black.
En la cure de la brisure, pren garde as accidens dou malaide, et se tu vois nul malvais accident, si com vomissement de cole, et amission d’entendement, et estension, et paumeson, et fievre ague, et les eulz issir fuer et rougir, et autres semblans em plusors dispositions, si ne puet saner sens doute.	In the treatment of the fracture, be mindful of the patient's symptoms, and if you see any bad signs, such as vomiting bile, loss of consciousness, convulsions, paralysis, intermittent fever, and eyes protruding and reddening, along with other similar conditions in many cases, they cannot heal without doubt.
Et se tu ne vois accident espoantauble, et tu esperes salut, si comence la cure.	And if you do not see any alarming symptoms and hope for recovery, then begin the treatment.
Et quant li navrez vient premier a toi, et c’est en yver, si covient oster l’os devant lou quatorzime jor au mues que tu pues.	And when the wounded person first comes to you, and it is in winter, then you must remove the bone before the fourteenth day from the wound that you can.
Et se c’est en esteit, si te haste d’oster l’os devant lou septime jor, ainsois que li toile desoz l’os soit corrumpue, et vienent li accident que nos avons dit.	And if it is in summer, then hasten to remove the bone before the seventh day, so that the tissue under the bone does not become corrupted, and prevent the accidents we have mentioned.
Et se li brisure de l’os vient jusc’a la toile que cuevre lou cerveil, si covient que tu fendes la partie fendue ensi: et est que tu preignes lou chief dou malaide navreit, et descuevre sus l’os en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et sus la figure de la plaie plus souef que tu pues, et se decorrement de sanc vient au descovrir l’os, ou aposteme chaus, se li aide de ceu qu’il covient, et est que tu emplisses lou leu de drapelz moilliez en oile roset; et fai reposer la plaie tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et soies asseurez de decorrement de sanc; puis comence entor l’os a oster, et c’est fait selonc II manieres d’ovraige: l’une manieres si est que tu copes au taillement estroit devant, et c’est li forme:	And if the break in the bone reaches to the tissue that covers the brain, then you must split the broken part as follows: take the head of the wounded person and expose the bone in all ways possible, and around the wound area deeper than possible. If blood flows during exposure or abscesses occur, handle them appropriately; apply strips soaked in rose oil to fill the area, and keep the wound still until the abscesses are calmed and bleeding stops; then begin removing around the bone according to two methods of work: one method is to cut closely along the incision line, and this is the form:
Et puis i boute I autre taillement plus grant que lou premier.	And then make the other incision larger than the first one.
Et li seconde maniere si est que tu aies nombre de taillemens divers, les uns estrois et les autres larges, et soient a pointe, et soient de fer inde; et en oevre legierement, que tu ne bleces le chief.	And the second method is that you have various incisions of different sizes, some narrow and others wide, with pointed ends, and they should be made of iron; and work gently, so as not to injure the head.
Et se li os est fors et durs, si covient que tu lou perces entor, ainsois que tu i aministres taillemens avec tareres, ne mie parfont qu’il ne percent outre l’os dou test, et doit avoir desus la pointe une marge ou I cercle, que ne laisse passer la pointe outre l’os; et t’en covient avoir plusors, si que chescuns viegne en son leu de l’espés de l’os, si que tu aies tareres por toz test; et c’est li forme des III manieres de tareres:	And if the bone is hard and protruding, you must pierce around it, thus applying incisions with trepanning tools, but not so deeply that they penetrate beyond the skull bone, and should have above the point a margin or a circle to prevent the point from passing through the bone; and you need to have several of them, each fitting in its place according to the thickness of the bone, so that you have trepanning tools for the entire skull; and this is the form of the third method of trepanning tools:
Li qualitez por percier entor l’os brisiet est que tu mettes I tarere sus l’os, et torne a tes dois tant que tu saiches que li os est perciez; puis remet lou tarere autre part un poc aprés, et ensi fai tout entor, puis cope as incisoires l’espaice de l’os qui est entre les pertu, et fai ceu plus subtilment que tu pues, et legierement, si com nos avons dit, tant que tu en traies l’os a ta main, ou a aucun des estrumens que tu as si com tenailles, pinceures; et garde que tu ne touchier au cerveil ne au syfac.	The quality to pierce around the broken bone is that you place one probe on the bone, and turn it with both hands until you know the bone is pierced; then move the probe a little further away, and do this all around, then cut the space of the bone between the holes as carefully as you can, gently, as we have said, until you draw out the bone in your hand, or with any tools that you have such as pincers, forceps; and be careful not to touch the brain or the dura mater.
Et quant tu avras l’os perciet, et trait, si couvient que tu reses l’apreteit qui est demoree de l’os a tout I autre estrument semblant a un incisoire, mais il covient qu’il soit plus tenves et plus subtilz que li autre incisoire; et s’il demore rien des petis os, ne nulles escailles, si les oste legierement a I des estrumens; puis cure la plaie de tentes et d’oignemens que nos avons dit.	And when you have pierced and removed the bone, it is necessary to remove any remaining parts of the bone left with another similar instrument resembling an incisor, but it must be thinner and more delicate than the other incisor; and if there are small bones or scales left behind, gently remove them with the tools; then treat the wound with bandages and ointments as we have described.
Et li autre maniere d’ovraige si est cil que Galiiens dist, qui est plus saus; et le loa molt fort, et c’est sa parole.	And the other method of work is that which Galen says, who is more skilled; and he praises it very much, and this is his word.
Il covient premier que tu descuevres une partie de l’os, lai ou li brisure apert mues, si que quant tu avras descovert celle partie, si metras desoz lou chief de cest incisoire lenticulaire, de coi ci est li forme:	It is necessary first that you uncover a part of the bone where the fracture has moved out, so that when you have uncovered this part, you place below the head of this chisel, here is its form:
Et ne trenche mie d’une part, et est li partie ague en II costez, si que li trenchans est devers l’os; puis fier d’un petit maillet sus, si que tu copes legierement l’os tout entor, et te done bien en garde de la toile que est desoz; s’elle est aerse a l’os, si l’oste legierement, car on l’oste bien sens nuisement, et sens paor.	And do not cut from one side, and the part is beveled on two sides, so that the cutting edge is towards the bone; then strike with a small hammer, so that you lightly groove the bone all around, and take great care of the tissue beneath; if it is loose from the bone, remove it gently, as it can be removed without harm and without fear.
Et se li brisure de l’os ne perce jusc’a la toile, et li os est copez tant soulement par desus, et il i a petites pieces, si couvient rere celle asperiteit, et oster les escailles au raseur subtil dont tu dois avoir diverses quantitez, por amenistrer en chescun leu le plus covenauble, selonc l’ovraige et la figure de la brisure.	And if the bone fracture does not penetrate to the skin, and the bone is broken only from above, with small pieces, then it is necessary behind that roughness, to remove the scales with a fine scraper of which you must have various quantities, to apply in each place the most suitable, according to the work and the shape of the fracture.
Si reis devant de grant raseurs, et aprés de plus subtilz, et ne cesser de ceu faire tant k’il soit bien.	Start with large scrapers and then use finer ones, and do not stop doing this until it is well done.
En chescune des autres tailleures capillaires et brisure subtil, covient que tu amenistres cause selonc son adrecement; et c’est chose que n’est mie reponue a celui qui a mis son estude en cest art.	In each of the other hair cuts and fine fractures, you must treat according to its direction; and this is something that cannot be mastered by one who has not dedicated study to this art.
Et se li syfac est descovers, si covient que tu preignes I drapeil de lin, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et le moille en oile roset, et le mete sus la plaie; puis pren I autre drapeil doublé en II ou en III, et le moille en vin et en oile roset, et le met sus le premier drapeil; et fai ceu plus legierement que tu pues, que tu ne grever lou syfac, puis aministre par desus I autre liien, et ne l’estraindre mie fuer que tant k’il teigne la plaie soulement; et le laisse ensi I jor ou II, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, puis le deslie, et i aministre medicines si com racines de lis, et farine de veces, et poudre d’encens, et aristologe, et semblans choses; et de ces choses fai poudre, et met sus la plaie, et i aministre adés medicines mondefians sens mordication; et warde que li plaie soit adés nette, que tu n’i laissier mie l’oignement, ne n’i laissier mie assembler bowe, car quant bowe s’asemble sus la toile dou cerveil, si la corront et porrist, et avient au malaide grans malice; car quant on met sus lou syfac chose mordant, si nercist par desus.	And if the wound is open, you should take a piece of linen according to the size of the wound, and soak it in rose oil, then place it over the wound; then take another double layer of cloth, and soak it in wine and rose oil, and place it on top of the first piece of cloth; do this as gently as possible so that you do not aggravate the wound, then administer another bandage on top, but do not tighten it too much that it only covers the wound; leave it like this for one or two days until the swelling is reduced, then loosen it and apply medicines such as lily roots, flour of barley, powder of incense, artemisia, and similar things; make a powder from these things and place it on the wound, and quickly administer cleansing medicine without irritation; be careful that the wound remains clean, do not leave any ointment on it, nor allow pus to accumulate on the cloth, for when pus accumulates on the cloth of the brain, it will corrupt and rot, which causes great harm to the patient; because when something irritating is applied to the wound, it can become inflamed if covered.
Pren warde donques, se nulz mavais accidens vient au malaide, si com nos avons dit, si est doutable sens doute.	Therefore, pay attention if any harmful accident happens to the patient, as we have said, it is doubtful without doubt.
Et se noiror n’i vient fuers que por la medicine c’on a mise sus, que teil vertu ait, si covient que tu preignes une partie de miel, et III parties d’oile roset et en glue I drapel, et lou met sus lou syfac; puis lou cure de manieres de cures qu’il couvient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if blackness appears other than from the medicine that has been applied, which has such efficacy, then you should take one part honey, and three parts rose oil, and mix in one drachm of glue, and apply it to the surface; then treat it according to appropriate methods until it is healed.
Saiches que aucune fois sont brisies les II parties dou neis desus, ou li une par li soulement, car ce sont II os; et cil desoz est cartillaginous, et ne brise mie, si ne fait fuer k’enbower ou tordre, et puis saine.	Know that sometimes the two parts of the nose above are broken, or just one part, because they are two bones; and the lower one is cartilaginous, and does not break unless it is forced to bend or twist, and then heals.
Et se l’une des II parties est brisie, si covient que tu boutes ton petit doi ou pertus dou neis, et met igal cele brisure dedens a ton doi indice, et au pouchet par defuer, tant que li neis reveigne selonc sa figure natureil; et fai ce legierement, et warde que li malaides ne sente dolor par ton ovraige.	And if one of the two parts is broken, you must insert your small rod or pin through the nose, and place that break evenly inside your index rod, and outside the pouch, until the nose returns to its natural shape; and do this gently, and be careful that the patient does not feel pain from your work.
Et se li brisure est en la partie desus lou neis, et ne puet venir li dois au leu, si couvient que tu lou mettes igal au chief d’un rait un poc gros.	And if the break is in the part above the nose, and cannot come to its place, then you must set it equally along a thin rod.
Et se li brisure est de II pars, si refai autretel, et te haste de restorer lou premier jor, se tu pues; se ce non, aprés lou septime ou le disime, quant li apostemes chaus est apaisiez, puis bouthe au chief dou neis tentes de drapelz de lin, se li brisure est en une partie.	And if the break is in two parts, then do as before, and hurry to restore it on the first day if you can; if not, after seven or ten days when the abscess has subsided, then insert into the head of the nose pieces of linen cloth if the break is in one part.
Ou tu boutes I autre d’autre part, se li brisure i est; et soient les tentes si grosses qu’eles emplissent les pertus dou neis.	When you insert one from the other side, if there is a fracture; and let the tents be so thick that they fill the passages of the nose.
Et dirent aucun restorour c’on doit moillier les tentes em burre, et muer chescun jor.	And some responders say that the tents should be lubricated with butter, and changed each day.
Il ne me semble mie que ce soit bien, mais covient qu’elles soient moillies en confection d’aubun d’uef, et de poudre de molin; puis laisse la tente, tant que li os soit fers, et li cartilaiges endurcis.	I do not think that is good, but they should be lubricated with a mixture of egg whites, and flour powder; then leave the tent in place until the bone is set, and the cartilage hardened.
Et aucune fois boute on ou neis pennes d’oie en leu de tentes, et si a I souef drapeil entor, et se tient la briseure, et soffle li malaides parmi; or fai lou kel ke tu vues.	And sometimes one inserts goose feathers in place of tents, and if there is a gentle breeze around, it helps to keep the fracture stable, and the patient breathes through them; do as you wish.
Et se apostemes chaus vient au neis tandis com tu i oevres, si i met cerote ou coton moilliet en oile roset, ou en I poc de dyaquilon.	And if abscesses come to the nose while you are working on them, apply plaster or cotton moistened in rose oil, or a little piece of myrrh.
Et se apostemes chaus n’i vient, si met emplastre par defuer, de farine de sisament, et de poudre d’encens, confites avec aubun d’uef, puis met sus estoupes legieres, et ne liier mie lou neis; et se li brisure dou neis est petite, et il est brisiés em menues pieces, si l’estrai as estrumens covenables a ceu, puis cout la fendure, et la cure de choses enjanrans char, et soudant, si com emplastres et oignemens covenables a ceu; et s’il n’a dedens lou neis nule plaie, si lou cure de tentes, et i met cainnes de plonc, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if no abscesses come to them, apply an external plaster made of sesame flour and powdered frankincense, mixed with a decoction of egg whites, then place light tampons, but do not tie up the nose; and if there is a small fracture in the nose that is broken into small pieces, extract it with suitable instruments, then suture the wound, and treat with substances that promote flesh growth and healing, such as plasters and ointments appropriate for this; and if there are no wounds inside the nose, treat it with tents, and place strips of cloth, until it heals.
de la routure de la mandibule	of the fracture of the jawbone
Quant li mandibule est route desoz, et il n’i a point de plaie defuer, et li brisure est defuer tant soulement, et n’est mie brisiez en dous, fuer que corbelz dedens, si le conoist on legierement.	When the mandible is fractured from below, and there is no wound to surface, and the fracture is only superficial, and it is not broken into two parts, except possibly a small chip inside, one can easily recognize this.
Il covient, se li brisure est en la destre partie, que tu boutes ton doi indice en la bouche dou malaide; et se li brisure est en la mandibule senestre, si boute ton doi indice de la main destre, et boute la brisure dedens legierement, et l’afaite a l’autre main par defuer, et met igal.	If the fracture is on the right side, you should place your index finger in the patient's mouth; and if the fracture is on the left mandible, use your right index finger, gently insert it into the fracture from above, and secure it with your other hand from below, making it equal.
Et se li brisure de la mandibule est desevree en II, si covient que tu aministres extension de II pars, tant qu’il soit igalz.	And if the fracture of the jawbone is displaced in two parts, it is necessary to administer an extension of both sides until they are equal.
Et se commovemens des dens avient, ou routure, si les estrain d’un fil d’or ou d’argent ou de soie, puis met sus la mandibule brisie cerote, et met sus I drapel double; et met sus lou drapel une grant estele bien faite, ou une piece de cuir igal, longe et large selonc la mandibule, et la lie sus au mues que tu pues, et comande a malaide qu’il se repose, et menjuce viandes legieres.	And if the movement of the teeth occurs, or a fracture, then pull them with a gold or silver or silk thread, then place on the broken mandible wax, and put on the wax a double cloth; and place on the cloth a large splint well made, or a piece of leather equal in length and width to the mandible, and tie it securely as you can, and instruct the patient to rest, and eat light foods.
Et se tu vois que li figure se chainge, si le deslie au tier jor, et puis remet a point ceu que c’est chaingiet; et met emplaustre sus, de la poudre dou moulin avec abun d’uef ou farine de sisament, aprés ceu que tu as osteit lou cerote; et met sus l’emplaustre lainne legiere, et se li emplaustres s’aert, et li disposition dou malaide ne se chainge, laisse le tant k’il soit sanez; maintes fois est sanez en III semainnes.	And if you see that the figure changes, then loosen it on the third day and then properly adjust what has changed; and apply a poultice made of mill powder with plenty of eggs or sesame flour, after removing the wax; and place light wool over the poultice, and if the poultices stay in place and the patient's condition does not change, leave it until they are well; often they become well within three weeks.
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit maintes fois.	And if abscesses come, then treat them as we have said many times.
Et s’il i a brisure et plaie ensamble, rewarde se nule piece de l’os en est ostee; si subtilie de l’oster as estrumens covenaubles a ceu.	And if there is both a fracture and a wound, examine whether any part of the bone has been removed; then carefully remove it with suitable instruments.
Et se li plaie est estroite, si l’eslarge a flaime selonc ta necessiteit.	And if the wound is narrow, then widen it with flame according to your necessity.
Et quant tu avras ostees toutes ces pieces, et il n’i demore nule, si cout la plaie, s’ele est large, et met sus I des emplaustres covenaubles a ceu, por enjanrer char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you have removed all these pieces and none remain, then close the wound if it is wide, and apply suitable plasters to it, to heal flesh until it is healthy.
de la forcele	Of the strength
Li forcele brise plusors fois devant, devers l’espaule, et li brisure si est selonc III manieres: ou elle est brisie et desevree en II, et i a pieces, et est li plus legiere a restorer; ou il i a brisure avec plaie.	The collarbone breaks multiple times before the shoulder, and the fracture occurs in III manners: where it is broken and separated into two parts, with fragments, and this is the easiest to restore; where there is a fracture with an open wound.
Et li ovraiges si est quant li brisure est sens plaie, que tu aies II ministres, si que li uns teigne l’ajutoire que sent la forcele brisie; et li autres estende lou col vers la partie; puis met igal la brisure a tes dois, si que li forme soit si com il covient, et n’i ait ne apparance ne chevement.	And the work is such when the fracture is without an open wound, that you have two assistants, so one holds the shoulder where the collarbone is broken; and the other extends the neck towards the affected part; then align the fracture with your hands, so that the form is as it should be, and there appears neither gap nor overlap.
Et se tu a mestier de plus estendre, si met desoz l’espaule au malaide une spere reonde de drap, ou de lainne, et soit grosse selonc ta necessiteit; et estent et lieve la forcele, et estraint le spere a ta main, si que tu mettes igal la brisure, si com il covient.	And if you need to extend further, place under the patient's shoulder a round ball of cloth or wool, and its size should be according to your necessity; then lift the collarbone, and hold the ball with your hand, so that you align the fracture as it should be.
Et se tu ne pues traire le chief de la forcele au defuer, por ceu qu’elle vient em parfont, si covient que li malaides gise sovin sus son hatereil, et met desoz l’espaule I oreillier moien, et boute li ministres l’espaule aval, tant que li os de la forcele soit levez.	And if you cannot draw the head of the humerus out due to its position, then the patient must lie supine on their back, and place a medium-sized pillow under the shoulder, and the assistant should push the shoulder down until the bone of the humerus is raised.
Et puis adrece la brisure a tes dois, et se tu lou trueves debrisiet, si covient que tu fendes sus; et trai fuer les pieces legierement, et se li os ne puet joindre por aucun sormontement, si le cope a l’un des incisoires que tu as; mais que tu mettes desoz la forcele cest estrument, por warder lou syfac:	Then align the fracture with your hands, and if you find it fragmented, you must split it open; gently draw apart the pieces, and if the bone cannot join due to any prominence, cut it with one of your incisors; but place this instrument under the humerus to protect the surface.
et semble une cuiller, et n’est mie chevez, et soit ausi large com il lou covient, selonc la grandor de l’os et la possance de l’uevre; et ait II chiés, si com tu vois, et soit li uns larges, et li autres estrois, si com est li routure de la plaie que tu as fait quant tu as trait les os; et quant tu es asseurez d’aposteme chaut, si cout la plaie, et se li routure est petite, ou tu doutes aposteme chaut, si emple la plaie de drapelz et de tentes, selonc sa quantiteit.	And it resembles a spoon, and is not hairy, and should be as wide as necessary, according to the size of the bone and the strength of the work; and let it have two edges, as you see, one broad and the other narrow, like the shape of the wound that you made when treating the bones; and when you are sure of a hot abscess, cauterize the wound, and if the wound is small, where you doubt a hot abscess, pad the wound with cloths and tents according to its size.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si moille I drapel en oile roset et en aisil et en vin, et met sus.	And if painful abscesses come, moisten a cloth in rose oil and egg yolk and wine, and apply it.
Li estrignement de l’os, quant il est sens plaies et sens tailleure, est que tu mettes sus l’os l’enplaustre de la poudre dou molin et d’aubun d’uef, et met estoupes legieres sus, et met une spere desoz l’assele, se tu en as mestier; puis pren une tres grant bende d’une palme de large, puis met I drapeil double sus estoupes, et l’emplaustre; puis pren une estele subtil de III dois de large et de lonc, et l’envoloupe entor celui bendeil, si que li chief dou bendeil soient pendant; et met l’estele sus la briseure, et torne le bendeil sus lou col, et desoz l’asselle sainne, et desoz l’asselle malaide; et la ramoinne de chescune partie, et quant tu vois ke li lieure tient la briseure avenanment, et tu vois clerement que li estele ne se muet desus l’os brisiet, si le rewarde chescun jor, et quant li liiens eslaiche, si lou restraint; et fai gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et li met quant il dort I petit orillier desoz l’assele, por lever l’ajutoire en haut; si aligera li brisure de la forcele par l’aligement de l’espaule, ou tu li lie lou bras au col, et ne lou desliier se malvais accidens n’i vient, jusc’a XX jors; puis rencomence l’emplaustre, se tu vois qu’il en ait mestier, et l’estraint et le laisse ensi, tant qu’il soit restorez; et elle est restoree au plus en XXVIII jors, et en moins a aucuns homes.	The treatment of the broken bone, when it is not cut or sawed, is that you place on the bone the plaster made from mill powder and egg albumen, then put light bandages over it; if necessary, place a ball under the shoulder blade. Then take a very wide bandage about one palm in width, apply a double layer of cloth and the plaster on top of the bandages, then take a thin stick three fingers wide and long, wrap the bandage around it so that its ends hang down, and place the stick over the fracture; turn the bandage around the neck, under both shoulder blades, and tie each part securely. When you see that the ligature holds the bone properly in place, and clearly the stick does not move over the broken bone, check it daily, and when the ligature loosens, retighten it. Have the patient lie on their back and place a small pillow under the shoulder blade at night to lift the shoulder up; this will ease the fracture by raising the shoulder, where you tie the arm to the neck, and do not untie it unless an unfortunate event occurs, until twenty days have passed. Then start applying the plaster again if needed, tighten it and leave it as is, until it is healed; it usually takes about twenty-eight days or less for some people.
de la brisure de l’espaule	of the fracture of the shoulder
Poc avient que li espaule brise ou large leu ne em mileu, et ne lou seit on fuers que par lou touchement; si l’apareille selonc la figure de la brisure, et la ramoinne selonc sa forme natureil, en toutes les manieres que tu pues; puis met sor le leu poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, et estoupes legieres, et met sus I drapeil double; puis met sus une estele large et subtil, un poc plus large de l’espaule, et se desoz l’estele est chevemens en aucun leu de l’espaule, si emple celle cheveure d’estoupes de lin, si que li estele siece igalment; et puis l’estraint a tout une grant bende fermement, si que li estele ne se mueve de son leu, et regarde le liien chescun jor; et toutes les fois k’il amolist, si l’estraint, et met igal l’estele s’elle est fuer de son leu, et gise li malaides sus son costeit; et li espaule est restouree en XX jors ou en xxv, Et quant cist nombres est acomplis, si le deslie, et soies seur, car ce n’est mie os qui se mette fuer legierement.	Rarely does the shoulder fracture at its widest point or in the middle; and one only knows it by touch. Set it according to the appearance of the fracture, and reset it according to its natural form in all ways you can; then place on the area powder from the mill with plenty of egg, and light bandages, and put a double cloth over it; then place a broad and fine splint slightly wider than the shoulder, and if any part of the splint rests upon the bone of the shoulder, fill that space with linen bandages so that the splint lies evenly; and then bind it firmly all around with a wide strip so that the splint does not move from its place, and check the binding every day; and each time it loosens, tighten it again, and ensure the splint stays straight if it moves out of position, and have the patient lie on their side; and the shoulder will be restored in twenty days or twenty-five. And when this number of days is completed, release it, and be sure, for this is not a bone that resets easily.
Et se une piece de l’os tent avant, et point desoz lou keur, si fent sus, et l’oste, et fai ceu que nos avons dit en la brisure de la forcele d’apaisier aposteme chaut.	And if a piece of the bone protrudes and sticks out from near the heart, cut it off, and do as we have said regarding the fracture to alleviate a hot abscess.
de la brisure dou pis	of the fracture of the foot
Li peis est aucune fois brisiez em mileu, mais ce avient poc; mais il brise sovent au defuer.	The foot is sometimes fractured in the middle, but this happens rarely; however, it often breaks at the tip.
Et quant il est brisiez emmi, si decline au desoz, et sent li malaides grant dolor, et faute d’alainne, et toust, et par aventure vomist sanc, et apert li chevemens en l’os brisiés, et lou sent om bien.	And when it is fractured in the middle, it tilts outward, and the patient feels great pain, and lacks alignment, and swells, and sometimes vomits blood, and the movement of the bone can be felt through the skin.
Et li restoracion si est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos, et li met I cussin entre les espaules, puis presse les espaules, et li assemble les costes des II costelz a tes mains, et subtilie dou mettre igal a toutes les manieres que tu pues, tant que li figure de l’os soit si com il covient; puis met sus emplaustres et estoupes desus l’estele subtil de salz, ou d’autre fust legier, et l’envoloupe en I drapeil, et la lie sus l’os brisiet, si qu’elle ne se mueve; et torne le liien reondement au dos, et l’estraint avenanment, et rewarde chescune houre la liure, et s’elle ramolist, si l’estraint; et s’il lou covient desliier, por corrosion ou por prurite que vient au leu, ou dolor ou aposteme, si te haste, et lou deslie, et raie l’emplaustre, et adresce ceu qui i est venus de manieres de cures; puis ramoinne l’emplaustre, et l’estraint tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the restoration is as follows: the patient lies down on their back, and a cushion is placed between the shoulders, then press the shoulders together, and bring together the ribs with both hands, carefully making them even in all ways possible so that the bone's position is correct; then place poultices and bandages made of fine salt or another light material over the fracture, wrap it securely around the bone so that it does not move; then bind the back tightly, and check every hour the bandage, and if it loosens, tighten it again; if it needs to be removed due to corrosion, itching, pain, or abscess, do so quickly, remove it, treat what has come up from the affected area in appropriate ways; then reapply the poultice and bind it tightly until it is healed.
de la brisure des costes	Of the fracture of the ribs
Saiches que li briseure des costes ne vient fuer que en leus gros aprés le dos, et au chief dedens, et ne ploient fuer que por ceu qu’eles sont glairouses; et le sent om bien a l’inquisition as dois.	Know that the fracture of the ribs only occurs in their thick part behind the back, and at the top because they are smooth; and one feels this well upon examination with both hands.
Et li restoremens si est que tu met igal la brisure, si com il covient.	And the restoration is that you place the fracture evenly as it should be.
Et puis met l’emplaustre, et l’estraint d’une estele, se tu en as mestier.	And then apply the plaster, and bind it with a bandage if you need to.
Et se li brisure des costes est declinans au dedens, si sent li malaides tres grant dolor, et pointure, ausi com de pleuresin, car li os point la toile; et alaine a poinnes, et toust et vomist grant planteit de sanc, et c’est de grief santeit, et li ancien i ont mis grant engien.	And if the fracture of the ribs is displaced inward, the patient feels great pain and piercing, similar to pleurisy, because the bone pierces the tissue; it leads to bleeding, coughing up blood, vomiting large quantities of blood, and this is a serious condition, especially for the elderly.
Et si a de ces qui dient qu’il le covient aministrer viandes qui enflent le ventre, por bouter la briseure au defuer.	And there are those who say that it is necessary to administer foods that swell the belly, to push the fracture outwards.
Nos ne faisons mie ceu, que apostemes chaulz n’i viegne, s’il n’i est venus.	We do not do this, that abscesses may not come, if they have already come.
Et s’il i est venus, si le saine.	And if they have come, then heal them.
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on met ventouses sor le leu, por sucier forment, et c’est semblant a raison; toutevoie, doutance i a que li ventouse n’atraie les superfluitez au leu por la disposition de foiblece.	And some say that one should apply suction cups to the area, to draw out forcefully, and this seems reasonable; nevertheless, there is doubt whether the cups will attract the excesses to the site due to the disposition of weakness.
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on doit covrir le leu de lainne moillie en oile chaut, et met on tentes entre les costes por metre igal la lieure entor, puis soit curez de la cure de pleurisin, de viande et de medicine.	And some say that one should cover the area with wool soaked in hot oil, and place tents between the ribs to evenly distribute the poultice, then treat it according to the treatment for pleurisy, with food and medicine.
Et se li malaides sent grant dolor qu’il ne puet soffrir par l’os qui point la toile, et doutance est au malaide, si covient fendre sus lou leu de la coste brisie, et covient mettre desoz I estrument por warder lou syfac; et adonques doit on trenchier l’os, et traire legierement, et puis coudre les II levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, et le curez d’emplaustres, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the patient feels great pain that they cannot bear from the bone piercing the skin, and there is doubt for the patient, it is necessary to cut along the area of the broken rib, and place an instrument to protect the surface; then one must cut the bone lightly, and then stitch together the two edges of the wound if it is large, and treat with plasters until he is healed.
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si met sus drapelz moilliez en oile roset, et met sus lou leu; et cure tandis le leu de ceu qu’il covient a aposteme, et soit gisans sovins sus lou costeit ou il doit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if hot abscesses come, place cloths moistened in rose oil on it; and treat the area as needed for an abscess, and have them lie comfortably on their side where it is necessary, until they are healed.
de la brisure dou col	of the fracture of the neck (or collarbone)
Aucune fois vient briseure as os dou col, et poc avient k’il ploie; et ausi a l’espinee dou dos.	Sometimes there is a fracture of the neck bones, and it can happen that they bend; and similarly for the spine.
Et quant ce avient a aucun, et tu vues savoir s’il sera sanez ou non, si pren warde se tu vois ses mains mollifiies et enflees et mortes, et ne les puet movoir ne estendre, et quant tu les poins d’une aguille, si ne lou sent.	And when this happens to someone, and you wish to know if they will be well or not, observe if you see their hands soft, swollen, and dead-colored, and cannot move or stretch them, and when you prick them with a needle, they do not feel it.
Saiches qu’il est mortelz em plusors dispositions, et s’il les muet et sent bien quant on les estraint et point, saiches que li jointure de l’os est sauve, et que li malaides iert curez, s’on i met cure.	Know that it is mortal in many cases, and if they move and feel well when you pinch and prick them, know that the joint of the bone is safe, and that the patient can be treated, if proper care is applied.
Et se semblans chose vient a l’espinee dou dos, et tu vues savoir s’il iert sanez ou non, si pren warde se li piez sont amollis, et se li accident i sont qui sont em mains, et sus lou dos saut ventositeit et egestion sens volonteit; et quant on l’a sovineit sus son ventre, si saut egestion sens volonteit.	And if a similar thing happens to the spine, and you wish to know if they will be well or not, observe if the feet are weak, and if the symptoms are like those in the hands, and on the back there is swelling and involuntary evacuation; and when you turn them over onto their belly, there is also involuntary evacuation.
Et quant il est sovinez sus son dos et il vuet asseller, si ne puet.	And when he is lying on his back and wants to sit up, he cannot.
Saiches qu’il est mortelz: si ne laboreir mie en sa cure.	Know that it is deadly: do not labor in its cure.
Et se cist accident ne li vienent, si est li chose plus legiere.	And if these accidents do not occur to him, then the matter is lighter.
Et li cure si est que tu rewardes s’il i a aposteme chaut, si met sus l’espinee oile roset ou oile de moieuf d’uef, tant qu’il soit apaisiez; puis met sus un des emplaustres confortans et sechans, et le lie d’un liien, et comande au malaide a reposer; et ne dorme mie sus celle partie ou il sent la dolor, tant k’il soit sanez.	And the treatment is that you should apply it if there is a hot abscess, using rose oil or boiled egg oil until it subsides; then place one of the comforting and drying plasters on it, and bind it with a bandage, and instruct the patient to rest; and do not let him sleep on the part where he feels pain until he is healed.
Et se aucuns os se dessevre, si covient coper sus lou keur; et oste l’os, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, a une costure, puis le cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li chiés de l’os est brisiez, ki est apelez li «chiés de la kowe», se i boute ton pouchet de ta main senestre, et le met igal a l’autre main a ton pooir, puis met l’emplaustre et l’estele sus, se tu en a mestier; puis l’estraint, et s’il i a os desevreit, si fent sus, et l’oste, et cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And if any bone breaks, it must be treated on the chest; remove the bone, then stitch together the two edges of the wound if it is large, with stitching, and treat it with an ointment that promotes flesh growth until it is healed; and if the head of the bone is fractured, which is called the "head of the shoulder," place your left palm in there, and set it equal to your other hand as far as you can, then apply the plaster and bandage if needed; then compress it, and if any bones are broken apart, cut them up, remove them, and treat the wound until it is healed.
de la brisure de l’os de la hainche	Of the fracture of the hip bone
Poc avient que li os de la hainche soit brisiez, et s’il avient, si n’avient fuer c’un poc d’amenuisement au chief; et fent dou lonc, et decline au pardedens, et vient au malaide dolor au leu, et pointure, et enfle ceu que brise.	It rarely happens that the hip bone is fractured, and if it does happen, there is only a slight reduction at the top; it extends along its length, and tilts inward, causing pain to the patient at the site, and bruising, and swelling where it is broken.
Et li restoration si est que tu estendes ta main sus, tant que tu soies sus la briseure; et saiches quelz est li brisure et li figure de li; et se li brisure est au chief soulement, si met igal cele brisure, tant qu’ele soit a figure natureil.	And the restoration is such that you extend your hand above, until you are above the fracture; and determine where the fracture is and its shape; and if the fracture is only at the top, then make it even so that it has a natural appearance.
Et se li brisure est dou lonc, ou elle decline au dedens, si fai gesir le malaide sus son ventre, tant que li restauration de cele brisure te soit aparillie.	And if the fracture extends along its length and tilts inward, make the patient lie on their stomach until the restoration of that fracture is prepared.
Et quant tu l’avras mise igal, si met sus l’emplaustre, puis met sus une estele de fust ou de keur, et estraint la briseure, si qu’ele ne se mueve; et emple le leu desoz les costes, tant que li lieure soit igalz.	And when you have made it even, apply the poultice, then place a splint of wood or cork, and secure the bandage so that it does not move; and cover the area under the ribs until the flesh is even.
Et comande au malaide k’il dorme sus son costeit sain, ou sus son dos.	And instruct the patient to sleep on their healthy side or on their back.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si n’i tochier, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et met sus ceu que nos avons devant dit; et puis revien a la restauration, et l’estraint si com il covient, s’il n’i a nul mavais accident; et c’est li maniere.	And if hot abscesses occur, do not touch them until the hot abscesses are eased, and apply what we have mentioned before; then return to the restoration process, and bind it as is appropriate, if there is no bad accident; and this is the method.
de la brisure de l’ajutoire	of the fracture of the shoulder
Li adjutoires est ceu qui est entre lou coute et lou chief de l’espaule, et s’il est brisiez, si le doit on restorer selonc l’une des II manieres: dont l’une est que tu pren I fust plain de moiene groissor, selonc ceste forme:	The shoulder joint is what lies between the collarbone and the head of the shoulder, and if it is broken, then it must be restored according to one of two methods: one of which is that you take a stick filled with medicinal poultice, in this form:
Et lie as II chiés II liens, et les pent en haut, et siece li malaide sus I siege; puis li giete som bras brisiet sus le fust, tant qu’il viegne a l’aissele, et ait em mi une corbeure de fust, puis pent sus aucune pesant chose ou li ministres l’estende aval; puis mette li mires la briseure igal a ses mains ensamble, tant que li briseure retorne si com il covient.	And tie the two ends with two ropes, and pull them up, and seat the patient on a chair; then place the broken arm on the stick, as far as the armpit, and have it bend in a wooden hoop, then lift it with some heavy object while the assistant holds it down; then place the splint equal to both hands, so that the splint returns as needed.
Et li autre maniere si est que on sovine le malaide sus son hatereil, et li lie la main a son col, puis comande a II ministres que li uns teigne ceu qui est sus la briseure a ses mains, et li autres teigne desoz a tout I liien, et estende chescuns a sa partie.	And the other method is that you lift the patient onto his back, and tie the hand to his neck, then instruct two assistants that one pull from above at the point where it meets the hands, and the other pull from below along the entire length, stretching each part accordingly.
Et se tu vues que li estraction soit plus fors, si estraint I liien desoz la briseure, et sus la briseure, et estende chescuns des ministres a sa part.	And if you wish for the extraction to be stronger, then remove the ligament below the fracture, and above the fracture, and extend each of the muscles to their part.
Et se li briseure est prochiene au chief de l’espaule, si covient que tu mettes I liien moien desoz l’assele, et I autre vers lou coute, desoz la briseure; et ausi se li briseure est devers lou coute, si i covient mettre I liien legierement, sens labor, tant que li briseure soit igalz sus lou leu, et sus lou coute; puis met igal la brisure, si com il covient, et l’estraint, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	And if the fracture is close to the head of the shoulder, then it is necessary to place one ligament under the collarbone, and the other towards the side, below the fracture; and similarly, if the fracture is towards the side, then it should be placed lightly without labor, until the fracture is level on the spot, and on the side; then make the fracture even as it should be, and secure it, unless abscesses cause issues.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si ne l’estraindre mie jusc’a VII jors, et met sus lainne moillie en aisil et en oile roset, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez; puis l’estraint, et li maniere de l’estraindre si est que tu mettes l’emplaustre sus la briseure, puis assemble le bras sus l’ajutoire, et met ta main sus l’espaule ou sus lou sein; et met le drapeil, et estraint sus l’ajutoire, et sus lou bras, si que li bras soit en leu d’esteles, s’aucune chose ne le te deffent, ou se li os n’est muez.	And if abscesses appear, then do not extract until VII days have passed, and place linen moistened in grease and rose oil on it until the harmful abscess is calmed; then secure it, and the method of securing it is to apply a poultice over the fracture, then bring the arm onto the shoulder joint, and put your hand on the shoulder or chest; and place the bandage, and secure it over the joint and the arm, so that the arm is in position straight, if nothing prevents it, or if the bone has not moved.
Et se tu doutes que li os ne se mueve, si use d’esteles, et met sus la brisure une estele plus large et plus fort des autres, et ait entre chescune estele I doi d’espaice, et soit chescune estele si grans qu’elle passe la briseure III dois de chescune part; puis estrain sus les esteles, ensi com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre sus la briseure, plus fort et moins en aloignant.	And if you doubt that the bone does not move, use splints, and place on the fracture a splint wider and stronger than the others, and have between each splint one thumb's width of space, and let each splint be so large that it extends three thumbs' widths beyond each side; then bind over the splints as I said at the beginning of the chapter over the fracture, more firmly and less in stretching.
Et se tu vois l’assise des esteles, et l’estrignement, si com nos avons dit, en l’oure que tu restoures le membre brisiet, et tu doutes l’aposteme chaut, si le laisse a liier jusc’a septime jor, si com nos avons dit; puis regarde chescuns III jors lou lien, que prurite ne enfleure n’i viegne au leu, ou li norrissemens ne puist venir au membre por ceu k’il est trop estrois.	And if you see the arrangement of the splints and the binding as we have said, when you restore the broken limb, and you fear a hot abscess, leave it bandaged until the seventh day, as we have said; then check the bandage every three days to ensure that itching or swelling does not occur at the site where new tissue cannot form because it is too tight.
Si l’adrece, si com nos avons dit.	If he is positioned as we have said.
Et se nulz telz accidens n’i vient, si ne lou desliier fuer que aprés III jors ou plus, et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ait ses mains sus son stomac; et met desoz l’ajutoire I cussin plain de laine igalment, et regarde chescune houre dou jor ou de la nut, que li figure dou membre brisiet ne se mueve, ou ne soit amollis li liiens; si l’adrece par la vertu de medicine, et li done la viande que nos avons devant mis, en teil maniere que li viande soit au premier subtilz; et quant il comance a reprendre, si soit grosse.
